# THE BOOK OF JOSHUA {.heading_sH}

# Introduction {.heading_s2B}

Joshua is the sixth book in the Bible. In the Jewish division of the Old Testament (see Luke 24:44), the book would fall in the "writings" ([Nahbim,]{.class_s2FX} what Jesus called ["the prophets"]{.class_s2FW}). In the "Christian" division of the Old Testament, the first five books of the Bible are called "the Pentateuch" ("five books"). Sometimes the book of Joshua is added to those books, and they are referred to as "the Hexateuch" ("six books"). The reason for doing that is because Joshua's ministry is viewed as a continuation of Moses' ministry (see 1:5). Normally, though, Joshua is included in the "History" books (Joshua--Esther).

The book of Joshua contains 24 chapters, 658 verses, and 18,854 words. Archbishop Ussher places the dates for the events of the book between 1451 B.C. and 1427 B.C., although, personally, I would place the dates around 1510--1486 B.C.

The author of the book is obviously Joshua himself. There is a possibility that a few additions may have been made during the time of the judges, and even possibly by [Samuel]{.class_s2FX} (although that last part is conjecture). When Joshua wrote his book, he also made some entries into Deuteronomy and possibly even Genesis (Josh. 24:26 cf. Gen. 14:14).

Joshua first shows up in Exodus 17:9, and from the start, he is involved in [combat.]{.class_s2FX} Joshua always thinks as a [military commander.]{.class_s2FX} When Moses comes down from Sinai after receiving the Ten Commandments and hears the "rock concert" going on around the golden calf, it is Joshua who mistakes it for ["a noise of war in the camp"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 32:17). Of course he was wrong, but you can see his mindset.

Joshua was from the tribe of  [Ephraim]{.class_s2FX} and was chosen as one of the twelve men to spy out Canaan (Num. 13:8). He and Caleb were the only two who preached ["the gospel"]{.class_s2FW} that the Israelites were ["well able to overcome"]{.class_s2FW} the giants of the land (Heb. 4:2 cf. Num. 13:30, 14:6--9). His philosophy of warfare can be summed up by the old expression from World War II: "Praise the Lord and pass the ammunition." He had faith to believe that as long as he was doing []{#c25.xhtml_page_4}what God told him to do, he would always be assured the victory.

Joshua starts out as a slave laborer in Egypt and ends up as a conquering military leader in the Promised Land. As such, he stands out as a great picture of the Lord Jesus Christ in His humiliation and exaltation (Phil. 2:5--11).

The book is divided into three main sections, with a postscript in the last two chapters. Chapters 1--12 cover the conquest of Canaan; chapters 13--21 cover the division of the land; chapter 22 deals with the departure of the Transjordanian tribes (Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh) to their inheritance. The "postscript" to the book (chaps. 23-24) covers the last days of Joshua.

The doctrinal import of the book is that Joshua is a type of the Lord Jesus Christ at His Second Advent. The name [Joshua]{.class_s2FX} is the Hebrew word for [Jesus.]{.class_s2FX} Look at Hebrews 4:8 and Acts 7:45.

["For if JESUS had given them rest, then would he not afterward have spoken of another day"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 4:8). Historically, that's a reference to Joshua bringing Israel into the land after the forty years of wandering in the wilderness (Heb. 4:7; Psa. 95:7--11; Num. 14:28--35). Joshua was able to bring the Israelites into the land, but they had no permanent rest. The warfare that began in Joshua continued into the book of Judges after Joshua was dead (see Judg. 1--2).

But look at the application put on Hebrews 4:8 in its context. What the Old Testament Joshua could not do, the New Testament "Joshua" could (Heb. 4:9--16), [spiritually]{.class_s2FX} in the Church Age and later [literally]{.class_s2FX} in the Millennium.

["Which also our fathers that came after brought in with JESUS into the possession of the Gentiles, whom God drave out before the face of our fathers, unto the days of David" ]{.class_s2FW}(Acts 7:45).

That's [historically]{.class_s2FX} true in the book of Joshua; it will be [prophetically]{.class_s2FX} true of Jesus Christ at the Second Advent. When Jesus returns, He drives out the United Nations forces under the command of the Antichrist, and the picture given by the Holy Spirit is [Joshua]{.class_s2FX} (Zech. 14:3 cf. Josh. 10:14). When that happens, He does what Joshua could not: end all warfare (Isa. 2:4). Israel is finally in the land God promised to Abraham in Genesis 15:18 (cf. Ezek. 48), and []{#c25.xhtml_page_5}there is no nation that can stand against the King who is the Creator (Zech. 14:9, 16--19).

Now if you look up Hebrews 4:8 and Acts 7:45 in nearly any "modern translation," you will find ["Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} has been changed to ["Joshua."]{.class_s2FX} That may not seem like much, but it is a subtle attempt by the Devil to [destroy revelation]{.class_s2FX} given to you by the Holy Ghost in the [Authorized Version.]{.class_s2FX} You see, the word for ["Joshua"]{.class_s2FX} in Hebrews 4:8 and Acts 7:45 is the Greek word [Iesous.]{.class_s2FX} That's the same word that [any]{.class_s2FX} English Bible transliterates as the word [Jesus]{.class_s2FX} in regards to the Lord. So by changing ["Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} to ["Joshua"]{.class_s2FX} in Hebrews 4:8 and Acts 7:45, the connection of Joshua to Jesus Christ is lost. So even though we may acknowledge that the ["Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} of those two verses is the historic Joshua, we will not change the God-honored English text lest we destroy revelation given by its Author.

Take, for instance, Acts 7:45. Not only is that passage an historic reference to Joshua, it is also [literally true]{.class_s2FX} of the Lord Jesus Christ. You see, in the Old Testament, the Lord Jesus appeared in His preincarnate state as the Angel of the Lord (see Hos. 12:3--4). It was the Angel of the Lord who appeared to Joshua as ["the captain of the LORD'S host"]{.class_s2FW} in Joshua 5:13--15.

Brethren, I don't care how innocent it may seem, any change to that Book ([AV]{.class_s2FX} 1611) results in a [loss of revelation.]{.class_s2FX} I will [expound]{.class_s2FX} the text, [define]{.class_s2FX} the text, [teach]{.class_s2FX} the text, etc.; but I refuse to [change]{.class_s2FX} the text.

The main theme of the book of Joshua is [warfare.]{.class_s2FX} Now every passage of Scripture has [three]{.class_s2FX} applications: [historical, doctrinal,]{.class_s2FX} and [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} or [devotional.]{.class_s2FX} In the Old Testament, the [historic]{.class_s2FX} application of Joshua is to a [literal, visible, physical nation]{.class_s2FX} given promises to a [literal, visible, physical land.]{.class_s2FX} As such, the warfare of Joshua is [physical,]{.class_s2FX} with physical swords, spears, helmets, shields, bows, arrows, etc.

When it comes to that physical warfare, there are two approaches by a lost world. One is the accusation of [injustice]{.class_s2FX} by the Liberals, skeptics, atheists, and agnostics. Those Jews were commanded by [God]{.class_s2FX} to go into the land of Canaan and kill every man, woman, and child (Deut. 20:16--18): [genocide.]{.class_s2FX} Well, obviously "the God of the Old Testament" cannot be the "loving God" of the New []{#c25.xhtml_page_6}Testament (1 John 4:8). After all, no "loving God" would approve of wiping out whole races of people, would He? Would He?!

The idea of a primitive, unjust God in the Old Testament ignores two important things. First, it ignores the very [nature]{.class_s2FX} of God. The God of that Bible is not only loving and merciful, He's also absolutely [holy]{.class_s2FX} and [righteous.]{.class_s2FX} As a holy, righteous God, He is not going to put up with man's sin forever. God in His mercy and longsuffering may extend long periods of time for men to get right (e.g., Gen. 6:3), but when the axe finally falls, sinners have no one to blame but themselves. God extends the opportunity to repent and get right on more than one occasion.

You take those Hittites, Amorites, Canaanites, Perizzites, Hivites, Girgashites, and Jebusites God told Joshua to wipe out. The Lord gave them [400 years]{.class_s2FX} to get right, and they wouldn't do it (Gen. 15:13--16). By the time He sent His chosen people in there on a campaign of genocide against them, it was against seven races of people whose ["iniquity"]{.class_s2FW} was finally ["full."]{.class_s2FW} The inhabitants of Canaan weren't just idolaters, they were committing some of the most depraved practices a sinner can commit (Lev. 18:3). They were involved in [incest, child sacrifice, sex perversion,]{.class_s2FX} and [bestiality;]{.class_s2FX} in other words, [everything the American government is now teaching your children in the public school system.]{.class_s2FX}

God Almighty told you those kinds of abominations [defile a nation and its land]{.class_s2FX} (Lev. 18:24--25). A nation which practices such filth (like America has for the last thirty years) has one destiny: ["the land itself vomiteth out her inhabitants"]{.class_s2FW} (Lev. 18:25). When those Jews began to practice all the abominations found in Leviticus 18, they got the same treatment the inhabitants of Canaan did (Lev. 18:27--28 cf. 2 Kings 17:20--23). The only thing that kept them from being completely wiped out, like the land's former occupants, was the promises God made to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob (Rom. 11:28).

[America has no such promises.]{.class_s2FX} You can expect God to treat this country just like He treated the antediluvians, the Canaanites, the Egyptians, the Israelites, the Babylonians, the Persians, the Greeks, the Romans, etc. The United States will not be the exception to the rule, no matter how arrogant it has become in its pride and conceit.

The other approach to the physical warfare of Joshua is to try to []{#c25.xhtml_page_7}duplicate the God-ordained "Church-State" of the Old Testament. The Roman Catholic Church justified the slaughter of millions of people during the Dark Ages on the belief that [it]{.class_s2FX} was the replacement for the Jewish theocracy of the Old Testament. That is why the Catholic Church has "holy" water, "holy" vestments, altars, incense, censers, bells, literal sacrifices (in the guise of a starchy cookie and hootch, of course, of course), priests, "holy" vessels, "tabernacles," etc.; even though all those things were done away with for the New Testament Christian at Calvary (Col. 2:14). The Roman Catholic Church is nothing but a pagan counterfeit of Old Testament Israel.

The other "pretender to the throne" which claims to take the place of Israel (Matt. 21:43) is Mohammed's "Islamic Nation." Mohammed never had an original thought in his life; everything he taught he stole from other religions. When he wanted to justify rape, murder, slavery, and conquest, he simply went back into the Old Testament (specifically Deut. 20) and stole every instruction given to Israel by God on how to conduct physical warfare and twisted them to fit his own perverted desires.

While Islam claims that its adherents only conduct "defensive warfare," the fact of the matter is that, outside of defending Palestine against Roman Catholic Crusaders, every military campaign carried out by Moslems for six hundred years after Mohammed began going into epileptic fits when receiving his revelation from a 600-winged angel ("Gabriel") was [offensive]{.class_s2FX} warfare. Nobody in Palestine, Egypt, Persia, India, North Africa, Spain, France, Poland, Asia Minor, the Balkans, or Italy attacked any Mohammedan first.

To a Mohammedan, physical warfare for the purpose of [conquest]{.class_s2FX} is justified when a nation [won't accept his religion.]{.class_s2FX} "The peace of Allah" doesn't mean a cessation of hostilities; it means there is [no opposition left to "Allah"]{.class_s2FX} in a country. If a nation "rejects Allah," that's an "offense" which must be "defended." Hence, every [offensive invasion]{.class_s2FX} "in the name of Allah" becomes "defensive warfare" and a ["jihad"]{.class_s2FX} (a "holy war") in Mohammed's twisted system.

The fact of the matter is that Mohammed was from the [rejected]{.class_s2FX} son of Abraham. Mohammed claimed to be seventieth in descent from Abraham's son [Ishmael.]{.class_s2FX} That was the son God told Abraham to ["cast out"]{.class_s2FW} in [two Testaments]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 21:10--12; Gal. 4:30).

The God who spoke [personally]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c25.xhtml_page_8} to Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, Moses, and Joshua [didn't say one word]{.class_s2FX} to Mohammed. Not one word in the [Koran]{.class_s2FX} was given to Mohammed by Allah directly; the whole thing was "relayed" to him by "Gabriel." Whoever "the God" was (the word [Allah]{.class_s2FX} means "the God"), he certainly [wasn't]{.class_s2FX} the God of the Old Testament or the New (see our work ["Will the Real 'Allah' Please Stand Up?"]{.class_s2FX}).

The God who commanded Moses and Joshua to carry out genocide against the inhabitants of Transjordan and Canaan never told any Jew to spread his religion [by force.]{.class_s2FX} The only "offensive warfare" carried out by the nation of Israel to take land by military conquest was for territory [promised by God]{.class_s2FX} in Genesis 15:18 (see 2 Sam. 8:3). Outside of [that]{.class_s2FX}, no Jewish King (from either the northern or southern kingdoms) took one square inch of Turkey, Greece, Libya, Algeria, Persia, India, Spain, France, etc.

When God [temporarily]{.class_s2FX} dumped His chosen people for rejecting their Messiah (Matt. 21:43), and in their place created a new nation and priesthood through the New Birth (1 Pet. 2:2--9), [physical]{.class_s2FX} warfare went out the window. The Apostle Paul said, ["the weapons of our warfare are NOT CARNAL"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 10:4). The weapons of the Christian are not swords, bombs, rockets, knives, etc.; they are the [word of God]{.class_s2FX} and [prayer]{.class_s2FX} (Eph. 6:17--18).

So although the book of Joshua cannot be applied [physically]{.class_s2FX} to the New Testament Christian, there are certainly [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} lessons to be drawn for his [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} warfare against the world, the flesh, and the Devil. The born-again child of God is to ["war a good warfare"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 1:18). He is to ["endure hardness as a good soldier of Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:3). And the same ["captain"]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}who appeared to Joshua on the plains of Jericho (Josh. 5:13--15) is [our ]{.class_s2FX}["captain"]{.class_s2FW} also (Heb. 2:10).

The book of Joshua is a [picture]{.class_s2FX} of the Christian's warfare. In the book of Joshua, those Israelites cross Jordan to go into the Promised Land. That's a picture of two things. First of all, it's a picture of going across the river of death to Heaven. "I won't have to cross Jordan alone; Jesus died for my sins to atone. When the darkness I see, He'll be waiting for me. I won't have to cross Jordan alone." If you've trusted Jesus Christ as your Saviour, when it comes []{#c25.xhtml_page_9}time to die, your "Joshua" will be there to get you across "Jordan" and into the inheritance God promised you (1 Pet. 1:4).

But in the book of Joshua, those Jews have to fight to get their inheritance. Well, that's not a picture of Heaven. Once you're up there with your Lord and Saviour, you don't have to fight to stay there; your "warfare" is over. The saints of yesteryear used to talk about the "Church Militant" (the saints down here on earth) and the "Church Triumphant" (the saints up in Heaven).

So the book of Joshua is also a picture of a Christian being given a new life in Christ at salvation. The Christian life after that is a fight against the world, the flesh, and the Devil to see that the believer doesn't lose his joy, his testimony, his fellowship, and his rewards. The book of Joshua is a picture of that fight. The problem with Christians today is they don't want to fight. One pastor said he couldn't get his choir to sing "Onward Christian Soldiers" because there were too many [conscientious objectors.]{.class_s2FX}

All right, the [historical]{.class_s2FX} application is to Joshua [literally]{.class_s2FX} taking the land by military force. The [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} application is to the Christian's [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} battle against ["principalities," "powers," "the rulers of the darkness of this world,"]{.class_s2FW} and ["spiritual wickedness in high places"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:12). The [doctrinal]{.class_s2FX} application is to the [Second Advent of the Lord Jesus Christ.]{.class_s2FX}

Although the Lord Jesus did not come the first time as a conquering King, He will the second time (2 Thess. 1:7--9; Rev. 19:11--21; Zech. 14:1--15; Isa. 63:1--6). Joshua 10:13--14 shows up [twice]{.class_s2FX} in regards to the Second Advent (Hab. 3:11; Zech. 14:3). When Jesus Christ returns, He crosses Jordan at the place where Joshua crossed it and where Jesus Himself was baptized at His First Coming (see[ The Path of the Second Advent]{.class_s2FX}). He will fight against a cursed city (Mystery Babylon---Rev. 17--18). He will lift the curse on the remnant of Israel at the same place Achan was stoned to turn the Lord from His anger over Achan taking ["the accursed thing"]{.class_s2FW} (Josh. 7 cf. Isa. 65:10; Hos. 2:15). So when you read about the conquest of Canaan, you are getting a doctrinal picture of what Jesus does at His return in power.

Now before getting into the text of Joshua, the Bible believer should note one last great doctrinal lesson of the book. When it came []{#c25.xhtml_page_10}to bringing the nation of Israel into the Promised Land, it wasn't [Moses;]{.class_s2FX} it was [Joshua.]{.class_s2FX} The Lawgiver couldn't get those Jews into the Promised Land; he couldn't even get himself into the Promised Land. It took ["Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} to get them in (Acts 7:45).

The lesson for the New Testament believer should be obvious. If you are ever going to get to your "Promised Land" (Heaven or the New Jerusalem---Heb. 12:22), Moses (the Law) can't do a thing for you. It's going to take the "Joshua" of the New Testament.

["For the law was given by Moses, but grace and truth came by Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (John 1:17).

["And by him]{.class_s2FW} \[i.e., [Jesus Christ]{.class_s2FX}\][ all that believe are justified from all things, from which ye could not be justified by the law of Moses"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 13:39).

With those great Biblical truths before us, let us now delve into the book of one of the greatest Generals in military history. Joshua is one of only three commanders who never lost a battle as long as he was personally leading the troops (the other two being [David]{.class_s2FX} and [Oliver Cromwell]{.class_s2FX}). As in every volume in the Bible Believer's Commentary Series, we will believe the [King James]{.class_s2FX} text as it stands. We will not change one word of it to meet the demands of scholarship, "science" (1 Tim. 6:20), or ecclesiastical authority. We take it up as the great ["sword of the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:17), given to us by our "Commander-in-Chief": the New Testament "Joshua," the Lord Jesus Christ (Heb. 2:10). We are convinced that when that Book is [believed]{.class_s2FX} and [obeyed,]{.class_s2FX} it will [do the job every time.]{.class_s2FX}

Heil Jesus! Heil the Book!

[]{#c3T.xhtml}

# Chapter 1 {.heading_s2B}

1:1 Now after the death of Moses the servant of the LORD it came to pass, that the LORD spake unto Joshua the son of Nun, Moses' minister, saying,

2 Moses my servant is dead; now therefore arise, go over this Jordan, thou, and all this people, unto the land which I do give to them, even to the children of Israel.

3 Every place that the sole of your foot shall tread upon, that have I given unto you, as I said unto Moses.

4 From the wilderness and this Lebanon even unto the great river, the river Euphrates, all the land of the Hittites, and unto the great sea toward the going down of the sun, shall be your coast.

5 There shall not any man be able to stand before thee all the days of thy life: as I was with Moses, so I will be with thee: I will not fail thee, nor forsake thee.

The book of Joshua opens up with Joshua taking command in Moses' place. Verse 1 makes it clear that this takes place after the death of Moses in Deuteronomy 34.

Joshua was not only the commander of the troops, he was Moses' ["minister"]{.class_s2FW} as well (Exod. 24:13). That is, he saw to Moses' personal needs. You have a similar situation with Elijah and Elisha. Elisha was chosen ["to be prophet"]{.class_s2FW} in Elijah's place (1 Kings 19:16), and his "on-the-job training" was to help Elijah wash his hands (2 Kings 3:11). The practical lesson, as given by the Lord Jesus, is:

["Whosoever will be great among you, let him be your minister; And whosoever will be chief among you, let him be your servant: Even as the Son of man came not to be ministered unto, but to minister, and to give his life a ransom for many"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 20:26--28).

Moses served God and became the greatest prophet in the Old Testament before John the Baptist and Jesus Christ showed up (Deut. 34:10). Joshua served Moses and was promoted to Moses' place when the time came. The rule in the Christian life is the way [up]{.class_s2FX} is []{#c3T.xhtml_page_12}[down.]{.class_s2FX}

["Humble yourselves therefore under the mighty hand of God, that he may exalt you in due time"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 5:6).

Notice in verse 1 that the Lord spoke [directly]{.class_s2FX} to Joshua. He didn't require any 600-winged demon masquerading as an "angel" (2 Cor. 11:14). When God did use an angel to reveal His word (as He did in Dan. 8--9; Luke 1), it was certainly [nothing]{.class_s2FX} like what happened to Mohammed when he received his "revelation." Mohammed would hear a ringing in his ears and turn beet-red in the face. He would fall to the ground and roll and thrash around, while sweating profusely. He would pass out and snore like a camel. When he came to, he would recite the portion of the [Koran]{.class_s2FX} given to him by "Gabriel" (see [Holy Hadith,]{.class_s2FX} Bukhari, vol. I, nos. 1--4; vol. II, nos. 16, 544; vol. III, nos. 17, 829; vol. IV, nos. 95, 438, 458, 461; vol. V, nos. 170, 462, 618, 659; vol. VI, nos. 447--448, 468, 478, 481, 508).

Angels in the Bible may have caused those to whom they appeared to be afraid, but the command when that happened was ["Fear not"]{.class_s2FW} (see Luke 1:13, 30, 2:10 and comments on those verses in that Commentary). The Gabriel of the Bible managed to reveal what God said to Daniel, Zechariah, and Mary without all the "theatrics" that accompanied Mohammed's revelation of the [Koran.]{.class_s2FX}

Now, Joshua is called ["the son of Nun"]{.class_s2FW}; hence, the joke (riddle): "Who in the Bible had no mother? Joshua, he was the son of Nun (none)." The word [nun]{.class_s2FX} in English, of course, is a monastic religious order of women in the Catholic Church. This is one of those peculiar "coincidences" of history. Our word [nun]{.class_s2FX} comes from the Latin [nonna]{.class_s2FX} which was a word of endearment for an elderly woman like a mother or grandmother; it came to be associated with a [female tutor,]{.class_s2FX} and later a [female monk.]{.class_s2FX} The Hebrew name of Joshua's father was actually the fourteenth letter in the Hebrew alphabet (see the header to Psa. 119:105--112). So despite the identical spelling, the two words are not related.

["Moses my servant is dead"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2). Again, notice the typology. Moses represents the Law; Joshua represents Jesus Christ (see John 1:17). The Law cannot get you into the "Promised Land," spiritually speaking. The Apostle Paul wrote, ["Therefore by the deeds of the law there shall no flesh be justified in his sight: for by the law is the knowledge of sin"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c3T.xhtml_page_13} (Rom. 3:20). All the Law can do for you is let you know you are guilty before God; it can't expunge that guilt. That's going to take "Joshua" (Gal. 3:24). "Moses" has to "pass on" so that "Joshua" can be in control (Gal. 3:25).

["Now therefore arise, go over THIS Jordan."]{.class_s2FW} Like Mount Zion, there are [two]{.class_s2FX} "Jordans." There is the [physical]{.class_s2FX} river in Israel, and there is its spiritual counterpart, [death.]{.class_s2FX}

The word [Jordan]{.class_s2FX} means "the descending one." It goes from 1,100 feet [above]{.class_s2FX} sea level at Mt. Hermon to 1,388 feet [below]{.class_s2FX} sea level at the Dead Sea. It is one of the most crooked, winding rivers in the world. If you measured the distance it travels from the Sea of Galilee to the Dead Sea in a straight line, it would be 65 miles, but if you measured it by the winding path of the river, you would get [200 miles.]{.class_s2FX}

The picture is [death.]{.class_s2FX} The Jordan leads to [death]{.class_s2FX} (the Dead Sea). Jesus was baptized in the Jordan, and when you go down under the water at baptism, that's a picture of [death]{.class_s2FX} (Rom. 6:3). The children of Israel crossed the Jordan just like they crossed the Red Sea (Josh. 3). Paul describes that crossing as a [baptism]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 10:1--2), so those Israelites were experiencing a type of [death.]{.class_s2FX}

Now there are two types of death that the Jordan typifies. It pictures the actual, physical death that takes you home to Glory. The old song goes: "There's a river of death they call Jordan. And they say that it's deep and it's wide. And they say that the prince and the beggar on that shore will stand side by side." Death is the great equalizer; nobody gets out of it.

Another song goes: "On Jordan's stormy banks I stand and cast a wishful eye to Canaan's fair and happy land where my possessions lie." That's the Christian standing on the edge of death and longing for Heaven.

The picture of death as a river or body of water you have to cross is almost universal. The Greeks pictured death as a black river called the Styx over which the boatman Charon transported you to Hades or the Elysian Fields (Hell and Paradise---see Luke 16). In [Pilgrim's Progress,]{.class_s2FX} Christian has to ford the River of Death to get to the Celestial City. When another fellow tries to cross it by boat, the angels take him and pitch him into Hell.

But as we pointed out in the introduction, the children of Israel don't have rest when they cross Jordan into Canaan; they have to fight. So there is another picture of death: death to [self.]{.class_s2FX} In baptism, the picture is death to old man Adam and resurrection life to the new man in Christ. But that new man still has to fight his body of sinful flesh the rest of his life (Rom. 6--7), along with the world and the Devil (James 4), in order to obtain rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ.

["And all this people, unto the land which I do give them, even to the CHILDREN OF ISRAEL."]{.class_s2FW} That is [literal.]{.class_s2FX} It is the death knell for the United Nations, the European Union, NATO, the Arab League, the "Palestinian Authority" (the [PLO,]{.class_s2FX} a [terrorist]{.class_s2FX} organization), the Muslim Brotherhood, the Roman Catholic Church, and the [United States.]{.class_s2FX} That's God giving the land of Palestine to [one race]{.class_s2FX} and [one nation;]{.class_s2FX} and it isn't any European, African, American, Chinaman, Arab, Moslem, or "Palestinian." It's [Jews]{.class_s2FX} from the [twelve tribes of Israel.]{.class_s2FX} It's [Reuben, Simeon, Levi, Judah, Issachar, Zebulun, Dan, Naphtali, Gad, Asher, Benjamin, ]{.class_s2FX}and[ Joseph]{.class_s2FX} ([Manasseh]{.class_s2FX} and [Ephraim]{.class_s2FX}); it's not Palestinians, Arabs, Jordanians, Lebanese, Syrians, Egyptians, Iraqis, Iranians, Moslems, Catholics, Greek Orthodox, "spiritual Jews," or ["the Israel of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 6:16). God promised that land to those Jews more times in one book than He mentioned the virgin birth of His Son in the New Testament (see Deut. 1:7--8, 2:24, 6:1, 10, 7:1, 9:1--4, 26--28, 11:23--25, 12:1--3, 16:20, 17:14, 19:1--3, 21:1, etc.).

Those promises aren't limited to the Old Testament either. The Lord promised to bring those Jews back to the land a [second]{.class_s2G6} time (Isa. 11:11; the first time was in Ezra and Nehemiah), and that they would be there at Jesus Christ's Second Advent, even though they would be there in unbelief (Zech. 12). Moreover, He promised to [fight against]{.class_s2G6} and [destroy]{.class_s2G6} any Gentile nation that comes against His people in that land (Zech. 14). So if you want to sign your death warrant as a nation, just support a "Palestinian State" like Bush, Clinton, and Obama; and you're done for.

If you are going to apply the passage devotionally to the Christian, you would have to say that the victory and blessings you are promised in Christ are to [every]{.class_s2FX} Christian in the Body of Christ. That Bible says you have been []{#c3T.xhtml_page_15}["blessed . . . with all spiritual blessings in heavenly places in Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:3). It says you ["have obtained an inheritance, being predestinated according to the purpose of him who worketh all things for the counsel of his own will"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:11). It says you've been ["sealed with that holy Spirit of promise, Which is the earnest of our inheritance until the redemption of the purchased possession"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:13--14). As a born-again child of God, you can [know]{.class_s2FX} ["what the riches of the glory of his inheritance in the saints . . . Which he wrought in Christ, when he raised him from the dead, and set him at his own right hand in the heavenly places, Far above all principality, and power, and might, and dominion"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:18, 20--21).

Jesus Christ died and rose again to purchase an inheritance for you [now]{.class_s2FX} and [in Heaven]{.class_s2FX} to come. He ascended up to Heaven above the Devil and all His principalities and powers. Colossians 2:15 says He triumphed over them openly and spoiled them at Calvary.

So Jesus Christ is up there at the right hand of God the Father, having gained the victory over the Devil and all his crowd. The Lord has determined ahead of time (["predestinated"]{.class_s2FW}) that if you will trust Jesus Christ as your Saviour, you get all the riches and blessings of God that Jesus Christ purchased when He died on the cross. When you get saved, the Holy Spirit of God comes to live in you and seals you ["unto the day of redemption"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 4:30). That's God's "earnest money," His [downpayment,]{.class_s2FX} that you'll get everything He promised you. The Holy Spirit in you is ["Christ in you, the hope of glory"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 1:27). Jesus Christ is in you, and you are [in Him.]{.class_s2FX} That means that [spiritually]{.class_s2FX} you are up there in Heaven seated with Jesus Christ at God's right hand (Eph. 2:5--6).

Well, if you are up there with Christ, that means you are ["far above all principality, and power, and might, and dominion"]{.class_s2FW} just like He is. That's your spiritual [position]{.class_s2FX} in Christ, your [standing;]{.class_s2FX} your [state]{.class_s2FX} is something else. Your state is down here on earth in a body of sinful flesh. As such, you are in a struggle, a wrestling match, against those same principalities and powers that you are over spiritually in Christ (Eph. 6:12). To gain the victory you have been promised in Christ, you are to []{#c3T.xhtml_page_16}["put on the whole armour of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:11, 13) and FIGHT. If you don't, you are going to be in the same state as the children of Israel were in the book of Judges: constant defeat and enslavement by the Devil, the world, and the flesh. You have to pick up ["the sword of the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:17; Heb. 4:12) and follow your ["captain"]{.class_s2FW} into battle (Heb. 2:10).

["Every place that the sole of your foot shall tread upon, that have I given unto you"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3). Notice the connection between the believer's responsibility in the fight and the Lord's responsibility. The promise here in verse 3 is given in the [past]{.class_s2FX} tense---["that HAVE I GIVEN unto you"]{.class_s2FW} (see also vss. 13--15). The Israelites hadn't gotten one square inch of Canaan yet, but in God's sight, it was an [accomplished fact.]{.class_s2FX}

Now as a Christian, you have been ["blessed . . . with all spiritual blessings in heavenly places IN CHRIST. According as he hath chosen us IN HIM before the foundation of the world . . . Having predestinated us unto the adoption of children BY JESUS CHRIST to himself"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:3--5). Our ["spiritual blessings . . . in Christ"]{.class_s2FW} are based on a decision God made ["before the foundation of the world."]{.class_s2FW} TULIP-sniffing Calvinists read that as God electing you unconditionally before Genesis 1:1. [You weren't in Christ until the Holy Spirit put you there at salvation]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 12:13).

What God determined before Genesis 1:1 is that if you got in Christ by faith in His blood atonement, then the Lord would choose you to be one of His children and to have all the spiritual blessings purchased by your Saviour at Calvary. He determined way back there that such a person would end up just like His Son (cf. Rom. 8:29).

In God's sight, that's an accomplished fact. In the meantime, though, you had better ["walk in the Spirit, and . . . not fulfil the lust of the flesh"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:16). You had better ["grow in grace, and in the knowledge of our Lord and Saviour Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Pet. 3:18). You had better ["yield yourselves unto God, as those that are alive from the dead, and your members as instruments of righteousness unto God"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:13). You need to []{#c3T.xhtml_page_17}["press toward the mark for the prize of the high calling of God in Christ Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 3:14).

In other words, live out in your body what is true in your spirit. And to do that, you will have to fight the world, Satan and his forces, and your own sinful flesh. If you don't, you are going to pay the price in your body here on earth (Gal. 6:7--8; Rom. 8:12--13; 1 Cor. 5:5) and lose rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ (1 Cor. 3:13--15).

Verses 3--5 are promises originally given by Moses in Deuteronomy 11:24--25; hence the words in verse 3: ["as I said unto Moses." "Every place that the sole of your foot shall tread upon, that have I given unto you"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3). God promised the land to those Jews, but they had to go in and fight. That's what He meant by ["the sole of your foot shall tread upon."]{.class_s2FW} If they didn't march into battle and take the land, they didn't get the promise.

That was the problem back in Numbers 13--14. The people became disheartened by the evil report of the ten spies and refused to go in and fight. That's why God made them wander in the wilderness for forty years. A lot of Christians wander aimlessly in their Christian lives because they refuse to ["fight the good fight"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:12). As a result, they never experience the reality of God's promises. If you get engaged in combat, it will drive you to your knees, boy; I kid you not. You will know what it means to "claim the promises" when you are under fire.

Verse 4 is a description of the Abrahamic land grant of Genesis 15:18. When those Jews finally get everything God promised them, not only will they get the "West Bank" and the "Gaza Strip" ([half]{.class_s2FX} the land of Palestine), they'll get [all]{.class_s2FX} of Jordan, [all]{.class_s2FX} of Lebanon, [most]{.class_s2FX} of Syria (including the "Golan Heights"), [half]{.class_s2FX} of Iraq, the [Sinaitic Peninsula,]{.class_s2FX} the [Nile Delta,]{.class_s2FX} and [northern Arabia.]{.class_s2FX} The Moslems are going to have to "eat crow" and plenty of it. Not only will there be no "Palestinian State," there won't be any "Jordanian State," "Lebanese State," or "Syrian State"; and Egypt, Saudi Arabia, and Iraq will give up huge portions of their present territories to the [Israeli State.]{.class_s2FX}

["The wilderness"]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}is generally considered to be the southernmost boundary by the commentators (what is known as "the Negev"), and Lebanon is the northernmost border. The eastern border is the Euphrates River, and the western border is the []{#c3T.xhtml_page_18}Mediterranean Sea. (The Moslems have a surprise coming if they think they can drive Israel into the Mediterranean---see [Israel: A Deadly Piece of Dirt]{.class_s2FX}.)

There seems to be a problem identifying ["all the land of the Hittites"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 4. The older commentaries like Clarke and Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown say it's "the southern extremities" of the land of Canaan. That would place the Hittites around Kadeshbarnea, where Israel originally tried to enter the land (Num. 13--14).

The "original" Hittites in the Bible were located in Hebron (Gen. 23:10, 19) in southern Canaan, where Judah had its inheritance (Josh. 15). It is nineteen miles south of Jerusalem, in the Judean mountains (Num. 13:29). That is hardly "the southern [extremities]{.class_s2FX}."

The Hittite Empire, though, was located up in Asia Minor, where Turkey is today. Some scholars place the new city of Luz that was built in ["the land of the Hittites"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 1:26) up in northern Canaan around the Golan Heights, near Syria.

In the Millennium, the northern border of Israel is up in northern Syria and southeastern Turkey near the headwaters of the Euphrates River (Ezek. 48:1). That is when the Abrahamic land grant promised in Genesis 15:18--21 is finally fulfilled in its entirety, so ["all the land of the Hittites"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 4 here in Joshua 1 would include everything west of the Euphrates River to the Mediterranean Sea, not just "the southern extremities" of Canaan.

Notice again the peculiar use of ["this"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 4: ["this Lebanon."]{.class_s2FW} The implication is that there is [another]{.class_s2FX} Lebanon. Do you know what you find in Song of Solomon 4:8? You find the name of a [deep freeze:]{.class_s2FX} ["Amana."]{.class_s2FW} This "deep freeze" is found in Lebanon, [north]{.class_s2FX} of Israel. What you have is the land of Palestine as a picture of the universe, with the second heaven being separated from the third by a body of water that is [frozen]{.class_s2FX} at the top, forming a ["sea of glass like unto crystal"]{.class_s2FW} (see our comments on Job 38:30; Song of Sol. 4:8; Rev. 4:6 in their respective Commentaries). So there is ["this Lebanon"]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}downstairs and [another one upstairs.]{.class_s2FX}

["There shall not any man be able to stand before thee all the days of thy life"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5). Now how would you like to have a promise like that when you went into battle? That promise stated []{#c3T.xhtml_page_19}that any man Joshua fought, he would whip. Don't you know that old boy was a terror in combat. When he drew his sword, there was no reasoning with him; he knew when he went into a fight, any man he took on, he would kill. The only problem he probably had was getting worn out from all the people he was killing; after killing several hundred people on his own (see those ["mighty men"]{.class_s2FW} in 2 Sam. 23), he probably was so tired that he couldn't run after and "whack" another one.

The promise given to Joshua here in verse 5 is true also of Christ at His Second Advent.

["But who may abide the day of his coming? and who shall stand when he appeareth?"]{.class_s2FW} (Mal. 3:2).

["For the great day of his wrath is come; and who shall be able to stand?"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 6:17).

The answer according to Joshua 1:5 is [no one.]{.class_s2FX} When Jesus Christ comes back, He squashes 200 million UN troops without breaking a sweat (Rev. 9:16 cf. Rev. 14:14--20, Isa. 63:1--6). How's [that]{.class_s2FX} for ["There shall not any man be able to stand before thee"]{.class_s2FW}? They can't ["stand"]{.class_s2FW} because [He stomps them into the ground.]{.class_s2FX} If those Gentile nations don't "knuckle under" during the Millennium, He shuts off the rain, and [they starve to death]{.class_s2FX} (Zech. 14:17--19).

["There shall not any man be able to stand before thee ALL THE DAYS OF THY LIFE."]{.class_s2FW} That's a [thousand years]{.class_s2FX} during Christ's reign. And if you apply that verse to Christ in Eternity, that means once a lost sinner is in the Lake of Fire, he will [never]{.class_s2FX} get out. He will be there as long as his Judge (John 5:22; Acts 17:31; Rom. 2:16) lives.

If you apply that promise devotionally to the born-again believer, you have a picture of complete victory in Christ. The New Testament counterpart of this promise is found in Romans 8:31--37.

"What shall we say to these things? If God be for us, who can be against us? He that spared not his own Son, but delivered him up for us all, how shall he not with him also freely give us all things? Who shall lay any thing to the charge of God's elect? It is God that justifieth. Who is he that condemneth? It is Christ that died, yea rather, that is risen again, who is even at the right hand of God, who also []{#c3T.xhtml_page_20}maketh intercession for us. Who shall separate us from the love of Christ? shall tribulation, or distress, or persecution, or famine, or nakedness, or peril, or sword? As it is written, For thy sake we are killed all the day long; we are accounted as sheep for the slaughter. Nay, in all these things we are more than conquerors through him that loved us."

We're not just [conquerors]{.class_s2FX} of the things that come against us; ["we are MORE than conquerors."]{.class_s2FW} Of course, I have only read of one man who ever attained that level of victory: it was the Apostle Paul. In thirteen epistles (fourteen if you count Hebrews), you will never find Paul lodging a complaint against the Lord one time.

That's quite a feat, did you know that? That couldn't be said of Moses. Those Jews got to griping about having to eat manna all the time; and Moses got fed up with the whole mess and complained to the Lord, ["Wherefore hast thou afflicted thy servant? and wherefore have I not found favour in thy sight, that thou layest the burden of all this people upon me?"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 11:11).

David couldn't say that. Over and over again in the Psalms he asks, "Why have you done this; why have you done that?" He complains to the Lord and says things like: ["how long shall the wicked triumph?"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 94:3), ["how long shall mine enemy be exalted over me?"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 13:2), ["Why hast thou forgotten me? Why go I mourning because of the oppression of the enemy?"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 42:9).

Jeremiah couldn't say that. He complained to God, ["Wherefore doth the way of the wicked prosper? Wherefore are all they happy that deal very treacherously?" ]{.class_s2FW}(Jer. 12:1).

Job couldn't say that. He got so mad at God at one point in his troubles that he said, ["How long wilt thou not depart from me, nor let me alone till I swallow down my spittle?"]{.class_s2FW} (Job 7:19).

But you never hear Paul talking like that. He gets beaten, stoned, shipwrecked, waylaid, persecuted, betrayed, starved, and exposed to the elements (2 Cor. 11:23--27); yet  he never says, "God, why did you do this to me? Why did you let this happen?" Even after the Lord turns him down three times about taking out that thorn in his flesh, Paul doesn't gripe or complain; he [glories]{.class_s2FX} and [takes pleasure]{.class_s2FX} in his []{#c3T.xhtml_page_21}infirmities (2 Cor. 12:8--10). Paul had the victory, and he is your pattern (1 Tim. 1:16) and example to follow (1 Cor. 11:1), Christian.

["As I was with Moses, so I will be with thee."]{.class_s2FW} Way back in Exodus 3:12, the Lord promised to be with Moses to lead the children of Israel out of Egypt. Now the time has come to lead them into the land of Canaan. Both Moses and Joshua are types of Christ (see Deut. 18:18 for Moses as a type of Christ). So just as Jesus Christ can save you ["from this present evil world"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 1:4), He can give you the victory in your Christian life as well.

["I will not fail thee, nor forsake thee."]{.class_s2FW} Here is a good spot for our Hyperdispensationalist brethren to see that you can find New Testament truth in the Old Testament. That promise is quoted in the New Testament in Hebrews 13:5---["I will never leave thee, nor forsake thee."]{.class_s2FW}

That's a great promise on the eternal security of the believer. In the Old Testament, it was applied to the [nation of Israel as a whole;]{.class_s2FX} no matter how much God punished His people for their sins, He never rejected that nation completely because of His promises to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob (Rom. 11:28--29). In the New Testament, that promise is to the [individual believer in Jesus Christ;]{.class_s2FX} no matter how much the Lord has to spank His children (Heb. 12:5--7), He will never dump them and send them to Hell (Eph. 4:30), [no matter what they do]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 5:5). That doesn't mean you give in to sin, Christian; unless you just want to lose your joy, your assurance, your fellowship, your testimony, your rewards, your health, and [your life.]{.class_s2FX} A child of God can lose all kinds of things without losing his salvation.

["I will not fail thee."]{.class_s2FW} I have failed the Lord many times, but He has never failed me. That testimony is so common among Christians that it sounds trite, but it is true. You may fail the Lord time and time again, but He will never fail you. There's a little chorus that goes: "God can do anything, anything, anything; God can do anything but fail." That's true.

6 Be strong and of a good courage: for unto this people shalt thou divide for an inheritance the land, which I sware unto their fathers to give them.

7 Only be thou strong and very courageous, that thou mayest observe to do according to all the law, which Moses my servant commanded thee: turn not from it to the right hand or to the left, that thou mayest prosper whithersoever thou goest.

8 This book of the law shall not depart out of thy mouth; but thou shalt meditate therein day and night, that thou mayest observe to do according to all that is written therein: for then thou shalt make thy way prosperous, and then thou shalt have good success.

9 Have not I commanded thee? Be strong and of a good courage; be not afraid, neither be thou dismayed: for the LORD thy God is with thee whithersoever thou goest.

["Be strong and of a good courage"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). That command is given four times in this chapter (vss. 6, 7, 9, 18), after Moses gave Joshua the same charge three times back in Deuteronomy (Deut. 31:6, 7, 23). It shows up again in Joshua 10:25; 1 Chronicles 22:13, 28:20; and 2 Chronicles 32:7. The command is when you are faced with a choice of doing right or wrong, of honoring God and His word or not honoring God and His word, of obeying the Lord or disobeying Him; you are to muster all the strength you can and do what you know to be right [no matter what it costs you.]{.class_s2FX} Courage is knowing the consequences and doing the right thing anyway. That takes guts, boy.

There's a verse in the Bible that's not even given by a saved person. It's from a bunch of lost, idol-worshipping heathen, but it's got some good advice for a Christian.

["Be strong, and quit yourselves like men, O ye Philistines, that ye be not servants unto the Hebrews, as they have been to you: quit yourselves like men, and fight"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Sam. 4:9).

The Jews had brought out the Ark of the Covenant in their battle with the Philistines, and the Philistines knew what happened to the enemies of Israel when Moses and Joshua hauled it around. But instead of giving up, the Philistines decided to [act like men]{.class_s2FX} and fight anyway. They ended up winning the battle because the Israelites []{#c3T.xhtml_page_23}were treating the Ark as an idol. But the Philistines didn't know that, see; they fought despite the fact that it seemed doomed to failure.

Now before you dismiss that because it was the advice of a bunch of unsaved heathen, do you know what the Apostle Paul told the New Testament Christian in the Body of Christ? He said, ["Watch ye, stand fast in the faith, QUIT YOU LIKE MEN, BE STRONG"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 16:13). When it comes to [courage,]{.class_s2FX} unsaved "dog faces" can teach the Christian something (see our comments on 1 Cor. 16:13 in that Commentary).

Notice, it is not merely courage; it is ["good courage."]{.class_s2FW} The Christian soldier should have more than just grim resolve; he should have a cheerful commitment based on faith in the promises of God (see David's charge to Soloman in 1 Chron. 22:13, 28:20). The Christian isn't just to ["be strong"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 16:13); he is to ["be strong IN THE LORD, AND IN THE POWER OF HIS MIGHT"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:10), and ["be strong IN THE GRACE THAT IS IN CHRIST JESUS"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:1).

Now here in verses 6--7, Joshua is commanded to ["be strong and of a good courage"]{.class_s2FW} for two purposes. One is a [physical]{.class_s2FX} reason, and one is a [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} reason. Joshua is to be strong and courageous: 1) to divide a [physical]{.class_s2FX} land to [physical]{.class_s2FX} tribes for a [physical]{.class_s2FX} inheritance, and 2) to keep a [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} Law. The success of the former depended on the observance of the latter. If you are going to get an inheritance from the Lord, you are going to have to ["walk in the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:16--25), and there's no way to ["walk in the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} without getting into the [words]{.class_s2FX} that are [spirit]{.class_s2FX} and [life]{.class_s2FX} (John 6:63) and [doing]{.class_s2FX} what you find written there (James 1:22). The Holy Spirit is going to lead and guide you through the truth of His [words]{.class_s2FX} (John 16:13, 17:17). You won't hear the words of your Lord ["Well done, thou good and faithful servant"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 25:21, 23) unless you have been faithful to observe and do the words He has left for you in His Book right now.

And then a great verse: ["This book of the law shall not depart out of thy mouth; but thou shalt meditate therein day and night, that thou mayest observe to do according to all that is written therein: for then thou shalt make thy way prosperous, and then thou shalt have good success"]{.class_s2FW} []{#c3T.xhtml_page_24}(vs. 8).

There are two great truths in this verse. The first is that you are[ saved to serve.]{.class_s2FX} You are not saved just to enjoy salvation; God wants you to [do]{.class_s2FX} something. You are [not saved]{.class_s2FX} by works; you are [not kept]{.class_s2FX} by works. But after you are saved, God wants you to work. Right after Paul tells you that you are not saved by works and that saving faith is a free gift from God, you are told:

["For we are his WORKMANSHIP, created in Christ Jesus UNTO GOOD WORKS, which God hath before ordained that we should walk in them"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 2:10).

When the Lord saved you, He made you ["a new creature"]{.class_s2FW} ["in Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:17) who is finally capable of doing a good work. As a lost sinner ["dead in trespasses and sins,"]{.class_s2FW} you were incapable of performing any good work that would please God: ["there is none that doeth good, no, not one"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 3:12). But the believer in Christ has a new man living inside of him that the Holy Spirit produced through the New Birth. That new man can do good works because it was created and ordained for that very purpose.

The next great truth is that this is the first time in history when a man is guided completely by a [book.]{.class_s2FX} Adam, Noah, Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, Joseph, and Moses all got their revelation and instructions directly from God. By the time Joshua comes along though, the first five books of the Bible---Genesis, Exodus, Leviticus, Numbers, Deuteronomy: the Law, the Pentateuch---were all completed (Deut. 31:26). Joshua is the first leader of the people to be under the authority of that Book. Now Moses commanded the Kings of Israel to make a copy of the Book and read it every day (Deut. 17:18--19), but there were no Kings in Joshua 1. The first command for a man to be subject to the Book was given to Joshua.

That is a great lesson for the Christian. The Christian is to go by the Book. Peter calls the Scriptures ["a more sure word of prophecy"]{.class_s2FW} than even the spoken words of God (2 Pet. 1:16--20). The old saying is: "put that down in your little black book." That expression comes from the fact that for 400 years, the standard way of publishing [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bibles was with black covers. The color black symbolizes [death.]{.class_s2FX} That Book is given to make you [dead]{.class_s2FX} to sin and self and make you ["alive unto God through Jesus Christ our Lord"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c3T.xhtml_page_25} (Rom. 6:11). When the Holy Spirit guides the believer ["into all truth"]{.class_s2FW} (John 16:13), He does it through the [Scriptures]{.class_s2FX} because ["thy word is truth"]{.class_s2FW} (John 17:17). In Genesis 41:40, Pharaoh (a type of God the Father in the context) said to Joseph (a type of God the Son), ["according unto THY WORD shall all my people be ruled."]{.class_s2FW}

Notice in verse 9 that the command to be courageous follows the command to get in the Book in verse 8. There are four ways of getting courage from the Bible.

1. You can get courage from [reading]{.class_s2FX} the Book. Paul told the Ephesian Christians, ["I commend you to God and THE WORD OF HIS GRACE, which is able to BUILD YOU UP, and to give you an inheritance among all them which are sanctified"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 20:32). You won't be built up if you don't get into the word and READ IT.

2. You get courage from [speaking]{.class_s2FX} the Book. ["This book of the law shall not depart out of thy mouth."]{.class_s2FW} You should memorize the promises of Scripture and quote them when in need; that will encourage you.

You should quote Scripture when trying to win a soul to Christ. Brethren, the power is in the words of Scripture, not in your own cleverness or ability to persuade. If a person gets saved, if he gets born again, that transaction takes place by the word of God, not by manipulation or out-arguing the sinner (James 1:21; 1 Pet. 1:23).

That Bible says, ["cursed be he that keepeth back his sword from blood"]{.class_s2FW} (Jer. 48:10). You've got to take ["the sword of the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:17) and use it to stab and cut (Heb. 4:12). If you witness to a person and he won't listen to you, at least leave him with something about which to think and make him bleed spiritually.

The man who got me into the ministry, Glen Schunk, witnessed to a Jewish merchant one time in Greenville, South Carolina; and, of course, that Christ-rejecting Jew wouldn't listen to him and told him to get out. Schunk said, "OK, I'll leave; but remember, ['it is appointed unto men once to die, but after this the judgment']{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 9:27)." That Jew said, "Well, I don't believe that." Schunk said, "It doesn't matter if you believe it; ['it is appointed unto men once to die, but after this the judgment.']{.class_s2FW}" He must []{#c3T.xhtml_page_26}have quoted that verse to that lost Jew four or five times.

Well, Glen Schunk would go into that store from time to time to buy something, and every time he did, that Jew would wave at him and yell at the top of his voice, "Hey, Mr. ['It is appointed unto men once to die, but after this the judgment,']{.class_s2FW}" and mock him like that. But one day when Schunk came in, that Jewish businessman pulled him aside and wanted to talk to him. That verse of Scripture Schunk had put on that fellow had been working him over until he couldn't take it anymore, and Schunk led him to Christ. That came from quoting the Scriptures to "draw blood." At His temptation, when Jesus wanted to defeat the Devil, He quoted the Scriptures.

3. You can get courage by [meditating]{.class_s2FX} on the Book. That's not "transcendental meditation" like you find in Hinduism and Buddhism; it's not trying to achieve a passive state and "trip out of the frame." There's a new movement in these neo-Liberal churches (known as "emergents")where they go back to the mystic practices of Roman Catholic monks in the Middle Ages. A portion of Scripture is repeated in prayer like a Hindu mantra; this is supposed to bring the one praying the Scripture closer to God. Jesus Christ called it the ["vain repetitions"]{.class_s2FW} of ["the heathen"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 6:7).

There's nothing wrong with claiming the promises of Scripture in prayer or meditating on Scripture, but repeating something over and over again in an attempt to get closer to God does nothing for you. The way to stay close to God in prayer is to stay "'fessed up" on your sins (Isa. 59:2 cf. 1 John 1:9), and stay clean daily by ["the washing of water by the word"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 5:26). The Christian has access to ["the throne of grace"]{.class_s2FW} by the merits of his High Priest (Heb. 4:14--16), not by any mystic meditation.

When the Bible speaks of meditating on the word, it is talking about [thinking]{.class_s2FX} about what you have read in the Scriptures and [considering]{.class_s2FX} how what you have read can be applied properly to your Christian life. The picture is [digestion.]{.class_s2FX} To get the good out of a meal, you have to digest it properly.

If you want a really good picture of meditation when it comes to the Bible, watch a cow. A cow will graze out there in the field; then it will go lie down somewhere and bring that food back up and chew on []{#c3T.xhtml_page_27}it for a while. That's called "chewing the cud." You don't get everything out of the Bible just by reading it. You have to bring up what you read throughout the day and think about it and consider it. That will help build the courage you need, because you are reinforcing what you read until it is real to you.

["But thou shalt meditate therein day and night."]{.class_s2FW} When you lie in your bed at night and can't get to sleep, work on a verse of Scripture for a while. Take a passage you haven't mastered and see if you can master it.

Here's a good example: ["And the Spirit of God moved upon the face of the waters"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 1:2). Well, where were ["the waters"]{.class_s2FW}? How big were they? What did ["the Spirit of God"]{.class_s2FW} do when He ["moved upon the face of the waters"]{.class_s2FW}? What was it like at the top of those ["waters"]{.class_s2FW}? Just think about some of those things and work on them in your mind. Later on, when you wake up, you can study them further. That's true Bible meditation.

4. Finally, you get courage by [doing]{.class_s2FX} what the Book says. James wrote, ["But be ye doers of the word, and not hearers only,"]{.class_s2FW} and if you don't "do" the word, then you deceive yourself (James 1:22). You have to put the Book into practice to get courage. A soldier can learn all about fighting techniques and how to take care of and use his weapon, but until he gets into the attack and the one-on-one combat with the enemy and the fire fight and the X-ambush, etc., he will never know what real courage is. You have to become involved in the conflict, Christian, and put into practice what you get from the Book by reading, quoting, and meditation.

["For then thou shalt make thy way prosperous, and then thou shalt have good success."]{.class_s2FW} In the context, it's success in taking the land and becoming prosperous from the spoils of the heathen, but you can certainly apply it spiritually to a Christian in the New Testament. The thing to remember in the New Testament is that the believer in Christ has a promise of [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} prosperity, not necessarily [physical]{.class_s2FX} or [financial]{.class_s2FX} prosperity (see our comments on 3 John 2 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the General Epistles,]{.class_s2FX} Vol. 2). Joshua 1:8 is the only place where the word ["success"]{.class_s2FW} appears in your [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible. Bob Jones Sr. defined [success]{.class_s2FX} as finding out what God wants you to do and doing it. A man can be a []{#c3T.xhtml_page_28}multi-billionaire like Bill Gates and Warren Buffet and yet be a miserable failure spiritually. In light of eternity, it is more important to find out what God's will is for your life and to fulfill that will than to be a millionaire (or a billionaire), a Hollywood star, a "teen idol," or a President.

David said that the righteous man who delights in the Book and meditates in it would ["be like a tree planted by the rivers of water, that bringeth forth his fruit in his season; his leaf also shall not wither; and whatsoever he doeth shall prosper"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 1:2--3). Notice there that the prosperity has nothing to do with wealth, fame, popularity, or political power; it has to do with [fruit-bearing.]{.class_s2FX} If you want to bear ["fruit," "more fruit,"]{.class_s2FW} and ["much fruit"]{.class_s2FW} like your Saviour commanded (John 15:1--8), then you have to get into the Book (note that ["word"]{.class_s2FW} there in John 15:3) and meditate on it and practice it. That is the only way to be ["prosperous"]{.class_s2FW} and ["have good success"]{.class_s2FW} when it comes to bearing fruit in the Christian life.

Now when it comes to [national]{.class_s2FX} prosperity and success, there is no doubt that the Lord blesses the nation that follows that Book. England was at the height of its power and influence as an empire under Queen Victoria. Do you know why? Because she did more to promote that [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible than any other five rulers on the planet at that time, including the Presidents of the United States. Queen Victoria kept a copy of the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible on a little table beside her throne; and one time when a Zulu chief from South Africa visited her and asked her what made her people so great, she pointed to [the Book.]{.class_s2FX} That [AV]{.class_s2FX} 1611 built the British Empire. Victoria wouldn't trade with a country unless it allowed Bibles to be distributed; she was responsible for the worldwide propagation of something like eight million copies a year through a reign of 63 years. That's why the Marxists and Libertines hate her so and mock the Mid-Victorian Era and Mid-Victorian morality. They hate her guts for sticking by the Book.

During her reign, it was said that "the sun never set on the British Empire." When the sun set in England, it rose in Canada; when it set in Canada, it rose in Australia; when it set in Australia, it rose in India; when it set in India, it rose in South Africa; and when it set in Johannesburg, it rose in London. [It has set now!]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c3T.xhtml_page_29} In 1904, Britain dumped the Book and started promoting the corrupt Westcott-Hort text, and when that happened, God dumped the British Empire and took away every colonial holding it had.

The enlightenment and prosperity of any country is always in direct proportion to the prominence it gives to the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible; its financial prosperity is conditioned upon its attitude towards the Book. America is arguably the wealthiest nation in the world, or at least was at one time. Why is (was) that? Somebody says, "Because of its capitalistic system." No, it's not; capitalism without morality and the Bible breeds greed and all the vices that accompany it. Somebody else says, "It's the Constitution." Nonsense, we haven't had a Constitution since 1865. Still others say, "It's our democratic principles." You're wrong.

It was the Book that gave America its wealth and freedom. The Pilgrim forefathers came over here "for the Glory of God, and advancements of the Christian faith" (Mayflower Compact). In 1777, the Continental Congress approved the importation of 20,000 copies of the [AV]{.class_s2FX} because "the use of the Bible is so universal and its importance so great." In 1782, Congress approved the printing of the [AV]{.class_s2FX} here in the United States by Robert Aitken and "recommended" it "to the inhabitants of the United States." Several of the Founding Fathers either helped found or became presidents of Bible societies that distributed the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible only in English. Even a Unitarian like John Quincy Adams and a Deist like Thomas Jefferson promoted the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible. John Quincy Adams served as chairman of the American Bible Society in 1844, and when Thomas Jefferson served as the third President of the United States, he required two books to be taught in the public schools of Washington, D.C.: the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible and Isaac Watts' hymnal. In fact, the original purpose of the public schools was to teach the Bible to the boys and girls so they would not be deceived by the Devil (Old Deluder Satan Act of 1647).

[That]{.class_s2FX} is what made this country great. The reason you are in the mess in which you are today is because since the end of World War II, this nation has been trying to dump the Book just as quick as it can dump it. As a result, God has dumped this nation just as He did []{#c3T.xhtml_page_30}Great Britain. When England honored the Book, God made it a great nation; when America honored the Book, God made it a great nation. And when they didn't honor the Book anymore, God took away their freedoms, their money, their power, and their stability. If you don't believe me, [study history.]{.class_s2FX}

["Have not I commanded thee? Be strong and of a good courage; be not afraid, neither be thou dismayed: for the LORD thy God is with thee whithersoever thou goest"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 9). When I sign a Bible for a man or a boy, that is the reference I give him. It may be Old Testament under the Law, but it is still present truth for the Body of Christ in this age.

Look it, if you are saved, then the Lord is [in you,]{.class_s2FX} right? That's right: ["Christ in you, the hope of glory"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 1:27). So ["the LORD thy God is with thee withersoever thou goest."]{.class_s2FW} Why shouldn't a Christian commit fornication? Because his ["body is the temple of the Holy Ghost which is in you"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 6:18--19). Wherever you go, you take the Lord Jesus Christ and the Holy Ghost with you, because when you got saved, Jesus Christ came to live in your body in the person of His Holy Spirit. So the command to be strong and courageous is for you, Christian (see comments above on vs. 6).

When you lose courage, you lose it all. When courage is gone, the battle is already lost.

"Courage is armor that a blind man wears; courage is [fear that has said its prayers."]{.class_s2FX} Courage is not a lack of fear; it is being afraid and going forward anyway. General George Patton said, "Courage is fear holding on a minute longer." Don't give up. Get up and go one more round. You can take encouragement from the fact that when you do, the Lord is with you, and no matter what happens, you are in His hands and in His care. ["Be not afraid, neither be thou dismayed: for the LORD thy God is with thee whithersoever thou goest."]{.class_s2FW}

10 Then Joshua commanded the officers of the people, saying,

11 Pass through the host, and command the people, saying, Prepare you victuals; for within three days ye shall []{#c3T.xhtml_page_31}pass over this Jordan, to go in to possess the land, which the LORD your God giveth you to possess it.

12 And to the Reubenites, and to the Gadites, and to half the tribe of Manasseh, spake Joshua, saying,

13 Remember the word which Moses the servant of the LORD commanded you, saying, The LORD your God hath given you rest, and hath given you this land.

14 Your wives, your little ones, and your cattle, shall remain in the land which Moses gave you on this side Jordan; but ye shall pass before your brethren armed, all the mighty men of valour, and help them;

15 Until the LORD have given your brethren rest, as he hath given you, and they also have possessed the land which the LORD your God giveth them: then ye shall return unto the land of your possession, and enjoy it, which Moses the LORD'S servant gave you on this side Jordan toward the sunrising.

Verses 10--11 give you the method of how Moses and Joshua spoke to 600,000-plus people. Moses and Joshua spoke to the elders and officers of the people, and the elders and officers passed the message on to the people in their charge (see Exod. 12:21, 19:7--8; Deut. 5:23).

["Prepare you victuals"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11). Down South, they pronounce ["victuals"]{.class_s2FW} as "vittles." Southerners are bad about slurring words and abbreviating them (like "maters" and "taters" for [tomatoes]{.class_s2FX} and [potatoes]{.class_s2FX}). How you get [vittles]{.class_s2FX} out of ["victuals,"]{.class_s2FW} I have no idea. I mean, the word is conVICtion; it's visUALS. But however you pronounce v-i-c-t-u-a-l-s, it means "prepared food." The old saying is: "An army travels on its stomach." An army has to have the field kitchen, the C-rations and the K-rations, and the MREs; or it is going to run out of steam quick (see 1 Sam. 14:24--34).

["Prepare you victuals."]{.class_s2FW} They are about to cross a river at the height of its flood stage (see 3:15). Why weren't they told to prepare [boats?]{.class_s2FX} They are about to go into battle. Why weren't they told to prepare [weapons?]{.class_s2FX} Well, the Lord is going to get them over the river His way, and when they get to the other side, He has His own battle []{#c3T.xhtml_page_32}plan. Their responsibility was to take care of what they needed to eat and let the Lord worry about everything else.

Now verses 12--15 are addressed to the tribes of Reuben, Gad, and half the tribe of Manasseh. These are the tribes back in Numbers 32 that asked Moses for their inheritance on the [east]{.class_s2FX} side of Jordan, what is known as [Transjordan]{.class_s2FX} or the nation of Jordan today. Moses bawls them out in verses 6--15 of Numbers 32, thinking they mean to demoralize the people by refusing to go to war to take the land of Canaan. Moses was afraid that they would do to the new generation of the children of Israel what the ten spies who brought back the evil report did to their fathers back in Numbers 14; this time, though, the people would wander in the wilderness until everyone was destroyed.

The three tribes insisted, though, that that was not the case. They built cities for their wives and children and folds for their cattle, but the men of "draft age" promised: ["we ourselves will go ready armed before the children of Israel, until we have brought them unto their place . . . We will not return unto our houses, until the children of Israel have inherited every man his inheritance"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 32:17--18). That being said, Moses agreed to their request, but with one stipulation: ["But if ye will not do so, behold, ye have sinned against the LORD: and be sure your sin will find you out"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 32:23).

So Joshua is reminding these three tribes of the promise they made to Moses. The first spiritual lesson for the Christian is that God looks at the promised inheritance of the believer in this life as an [accomplished fact]{.class_s2FX} (see our comments on vs. 3). The New Testament says you are to ["reckon ye also yourselves to be dead indeed unto sin, but alive unto God through Jesus Christ our Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:11). In other words, as far as God is concerned, when you got saved, your life of sin was over. Your old sin nature was crucified with Christ and buried, and you were resurrected a new man in Christ (Rom. 6:3--4).

From your standpoint, however, it is something else. You are living in the body of sinful flesh, having your new man cut away from it by ["the circumcision made without hands"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 2:11). While the new man is pulling you one way, the sinful flesh is pulling you another way. So you have to ["reckon"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c3T.xhtml_page_33} (i.e., count it as so) that old nature the way God looks at it: dead and unable to affect you. Then you are to yield the members of your body ["as instruments of righteousness unto God"]{.class_s2FW} and not let sin ["have dominion over you"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:13--14). You have to [believe]{.class_s2FX} what God said about you and act on it accordingly.

Believing what God says is the trouble we all have---before or after we are saved. When Hugh Pyle led me to Christ, I had a hard time believing that all it took to be saved was just trusting in Jesus Christ. I mean, I had been raised Episcopalian and was going through Catholic convert courses; I figured I had to [do something]{.class_s2FX} to be saved. After Bro. Pyle led me to the Lord, he showed me 1 John 5:13 and said I could know I was saved. Well, I didn't feel that I did, but I didn't want to argue with the Bible, so I said I knew even though I didn't. The next Sunday night, I walked the aisle at the Brent Baptist Church and got assurance of my salvation, but do you know what my problem was in the interim? It was [unbelief.]{.class_s2FX}

Well, after you are saved, the Lord says you are dead to sin, you don't have to serve your body of sinful flesh, your flesh doesn't have dominion over you, you can have dominion over it, and you can get the victory over sin every day of your life. So why isn't that true in the life of nearly any Christian you know? It's an evil heart of unbelief: you just can't take God at His word when He says those things.

[The next spiritual lesson for the Christian in this passage is that Christians should help each other and pray for each other: ]{.class_s2G5}["ye shall pass before your brethren armed . . . ]{.class_s2G4-1}[and help them"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 14). Paul says, ["Brethren, if a man be overtaken in a fault, ye which are spiritual, restore such an one in the spirit of meekness; considering thyself, lest thou also be tempted"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 6:1). Peter says that Christians are to have ["compassion one of another, love as brethren, be pitiful, be courteous: Not rendering evil for evil, or railing for railing: but contrariwise blessing; knowing that ye are thereunto called, that ye should inherit a blessing"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 3:8--9). In other words, if you want to ["inherit a blessing,"]{.class_s2FW} you need to [be]{.class_s2FX} a blessing to others; specifically the brethren, in the context.

["Then ye shall return unto the land of your possession, and enjoy it"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 15). The third spiritual lesson for the Christian is that there is no enjoyment until the battle is won. Paul says that ["God . . . giveth us richly all things to enjoy"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:17). I can enjoy any good thing this world has to offer because God gave it to me. The catch is I can't enjoy it all[ right now.]{.class_s2FX} It's not ["Your Best Life Now" ]{.class_s2FX}(Joel Osteen). It's the ["outward man"]{.class_s2FW} perishing now and affliction now while the ["inward man is renewed day by day"]{.class_s2FW} until you end up with Christ in Glory (2 Cor. 4:16--17). It's the cross before the crown; it's the "spinach" before the "dessert."

Over in Proverbs, the Bible says, ["Prepare thy work without, and make it fit for thyself in the field; and afterwards build thine house"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 24:27). That's talking about a farmer. He should get the land cleared, plow the fields, plant the crops and tend them, bring in a good harvest to sell at market, get some money set aside from the sale of the crops, and [then]{.class_s2FX} build a nice farm house or ranch house in which to live.

You can apply that principle to nearly every walk of life. Before an evangelist settles down in a permanent residence, he needs to make sure he has enough meetings where the offerings are sufficient to pay the mortgage and his bills. Some of the brethren, like Sam Gipp, have sold their house and live "on the road" in an RV. If a pastor is going to go out and plant a church, he has to start out in a store front or community center, and do the leg work knocking on doors and witnessing and inviting folks out to the meetings. He's not going to start out in some big building that seats 500--1,000. One of our graduates, Art Martin, started out in his basement before the Lord gave him a church building.

The problem with this modern generation is that they want everything momma and daddy have without doing the work momma and daddy did to get it. They want the new car, the big house, the colored television, the nice furniture, the washer/dryer, etc., right off the bat; and they go into debt up to their eyeballs to get it. As a consequence, a lot of marriages break up for that very reason. You had better start out small and do the work necessary to gradually get what you need.

Some people look at me and see me living in a big house, with a []{#c3T.xhtml_page_35}big yard, with a pond and big garden on it. The church is paid for; the gym is paid for; the school is paid for; the bookstore is paid for. They look at that and think that's the ministry. [That's not the ministry.]{.class_s2FX} That's not how I started out.

I started out in Bible school in a second-hand, forty-foot plywood trailer. It had [no]{.class_s2FX} bathroom, [no]{.class_s2FX} hot water, and [no ]{.class_s2FX}refrigerator. It had an "ice box": I literally had to haul blocks of ice to put in a cabinet at the bottom of the box, and that kept the food cold. I had to heat water on a kerosene stove. I used a community bathroom at the end of the trailer court. My income was thirty dollars a week. I raised a family like that for five years. [That's]{.class_s2FX} what I had to do before the house, the cars, the church, the school, the bookstore, and the gym. I had to make my work fit ["in the field"]{.class_s2FW} before I could build my ["house."]{.class_s2FW}

16 And they answered Joshua, saying, All that thou commandest us we will do, and whithersoever thou sendest us, we will go.

17 According as we hearkened unto Moses in all things, so will we hearken unto thee: only the LORD thy God be with thee, as he was with Moses.

18 Whosoever he be that doth rebel against thy commandment, and will not hearken unto thy words in all that thou commandest him, he shall be put to death: only be strong and of a good courage.

["All that thou commandest us we will do"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 16). That's quite a commitment. They told Moses something similar back before God gave the Ten Commandments: ["All that the LORD hath spoken we will do"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 19:8). Such a statement must have made Joshua's blood run cold. Look at verse 17:

["According as we hearkened unto Moses in all things, so will we hearken unto thee."]{.class_s2FW} Well, their "track record" doing what God said or hearkening to Moses ["in all things"]{.class_s2FW} wasn't that great. Joshua probably thought, "If they are going to obey me like they obeyed Moses, then I'm in for plenty of trouble."
