["Only the LORD thy God be with thee, as he was with Moses."]{.class_s2FW} Although Joshua himself was not the prophet []{#c3T.xhtml_page_36}["like unto Moses"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 34:10), he certainly was a type and the closest thing you will find to it in the Old Testament. The Lord promised to be with Joshua just as He had been with Moses (see vs. 5); He didn't say that to anyone else in the Old Testament. When it comes to being God's "prophet," Mohammed couldn't stack up to Joshua, much less the Lord Jesus Christ (Acts 3:22--26).

["Whosoever he be that doth rebel against thy commandment, and will not hearken unto thy words in all that thou commandest him, he shall be put to death"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 18). That is what happens to Achan, and we will cover that more when we get to chapter 7.

We have already covered the exhortation to ["be strong and of a good courage"]{.class_s2FW} up in verses 6 and 9, which see. Here, it is the [people]{.class_s2FX} giving Joshua the exhortation and not God. That's good, because the people are finally thinking like the Lord.

Paul said, ["Let this mind be in you, which was also in Christ Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 2:5). If you are going to think like God thinks about things, you are going to have to saturate your mind with the words of God from His Book. That is where God tells you exactly what He thinks.

[]{#c88.xhtml}

# Chapter 2 {.heading_s2B}

2:1 And Joshua the son of Nun sent out of Shittim two men to spy secretly, saying, Go view the land, even Jericho. And they went, and came into an harlot's house, named Rahab, and lodged there.

2 And it was told the king of Jericho, saying, Behold, there came men in hither to night of the children of Israel to search out the country.

3 And the king of Jericho sent unto Rahab, saying, Bring forth the men that are come to thee, which are entered into thine house: for they be come to search out all the country.

4 And the woman took the two men, and hid them, and said thus, There came men unto me, but I wist not whence they were:

5 And it came to pass about the time of shutting of the gate, when it was dark, that the men went out: whither the men went I wot not: pursue after them quickly; for ye shall overtake them.

6 But she had brought them up to the roof of the house, and hid them with the stalks of flax, which she had laid in order upon the roof.

7 And the men pursued after them the way to Jordan unto the fords: and as soon as they which pursued after them were gone out, they shut the gate.

Before crossing over Jordan, Joshua sent two men to spy out the first city the Israelites would be taking on: Jericho. Of course, God didn't command it, and it didn't really need to be done, but He allowed it.

Joshua was just starting out as leader, and he hadn't completely learned to ["walk by faith"]{.class_s2FW} and ["not by sight"]{.class_s2FW} yet (2 Cor. 5:7). When you start out as a new babe in Christ, the Lord allows a little bit of leeway on that, but He expects you to [grow up]{.class_s2FX} in the faith. A normal child should learn to walk and feed himself by the time he is []{#c88.xhtml_page_38}three years old. If you see a kid ten years old, fifteen years old, eighteen years old, who can't walk, can't feed himself, and can't dress himself, there is something wrong with that kid. If you have been saved any length of time and can't feed yourself from the Scriptures and can't ["walk in the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:16, 25) and can't ["put on the new man"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 4:24) or ["put on the armour of light"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 13:12), there is something wrong in your Christian life: your growth is stunted.

Now Joshua chooses [two ]{.class_s2FX}spies. Undoubtedly this hearkens back to the fact that there were only two spies who brought back a good report in Numbers 14: himself and Caleb. However, there is prophetic significance to this as well. You see, what you are about to read in Joshua 3--11 is a picture of the New Testament "Joshua" taking the land of Palestine at His Second Advent. Before Jesus Christ returns to this earth, He sends two witnesses down to earth to preach (Rev. 11). When Jesus chooses the twelve apostles in Matthew 10 and sends them out to preach the literal, visible, physical Kingdom of Heaven to Israel (Matt. 10:7), He sends them out by twos (Mark 6:7); [there is a reference to the Second Advent right in the passage]{.class_s2FX} (Matt. 10:23). So these two spies are a picture of the two witnesses who preach in Israel just before the Second Advent.

["And they went, and came into an harlot's house, named Rahab, and lodged there"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1). They end up in the "red-light district." Rahab is a "hooker," a prostitute. But she's not merely a run-of-the-mill "lady of the night"; she's "madam" of the "cat house"! How do you know that is so? [The King knows her by name]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 3).

Now what you have here is a picture of [salvation]{.class_s2FX} (Heb. 11:31). But it's not just salvation by faith; [works]{.class_s2FX} are involved too (James 2:25). This is salvation in the Old Testament, under the Law: it's faith [and]{.class_s2FX} works together. Rahab doesn't just [believe]{.class_s2FX} something (which she does---vss. 9--11); she has to [do]{.class_s2FX} something (which she does---vss. 18--20). Nevertheless, there is a great picture of the blood atonement of Jesus Christ here in the account.

Verses 4--5 are used by the modern "values clarification" crowd to teach "situation ethics"; that is, your ethics---the morals you []{#c88.xhtml_page_39}practice---change with the situation. What may be right in one situation may not be right in another, so there are no absolute morals or absolute standards.

What happens here is that Rahab [lies]{.class_s2FX} about the spies and sends the King's men on a "wild goose chase." As an indirect result of that, the Lord spares her when the city is destroyed (James 2:25). If you want to see the same kind of thing again, look at Exodus 1:15--20 where the Hebrew midwives don't tell the whole truth to Pharaoh about sparing the Hebrew baby boys. The Bible says of the midwives, ["Therefore God dealt well with the midwives"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 1:20). Why? For concealing part of the truth[ ]{.class_s2FX}(cf. Gen. 20:12)[.]{.class_s2FX}

Don't you see what is going on? The libertines are using [the exception to overthrow the rule.]{.class_s2FX} The rule is: ["Thou shalt not bear false witness"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 20:16). But you take two isolated instances and use them to nullify the law against lying in any instance you choose.

Now what is going on here? Why does God overlook lying in this instance? First, one should note that these are the [only]{.class_s2FX} two examples of such a thing in the entire Bible. In both instances, it is to protect someone from losing his life, and not just anyone, but [innocent Jews.]{.class_s2FX} So you have two other Scriptures come into play here: ["Thou shalt not kill"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 20:13), and ["I will bless them that bless thee, and curse him that curseth thee"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 12:3). The Lord is not going to overlook a lie to cover up your sin or its consequences (see 1 Sam. 15; 2 Sam. 11--12).

In Exodus 1 and Joshua 2, the government is telling someone to violate what God said. You are to obey the government right up to that point (Rom. 13:1--5 cf. Acts 5:29). So there are reasons why God did what He did in Exodus 1 and Joshua 2, and they have nothing to do with "values clarification" or "situation ethics" or "the end justifies the means."

Before you try to follow the example of the midwives and Rahab, you had better [know your Bible]{.class_s2FX} and [pray about it.]{.class_s2FX} If you are in a circumstance like Richard Wurmbrand found himself, that's one thing. Richard Wurmbrand was a preacher in Romania who was imprisoned by the Communists. After some particularly excruciating persecution by the guards, Wurmbrand used to be []{#c88.xhtml_page_40}alone in his cell and preach at the Lord on "God's Unjust Laws." He would say things like, "God, you say, ['Thou shalt not bear false witness.']{.class_s2FW} You know we can't keep that law. If we didn't lie, the Communists would get our wives, our children, and our fellow Christians and throw them in prison and torture them like they're torturing me. We have to lie to protect them." If that is your case, then you probably have the right to follow Exodus 1 and Joshua 2, but if not, you had better leave it alone.

["Whither the men went I wot not"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5). That was the lie Rahab told. She knew exactly where they were. ["Wot"]{.class_s2FW} is an archaic English word meaning "to know." The word was not that hard to figure out in the context, and if it were, there is no need to make 36,000 ([NASV]{.class_s2FX}) to 64,000 ([NIV]{.class_s2FX}) changes in the [AV]{.class_s2FX} text to get rid of one archaic word. All you have to do is put a note in the margin giving the definition. When we put out the [Ruckman Reference Bible,]{.class_s2FX} that's exactly what we did; we didn't touch one word in the text.

Rahab knew where the two men were. Verse 4 says she ["took the two men, and hid them,"]{.class_s2FW} and verse 6 tells you where: ["she had brought them up to the roof of the house, and hid them with the stalks of flax, which she had laid in order upon the roof."]{.class_s2FW} (For a similar situation, see 2 Sam. 17:18--21.)

In Bible times, the roofs on houses were flat, which is why the Jews were required by the Law to put a ["battlement"]{.class_s2FW} on the roof so that no one would fall off (Deut. 22:8). Flax is a plant that was used by the ancients for its fibers to make linen and rope. The stalks were placed on the roof to be dried by the sun so the fibers could be taken out and used. So the two men were on Rahab's roof, hidden underneath the flax stalks. In verse 15, you read that Rahab's ["house was upon the town wall,"]{.class_s2FW} with a window facing outward. So Rahab's house was probably on top of the wall of Jericho (see our remarks under 6:20). The wall with the window in it was part of the outward wall of the city.

["And the men pursued after them the way to Jordan unto the fords: and as soon as they which pursued after them were gone out, they shut the gate"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 7). The men of Jericho are following up on Rahab's lie in verse 5. ["The fords,"]{.class_s2FW} here, are not a reference to a car lot. A ford is a shallow place in a []{#c88.xhtml_page_41}river or stream which can be crossed on foot without one having to swim. Once the pursuers leave the city, the gates are shut and locked so that the Israeli spies could not leave the city that way just in case they were still there.

8 And before they were laid down, she came up unto them upon the roof;

9 And she said unto the men, I know that the LORD hath given you the land, and that your terror is fallen upon us, and that all the inhabitants of the land faint because of you.

10 For we have heard how the LORD dried up the water of the Red sea for you, when ye came out of Egypt; and what ye did unto the two kings of the Amorites, that were on the other side Jordan, Sihon and Og, whom ye utterly destroyed.

11 And as soon as we had heard these things, our hearts did melt, neither did there remain any more courage in any man, because of you: for the LORD your God, he is God in heaven above, and in earth beneath.

12 Now therefore, I pray you, swear unto me by the LORD, since I have shewed you kindness, that ye will also shew kindness unto my father's house, and give me a true token:

13 And that ye will save alive my father, and my mother, and my brethren, and my sisters, and all that they have, and deliver our lives from death.

["And before they were laid down, she came up unto them upon the roof?"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 8). The ["laid down"]{.class_s2FW} refers to lying down to go to sleep. The Hyper-Calvinist A. W. Pink implies that the Jewish spies went in to Rahab to "conduct business," as it were. Of course, that is just nonsense. If the spies knew they were being followed by agents of the King, they would have taken shelter wherever they could ("any old port in a storm"), possibly reasoning that no one would suspect a couple of Law-observing Jews of hiding out with a whore.

Now Pink wrote some good stuff. He has a good book on the inspiration of the Scriptures; his [Exposition of John]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c88.xhtml_page_42} is good; his "Gleanings" books on Genesis, Exodus, Elijah, and David are all good. But then he wrote a book called ["The Sovereignty of God"]{.class_s2FX} where he went to seed on five-point Calvinism. After that, he got completely off base, and as a result, his later works are inferior in their material; that includes his [Gleanings in Joshua.]{.class_s2FX} Pink said the spies were wrong for going in to Rahab and Rahab was wrong for lying to save the spies. Pink got so theological and self-righteous that he forgot to be practical, but that is par for the course for most Calvinists. Pink says Rahab should have waited on God to save them some other way. He professed to have such faith in the sovereignty of God that he said one should never lie even if someone were going to kill your family and friends. I wonder if Bro. Pink ever had the chance to test his faith in the matter.

It's one thing to sit in an air-conditioned office and make divine fiats and quite another to watch as a Moslem cuts off your daughter's arm on one side because she won't deny Christ and then cuts off her leg on the other side because she still won't deny Christ. Do you honestly think you wouldn't lie to protect your daughter, your wife, or your son from a barbarian like that? Then maybe you had better shut your mouth before you judge a brother or sister in Christ who has to live through such horrors.

Now how do you know that the men aren't lying down for the purpose of fornicating with a whore? Look at verse 9: ["I know that the LORD hath given you the land."]{.class_s2FW} Verse 10: ["For we have heard how the LORD dried up the water of the Red sea for you."]{.class_s2FW} Verse 11:[ "for the LORD your God, he is God in heaven above, and in earth beneath."]{.class_s2FW} Verse 12: ["Now therefore, I pray you, swear unto me by the LORD."]{.class_s2FW}

Rahab is a [convert.]{.class_s2FX} She has rejected her false gods and is calling ["on the name of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} just like those heathen do at the Second Advent (Joel 2:32), and she is delivered both [physically]{.class_s2FX} and [spiritually]{.class_s2FX} (cf. Rom. 10:13) just as they are. She has obviously repented of her sinful profession, for when she is delivered, she [gets married to an Israelite]{.class_s2FX} (Matt. 1:5).

["I know that the LORD hath given you the land, and that your terror is fallen upon us, and that all the inhabitants of the land faint because of you. For we have heard . . ."]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c88.xhtml_page_43} (vss. 9--10). The people of Canaan were scared stiff of the Israelites because they had heard what God did to Pharaoh and his army at the Red Sea and how the Israelites had defeated Sihon the King of the Amorites on the east side of Jordan and Og the King of Bashan who was a thirteen-foot giant (Deut. 3:11). It's like Paul told Agrippa: ["this thing was not done in a corner."]{.class_s2FW} I bet you before the children of Israel left Sinai, the news of what God did in Egypt---the ten plagues and the crossing of the Red Sea---had spread from Gibraltar to Persia.

["And as soon as we had heard these things, our hearts did melt, neither did there remain any more courage in any man, because of you"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11). The Canaanites are totally demoralized. The Jews have them "spooked." The first thing that "deflated their balloon" was what God did at the Red Sea. Those Canaanites had the fire scared out of them forty years earlier when the twelve spies came through, for it hadn't been three years since God had drowned out the greatest army of that time (Exod. 16:1 cf. Num. 1:1, 9:1). If the children of Israel had only believed ["the gospel"]{.class_s2FW} (see Heb. 3:15--4:2 and comments in that Commentary), they could have gone in and taken the land forty years earlier.

["For the LORD your God, he is God in heaven above, and in earth beneath"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11). There's the faith of Hebrews 11:31; the works of James 2:25 take place down in verses 21--22. The works manifested her faith.

Notice in verse 13 that Rahab not only asks for her salvation when the armies of Israel come in to destroy Jericho, she also asks for the salvation of her father, mother, brothers, and sisters---[household salvation.]{.class_s2FX} Paul tells the Philippian jailor, ["Believe on the Lord Jesus Christ, and thou shalt be saved, and thy house"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 16:31). That's not saying the faith of the Philippian jailor would automatically save all his family; it's saying that if anyone in the household of the Philippian jailor believed on Jesus Christ like he did, that person would be saved just as the jailor was. That's what ends up happening here.

When the spies promise to save Rahab's family, it is conditioned on them being in Rahab's house when the Jews take the city. Rahab's family members had to believe that the God of Israel was the true []{#c88.xhtml_page_44}God who was going to allow His people to destroy the Canaanites, just as she believed. Acting on that belief, they would come to her house and stay there until they were brought out to Joshua (6:22--23). So for "household salvation" to take place, there has to be the individual faith of each family member, and in the case of the Old Testament, works had to accompany the faith of each individual.

14 And the men answered her, Our life for yours, if ye utter not this our business. And it shall be, when the LORD hath given us the land, that we will deal kindly and truly with thee.

15 Then she let them down by a cord through the window: for her house was upon the town wall, and she dwelt upon the wall.

16 And she said unto them, Get you to the mountain, lest the pursuers meet you; and hide yourselves there three days, until the pursuers be returned: and afterward may ye go your way.

17 And the men said unto her, We will be blameless of this thine oath which thou hast made us swear.

18 Behold, when we come into the land, thou shalt bind this line of scarlet thread in the window which thou didst let us down by: and thou shalt bring thy father, and thy mother, and thy brethren, and all thy father's household, home unto thee.

19 And it shall be, that whosoever shall go out of the doors of thy house into the street, his blood shall be upon his head, and we will be guiltless: and whosoever shall be with thee in the house, his blood shall be on our head, if any hand be upon him.

20 And if thou utter this our business, then we will be quit of thine oath which thou hast made us to swear.

21 And she said, According unto your words, so be it. And she sent them away, and they departed: and she bound the scarlet line in the window.

22 And they went, and came unto the mountain, and abode there three days, until the pursuers were returned: []{#c88.xhtml_page_45}and the pursuers sought them throughout all the way, but found them not.

The spies agree to Rahab's request but on three conditions: 1. She had to keep her mouth shut about the spies (vss. 14, 20), 2. the rope by which she let them out her window and down the wall had to be hanging out the window in plain sight when the Jews crossed over Jordan into the land (vs. 18), and 3. her family had to be in her house to be spared (vs. 19).

Note that last condition. In order for Rahab's family to be saved, they had to go down to the seedy part of town, the red-light district, and stay in the whorehouse with the "black sheep" of the family. They had to be ["numbered with the transgressors"]{.class_s2FW} (Mark 15:28) and ostracized from respectable society to be saved. And if you ever get saved, that will be your case as well. You will have to take your place with the murderers, thieves, seditionists, extortioners, and prostitutes; because those are the ones Christ came to save (see our comments on Luke 5:32 in that Commentary). The corrupt modern translations remove Mark 15:28 from the text so you won't have to associate yourself with such riff raff since you are such a fine, outstanding citizen (read Rom. 3:10--23).

["Then she let them down by a cord through the window"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 15). This ["cord"]{.class_s2FW} becomes essential to Rahab's salvation (see the second condition above). It is also called a ["line of scarlet thread"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 18 and a ["scarlet line"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 21. What you have is a [line]{.class_s2FX} made up of [cords,]{.class_s2FX} and each cord is made up of smaller [threads,]{.class_s2FX} with the threads of one of the cords being [scarlet]{.class_s2FX} in color. So you have a line probably an inch or more in thickness, with a ["scarlet thread"]{.class_s2FW} twisted down and around the line from top to bottom. That scarlet thread was hung out of the window of a hooker, so to this day, the area of town frequented by "street walkers" is called a "red-light district."

What you have in the scarlet thread is obviously a picture of salvation. So you will hear preachers and Bible teachers talk about "the scarlet thread of redemption" that runs through the Bible: they are talking about the types of Christ redeeming sinners in the Old Testament (e.g., God making coats of skin for Adam and Eve, Abel, []{#c88.xhtml_page_46}Noah's ark, Abraham sacrificing Isaac, the Passover lamb, etc.) leading to Christ's death for sinners on the cross and the preaching of the Gospel in the New Testament.

The scarlet thread here in the passage is a picture of the blood of Christ, exactly as the blood on the doorposts was in Exodus 12. In fact, look at verse 19 and notice that the same stipulation was put on Rahab and her family as was put on the Jews at the first Passover. They were not supposed to leave the house with the blood on it, and if they did, they were "fair game" for the "death angel" (Exod. 12:22--23).

The scarlet thread hung out of the window of the worst woman in town, protecting her and her family. Jesus told the Pharisees and scribes, ["the publicans and harlots go into the kingdom of God before you"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 21:31). That's because a bad woman like Rahab [knew]{.class_s2FX} she was a sinner in need of redemption. Highly religious people don't think they need to repent and trust a bloody sacrifice for their sins. They think they're good enough to make it on their own; as a consequence, they miss out on salvation.

The modern "plan of salvation" you hear preached these days leaves the sinner respectable when it finds him, it leaves him respectable when it finishes with him, and it will land him flat on his back in [Hell,]{.class_s2FX} I might add. There is no such thing as a "respectable salvation" anywhere in the word of God. Your Saviour died like a thief and murderer. He suffered capital punishment as a criminal ["without the camp"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 13:12--13). He was naked; He was shamed; He was whipped; He was spat on. There's nothing respectable about that. If you are going to get saved, you are going to have to "come down off your high horse" and associate yourself with all that. That is what your average middle-class and upper-class American is unwilling to do.

Now first of all, this rope Rahab lets down is called a ["cord."]{.class_s2FW} A cord binds one thing to another. The blood of Christ binds the sinner to his Saviour. Over in 1 Samuel 25:29, Abigail said to David, ["the soul of my lord shall be bound in the bundle of life with the LORD thy God."]{.class_s2FW} The old song goes: "Standing on the promises of Christ my Lord, Bound to Him eternally by love's strong cord." That thing is so strong that the picture in the New Testament is a wife []{#c88.xhtml_page_47}being bound to her husband (see Rom. 7:2; 1 Cor. 7:27, 39). If you are saved, you are part of the Bride of Christ, and you are bound so close to the Bridegroom that you are part of His flesh and bones (Eph. 5:22--32). You can't get much closer than that.

God told Israel over in Hosea 11:4, ["I drew them with cords of a man, with bands of love: and I was to them as they that take off the yoke on their jaws, and I laid meat unto them."]{.class_s2FW} Being bound to Christ and His righteousness is a liberating thing (["take off the yoke on their jaws"]{.class_s2FW}); it is a life-giving thing (["laid meat unto them"]{.class_s2FW}).

Jesus said, ["Come unto me, all ye that labour and are heavy laden, and I will give you rest. Take my yoke upon you, and learn of me; for I am meek and lowly in heart: and ye shall find rest unto your souls, For my yoke is easy, and my burden is light"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 11:28--29).

Second, the rope is called a ["thread."]{.class_s2FW} A thread is connected with mending things. Salvation mends the sinner; it fixes him. Moreover, a thread is a tiny, insignificant thing. The world doesn't think much of Jesus Christ and His death on the cross for their sins.

Isaiah said, ["He is despised and rejected of men . . . he was despised, and we esteemed him not"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 53:3). Paul said, ["For the preaching of the cross is to them that perish foolishness"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 1:18).

So when God wants to picture salvation through the blood of His Son, He picks a small, insignificant thing like a scarlet thread. The Bible says, ["For who hath despised the day of small things?"]{.class_s2FW} (Zech. 4:10). How do you get to Heaven? [You have to trust a dead Jew nailed to a post.]{.class_s2FX} What could be more insignificant or less effectual than that? It's crazy. [But that's the method God chose.]{.class_s2FX}

You say, "There has to be more to it than that." Nope, that's it. That's how the Lord makes fools out of men who won't believe what He says. The natural man can't get it. How could a dead Jew nailed to a pole get you to Heaven? That's what the Bible calls ["the foolishness of God"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 1:25). It says, ["God hath chosen the foolish things of the world to confound the wise"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 1:27). But if you are going to get ["wisdom, and righteousness, and sanctification, and redemption"]{.class_s2FW} from God, you are going []{#c88.xhtml_page_48}to have to come through that dead Jew on the cross (1 Cor. 1:30).

Finally, that rope is called a ["line."]{.class_s2FW} A line is put up to hold something. A clothesline holds the clothes pinned to it. A powerline holds the electricity traveling through it. A lifeline will hold [you]{.class_s2FX} if you grab onto it. Salvation is a line that holds you and keeps you from going to a Lake of Fire.

Not only that, but a line connects one thing to another. A telephone line and a telegraph line connect one party to another. Salvation connects you to God. You can get on the line any time and call Heaven for help when you need it (Heb. 4:16).

Back to Joshua 2, verse 20: ["And if thou utter this our business, then we will be quit of thine oath which thou hast made us to swear."]{.class_s2FW} Notice another definition of [quit]{.class_s2FX} here. Over in 1 Samuel 4:9 and 1 Corinthians 16:13, it means to act or conduct yourself in a certain way. ["Quit you like men"]{.class_s2FW}: [act]{.class_s2FX} like a man; [conduct yourself]{.class_s2FX} like a man. Here, [quit]{.class_s2FX} means "released from an obligation or charge." In other words, if Rahab "turned stoolie" and informed on the spies so they could be caught before crossing back over Jordan, then "all bets were off" as far as being saved when the city would be taken.

["And they went, and came unto the mountain, and abode there three days, until the pursuers were returned"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 22). The spies take Rahab's advice in verse 16. ["The mountain,"]{.class_s2FW} according to the commentators and expositors, is a peak of a mountainous area north of Jericho that is riddled with caves. The spies hid there for three days until the search parties gave up and returned to Jericho. Since Joshua told the people back in 1:11 that in ["three days ye shall pass over this Jordan,"]{.class_s2FW} and this is repeated in 3:2, what you are reading here in Joshua 2 is an interlude in the narrative that goes back and describes what took place before 1:11.

23 So the two men returned, and descended from the mountain, and passed over, and came to Joshua the son of Nun, and told him all things that befell them:

24 And they said unto Joshua, Truly the LORD hath delivered into our hands all the land; for even all the []{#c88.xhtml_page_49}inhabitants of the country do faint because of us.

["So the two men returned . . . and came to Joshua the son of Nun, and told him all things that befell them"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 23). The two spies report back to Joshua and are "debriefed." A good spiritual lesson from the New Testament is that witnesses for Christ should testify to one another to encourage one another with what God has done through and for them. When Peter and John were threatened by the Sanhedrin in Acts 4, they reported back to the other believers (Acts 4:23); that resulted in prayer and the filling of the Holy Ghost (Acts 4:24--31). Paul and Barnabas reported back to the church at Antioch ["all that God had done with them, and how he had opened the door of faith unto the Gentiles"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 14:27). When Paul reported to James and the elders of the church at Jerusalem of ["what things God had wrought among the Gentiles by his ministry,"]{.class_s2FW} the brethren ["glorified the Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 21:19--20). So Christian witnesses should testify to one another and encourage and exhort one another by their testimonies.

Verse 24:[ "Truly the LORD hath delivered into our hands all the land; for even all the inhabitants of the country do faint because of us."]{.class_s2FW} They report to Joshua the "intel" they had gotten from Rahab in verses 9--11. Prophetically, verse 24 will be true at the Second Advent (see Rev. 6:15--17). Spiritually and devotionally for the Christian, this speaks of the believer's complete victory in Christ (see remarks under 1:2).

[]{#cAM.xhtml}

# Chapter 3 {.heading_s2B}

3:1 And Joshua rose early in the morning; and they removed from Shittim, and came to Jordan, he and all the children of Israel, and lodged there before they passed over.

2 And it came to pass after three days, that the officers went through the host;

3 And they commanded the people, saying, When ye see the ark of the covenant of the LORD your God, and the priests the Levites bearing it, then ye shall remove from your place, and go after it.

4 Yet there shall be a space between you and it, about two thousand cubits by measure: come not near unto it, that ye may know the way by which ye must go: for ye have not passed this way heretofore.

Joshua 3:1 takes place immediately after the charge of 1:10--18. ["Shittim"]{.class_s2FW} was a city on the plains of Moab (Num. 22:1 cf. Num. 25:1), about ten miles northeast of the Dead Sea and about eight miles from the Jordan River. It was the last encampment of the Israelites before crossing Jordan in this chapter. It is where Israel fornicated with the Moabites as part of their worship service (Num. 25:1--3) on the advice of Balaam to Balak after Balaam couldn't curse the children of Israel (Mic. 6:5). Joshua sent out the two spies from Shittim (2:1). During the Millennium, a river of life (a prelude to THE River of Life that flows from the throne of God in New Jerusalem---Rev. 22:1) that comes out of the temple (Ezek. 47) flows through ["the valley of Shittim"]{.class_s2FW} (Joel 3:18) on its way to bring life to the Dead Sea (for further study, see our comments on Zech. 14:8 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class_s2FX} Vol. II).

["They removed from Shittim, and came to Jordan, he and all the children of Israel, and lodged there before they passed over"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1). The spiritual lesson for Christian warfare is that there should be a time of rest and preparation before the battle. Before the Christian faces the challenges of the day, he should spend []{#cAM.xhtml_page_51}time preparing with prayer and the Scriptures.

For ["three days"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2, 1:11), Israel rests by Jordan. That gives them a chance to prepare their food as Joshua commanded them back in 1:11, and I am sure they also got their weapons and other equipment in order. But it also gave them time to access the difficulties. You see, at that time of year, the Jordan was swollen from the melting snows from Mt. Hermon and overflowed its banks (vs. 15). The water was rushing through there like a rapids. Those Jews must have looked at that thing and wondered how in the world they were going to cross it.

Before you get into battle, the Lord is going to let you see the difficulties involved. He'll test your faith to see if you are faint of heart. At the camp where I trained when I entered the Army, the engineers had cleared out a swamp. Then the rains came; it rained every day for something like three weeks. When it got through, the whole campground was under sixteen inches of water. The Army Corp of Engineers volunteered to come and fix the place, but some rich private contractor came in there and built the place back up for free. But that's what you'll run into in combat. Out there in the South Pacific, the monsoon rains will come through there in sheets, and a soldier has to be prepared to operate in that mess.

Those Jews are looking at those flood waters and wondering what they are going to do, but they are obeying Joshua at this point just as they promised. God is about to honor their faith and obedience and do something for them.

Verse 3: ["When ye see the ark of the covenant of the LORD your God, and the priests the Levites bearing it, then ye shall remove from your place, and go after it."]{.class_s2FW} Ever since the children of Israel left Egypt, the Lord had been leading them by a pillar of cloud by day and a pillar of fire by night (Exod. 13:21). They've been looking [up]{.class_s2FX} for their leadership. Now they are looking [ahead]{.class_s2FX} to men carrying the Ark of the Covenant; their guide is on the [ground.]{.class_s2FX}

The typology is when you get saved, you look up in faith to Heaven and receive the Son of God who came down from Heaven and went back to Heaven. But as you progress in your Christian life, you realize the "Ark," in your case, is [your body]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 6:19). Jesus []{#cAM.xhtml_page_52}Christ lives in you through the Holy Ghost (Col. 1:27). The Holy Spirit guides you through the truth of His [word]{.class_s2FX} (John 16:13, 17:17). So you realize your leadership is on the ground. That's the problem with the Charismatics and the neo-Liberals (emergents): they are not willing to follow the Lord's leadership through His word; they are always seeking some new revelation not found in the Book God placed in their laps.

Now, the people were to keep a space of 2,000 cubits between them and the Ark (vs. 4). That's a distance of about 3,000 feet, a little over half a mile. In that way, they had a clear view of which way the Ark was going. The Ark was leading them, and the God of the Ark was leading the priests carrying it. The reason this was necessary was because they had ["not passed this way heretofore"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 4). They were traversing new territory and having to follow God by faith.

That's why it's a wonderful thing to see a brand new Christian. Everything is new and fresh to him. He doesn't know anything about church politics or the brethren or even how to "act spiritual" yet. Just like a little child, he is open and without guile. All he knows is he is saved and loves the Lord.

["There shall be a space between you and it, about two thousand cubits."]{.class_s2FW} Now, I am not going to be dogmatic about this application, but you take that number 2,000: that's the amount of time (2,000 years) between Christ's First Coming and His Second (see our comments on 2 Pet. 3:8 in that Commentary). The Israelites are about to cross Jordan just as they had crossed the Red Sea forty years earlier. Do you know what the Red Sea typifies? It is a type of a body of water separating the first and second heavens that was [dyed red]{.class_s2FX} by the blood of Christ after His resurrection. That water is frozen at the top, but has a door through which you'll pass when you go up at the Rapture (Rev. 4:1).

So the crossing of the Red Sea is a type of the Rapture of the Church (among other things), and that's about to be repeated here in Joshua 3. What those 2,000 cubits between the Ark and the people look like is the 2,000 years between when your Lord ascended up through the "Red Sea" upstairs, and the time when you pass through it at the Rapture. Like I said, I am not dogmatic on that []{#cAM.xhtml_page_53}interpretation, but that's what it looks like to me. For further study on the matter, I refer you to our remarks on Hebrews 9:11--14 in that Commentary.

When it comes to a practical application for the New Testament child of God, the problem with most Christians is that they either follow the Lord too far off like Peter did (see comments on Matt. 26:58; Luke 22:54 in those Commentaries) or they rush too far ahead. The average Christian lags way behind the column so that when the Lord speaks to him about something, he is so far away that he can't hear Him. The reason some Christians don't feel called to be a preacher or missionary is because [they aren't within calling distance.]{.class_s2FX}

Then some Christians plan their lives without regard for the Lord's leadership. If they turned around and looked, they would be surprised (or scared) to find that the Lord had turned off some other way while they were going their own. The command of the Lord Jesus is: ["Follow me"]{.class_s2FW} (see Luke 5:27 and comments on that Commentary). That means He is the lead scout; He is the "point man." You are not to drag behind or run ahead.

If you are following the Lord in a life of faith like you should, then you are going to find that He leads you in a way you've never known before. Your safety and security will depend on obeying orders and following the Lord without getting ahead of Him.

I see it all the time with the young men who come here to school. Whether they have been saved a while or are still "wet behind the ears," most of them aren't expecting what they get into when they come here. They get down here and have to take a job that is half or a third of what they were making back home. They have to live in a trailer, and some of them have had to live on peanut butter and crackers. Then there are the cockroaches and mosquitoes; that's always a shock to some Yankees. There's little time for family or leisure activities because they're working, going to school, and studying. The Lord puts so much on them and so much with which to occupy their minds that they don't realize what's going on; but the whole time they're going through all that stuff, the word of God is working its way down in them, and they are growing in grace. They hadn't passed that way before, but they followed the Lord's []{#cAM.xhtml_page_54}leadership, and He got them through.

Then they leave here to go into the ministry. For three years, they've been in a place where they got good Bible teaching and preaching, and where they heard a lively congregation singing and shouting and praising God. Then they get back out in the world, and things can be rough. It's not the same as before they came down to Bible school; things are different now. They are entering the ministry. They haven't passed that way before. They have to keep on following the Lord by faith.

5 And Joshua said unto the people, Sanctify yourselves: for to morrow the LORD will do wonders among you.

6 And Joshua spake unto the priests, saying, Take up the ark of the covenant, and pass over before the people. And they took up the ark of the covenant, and went before the people.

7 And the LORD said unto Joshua, This day will I begin to magnify thee in the sight of all Israel, that they may know that, as I was with Moses, so I will be with thee.

8 And thou shalt command the priests that bear the ark of the covenant, saying, When ye are come to the brink of the water of Jordan, ye shall stand still in Jordan.

["Sanctify yourselves"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5). That's [separation.]{.class_s2FX} That's setting yourself apart to serve God, so it involves cleaning up. Paul said, ["present your bodies a living sacrifice, holy, acceptable unto God"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 12:1). Jesus said, ["Sanctify them through thy truth: thy word is truth"]{.class_s2FW} (John 17:17). Jacob told his family, ["Put away the strange gods that are among you, and be clean"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 35:2).

The ["wonders"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 5 are miraculous signs (Exod. 4:17, 21), and of course, the signs were given to the Jews (1 Cor. 1:22). God's about to give those Jews a miraculous sign to show them beyond a shadow of a doubt that He is with Joshua as He was with Moses (vs. 7).

["And Joshua spake unto the priests"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). That's important. You see, that's someone who was not a Levite ordering []{#cAM.xhtml_page_55}those priests around. Moses, of course, was a Levite; his brother Aaron was the first high priest. Moses was from the priestly tribe. Joshua, though, was from the tribe of Ephraim (Num. 13:8). Here is Joshua as another type of Christ. The New Testament "Joshua" wasn't from the tribe of Levi either; He was from Judah (Heb. 7:13--14). But Jesus Christ had a superior priesthood to the Levitical priesthood (Heb. 7:15--17). So here is Joshua, a type of the Lord Jesus Christ, in a superior position over the Aaronic high priest and the Levitical priests, even though he wasn't a Levite.

Now Joshua was to ["command the priests"]{.class_s2FW} to ["come to the brink of the water of Jordan"]{.class_s2FW} and ["stand still in Jordan"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 8). This was in preparation for the Lord parting the waters (vss. 15--17). But what you have here is a picture of both the First and Second Advents of the Lord Jesus Christ.

Joshua crossed Jordan at the fords where the spies crossed (cf. 2:7). This was called ["Bethbarah"]{.class_s2FW} in the Old Testament (Judg. 7:24) and ["Bethabara"]{.class_s2FW} in the New Testament (John 1:28). It means "house of the ford." It is where Christ was baptized (John 1:26--28, 3:26). What is about to happen here is a type of [baptism]{.class_s2FX} (cf. 1 Cor. 10:1--2).

Second, what you are about to read is a type of the Second Advent. Joshua is about to destroy a cursed city (6:26), just as Jesus Christ will at His return (Mystery Babylon---Rev. 18).

Do you know what Solomon said about his wife, ["the daughter of Pharaoh,"]{.class_s2FW} after the Temple was built and the Ark of the Covenant was placed in it? ["My wife shall not dwell in the house of David king of Israel, because THE PLACES ARE HOLY, WHEREUNTO THE ARK OF THE LORD HATH COME"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Chron. 8:11).

That Ark was built at Mt. Sinai and traveled up through Edom on the "King's Highway" to Moab where it crossed the Jordan at Bethabara into Canaan. Wherever that Ark went, slaughter followed. Three thousand died at Sinai. Through forty years of wandering in the wilderness, the generation which refused to enter Canaan in Numbers 14 were dropping like flies right and left. When the Ark arrived at Shittim (see comments on vs. 1), Moabites died, Midianites died, Israelites died, and Amorites died (Num. 21--31). []{#cAM.xhtml_page_56}And of course, when the Ark came into Canaan, the inhabitants of 31 City-States died (12:24). The Philistines captured the Ark in 1 Samuel 4, and several thousand of them died (1 Sam. 5). When the Ark returned to Israel, ["the men of Bethshemesh" ]{.class_s2FW}looked in it, and over 50,000 of them died (1 Sam. 6:19). And when David tried to bring the Ark to Jerusalem the first time, Uzzah tried to "help God out" and steady the Ark on the cart. He got 50,000 volts for his trouble and dropped dead (2 Sam. 6:6--7).

That Ark was holy, and wherever it went became holy. God proved it by killing anyone who violated His holiness. So when Jesus Christ returns, He follows the same path the Ark took (see Hab. 3 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class_s2FX} Vol. II) and slaughters everyone in His path. Why? Because He's the holy God coming back to take over the rulership of the earth (Zech. 14). When that time comes, you will either bow or be burned, beaten, and slashed to pieces. That's the "loving God" of the Liberals and "emergents."

Smile! Have a nice day! Remember, God loves you and has a wonderful plan for your life!

9 And Joshua said unto the children of Israel, Come hither, and hear the words of the LORD your God.

10 And Joshua said, Hereby ye shall know that the living God is among you, and that he will without fail drive out from before you the Canaanites, and the Hittites, and the Hivites, and the Perizzites, and the Girgashites, and the Amorites, and the Jebusites.

11 Behold, the ark of the covenant of the Lord of all the earth passeth over before you into Jordan.

12 Now therefore take you twelve men out of the tribes of Israel, out of every tribe a man.

13 And it shall come to pass, as soon as the soles of the feet of the priests that bear the ark of the LORD, the Lord of all the earth, shall rest in the waters of Jordan, that the waters of Jordan shall be cut off from the waters that come down from above; and they shall stand upon an heap.

Verse 9 should be the invitation of every God-called preacher to his congregation: ["Come hither, and hear the words of the LORD your God."]{.class_s2FW} These days, all the average parishioner in America gets is self-help, Socialism, warmed-over psychology, watered-down moralizing, and "positive thinking." Paul told his son in the faith, ["Preach the WORD"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 4:2); not "Christian" psychiatry, civil rights, public opinion, or peace and prosperity. The reason this country is in the mess in which it is today is because the preachers failed to give their congregations ["the W-O-R-D-S of the LORD."]{.class_s2FW} They have traded ["the WORDS"]{.class_s2FW} that are ["spirit"]{.class_s2FW} and ["life"]{.class_s2FW} (John 6:63) for messages, principles, fundamentals, versions, translations, manuscripts, texts, and opinions of scholars that are all deader than a hammer on the beach last week.

The list of nations given in verse 10 which the Israelites were to destroy ranges anywhere from ten in Genesis 15:19--21 to five in Exodus 13:5, but the list here is the ["seven nations"]{.class_s2FW} given in Deuteronomy 7:1. All seven nations were from [Ham]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 10:15--20).

Then there is a peculiar expression in verse 11: ["the ark of the covenant of the Lord OF ALL THE EARTH."]{.class_s2FW} The expression in the Pentateuch is ["the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob."]{.class_s2FX} The closest you come to ["the Lord of all the earth"]{.class_s2FW} is in Genesis 18:25 where Abraham calls God ["the Judge of all the earth."]{.class_s2FW} Both expressions---["the Lord of all the earth"]{.class_s2FW} and ["the Judge of all the earth"]{.class_s2FW}---are connected with the Second Advent. In the Old Testament, He's the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob---the Jews. In the New Testament, He's the Lord of the Church---the born-again children of God. But when Christ returns, He judges ["all nations"]{.class_s2FW} in Matthew 25:31--46, and the Bible says, ["the LORD shall be King over all the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (Zech. 14:9).

We will discuss the purpose for twelve men being picked from each of the twelve tribes more in chapter 4 (which see). In verse 13, Joshua finally reveals to the people what the Lord is going to do: God is going to cause the waters of Jordan to stop so the children of Israel can go over on dry ground just as they crossed the Red Sea (vs. 17 cf. Exod. 14:22). In fact, this is going to be a miracle that trumps the Red Sea crossing. The apostate scholars have all kinds of []{#cAM.xhtml_page_58}explanations for the displacement of the water in the Red Sea, everything from a shallow "sea of reeds" to a tsunami sucking out the water when an island exploded in the Aegean Sea. But what do you do with a fast flowing river at flood season? The text here says the waters stood ["upon an heap."]{.class_s2FW} The waters kept piling up in the air until the whole host had finished passing over (vs. 16). Let's see you explain that away with "marshy ground" or a tidal wave.

14 And it came to pass, when the people removed from their tents, to pass over Jordan, and the priests bearing the ark of the covenant before the people;

15 And as they that bare the ark were come unto Jordan, and the feet of the priests that bare the ark were dipped in the brim of the water, (for Jordan overfloweth all his banks all the time of harvest,)

16 That the waters which came down from above stood and rose up upon an heap very far from the city Adam, that is beside Zaretan: and those that came down toward the sea of the plain, even the salt sea, failed, and were cut off: and the people passed over right against Jericho.

17 And the priests that bare the ark of the covenant of the LORD stood firm on dry ground in the midst of Jordan, and all the Israelites passed over on dry ground, until all the people were passed clean over Jordan.

Much of the text is simply the narrative of what happened as Joshua predicted in verse 13, and needs no explanation. Notice again the fantastic nature of the miracle in verse 16: ["the waters which came down from above]{.class_s2FW} \[i.e., the waters upstream\][ STOOD AND ROSE UP UPON AN HEAP very far from the city Adam, that is beside Zaretan."]{.class_s2FW} ["Adam"]{.class_s2FW} was a city at the mouth of the Jabbok River which flows into the Jordan; it was twenty miles north of Jericho.

The [International Standard Bible Encyclopedia]{.class_s2FX} ([ISBE]{.class_s2FX}) says some Moslem raghead ("An Arabian historian") said a landslide blocked the river. Aw, your father's moustache! That's quite a landslide you got there, son. It occurs so that the waters dry up at the exact []{#cAM.xhtml_page_59}moment those priests' feet hit the edge of that water, and the "dam" doesn't burst until the priests are back on dry land again (4:18). That landslide held long enough for over 600,000 armed troops (Num. 26:2, 51) to march across. Quite a "coinkidinky," wouldn't you say?

That's the kind of mess into which you get when you won't believe what God said. It's like Pharaoh and all his army drowning in some marshy ground they could have easily skirted. You have to have more faith to believe the explanation of an infidel than to believe the Scriptures. "Landslide" my foot!

This is a genuine miracle that violates five scientific laws. It is the Creator overriding the laws of nature He set up. It violates the law of [inertia:]{.class_s2FX} a body in motion continues in motion. A landslide that could stop a river that moves as fast and with as much volume as the Jordan River would have to be some landslide.

It violated the law of gravity. Water seeks its lowest level. That water rose up [in the air]{.class_s2FX} and piled up in a heap. It didn't come down until the last priest stepped out of that river bed.

It defied the law of expansion. When that stupid Moslem tried to explain away the Bible with a landslide, he forgot that the water would not only rise, it would expand out as well, flooding the land on both banks of the river. That didn't happen here. The water rose [up;]{.class_s2FX} it didn't flow [out]{.class_s2FX} and [around.]{.class_s2FX}

It defied the law of contraction. If you wanted to get the water to stop flowing, you would have had to freeze it until it contracted. That was impossible. This was [Spring,]{.class_s2FX} around the time of the Passover in March and April (5:10--11). The snows on Mt. Hermon were [melting,]{.class_s2FX} causing the river to flood. Do you realize how cold it would have to be to freeze a rushing torrent like that?

It defied the law of evaporation. If the river didn't freeze, then the water would have to evaporate almost instantaneously to cause the river to stop. The amount of heat (generated naturally) it would take to evaporate the waters of the Jordan that quickly so that 600,000 troops could march over on dry ground would flash burn the surrounding countryside for miles---including the area where Israel was. It would be as bad as a nuclear bomb going off.

Now what practical lessons can we draw from the chapter for the Christian life? Well, as I have said before, the crossing of Jordan is a []{#cAM.xhtml_page_60}type of baptism (cf. 1 Cor. 10:1--2), and part of the picture of baptism is [death]{.class_s2FX} (Rom. 6:3--4)---death to self. That work of death in the Christian cannot be accomplished by [active service.]{.class_s2FX} When those priests went down into that river bed, they [stood still;]{.class_s2FX} they didn't do any work to get the water to part. Of course, they went down to the water by an act of [will,]{.class_s2FX} but once down there, there was nothing they did that dried up that river. That was a miracle of God.

Calvinists teach that "Total Depravity" means [total inability]{.class_s2FX} to receive Jesus Christ by an act of free will. That's [baloney.]{.class_s2FX} Your will is not dead; it is alive to choose one way or the other. When the Lord says you are not born again by ["the will of the flesh, nor of the will of man"]{.class_s2FW} (John 1:13), He's not saying you can't choose to receive Jesus Christ of your own free will, because He had just gotten through saying that you could (John 1:12). But once you choose to receive Christ, then the work is completely of God; you can't will on your own for the New Birth to take place.

When the Holy Spirit accomplishes the New Birth in you, He is the one who accomplishes the death of self in you, both positionally and practically. Doing more work for the Lord doesn't make you more spiritual; in fact, sometimes it can be a mark of [carnality:]{.class_s2FX} a desire for attention and accolades from other Christians. Natural abilities and strengths are the [flesh.]{.class_s2FX} God gives talents to [unsaved men.]{.class_s2FX} The exercise of those natural talents is no proof of spirituality.

I'll give you a good test of your spirituality. If you can thank God for taking away your [blessings,]{.class_s2FX} that's a good mark of spirituality. Blessings please the flesh. If you can thank God for taking away things the flesh likes, that's spirituality.

Paul said, ["I have learned, in whatsoever state I am, therewith to be content. I know both how to be abased, and I know how to abound: every where and in all things I am instructed both to be full and to be hungry, both to abound and to suffer need"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 4:11--12). When you can say something like that and [mean it, ]{.class_s2FX}you're spiritual.

Also, there is no way to die to self without an accompanying resurrection. Baptism is death, burial, [and resurrection:]{.class_s2FX} you are raised to ["walk in newness of life"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:4). For that death, burial, and resurrection to be efficacious in your life, you have to [know]{.class_s2FX} something (Rom. 6:6, 9) and [reckon]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cAM.xhtml_page_61} it to be so (Rom. 6:11). The only way you gain that knowledge is to get into the [word.]{.class_s2FX} You have to know what [God said]{.class_s2FX} about the work He has accomplished in you and how to act on that work.

Jesus said, ["If any man will come after me, let him DENY HIMSELF, and take up his CROSS DAILY, and follow me"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 9:23). A cross is an instrument of death, so Paul said, ["I am crucified with Christ: nevertheless I live; yet not I, but Christ liveth in me" (]{.class_s2FW}Gal. 2:20). There's the death and resurrection of Romans 6:3--4. But you have to reckon that death to be so on a regular basis. That's why Paul said, ["I die daily"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 15:31). You have to ["mortify therefore your members which are upon the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 3:5); you have to ["yield yourselves unto God, as those that are alive from the dead, and your members as instruments of righteousness unto God"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:13).

You have to know all of that, and to know that, you have to read your Bible. God gave His words to Joshua, and Joshua gave God's words to the priests and the people. Jesus Christ has given you His words in a Book: the [King James Authorized Version.]{.class_s2FX} Now get in that Book and find out what it means to die to self and live to God.

[]{#cCU.xhtml}

# Chapter 4 {.heading_s2B}

4:1 And it came to pass, when all the people were clean passed over Jordan, that the LORD spake unto Joshua, saying,

2 Take you twelve men out of the people, out of every tribe a man,

3 And command ye them, saying, Take you hence out of the midst of Jordan, out of the place where the priests' feet stood firm, twelve stones, and ye shall carry them over with you, and leave them in the lodging place, where ye shall lodge this night.

4 Then Joshua called the twelve men, whom he had prepared of the children of Israel, out of every tribe a man:

5 And Joshua said unto them, Pass over before the ark of the LORD your God into the midst of Jordan, and take ye up every man of you a stone upon his shoulder, according unto the number of the tribes of the children of Israel:

6 That this may be a sign among you, that when your children ask their fathers in time to come, saying, What mean ye by these stones?

7 Then ye shall answer them, That the waters of Jordan were cut off before the ark of the covenant of the LORD; when it passed over Jordan, the waters of Jordan were cut off: and these stones shall be for a memorial unto the children of Israel for ever.

8 And the children of Israel did so as Joshua commanded, and took up twelve stones out of the midst of Jordan, as the LORD spake unto Joshua, according to the number of the tribes of the children of Israel, and carried them over with them unto the place where they lodged, and laid them down there.

9 And Joshua set up twelve stones in the midst of Jordan, in the place where the feet of the priests which bare the ark of the covenant stood: and they are there unto this day.

Notice the Southern expression in verse 1: []{#cCU.xhtml_page_63}["clean passed over."]{.class_s2FW} Southerners retained a lot of those Biblical expressions, much more so than Yankees. They say things like, ["I reckon"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:18) and ["you all"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 2:5) and ["shut to the door"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 19:10). The reason that is, is because after the Civil War, the Yankees went back to their industry and money. The South, though, was left devastated; all it had left were God and the Bible. As a result, the Southerners picked up and retained a lot of Biblical expressions in their speech. Of course, that has changed in the last thirty years or so as Southerners have dumped the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible for materialism.

Now what takes place in verses 2--3 is an action that represents everyone in all twelve tribes. As those priests stood there in that dry river bed, Joshua picked twelve men, one out of each tribe, and sent them down there where the priests with the Ark were. Each man was to get a stone about the size of a bowling ball or so, and bring it up on the other side of the river where they would camp that night. Then in verse 9, Joshua himself toted twelve stones from the land and put them on the river bed where the priests were. So there was one pile of twelve stones on the land that came from the river and another pile of twelve stones in the river that came from the land.

What did all that mean? Well, those stones were for a ["sign"]{.class_s2FW} (see 1 Cor. 1:22 and comments in that Commentary) and a ["memorial"]{.class_s2FW} to future generations of Jews as to the miracle God performed by cutting off the waters of Jordan so that the Israelites could cross over on dry ground. Again, this is a great picture of the death, burial, and resurrection of Christ as is pictured in baptism.

Death is pictured by a [stone.]{.class_s2FX} We say about death, "he is [stone cold dead]{.class_s2FX} on the market"; "he is still [as a stone."]{.class_s2FX} A grave is marked most often by [a stone.]{.class_s2FX} When God drowned Pharaoh and all his troops at the Red Sea, Moses said, ["they sank into the bottom AS A STONE"]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2FX}(Exod. 15:5), and ["by the greatness of thine arm they shall be as still AS A STONE"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 15:16). In that last reference, it also says, ["till thy people pass over, O LORD, till the people pass over, which thou hast purchased."]{.class_s2FW} That's what happened in Joshua 3--4 at the crossing of the Jordan. So a stone represents [death.]{.class_s2FX}

Look at Revelation 18:21. []{#cCU.xhtml_page_64}["And a mighty angel took up a STONE like a great millstone, and CAST IT INTO THE SEA, saying, Thus with violence shall that great city Babylon be thrown down, and shall be found no more at all."]{.class_s2FW}

So going into that water is a picture of death and burial. Joshua hauls twelve stones out of that river bed and stacks them up in the Promised Land, and that's a picture of [resurrection.]{.class_s2FX} ["Buried with him by baptism into death . . . raised . . . ]{.class_s2FW}\[to\][ walk in newness of life"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:4): that's what happens to you at salvation.

Of course, there is no interval between the deliverance and victory that were secured for the Christian at his Saviour's death as there was between the Red Sea and the Jordan. But the Holy Spirit records these events in the Old Testament so you up here in the New Testament can understand the sequence of how the Lord works in your life. Those Israelites got [saved]{.class_s2FX} at the Passover, they got [immersed]{.class_s2FX} at the Red Sea and died to the Devil's hold over them, they went through the wilderness journey and had to [die to self,]{.class_s2FX} and then they crossed over Jordan into Canaan and [got the victory.]{.class_s2FX}

But if you want to see something interesting, look at Psalm 114:3.

["The sea saw it, and fled ]{.class_s2FW}\[that's the Red Sea; see Psa. 114:1\][: Jordan was driven back."]{.class_s2FW}

There the Red Sea crossing and the Jordan River crossing are given right together with no interval of forty years in between. That typifies the Christian experience at salvation. Your salvation wasn't a [process,]{.class_s2FX} like those Old Testament saints; it was [instantaneous.]{.class_s2FX} When you got saved, you didn't just get your sins forgiven and get out of Hell, you got:

1. Born again: you were given a new, live spirit.

2. Placed in Christ: you were joined to the Lord in one spirit.

3. Spiritually circumcised: your soul got cut loose from the body of sinful flesh so it could not be affected by it.

4. Sealed by the Holy Spirit: you are guaranteed to get to Heaven no matter what.

All of that is afforded to the Christian at salvation, but it takes [growth]{.class_s2FX} and [faith]{.class_s2FX} to take advantage of it. Where a Christian doesn't claim his victory in the finished work of Christ, the process takes []{#cCU.xhtml_page_65}time. Nevertheless, when a sinner places his trust in the blood of the Lamb of God, everything is secured for him. When Jesus died and rose again, your death was [fixed,]{.class_s2FX} your burial was [fixed,]{.class_s2FX} your resurrection was [fixed,]{.class_s2FX} your new life was [fixed,]{.class_s2FX} and your victory was [fixed.]{.class_s2FX} It is all secure in Christ.

Now, Joshua places twelve stones at the bottom of the Jordan, and those twelve men bring up twelve stones and plant them on the shore: death, burial, and resurrection. Do you know what your Saviour is called? He's called ["the stone which the builders disallowed"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:7). God the Father sent that Stone down from Heaven to be the ["chief corner stone"]{.class_s2FW} there in Jerusalem (1 Pet. 2:6), but those chief priests and scribes rejected Him and stirred up the people against Him and had Him put to death. But God chose that Stone and raised Him up from the dead, so the Bible calls Him ["a living stone"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:4). He's not a dead stone anymore.

Jesus says, ["God is able OF THESE STONES to raise up children unto Abraham"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 3:8). So do you know what that ["living stone"]{.class_s2FW} does? He brings ["many sons unto glory"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 2:10) and makes them the spiritual seed of Abraham by faith (Gal. 3:7). And just as their Saviour is ["a living stone,"]{.class_s2FW} those to whom He gives ["power to become the sons of God"]{.class_s2FW} (John 1:12) are ["lively stones"]{.class_s2FW} in Him (1 Pet. 2:5).

So we are dead in Christ's death, and we live in Christ's resurrection: ["if we be dead with Christ, we believe that we shall also live with him"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:8). The ["old man is crucified with him, that the body of sin might be destroyed, that henceforth we should not serve sin"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:6). You are ["a new creature" "in Christ"]{.class_s2FW}; ["old things are passed away; behold all things are become new"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:17).

The problem is that the flesh keeps rising up. It's like Dracula and zombies in the movies: it's a [dead thing]{.class_s2FX} that keeps coming back to life to destroy the living (your new man). That flesh keeps telling you, "I'm alive." You say, "No, you're not; you're [dead."]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}"No, I'm not," it says. "I'm alive. See me move? I'm hungry; I'm thirsty." That's the flesh; it wants its lusts to be satisfied.

You say, "You're dead. The Bible says you're dead. Now SHUT UP!" That's reckoning yourself dead to sin (Rom. 6:11). That's dying daily (1 Cor. 15:31). That's mortifying []{#cCU.xhtml_page_66}["your members which are upon the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 3:5). To make the victory in Christ that was secured at His death, burial, and resurrection efficacious for you, [that's]{.class_s2FX} what you have to do.

Back to Joshua 4: ["and leave them in the lodging place, where ye shall lodge this night"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3). Notice that God didn't tell them where they were going to lodge that night. That's walking [by faith.]{.class_s2FX}

One time a fellow came to Jesus and said, ["Lord, I will follow thee whithersoever thou goest"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 9:57). Jesus told him, ["Foxes have holes, and birds of the air have nests; but the Son of man hath not where to lay his head"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 9:58): "If you follow me, you may not know where you're going to sleep tonight; you still want to come?" And the guy bowed out and went and found something else to do.

When Bob Jones Sr. was alive, he would get up there before a new student body each year and try to scare them off. He'd say something like this: "The Lord started His school with twelve disciples. Somebody asked Him, 'What are its requirements? Is it accredited? What's the curriculum? What are its standards?' Jesus said, 'The requirement is a [cross;]{.class_s2FX} get yourself a cross and follow me.' 'Is your school accredited, Jesus?' 'Nope.' 'Are you in good standing with denominational headquarters?' 'Nope.' 'Will you guarantee me a job when I graduate?' 'I guarantee you will get [murdered.]{.class_s2FX} I guarantee you will be stripped naked and nailed to a cross: I guarantee [that.]{.class_s2FX} You still want to come along?'"

If a president or chancellor of a Christian school went around trying to get students like that, he wouldn't have many students these days, would he? That has nothing to do with the pretty girls or the pink faces or the swimming pool or the marble halls or the fountains or the bowling alley, etc. "You're going to get crucified." Do you think you're going to get a big enrollment with that approach?

Brethren, do you see the discrepancy there is between modern Christianity and that Book? Those Jews didn't know where they were going to spend the night. They had to trust God to show them. If you are going to live by faith, it is going to cost you something. It may []{#cCU.xhtml_page_67}cost you financial security or the support of your family. I know; I've been through the hard times (see our remarks under 1:15). I am here to tell you that if I can make it, you can make it. I am here to tell you that God can get you through the family troubles, the money troubles, the health troubles, and the brethren troubles. How do I know that? [He got me through.]{.class_s2FX}

10 For the priests which bare the ark stood in the midst of Jordan, until every thing was finished that the LORD commanded Joshua to speak unto the people, according to all that Moses commanded Joshua: and the people hasted and passed over.

11 And it came to pass, when all the people were clean passed over, that the ark of the LORD passed over, and the priests, in the presence of the people.

12 And the children of Reuben, and the children of Gad, and half the tribe of Manasseh, passed over armed before the children of Israel, as Moses spake unto them:

13 About forty thousand prepared for war passed over before the LORD unto battle, to the plains of Jericho.

14 On that day the LORD magnified Joshua in the sight of all Israel; and they feared him, as they feared Moses, all the days of his life.

The Ark was the first thing into the Jordan (3:11), and it was the last thing out (vss. 10--11). The spiritual lesson for the New Testament believer is that Jesus Christ is ["the author and finisher of our faith"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 12:2). He tells John there in the book of Revelation, ["I am Alpha and Omega, the first and the last"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 1:11).

That Ark stays there in that river bed until all the people are out. The picture is of the Ark perishing while the people escape death. That's what Christ did on the cross. When Jesus hung on Calvary's cross, those chief priests and scribes mocked Him and said, ["He saved others; himself he cannot save"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 27:41--42; Mark 15:31). Now that was said in mockery and ridicule, but it was absolutely true. If He were going to save others, then He couldn't []{#cCU.xhtml_page_68}save Himself. The only way for Him to save you and me was to lose His life first.

A young lady was headed to the mission field one time, and she was brought before her mission board for examination. Well, one of her professors in Bible school wrote a note to the board saying, "You ought to examine her ideas on the atonement before you approve her for missionary service." Well, the board figured she was a heretic or held some unscriptural view of the atonement, but when they asked her about her view on the doctrine, they were taken aback by her answer. Her view on the atonement of Christ was that [if Christ died for us, we should die for Him.]{.class_s2FX} That was her "odd" view of the atonement.

If you are going to get people saved (i.e., win sinners to Christ), then [you can't save yourself.]{.class_s2FX} Jesus said, ["For whosoever will save his life shall lose it: but whosoever will lose his life for my sake, the same shall save it"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 9:24). There is no way you can get engaged in the ministry of seeing souls saved and save yourself; it won't work.

Verse 10 says, ["the people HASTED and passed over."]{.class_s2FW} When a person gets saved, there should be no long interval between the spiritual reality of being dead with Christ and alive to God, and implementing the practical realities of the new life in Christ. The problem these days is that most new converts are not taught in these matters and know nothing about them.

Still other people get saved and die to the outward world and die to self, but never do anything for the Lord thereafter. They will stop smoking, drinking, doing drugs; they'll quit cussing and chewing and dancing and everything else. But they don't witness; they don't win souls; they aren't avid students of the word of God; they aren't interested in getting the Gospel out overseas. [They do nothing.]{.class_s2FX} They just sit around on their old dead cans and brag about what they don't do. Well, they're dead and buried with Christ, but they have not risen to ["walk in newness of life"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:4).

Verse 12 is the Transjordanian tribes fulfilling their words to Joshua in 1:12--16, which see. Verse  13 tells you they were 40,000 in number. The total Israeli army numbered over 600,000 (Num. 26:2, 51).

["On that day the LORD magnified Joshua in the sight of all Israel; and they feared him, as they feared Moses, all the days of his life"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 14). This is the Lord fulfilling the promise He gave to Joshua in 1:5 and 3:7. It sets Joshua up as a type of the Prophet like unto Moses that was to come (Deut. 17:18; Acts 3:22--26).

15 And the LORD spake unto Joshua, saying,

16 Command the priests that bear the ark of the testimony, that they come up out of Jordan.

17 Joshua therefore commanded the priests, saying, Come ye up out of Jordan.

18 And it came to pass, when the priests that bare the ark of the covenant of the LORD were come up out of the midst of Jordan, and the soles of the priests' feet were lifted up unto the dry land, that the waters of Jordan returned unto their place, and flowed over all his banks, as they did before.

This is the end of the miracle (see our remarks under 3:16). The waters return to the course in which they had been flowing the moment the priests step out of that river bed. If this had been a landslide bursting to release the waters it had dammed up, then that river would have come rushing through there like a freight train and gone far beyond where it normally overflowed. Those priests carrying the Ark and the rear end of the column would have been washed away. "Landslide" your hind leg. That Mohammedan didn't know about what he was talking, but then again, neither did his "prophet."

Notice that Jordan is personified in verse 18: ["HIS banks."]{.class_s2FW} In the Bible, you will find impersonal, inanimate objects referred to in the masculine or feminine. That's called an "anthropomorphism": assigning human characteristics to non-human things. For example, the Golden Candlestick in the Tabernacle is referred to in the masculine: ["HIS shaft, and HIS branches, HIS bowls, HIS knops, and HIS flowers"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 25:31).

By the same token, there are times in the Bible where a masculine is referred to in the neuter. Take, for example, Philippians 4:13---[]{#cCU.xhtml_page_70}["I can do all things through Christ WHICH strengtheneth me."]{.class_s2FW} All the apostates will complain that the word ["which"]{.class_s2FW} should be ["who"]{.class_s2FX} because it refers to ["Christ"]{.class_s2FW}---a [person,]{.class_s2FX} not a [thing.]{.class_s2FX} Having made that change, they then kick Jesus Christ completely out of the verse and say, ["I can do all things through HIM who strengthens me."]{.class_s2FX} You talk about a bunch of lousy hypocrites! They forgot that when Jesus was in the womb of His mother Mary, the Holy Spirit called Him a ["holy THING"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 1:35). That goes for Greek or English. Corrupt, apostate translations like [Good News for Modern Man]{.class_s2FX} and the [CEV]{.class_s2FX} will stick a word in there that's not in any Greek text (["child"]{.class_s2FX}), and perverted translations like the [ESV]{.class_s2FX} drop the word ["thing"]{.class_s2FW} altogether. Anything to cover up the truth.

All the Fundamentalists and Conservatives who are continually running to the Greek to change your Bible will complain about the [AV]{.class_s2FX} calling the Holy Spirit ["itself"]{.class_s2FW} in Romans 8:16 without telling you the word for ["Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} is [neuter]{.class_s2FX} in Greek. Where were the Greek grammarians then?

Brethren, the issue isn't "the Greek" or "the Greek text"; it's [that Book]{.class_s2FX} ([AV ]{.class_s2FX}1611). You know that's so, because when the [King James]{.class_s2FX} matches the tense, the voice, the gender, the article, etc., of Greek grammar, [the apostates will change the text.]{.class_s2FX} You had better  stick with that Book instead of the vacillating, fluctuating opinions of Hebrew and Greek scholars.

19 And the people came up out of Jordan on the tenth day of the first month, and encamped in Gilgal, in the east border of Jericho.

20 And those twelve stones, which they took out of Jordan, did Joshua pitch in Gilgal.

21 And he spake unto the children of Israel, saying, When your children shall ask their fathers in time to come, saying, What mean these stones?

22 Then ye shall let your children know, saying, Israel came over this Jordan on dry land.

23 For the LORD your God dried up the waters of Jordan from before you, until ye were passed over, as the LORD []{#cCU.xhtml_page_71}your God did to the Red sea, which he dried up from before us, until we were gone over:

24 That all the people of the earth might know the hand of the LORD, that it is mighty: that ye might fear the LORD your God for ever.

Now this is the Passover season (5:10). ["The tenth day of the first month"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 19) was when the Passover lamb was selected (Exod. 12:3). It is no coincidence that the selection of the Passover lamb is connected with the "resurrection" of verses 11--18. The Lamb of God who was sacrificed for sinners (John 1:29) and rose again to give them eternal life (John 14:19) is said to be ["our passover"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 5:7).

If that were not enough, the "resurrected sinner," who was baptized into Christ's death, burial, and resurrection, is [spiritually circumcised]{.class_s2FX} (Col. 2:11--13), exactly as is about to take place [physically]{.class_s2FX} with the children of Israel in the next chapter (5:3--9).

Now think about that for a moment. There are three authors---Joshua, John, and Paul---writing 1,500 years apart, with no collusion between themselves, and all three [match doctrinally]{.class_s2FX} in these matters. Mohammed could not make the 114 Suras of the [Koran]{.class_s2FX} or the "sayings" of [his own life]{.class_s2FX} in the [Hadith]{.class_s2FX} match with him being in "collusion" with [himself.]{.class_s2FX} Mohammed's "revelation" changed depending on what kind of [lust]{.class_s2FX} he was trying to satisfy (wealth, power, or sex). Alongside the Holy Scriptures, the ["Holy" Koran]{.class_s2FX} and the ["Holy" Hadith]{.class_s2FX} are poor jokes that aren't even funny.

The ["Gilgal"]{.class_s2FW} of verses 19--20 is the first encampment on the west side of Jordan in the Promised Land. The word means "rolled away" because that is where God ["rolled away the reproach of Egypt"]{.class_s2FW} off the children of Israel by having all the men who came out of Egypt circumcised (5:8--9), and we will discuss that more in the next chapter. The little children in Sunday school sing, "Rolled away, rolled away, rolled away! Every burden of my heart rolled away!" In John Bunyan's [Pilgrim's Progress,]{.class_s2FX} when Christian knelt at Calvary, the burden of sin he had borne since the City of Destruction came off and rolled down the hill into an open grave at the bottom.
