That's a good illustration of the typology of Gilgal.

["Gilgal"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cCU.xhtml_page_72} first appears in Deuteronomy 11:30, indicating that Joshua added the location to the book (see our remarks on the authorship of the book of Joshua in the Introduction). It is where the Jewish men were circumcised and where Israel celebrated its first Passover in the Promised Land (5:1--10). It was Joshua's base camp for his military campaigns (9:6, 10:6--7, 15, 43, 14:6). It is where Saul was made King (1 Sam. 11:15), and out of where Saul operated when he went to battle (1 Sam. 13:4, 7--8, 12, 15, 15:12, 21, 33). It is where Elisha cured the pot of poisoned pottage (2 Kings 4:38--41). It was one of the prominent places where the northern kingdom of Israel sacrificed to false gods (Hos. 4:15, 9:15, 12:11; Amos 4:4, 5:5).

As far as the typology here in chapters 4 and 5 for the Christian, Gilgal represents:

1. The believer's first entry into the new life (vs. 19, 5:9--10).

2. His preparation for combat (5:15).

3. The death of the flesh (1 Sam. 15:33).

4. The source of apostasy (Amos 4:4).

5. Warnings from the Lord (Judg. 2:1).

6. The place where you will meet the King (2 Sam. 19:15).

7. The encampment for training and renewal (10:15, 43).

Verse 21: ["What mean these stones?"]{.class_s2FW} Stones hold a prominent place in the book of Joshua. They show up in 4:9, 20, 7:26, 8:29, 10:18, 27, 24:26.

["What mean these stones?"]{.class_s2FW} That's a good sermon to preach at a funeral. Those cemeteries have headstones there at each grave commemorating a person's life, but they are markers of [death.]{.class_s2FX}

Joshua said those stones were for ["a sign"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6) and ["for a memorial"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 7), so a lot of those graveyards are called ["memorial]{.class_s2FX} gardens." The graves face [east,]{.class_s2FX} because when Jesus returns, He returns like the sun coming up in the morning (see our comments on Mal. 4:2 in that Commentary), and the sun rises in the [east.]{.class_s2FX} Somebody is expecting a [resurrection.]{.class_s2FX}

Those headstones have words on them like a [sign.]{.class_s2FX} (You aren't going to get away from that [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible. It will dictate what to do, and you will do it, whether you are aware of it or not.) If you want an interesting study, look at the messages left on tombstones. Dr. M. R. DeHaan, the old-time radio evangelist and Bible teacher, []{#cCU.xhtml_page_73}had two words put on his tombstone: "Perhaps today!" That old boy preached on the Second Coming all his life, and he wanted all who read his tombstone to know that death didn't stop him waiting for Jesus Christ to come back.

["What mean these stones?"]{.class_s2FW} Well, they stood as a reminder of how Israel crossed the Jordan just as they crossed the Red Sea (vs. 23). If you want to learn the Bible, there are two important words you need to get: [like]{.class_s2FX} and [as.]{.class_s2FX} Those two words give [similarities]{.class_s2FX} between two things God wants you to compare. He said in Hosea 12:20, ["I have multiplied visions, and USED SIMILITUDES, by the ministry of the prophets."]{.class_s2FW} So when God wants to teach you something in the Scriptures, He will tell you what it's [like]{.class_s2FX} or [as.]{.class_s2FX} The Jordan crossing was [as]{.class_s2FX} the Red Sea crossing (vs. 23). The Red Sea crossing was [like]{.class_s2FX} baptism (Rom. 10:2). Baptism is [like]{.class_s2FX} death, burial, and resurrection (Rom. 6:4). So those stones sitting there at Gilgal represent a [resurrection.]{.class_s2FX}

["What mean these stones?"]{.class_s2FW} Well, there are [twelve]{.class_s2FX} of them, one for each tribe of Israel, and they are there [together]{.class_s2FX} in a pile. So those stones represent the [unity of Israel,]{.class_s2FX} redeemed and ransomed as a [unit,]{.class_s2FX} as [one nation.]{.class_s2FX} The high priest had twelve precious stones set in his breastplate, with the names of the children of Israel engraved under the stone which represented its particular tribe (Exod. 28:17--21). Elijah on Mt. Carmel set up an altar made up of twelve stones representing the twelve tribes of Israel (1 Kings 18:31--32). The foundation of the New Jerusalem is made up of twelve precious stones (Rev. 21:19--20), with each foundation stone bearing one of the names of the twelve apostles (Rev. 21:4). Each apostle rules over one of the twelve tribes in the Millennium (Matt. 19:28). So these twelve stones in Joshua 4 ["mean"]{.class_s2FW} the nation of Israel redeemed in its unity.

Now I am not going to be dogmatic about what I am going to say next, but if I were a betting man, I would place money on it. Gilgal is on the west side of the Jordan across from where Jesus was baptized (see our remarks under 3:8). Of course I don't know for sure that the twelve stones Joshua set up at Gilgal were still there when John was baptizing 1,450 years later, but I just bet you that when John said ["God is able of these stones to raise up children unto Abraham,"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cCU.xhtml_page_74} that he was referring to the stones Joshua set up. He was either doing it [literally]{.class_s2FX} (the stones were still there and visible to anyone) or [figuratively]{.class_s2FX} (reminding his hearers of the account in Joshua).

Notice in verses 21--23 that the stones were to remind the Israelites' children of what God did at the crossing of Jordan just as the Passover service was to remind them of the exodus from Egypt (Exod. 12:26--27). The language of the question posed by the children is almost identical: ["What mean ye by this service?"]{.class_s2FW} It is no coincidence, then, that the Jordan River crossing takes place at the Passover season (see remarks under vs. 19).

["What mean these stones?"]{.class_s2FW} Well, they were put there to [scare]{.class_s2FX} them: ["That ye might FEAR the LORD your God for ever"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 24).

That Bible says, ["The fear of the LORD is the beginning of wisdom"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 110:10; Prov. 9:10), and ["The fear of the LORD is the beginning of knowledge"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 1:7). Job 28:28 says, ["the fear of the Lord, that IS wisdom."]{.class_s2FW} A man is a [fool]{.class_s2FX} not to fear God (Prov. 1:7).

You live in a day and age when not even the [Christians]{.class_s2FX} fear God. They like to quote 1 John 4:18 like they had good sense (["perfect love casteth out fear: because fear hath torment"]{.class_s2FW}). Shut your mouth, stupid; you don't know what in the world you're talking about! The ["fear"]{.class_s2FW} in 1 John 4:18 has nothing to do with fearing God at all. It's talking about a Christian fearing he'll go to Hell (1 John 4:17). No born-again child of God need fear going to Hell because nothing can separate him ["from the love of God, which is in Christ Jesus our Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:39 cf. 1 John 4:16, 19).

Somebody says, "Well, the fear of God is 'holy reverence' for God." Baloney! [Reverence and fear are two separate things.]{.class_s2FX} Don't believe me? Look up Hebrews 12:28 and READ IT!

Somebody else says, "Well, fearing God is an Old Testament thing. That's what you have to do to a vengeful, wrathful God under the Law. That's not a loving God of grace." You had better read your Bible again, son. Paul told you to perfect ["holiness in the fear of God"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 7:1); he told you to submit ["yourselves one to another in the fear of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 5:21). Peter commanded you to ["Fear God"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:17), and the last ["gospel"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cCU.xhtml_page_75} preached on this earth is: ["Fear God, and give glory to him"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 14:6--7).

Fearing God is being so terrified and scared (2 Cor. 5:11; Heb. 12:21) of a Being who can make a furnace hotter than the sun (and put you in it---Psa. 9:17) that you watch your step and avoid violating His holiness and righteousness as much as possible (Job 28:28; Prov. 8:13, 14:27, 16:6). The problem with the wicked is that they don't fear God (Psa. 36:1; Rom. 3:18), and when the Christians have stopped fearing God, no wonder this nation is in the mess it is in today. The more you fear God, the more trouble you stay out of[.]{.class_s2GA}

[]{#cFT.xhtml}

# Chapter 5 {.heading_s2B}

5:1 And it came to pass, when all the kings of the Amorites, which were on the side of Jordan westward, and all the kings of the Canaanites, which were by the sea, heard that the LORD had dried up the waters of Jordan from before the children of Israel, until we were passed over, that their heart melted, neither was there spirit in them any more, because of the children of Israel.

Verse 1 is the follow-up to the last verse in chapter 4. Notice the use of the first person plural (["until WE were passed over"]{.class_s2FW}), indicating the verse was recorded by someone who was right there and went through the experience. Unlike the [Koran,]{.class_s2FX} the Bible is the [eyewitness testimony]{.class_s2FX} of men's encounters with God (see Luke 1:2 and comments on the verse in that Commentary).

When God dried up the Jordan River for the Israelites to cross over, it was to accomplish two things according to 4:24---to show the heathen the mighty hand of God and to cause the children of Israel to fear the Lord. Well here in verse 1, the Kings of the Amorites and Canaanites are so scared by what happened that they are completely disheartened and demoralized.

Now that shows you that there are two kinds of fear when it comes to God. One is the fear of a criminal trying to avoid being caught by the police, and the other is a fear of a child towards his daddy. If you had a good daddy, you know what I mean. If momma ever told you "Just wait till your father gets home," you got scared because you knew you were going to get a licking for doing something wrong. At the same time, you knew your daddy loved you. You loved your daddy and feared him at the same time. The reason you tried to behave yourself was not always out of love for momma and daddy; a lot of times you didn't do what you wanted to do because you were afraid of the belt or paddle.

That's the kind of fear God wants you to have toward Him. He wants you to be scared enough of Him to put a check on your devilment (Job 28:28; Prov. 3:7). That's not the fear the Canaanites []{#cFT.xhtml_page_77}and Amorites had. They were like a criminal scared of being caught by the police. Yeah, he's afraid of being caught and punished, but there is nothing in that fear that causes him to be a law-abiding citizen. He's still going to try to get away with breaking the law, and he may even go to extremes like fleeing, assault, and murder to avoid being caught. The Canaanites and Amorites were scared, but they weren't going to lay down their arms and surrender. They went ahead and fought anyway, despite what God showed them at the Jordan River.

Some people are just too tough for their own good. I preach to men in prison like that all the time. You would think that after a man loses his job, his family, and his freedom, he would be ready to get right, but not a lot of them. They are so tough that nobody's going to get them to do anything. They are going to prove how tough they are until it winds them up in Hell.

I'm not that tough. People think I must be really tough because of the way I talk and write, but in some things, I'm a wimp, boy. Somebody said to me once, "Ruckman, the only reason you got saved is because you didn't want to go to Hell." Amen! That's right! I got saved because I didn't want to [burn forever.]{.class_s2FX}

Even now, if I bump my head on a doorway going through it, I think of what I needed to get right about for God to let that happen. I've felt "the strap," brother, and it's no fun. I'm not tough enough to take it a year, two years, five years, or twenty to thirty years like some of you do. I'd rather just get right and stay right and avoid the whipping.

2 At that time the LORD said unto Joshua, Make thee sharp knives, and circumcise again the children of Israel the second time.

3 And Joshua made him sharp knives, and circumcised the children of Israel at the hill of the foreskins.

4 And this is the cause why Joshua did circumcise: All the people that came out of Egypt, that were males, even all the men of war, died in the wilderness by the way, after they came out of Egypt.

5 Now all the people that came out were circumcised: []{#cFT.xhtml_page_78}but all the people that were born in the wilderness by the way as they came forth out of Egypt, them they had not circumcised.

6 For the children of Israel walked forty years in the wilderness, till all the people that were men of war, which came out of Egypt, were consumed, because they obeyed not the voice of the LORD: unto whom the LORD sware that he would not shew them the land, which the LORD sware unto their fathers that he would give us, a land that floweth with milk and honey.

7 And their children, whom he raised up in their stead, them Joshua circumcised: for they were uncircumcised, because they had not circumcised them by the way.

8 And it came to pass, when they had done circumcising all the people, that they abode in their places in the camp, till they were whole.

9 And the LORD said unto Joshua, This day have I rolled away the reproach of Egypt from off you. Wherefore the name of the place is called Gilgal unto this day.

The passage relates the reinstitution of the rite of circumcision. The first time God commanded circumcision was in Genesis 17 to Abraham. Circumcision didn't come by the Law; it came [before]{.class_s2FX} the Law. It came to Abraham under [grace.]{.class_s2FX} Jesus said, ["Moses therefore gave unto you circumcision; (not because it is of Moses, but of the fathers:)"]{.class_s2FW} (John 7:22).

Now verse 2 says, ["circumcise again the children of Israel THE SECOND TIME."]{.class_s2FW} The first time God commanded circumcision, He told Abraham to circumcise every man and boy in his household. When a boy was born, he was to be circumcised the eighth day, and if he wasn't, he was to ["be cut off from his people"]{.class_s2FW}---he was to be [killed]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 17:10--14). That went on from the time of Abraham until the time those Jews came out of Egypt. But when the children of Israel wandered in the wilderness for forty years, they stopped circumcising the baby boys. So for forty years they were out of fellowship with God; they broke the covenant God made with Abraham (Gen. 17:14).

This is a marvelous picture of [God's grace.]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cFT.xhtml_page_79} According to the covenant God made with Abraham, the whole generation of Israeli boys born in the wilderness should have been killed, but God didn't insist on it. Instead, He gave them a second chance. [That's grace.]{.class_s2FX} Instead of killing them, He just counted them as a bunch of [Gentiles.]{.class_s2FX} What was Abraham before he was circumcised? He was a [Gentile.]{.class_s2FX} So here, God overlooks the broken covenant and lets them live. Instead, He treats them as He treated Abraham before he was circumcised. But now, God is reinstituting the Abrahamic covenant and requiring circumcision again.

God will do that for His children in the New Testament as well. If God killed every Christian who got out of fellowship and didn't get right for [years,]{.class_s2FX} you couldn't walk from Pensacola to Mobile without stepping on dead boddies. Instead, God shows grace and mercy to backslidden Christians, trying to woo them back to fellowship.

Now that is the [practical]{.class_s2FX} lesson for the Christian. [Doctrinally]{.class_s2FX} speaking, [every]{.class_s2FX} Christian is circumcised the moment he is saved.

["In whom ]{.class_s2FW}\[speaking of Jesus Christ\][ also ye are circumcised with the circumcision made without hands, in putting off the body of the sins of the flesh by the circumcision of Christ: Buried with him in baptism, wherein also ye are risen with him through the faith of the operation of God, who hath raised him from the dead"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 2:11--12).

There you have it just like you read it in Joshua: a baptism accompanied by a circumcision. When you get saved, you are spiritually baptized by the Holy Spirit into the Body of Christ (1 Cor. 12:13). At the same time that happens, the Holy Spirit comes to live in your body and [cuts]{.class_s2FX} [away]{.class_s2FX} the new spirit He created in you by the second birth (2 Cor. 5:17 cf. John 3:5--7) from your sinful body of flesh.

Back to Joshua 5: ["For the children of Israel walked forty years in the wilderness, till all the people that were men of war, which came out of Egypt, were consumed, because they obeyed not the voice of the LORD: unto whom the LORD sware that he would not shew them the land"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). That's what happened in Numbers 13--14. The ten spies came back with an evil report and convinced the people that they couldn't take []{#cFT.xhtml_page_80}the land, even though God said they could. Joshua and Caleb preached the good news that they were ["well able to overcome it"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 4:2 cf. Num. 13:30), but the people wouldn't believe that ["gospel."]{.class_s2FW} As a result, all the men who should have gone into the land to fight and take it, died in the wilderness instead.

The spiritual lesson for the Christian is that when you refuse to fight the world, the flesh, and the Devil, you lose the blessing God has for you. The problem is [sin]{.class_s2FX} and [unbelief,]{.class_s2FX} just as it was in Numbers 13--14. The moral for the believer is to [do right]{.class_s2FX} and ["fight the good fight of faith"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:12). The old song goes: "Fight manfully onward; dark passions subdue. Look ever to Jesus; He will carry you through."

Verse 8:[ "And it came to pass, when they had done circumcising all the people, that they abode in their places in the camp, till they were whole."]{.class_s2FW} That was a real act of [faith]{.class_s2FX} when you stop and think about it. The healing time was when they were most vulnerable. Their enemies could have come in there and wiped them out just like Simeon and Levi did to a whole city when Shechem raped their sister Dinah (Gen. 34:24--27). So this circumcision is another test of faith. The Israelites are helpless in enemy territory, and they have no choice but to trust God.

As a soldier in the army of the Lord Jesus Christ, you are going to have to trust God in the midst of danger. You are smack dab in the middle of enemy territory. There is no "Reconstructionism" or "Dominionism" or "Postmillennialism" where you are going to turn the whole world to following Jesus Christ. You are a [stranger]{.class_s2FX} and a [pilgrim]{.class_s2FX} in a [war]{.class_s2FX} (1 Pet. 2:11). The Apostle Paul says you are ["in the midst of a crooked and perverse nation"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 2:15). If you don't trust God for protection and victory, you are going to get it in the neck.

We have discussed the meaning of ["Gilgal"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 9) under our remarks on 4:19. ["The reproach of Egypt"]{.class_s2FW} was their state of uncircumcision for forty years (cf. Gen. 34:14). But ["the reproach of Egypt"]{.class_s2FW} was also the Egyptians sneering at God's ability to bring His people into the Promised Land. When the children of Israel wouldn't enter the land back there in Numbers 13--14, God was ready to wipe them all out and start the nation all over again with Moses, []{#cFT.xhtml_page_81}but Moses talked the Lord out of it. (Jack Hyles used to say that it's a good thing Moses and the Lord never got in a killing mood at the same time, or there wouldn't be a Jew left alive on the face of the earth.) Moses said, "Lord, if you kill all these people, the Egyptians are going to hear about it and are going to mock you by saying you never were able to bring them into the Promised Land to begin with. Then the Canaanites will hear about it, and they'll ridicule your name too" (Num. 14:11--16).

You know there had to be a little bit of that going on anyway when the Egyptians heard that their former slaves were wandering around in the desert, dropping dead right and left. So when God ["rolled away the reproach of Egypt,"]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}it not only had to do with the reproach of uncircumcision, it also had to do with making all the heathen nations "eat crow" for thinking the Lord wasn't going to bring His people into the Promised Land.

10 And the children of Israel encamped in Gilgal, and kept the passover on the fourteenth day of the month at even in the plains of Jericho.

11 And they did eat of the old corn of the land on the morrow after the passover, unleavened cakes, and parched corn in the selfsame day.

12 And the manna ceased on the morrow after they had eaten of the old corn of the land; neither had the children of Israel manna any more; but they did eat of the fruit of the land of Canaan that year.

Verse 10 is the first Passover celebrated in the Promised Land. It is also the last time the children of Israel had manna exclusively for their bread. One of Joshua's additions to the Torah was Exodus 16:35.

"And the children of Israel did eat manna forty years, until they came to a land inhabited; they did eat manna, until they came unto the borders of the land of Canaan."

Verses 11--12 give you the transition from manna to ["the fruit of the land of Canaan"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 12). On Passover, they ate manna. The day after the Passover, the first day of the Feast of Unleavened Bread, they not only had manna, they also []{#cFT.xhtml_page_82}["did eat of the old corn of the land"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11). (The word ["corn,"]{.class_s2FW} of course, can refer to either ["a corn of wheat"]{.class_s2FW} \[John 12:24\] or "corn corn"---see our comments on Luke 6:1 in that Commentary.) The ["unleavened cakes"]{.class_s2FW} were made from the manna, and the ["parched corn"]{.class_s2FW} is either wheat or corn kernels which had been dried and roasted for the purpose of preservation to be eaten later. On the second day of the Feast of Unleavened Bread, the manna stopped altogether, and they had to "live off the land."

What you have here is a picture of growing in grace. For forty years, the Israelites had been living on the miraculous. When they needed water, God would give it to them from a rock. When they needed bread, God would rain it down from Heaven. Their clothes and shoes never wore out (Deut. 29:5). As long as they were in a place where they couldn't plant and replace necessities (the wilderness), God gave them what they needed miraculously. But now they are in a place where they can plant and reap and spin and weave and provide for themselves by [work.]{.class_s2FX} The principle in Scripture is if a man won't [work,]{.class_s2FX} he shouldn't eat (2 Thess. 3:10). God's "welfare program" in the Old Testament was to allow the poor people to go out in the fields and glean the corners; they had to [work]{.class_s2FX} to get something to eat.

When you first get saved, God gives you a lot of stuff that could be considered "miraculous" in a providential, spiritual sort of way. The Holy Spirit will show the new babe in Christ a lot of things in the Scriptures just by [reading.]{.class_s2FX} There is a lot of emotion and excitement over the new life in Christ. Christians think that is the "norm," and when they hit the battles with the world, the flesh, and the Devil, they shrink back to those experiences and try to hold on to them instead of [fighting.]{.class_s2FX} They love that preaching about the Holy Spirit, Heaven, miracles, and the like. I mean, they'll shout, amen, hallelujah, and carry on; but when you get on exaggeration, gossip, gluttony, tithing, holding a grudge, etc., they get awfully quiet.

But that's growth, see. The children of Israel still experienced miracles in Canaan; sure they did. I mean, what do you think the walls of Jericho coming down and the sun and moon standing still were? But they didn't live on them from day to day. They got out []{#cFT.xhtml_page_83}there in the fields and plucked the corn instead of going out and picking up the manna. Not every city was taken miraculously like Jericho; it took regular combat to conquer the land.

In the Christian life, you eventually have to [grow up.]{.class_s2FX} You move on from just reading to [studying]{.class_s2FX} the word of God. You have to put some [work]{.class_s2FX} into it for the Holy Ghost to give you something from the Scriptures, and the purpose for that is so you will be ["a WORKMAN that needeth not to be ashamed"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:15). You have to move on from just ["the sincere milk of the word"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:2) to ["strong meat"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 5:12--14).

The problem with the Charismatics is that they want to remain babies all their Christian lives (1 Cor. 3:1--2). They want to subsist on emotion and experience instead of doctrine and sanctification. That's why they gravitate to the least of all the sign gifts (see our remarks under 1 Cor. 12:28--31 in that Commentary). They want a flashy, showy experience instead of putting down the flesh, opposing the world, and resisting the Devil. The Christian who has grown up and become hardened in battle doesn't need miraculous events every five minutes to guide him. He has the word of God and follows it by faith.

Here in the passage, the special provision is gone. Now the children of Israel have to rely on the common, ordinary means that are available to anyone. It is like a little baby growing up and learning to walk. When a baby takes that transition to toddler, the momma and daddy help their little darling. They hold the child's hand while he takes a few shaky steps and then collapses. But all too soon, that toddler doesn't want momma and daddy's hand anymore; he wants to walk all on his own. And eventually, the apprehension and insecurity dissipate, and the little child is walking all on his own just as pretty as you please.

That's the way it should be with you as a Christian. I don't like these songs that speak of Jesus walking beside you holding your hand. He's not beside you; He's [in]{.class_s2FX} you. In your Christian walk, He is walking [in you]{.class_s2FX} (2 Cor. 6:16), and you are walking [in Him]{.class_s2FX} (Col. 2:6). The Lord shouldn't have to "hold your hand" from the moment you get saved until you make it to Glory. You should learn to ["walk by faith"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:7), to ["walk in truth"]{.class_s2FW} (3 John 4), and to ["walk in the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cFT.xhtml_page_84} (Gal. 5:16, 25).

13 And it came to pass, when Joshua was by Jericho, that he lifted up his eyes and looked, and, behold, there stood a man over against him with his sword drawn in his hand: and Joshua went unto him, and said unto him, Art thou for us, or for our adversaries?

14 And he said, Nay; but as captain of the host of the LORD am I now come. And Joshua fell on his face to the earth, and did worship, and said unto him, What saith my lord unto his servant?

15 And the captain of the LORD'S host said unto Joshua, Loose thy shoe from off thy foot; for the place whereon thou standest is holy. And Joshua did so.

The ["man"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 13 turns out to be the Angel of the Lord. Joshua had to take off his shoes before the man (vs. 15) just as Moses had to do at the burning bush (Exod. 3:1--6), because Joshua, like Moses, was in the presence of [Deity.]{.class_s2FX}

All angels in the Bible---without exception---are thirty-three-and-a-half-year-old [males ]{.class_s2FX}(see our comments on 1 John 3:2 in that Commentary) [without wings.]{.class_s2FX} The angel who appeared to Manoah and his wife in Judges 13 (see Judg. 13:3) was said to be ["a MAN of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 13:6). That angel who measured the New Jerusalem in Revelation 21 was said to measure it ["according to the measure of a MAN, that is, of the ANGEL"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 21:17).

People have this weird idea that because angels can fly (Rev. 8:13), they must have wings. Haven't you ever heard of Superman? You say, "What do you mean?" Here's Superman flying around in the comic books [with no wings.]{.class_s2FX} But I'm not going to rely on "funny books" to prove my point. Look at Hebrews 13:2.

"Be not forgetful to entertain strangers: for thereby some have entertained angels unawares."

Let me ask you something. Suppose you got a knock at the door one day, and you went to answer it, and there stood a fellow with wings coming out of his back with a thirty-foot wing span. You reckon you would be "aware" of that?

You see, people don't think. When those angels went to get Lot out of Sodom (Gen. 19), nobody knew they were angels until they revealed themselves as such. Those Sodomites came to Lot's house to abuse those two strangers, and they said, ["Where are the MEN which came in to thee this night?"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 19:5). They had no idea they were angels.

Here in the passage, Joshua has no idea who this fellow is until he tells him. Joshua asks him, ["Art thou for us, or for our adversaries?"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 13). He has no idea that this is the Angel of the Lord. To Joshua, this was just some guy out in the field with a drawn sword.

Verse 13 shows you the character of Joshua. He goes out to survey his "objective" and sees a man near him with a drawn sword. Joshua doesn't miss a beat: ["Art thou for us, or for our adversaries?"]{.class_s2FW} I guarantee you that question was accompanied by Joshua drawing his sword and getting ready to lay into that fellow if the answer came back ["adversaries."]{.class_s2FW} Joshua's challenge has been shortened in today's military to "friend or foe?"

Now you take the angel here ["with his sword drawn in his hand."]{.class_s2FW} That shows up all through the Scriptures. Of course, cherubim are [not]{.class_s2FX} angels, but they are spiritual beings. When God threw Adam and Eve out of the Garden of Eden, He placed cherubim there at the gate with ["a flaming sword"]{.class_s2FW} to prevent anyone from getting back in there and eating from the Tree of Life (Gen. 3:24).

When Balaam traveled from his home on his way to curse the children of Israel there on the plains of Moab, the Angel of the Lord ["stood in the way"]{.class_s2FW} with ["his sword drawn in his hand"]{.class_s2FW} ready to kill Balaam (Num. 22:22--23). He would have too if Balaam's ass hadn't turned aside at one point and plopped herself on the ground at another (Num. 22:25--27).

When David sinned in numbering Israel, David saw the Angel of the Lord standing over Jerusalem with a drawn sword in His hand ready to cut down the inhabitants of the city (1 Chron. 21:16). The Bible says David couldn't go to the Brazen Altar at the Tabernacle ["to enquire of God: for he was afraid because of the sword of the angel of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Chron. 21:29--30). That is why he purchased the Temple mount and set up an altar there.

So that drawn sword in the hands of the Angel of the Lord was no idle threat. When the Assyrians came against Hezekiah, the Angel of the Lord killed 185,000 of them in one night (2 Kings 19:35). When Jesus Christ returns, ["out of his mouth goeth a sharp sword, that with it he should smite the nations"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 19:15).

That's what Joshua goes up against here. Of course, the sword was for the enemies of Israel here, but Joshua didn't know that. He had no couth or tact or diplomacy at all. He stepped right up to that stranger, and he said, "Are you for us or agin' us?"

[Two sides.]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2FW}There is no middle ground; there is no ecumenical movement. "You are either for us or against us; pick a side."

Jesus said, ["He that is not with me is against me; and he that gathereth not with me scattereth abroad"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 12:30). You are either for Jesus Christ, or you are against Him. There is no straddling the fence. If you don't accept Him, you reject Him.

Jesus also said, ["No servant can serve two masters: for either he will hate the one, and love the other; or else he will hold to the one, and despise the other. Ye cannot serve God and mammon"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 16:13). Elijah asked those Jews there on Mt. Carmel, ["How long halt ye between two opinions? if the LORD be God, follow him: but if Baal, then follow him"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 18:21). Later on in this book, Joshua is going to give the people of his day the same choice: ["choose you this day whom ye will serve" ]{.class_s2FW}(Josh. 24:15). Pick one side or the other, but stop straddling the fence.

["Art thou for us, or for our adversaries?"]{.class_s2FW} This is a good spiritual lesson in trying the spirits (1 John 4:1). Joshua doesn't take anything for granted; he tests the spirit to see whether it's of God or the Devil. You should too. If you are spiritual, you are going to judge ["all things"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 2:15), and you are going to judge them by Scripture with Scripture (1 Cor. 2:13).

Verse 14:[ "And he said, Nay]{.class_s2FW} \[in other words, "No, I'm not for your adversaries"\][; but as captain of the host of the LORD am I now come"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 14). So there's no doubt about it: this is the Angel of the Lord. Over in Exodus 23, God told Moses:

["Behold, I send an Angel before thee, to keep thee in the way, and to bring thee into the place which I have []{#cFT.xhtml_page_87}prepared. Beware of him, and obey his voice, provoke him not; for he will not pardon your transgressions: FOR MY NAME IS IN HIM. But if thou shalt indeed obey his voice, and do all that I speak; then I will be AN ENEMY UNTO THINE ENEMIES, and AN ADVERSARY UNTO THINE ADVERSARIES"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 23:20--22).

And there's no doubt that the Angel of the Lord here is a preincarnate appearance of Jesus Christ. Speaking prophetically of the Messiah, Isaiah writes, ["Behold, I have given him for a witness to the people, a leader and COMMANDER to the people"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 55:4). In Hebrews 2:10, Jesus Christ is called ["the CAPTAIN of]{.class_s2FW} \[our\][ salvation."]{.class_s2FW} To make sure you won't get the connection between Joshua 5:14 and Hebrews 2:10, the modern versions remove the word ["captain"]{.class_s2FW} from Hebrews 2:10. The revisers and translators of the new "Bibles" don't like the picture of Jesus Christ as a [military commander,]{.class_s2FX} but when He returns, He comes back at the head of [armies]{.class_s2FX} (Rev. 19:14).

In the Army, a Captain commands a company made up of anywhere from 80 to 250 men. In a rifle company, we used to call the Captain "the old man." You will often hear me refer to Bob Jones Sr. as "old man Bob." I don't mean that disrespectfully. It's disrespectful to call your father "old man," but when I say "old man Bob," I'm using the term as I would for the head of a rifle company. In that setting, it is a term of respect.

Back to Joshua 5:14, ["And Joshua fell on his face to the earth, and did worship."]{.class_s2FW} This shows you that the Angel of the Lord in the Old Testament was an [appearance of God]{.class_s2FX} (see Hos. 12:4--5 and comments in that Commentary). In theology, this is called a "theophany"; and since John said, ["No man hath seen God at any time; the only begotten Son, which is in the bosom of the Father, he hath declared him,"]{.class_s2FW} we would say that the Angel of the Lord is a preincarnate appearance of Jesus Christ, called a "Christophany."

Joshua worships the angel, and the angel does not stop him. Twice in Revelation, John tried to worship an angel (Rev. 19:10, 22:8--9), and both times he was told, ["See thou do it not."]{.class_s2FW} That shows you there is a difference between a particular angel and God appearing as the Angel of the Lord. The Angel here [accepts]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cFT.xhtml_page_88} Joshua's worship just like Jesus Christ accepted worship when He was here on earth (Matt. 8:2, 9:18, 14:33, 15:25, 28:9, 17; Mark 5:6; Luke 24:52; John 9:38). When someone bowed down to worship Jesus Christ, His attitude toward that person was: "That's right. You're right where you belong. Stay down there a while." That's because, contrary to what the Liberals say, Jesus Christ [did]{.class_s2FX} claim to be God in the flesh (John 10:30--33).

Now verses 13--14 give you three things you need spiritually if you are going to engage in Christian combat. You need [courage]{.class_s2FX} like Joshua had when he challenged the man in verse 13. You need [discernment,]{.class_s2FX} trying the spirits. Don't believe everything that comes down the pike. The Devil can "lead" a Christian just like the Holy Spirit can. The Holy Spirit isn't guilty of every "lead" He's accused of giving. Some preachers have what's known in ministerial circles as a "green lead": they're "following the money," taking the church that offers them the biggest paycheck.

Finally, you need the [word of God.]{.class_s2FX} Joshua bowed before the Captain of the Lord's host and said, ["What SAITH my lord unto his servant?"]{.class_s2FW} Jesus said, ["He that is of God heareth God's WORDS"]{.class_s2FW} (John 8:47). He said, ["If a man love me, he will keep my WORDS"]{.class_s2FW} (John 14:23). As a Christian, you are to be ["nourished up in the WORDS of faith and of good doctrine"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 4:6). It's the ["WORDS"]{.class_s2FW} of Scripture that are ["spirit"]{.class_s2FW} and ["life"]{.class_s2FW} (John 6:63), not the "message" or "fundamentals" or "principles."

["And the captain of the LORD'S host said unto Joshua, Loose thy shoe from off thy foot; for the place whereon thou standest is holy"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 15). Here is another death warrant for the United Nations, for it is directly tied to what God told Moses at the burning bush (Exod. 3:5). Both passages are connected with the Second Coming and the slaughter of millions of people. Exodus 3:5 takes place at Sinai where the Ark of the Covenant was constructed, and we have already seen the death that followed the Ark wherever it went (see our remarks under 3:8). When Jesus Christ returns, He follows the path the Ark took from Sinai to Canaan, crossing Jordan at the exact spot where Joshua encountered ["the captain of the LORD'S host"]{.class_s2FW} (see our work on [The Path of the Second Advent]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cFT.xhtml_page_89} and our remarks under Hab. 3:3 in that Commentary). When He does, He slaughters everyone who stands in His way, because that land is ["holy."]{.class_s2FW}

Don't you find it peculiar that the first time the word ["holy"]{.class_s2FW} appears in Scripture, it doesn't refer to God, the Holy Spirit, the Bible, or anything else like that. It has to deal with [dirt]{.class_s2FX} (see our comments on Exod. 3:5 in that Commentary). Everything from Sinai up through Edom and Transjordan is part of the original Abrahamic land grant (Gen. 15:18). That land is [God's]{.class_s2FX} land, and He set it apart from all the rest of the land on earth for [His people.]{.class_s2FX} It doesn't belong to the Arab League, the Muslim Brotherhood, the "Palestinian Authority" (the [PLO]{.class_s2FX}---a terrorist organization responsible for the deaths of thousands of innocent civilians), the Roman Catholic Church, the United Nations, or the United States. That land is [holy to God,]{.class_s2FX} and He is going to [forcibly remove]{.class_s2FX} all trespassers from [His land.]{.class_s2FX}

[]{#cJ7.xhtml}

# Chapter 6 {.heading_s2B}

6:1 Now Jericho was straitly shut up because of the children of Israel: none went out, and none came in.

2 And the LORD said unto Joshua, See, I have given into thine hand Jericho, and the king thereof, and the mighty men of valour.

3 And ye shall compass the city, all ye men of war, and go round about the city once. Thus shalt thou do six days.

4 And seven priests shall bear before the ark seven trumpets of rams' horns: and the seventh day ye shall compass the city seven times, and the priests shall blow with the trumpets.

5 And it shall come to pass, that when they make a long blast with the ram's horn, and when ye hear the sound of the trumpet, all the people shall shout with a great shout; and the wall of the city shall fall down flat, and the people shall ascend up every man straight before him.

The passage gives God's battle plan for Joshua and the people to take the city of Jericho. Verse 2 says, ["the LORD said"]{.class_s2FW}; but remember, this is ["the captain of the LORD'S host"]{.class_s2FW} speaking to Joshua (5:15). So there is no doubt that this is the Angel of the Lord, and that He is an appearance of the Lord to Joshua. This is the New Testament "Joshua" speaking to His Old Testament namesake.

Verse 1: ["Now Jericho was straitly shut up . . . none went out, and none came in."]{.class_s2FW} This is the old "fortress" mentality of warfare, made obsolete by advances in technology like mechanized cavalry, the development of artillery, missiles, aircraft, bombs, etc. The city is prepared for siege. It is a great spiritual picture of a sinner hardening his heart so that the Gospel cannot get in and conquer him for Christ. Calvinists counter this with the doctrine of "Irresistible Grace"; that is, no matter how much a sinner shuts out the Gospel and shuts out the Holy Spirit and shuts out a Christian witness, if he is one of the "elect" (chosen before Gen. 1:1---see our comments on Eph. 1:4 in that Commentary), his will is "bound" (Martin Luther) so []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_91}that he cannot resist the saving grace of God.

After that, you can write B-A-L-O-N-E-Y. You never got a bigger roll of baloney sausage from the deep freeze than that. Stephen told those Jewish leaders in Acts 7:51, ["ye do ALWAYS resist the Holy Ghost."]{.class_s2FW} Grace wasn't "irresistible" there. When Jesus wept over Jerusalem, He said, ["how often would I have gathered thy children together . . . AND YE WOULD NOT!"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 13:34; see our remarks on the verse in that Commentary). God wanted to save them, and they would have none of it: [their will]{.class_s2FX} overruled [His will]{.class_s2FX} in the matter. So the sinner can go into "siege mode" when he comes under conviction by the Holy Spirit. He puts up barriers to resist accepting Christ.

It can also be a spiritual picture of your sinful flesh as a Christian. The Holy Spirit may live in your body as a believer (1 Cor. 6:19), but that body itself is ["carnal, sold under sin"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 7:14), and ["no good thing"]{.class_s2FW} dwells in it as far as its sinful desires go (Rom. 7:18). It doesn't appreciate having to be subject to the Holy Spirit or having its lusts put to death at all. The Devil has an ally in the Adamic nature which does its best to resist the working of the Holy Ghost in the body of the believer. That carnal nature has to be overthrown, just as Jericho had to be overthrown, if the believer is to have the victory and gain the inheritance.

["Casting down imaginations, and every high thing that exalteth itself against the knowledge of God, and bringing into captivity every thought to the obedience of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 10:5).

Back to Joshua 6:[ "And the LORD said unto Joshua, See I have given into thine hand Jericho, and the king thereof, and the mighty men of valour"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2). It sure didn't look like it at the time. There stood the city. It was almost 7.8 acres in size around that time. It had a [double wall]{.class_s2FX} for protection: the outer wall was six feet thick and the inner wall was twelve feet thick. The walls were three stories high. The city was well stocked with food, and its people could withstand a long siege. Joshua had no siege engines and no ladders to scale the walls. Yet the Lord told him, ["I have given into thine hand Jericho,"]{.class_s2FW} as if the city were already taken. That's the Lord looking at that thing as an [accomplished fact]{.class_s2FX} (see our []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_92}remarks under 1:3).

But you can understand how Joshua must have felt about that statement. If you try to live for Jesus Christ, haven't you felt that way sometimes about what you read in the New Testament? I mean, the verse says, ["But my God shall supply all your need according to his riches in glory by Christ Jesus" ]{.class_s2FW}(Phil. 4:19). Haven't some of you looked at that promise around the time the mortgage is due or you incur hospital bills or the kids need braces or the car dies, etc., and thought, "Oh yeah?!" I am sure that you are much too pious to think that about the Lord, aren't you?

That Bible says, ["I can do all things through Christ which strengtheneth me"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 4:13). Haven't you ever looked at that promise and thought, "How can I get control over this bad habit or sinful practice that's plagued me for years?" Well, you can; that's the promise. But it sure looks formidable, doesn't it? That's what Joshua is going through here.

Now verses 3--5 are the Lord's battle plan for taking Jericho. There is no war council or Pentagon or Joint Chiefs of Staff. God tells Joshua what to do, and Joshua does it. If this had been the average Baptist church, there would have been a committee and a committee on the committee and a committee to check on the committees, and [nothing]{.class_s2FX} would ever have gotten done.

Here is one of the strangest battle plans in all of military history. For six days, the whole army of 600,000 men [was to do nothing but march around the city once each day, ]{.class_s2G1}bearing the Ark of the Covenant, with seven priests in front of the Ark blowing on rams' horns. For those six days, no one was to say a word or make a noise at all; the only noise was to be those seven priests blowing on seven rams' horns (vs. 10).

Then on the seventh day, the Israelites were to march around the city seven times. At the end of the seventh time around, the priests with the rams' horns were to sound one last, long blast. When they did, all the people were to shout, and the Lord said He would make the walls fall down flat so the people could run up them like a ramp.

Don't you know that was a strange battle plan for someone like Joshua who had already been through several campaigns. I mean, he had been in combat back there in Exodus 17 and then in Numbers 21 []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_93}and again in Numbers 31. Those actions were won by regular combat. Here, the combat is just "mopping up"; the main strategy which brings down the city is [marching, blowing the trumpets,]{.class_s2FX} and [shouting.]{.class_s2FX}

Now this is not just a Sunday school story to inspire the kiddies. What you are about to read is not only an actual, historical event, it is a foreshadowing of what will take place at the Second Advent. You see, Jericho was a [cursed city]{.class_s2FX} like [Babylon the Great]{.class_s2FX} will be at the Second Advent (vs. 17 of Rev. 17--18). That city was started in Genesis 10:10 by a type of the Antichrist (Nimrod, Gen. 10:8--9), and it runs 6,000 years to its mystery form under the rule of the actual Antichrist. So for "six days" (see our comments on 2 Pet. 3:8 in that Commentary), the Holy Spirit has been sending an army of preachers around this sin-cursed earth to "sound the trumpet" (see Isa. 58:1).

The seventh day of Joshua 6 is indicative of the seven "days" of Daniel's Sevenetieth Week (Dan. 9:24--27). Notice all the "sevens" in the passage: ["seven priests," "seven trumpets," "the seventh day," "seven times"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 4). All of that points to the seven years of the Tribulation.

That ["sound of the trumpet"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 5 has to do with a post-Tribulation rapture that takes place at the [Feast of Trumpets]{.class_s2FX} in the Fall (see our work on [The Two Raptures]{.class_s2FX}). This is followed by the Second Advent (see Joel 2:1; Zeph. 1:16; Zech. 9:14), where the Lord arises and [shouts]{.class_s2FX} (see Psa. 78:65, 47:5 and our comments on those passages in that Commentary).

What you are reading here is future history in type. ["The thing that hath been, it is that which shall be"]{.class_s2FW} (Eccl. 1:9). The events of Joshua 6 are going to take place again, but on a much grander scale.

Now there is a great devotional lesson in the fact that the trumpets here in Joshua 6 are [rams' horns;]{.class_s2FX} that is, the hollowed-out horns of male sheep which are blown through at the tip. You see, the Lord commanded Moses back in Numbers 10 to make a different set of trumpets: [silver ones.]{.class_s2FX}

["Make thee two trumpets of silver; of a whole piece shalt thou make them: that thou mayest use them for the []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_94}calling of the assembly, and for the journeying of the camps"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 10:2).

The silver trumpets were only [two]{.class_s2FX} in number, not seven, and they were not used for war. Their use was to call the assembly of the children of Israel together and to sound the alarm for the tribes to set off on their journeys. The seven rams' horns here were a warning to the enemies of Israel that they were about to get it in the neck.

The devotional application is to the [preacher.]{.class_s2FX} Isaiah 58:1 says, ["Cry aloud, spare not, LIFT UP THY VOICE LIKE A TRUMPET, and shew my people their transgression, and the house of Jacob their sins."]{.class_s2FW} The preacher is to be a watchman on the wall to blow the trumpet when he sees the enemy coming (Ezek. 33:3--6).

Sometimes the preacher is to blow the silver trumpet. His message should encourage his congregation in the faith and challenge and motivate them in their service for God. Preachers like R. G. Lee, Wally Criswell, and Lee Roberson were good with the silver trumpet.

But then you have preachers like J. Frank Norris, Maze Jackson, Sam Jones, and Billy Sunday who blew on the ram's horn. Their preaching was pointed and convicting. It was aimed at the sins of their congregations, as a rebuke and a call to repentance. More often than not, that is the kind of preaching that is needed. There were [seven]{.class_s2FX} rams' horns to [two]{.class_s2FX} silver horns. So a preacher who follows the Biblical pattern will preach three times as much against sin as he preaches encouragement and exhortation. It's ["reprove"]{.class_s2FW} and ["rebuke"]{.class_s2FW} before you ["exhort with all longsuffering and doctrine"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 4:2).

Now if you are called to preach, I don't know what kind of trumpet God will give you to blow, but whichever one He gives you, [blow it.]{.class_s2FX} Don't try to blow someone else's trumpet.

No two Bible preachers are ever the same---not if they are [Bible]{.class_s2FX} preachers. When you hear a certain group of preachers who all sound exactly alike, you are not dealing with [Bible ]{.class_s2FX}preachers.

Campbellites all have the same voice inflections and use the same expressions. They talk about being "BUP-tized." The word isn't "buptized": there's no "u" in it. It's [baptized]{.class_s2FX} with a short "a," as in [apple.]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cJ7.xhtml_page_95} But some dumb, stupid Campbellite years ago couldn't pronounce the word right. Every "Water Dog" who followed him thought that was how to preach and get his congregation wet in the bath tub, so they all picked up the mispronunciation and propagated it [ad nauseam.]{.class_s2FX} That's [not]{.class_s2FX} a Bible preacher.

I remember years ago, someone asked me if I had ever heard a "hack" preacher. I didn't know about what he was talking. I thought he meant one of those "wind sucker" preachers, but that wasn't it at all. It wasn't until I was driving through the mountains of Tennessee or North Carolina somewhere that I learned what he meant. I turned on the radio to get some preaching and came across a fellow who would be going along and periodically in his sentences he would say the word [hack.]{.class_s2FX} "Moses went up into the mountain (hack), and God gave him the Ten Commandments (hack)"---like that. That comes from some preacher years ago who had a throat problem, and God probably used him. Ever after, all those hillbilly preachers thought that if you really wanted to "preach," you had to sound like that one preacher. That's not preaching the Bible; that's just copying another preacher.

You will hear some of Hyles' graduates do that. Hyles had some kind of physical problem where he had to clear his throat all the time when he preached, and you will hear some preachers who trained under him do the same thing. They imitate some peculiarity of another preacher, thinking God will bless them like He blessed that preacher if they just [act]{.class_s2FX} like him. All that is is picking up another preacher's [bad habits.]{.class_s2FX}

The Bible produces a [rugged individualism.]{.class_s2FX} Lester Roloff, Harold Sightler, J. Harold Smith, Bob Jones Sr., Beauchamp Vick, Lee Roberson, J. Frank Norris, D. L. Moody were nothing alike when it came to the styles of their preaching. They may have picked up different things in their delivery from other preachers, but they were constantly in the Bible. God used that to make them their own individuals.

The "brethren" always warn young men about coming here to PBI. They say, "If you go down there, you'll turn out just like Ruckman." [That's a dirty lie!]{.class_s2FX} My associate pastor, Brian Donovan, graduated from here, and he's nothing like me in his style of []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_96}preaching. You couldn't have mistaken Weldon Jones (a graduate who went down to Guadalajara, Mexico and started several churches down there) for me if you tried. Kyle Stephens, Rick Sowell, Rick DeMichele, Nathan Bemis, and Steve Andrus are nothing like me at all. When young men come down here, they don't end up like "Ruckman." What the "brethren" don't like is that they end up [believing the Book]{.class_s2FX} ([AV]{.class_s2FX} 1611).

When you get in that Book and learn that Book, you come out the man God wants you to be and not like someone else. Some of the pastors who came out of J. Frank Norris' school tried to do what he did, and it didn't work at all. Norris once fired a board of 23 deacons for [disagreeing with him.]{.class_s2FX} Some of Norris' students got in some country church where the deacons were all "long-tenured" and set in their ways. The first time they crossed the new pastor, he tried firing them like Norris did, and he found out really quickly that he couldn't do what Norris did. You have to get in the Book and let God mold you into the preacher He wants you to be.

6 And Joshua the son of Nun called the priests, and said unto them, Take up the ark of the covenant, and let seven priests bear seven trumpets of rams' horns before the ark of the LORD.

7 And he said unto the people, Pass on, and compass the city, and let him that is armed pass on before the ark of the LORD.

8 And it came to pass, when Joshua had spoken unto the people, that the seven priests bearing the seven trumpets of rams' horns passed on before the LORD, and blew with the trumpets: and the ark of the covenant of the LORD followed them.

9 And the armed men went before the priests that blew with the trumpets, and the rereward came after the ark, the priests going on, and blowing with the trumpets.

10 And Joshua had commanded the people, saying, Ye shall not shout, nor make any noise with your voice, neither shall any word proceed out of your mouth, until the day I bid you shout; then shall ye shout.

The Ark here has something it did not have at the crossing of the Jordan: it has an [armed guard.]{.class_s2FX}[ "Let him that is armed pass on before the ark of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 7); ["And the armed men went before the priests that blew with the trumpets"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 9). Now you are not told who ["the armed men"]{.class_s2FW} were, but if Joshua 4:12--13 are any indicator, they are the three Transjordanian tribes.

"And the children of Reuben, and the children of Gad, and half the tribe of Manasseh, passed over armed before the children of Israel, as Moses spake unto them: About forty thousand prepared for war passed over BEFORE THE LORD unto battle, to the plains of Jericho."

So the Ark and the priests had a forward guard, and they were followed by the rest of the army. ["The rereward"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 9 is not a "re-reward." [Rere]{.class_s2FX} is the archaic English spelling of [rear.]{.class_s2FX} The ["rereward"]{.class_s2FW} is the [rear guard.]{.class_s2FX} Now who couldn't figure that out from the verse. ["The armed men went BEFORE the priests . . . and the rere-ward came AFTER the ark."]{.class_s2FW}

There is nothing more hypocritical than these modern Bible revisers complaining about the archaic Elizabethan English of the [King James]{.class_s2FX}, and then going to see a movie about [were]{.class_s2FX}wolves. What do you mean WEREwolf? Why, [were]{.class_s2FX} is the Old English word for [man.]{.class_s2FX} Well, why didn't you change the word in the movies because it was "archaic"? You mean to tell me [Hollywood fiction]{.class_s2FX} is more sacrosanct than the [Bible?]{.class_s2FX} If you want a good study on how archaic words are still used in modern parlance, get the work by Dr. Laurence Vance entitled [Archaic Words in the Authorized Version.]{.class_s2FX} You will see that the language of the [King James]{.class_s2FX} is not as "archaic" as the scholars make it out to be.

Verse 10:[ "And Joshua had commanded the people, saying, Ye shall not shout, nor make any noise with your voice, neither shall any word proceed out of your mouth, until the day I bid you shout."]{.class_s2FW} In ancient warfare, all the way up into the late Middle Ages, it was the common practice of an army to yell and scream and carry on before an attack. That was for two purposes: to cause fear in the enemy and to engender courage in the attackers. The command here is for the Israeli army to keep their mouths shut through six days of "marching in review," and then on []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_98}the seventh day, they were only to shout when given the order by Joshua.

Can you imagine how those G.I.s must have felt about that order? I know infantrymen, boy; griping and complaining are second nature to them. Not being able to complain about anything for seven days must have driven some of them mad. Six hundred thousand men marched around that city, and not a sound came out of them but the tramp of feet and the blasts of the rams' horns. If a guy stumbled and fell on the march, he couldn't say a word; no one could ask him if he was all right. If any of them got hungry or thirsty, he couldn't open his mouth to say anything. No one could pass the time with small talk. They were not to utter a word or make a noise with their voices.

I have often thought the Lord put that on them to get back at them for forty years of grumbling and complaining. For forty years, the Lord had to listen to: "Where's the food?", "Where's the water?", "How long do we have to stay out here in this wilderness?", "Why should Moses and Aaron be in charge?", "Why do we have to eat manna every day?", and on and on it went. I think this was a test to see if they could keep their yaps shut after forty years of that mess. To their credit, they did it.

The Apostle Paul told those new Christians in Thessalonica: ["And that ye study to be QUIET"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Thess. 4:11). Solomon wrote, ["a fool's voice is known by multitude of words"]{.class_s2FW} (Eccl. 5:3), and ["In the multitude of words there wanteth not sin: but he that refraineth his lips is wise"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 10:19). The old saying is: "Even a fish wouldn't get into trouble IF IT KEPT ITS MOUTH SHUT!"

["Neither shall any word proceed out of your mouth, until the day I bid you shout; then shall ye shout."]{.class_s2FW} That has good devotional application for the Christian. When the Lord bids you shout, [shout,]{.class_s2FX} brother!

Of course, I know you can get "in the flesh" when it comes to shouting and saying "Amen!" and "Hallelujah!" and "Praise the Lord!" in a service; but I think a lot more people grieve the Spirit when they get a blessing from the singing or the preaching and they keep their mouths shut. No shouting or amening in a church isn't necessarily a sign of "reverence"; it could just be a sign of being []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_99}[dead.]{.class_s2FX}

I'll be right frank with you: I am not a shouter. I don't even shout at a ball game. Even when I was a boy, I used to think everybody was crazy for carrying on at ball games. But I must admit, I think there have been times in my Christian life where I grieved the Spirit by keeping my mouth shut. I was in a meeting one time up in Rochester, New York, and the choir was singing a song about the Bible. The congregation went wild, boy, shouting and roaring. It took all I could to keep from screaming myself. I really think I grieved the Holy Spirit by doing that. There are times, brother, when He bids you shout, you had better SHOUT!

11 So the ark of the LORD compassed the city, going about it once: and they came into the camp, and lodged in the camp.

12 And Joshua rose early in the morning, and the priests took up the ark of the LORD.

13 And seven priests bearing seven trumpets of rams' horns before the ark of the LORD went on continually, and blew with the trumpets: and the armed men went before them; but the rereward came after the ark of the LORD, the priests going on, and blowing with the trumpets.

14 And the second day they compassed the city once, and returned into the camp: so they did six days.

15 And it came to pass on the seventh day, that they rose early about the dawning of the day, and compassed the city after the same manner seven times: only on that day they compassed the city seven times.

16 And it came to pass at the seventh time, when the priests blew with the trumpets, Joshua said unto the people, Shout; for the LORD hath given you the city.

17 And the city shall be accursed, even it, and all that are therein, to the LORD: only Rahab the harlot shall live, she and all that are with her in the house, because she hid the messengers that we sent.

18 And ye, in any wise keep yourselves from the accursed thing, lest ye make yourselves accursed, when ye []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_100}take of the accursed thing, and make the camp of Israel a curse, and trouble it.

19 But all the silver, and gold, and vessels of brass and iron, are consecrated unto the LORD: they shall come into the treasury of the LORD.

20 So the people shouted when the priests blew with the trumpets: and it came to pass, when the people heard the sound of the trumpet, and the people shouted with a great shout, that the wall fell down flat, so that the people went up into the city, every man straight before him, and they took the city.

21 And they utterly destroyed all that was in the city, both man and woman, young and old, and ox, and sheep, and ass, with the edge of the sword.

Verse 11 is [not]{.class_s2FX} a separate trip around the city apart from the seven days; it is simply a summary of what happened. Verses 12--14 give the details of what all was involved in verse 11. You see similar things occurring all through the Bible. One of the better known places is Genesis 1--2, which caused Jean Astruc and the higher critics of the Old Testament so much trouble. Being rather [stupid]{.class_s2FX} and unable to understand the literary tool of [repetition]{.class_s2FX} used by the Lord and the Hebrew writers (see our comments on Gen. 41:32 in that Commentary), they invented an unknown "E" writer for Genesis 1 and an unknown "J" writer for Genesis 2 (and eventually "P," "D," and "R" writers for the rest of the Pentateuch) to take the place of Moses and created two separate, conflicting creation accounts. Of course, Genesis 1 gives an overview of the creation, and Genesis 2 goes back and gives a detailed account on one aspect of creation. But such are the ways of infidelity: any stratagem will be used in order to reject what God said.

Now notice the wording of verse 15: ["And it came to pass on the SEVENTH DAY . . . ."]{.class_s2FW} Do you realize what is so significant about that? [They broke the Sabbath.]{.class_s2FX} They broke the Sabbath [doing what God told them to do.]{.class_s2FX}

There are a couple of lessons in that. First is [grace.]{.class_s2FX} God showed them grace for breaking the Sabbath just as He showed them grace []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_101}for not circumcising their boys for forty years (see our remarks under 5:2--9).

The second lesson is evident in the life of Christ at His First Advent. Over and over again during His ministry, the Lord Jesus healed on the Sabbath. This brought Him no end of animosity from the scribes and Pharisees. One ["ruler of the synagogue"]{.class_s2FW} even went so far as to say, ["There are six days in which men ought to work: in them therefore come and be healed, and not on the sabbath day"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 13:14). Jesus was not squeamish about pointing out the hypocrisy of such statements. Those religious rulers would feed and water their [beasts]{.class_s2FX} on the Sabbath, but would deny a woman being loosed by God from the bonds of Satan on the Sabbath (Luke 13:15--16).

When the Jewish leaders tried to kill Jesus for healing an impotent man on the Sabbath, the Lord told them, ["My Father worketh hitherto, and I work"]{.class_s2FW} (John 5:17). In other words, "If my Father chooses to work on the Sabbath day, then I'm going to follow my Father and do the work He's called me to do." God had the right to suspend His own law at His own choosing. And as the Son of God and the Messiah, Christ was ["Lord also of the sabbath"]{.class_s2FW} just like His Father (Luke 6:5). Here the Old Testament Joshua was "working" on the Sabbath because that's what God commanded him to do. The New Testament "Joshua" exercised the same prerogative.

["And the city shall be accursed"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 17). Again, a picture of ["Babylon the great"]{.class_s2FW} at the Second Advent (Rev. 18:2). Notice, though, that the accursed city is connected with ["the accursed thing"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 18. ["The accursed thing"]{.class_s2FW} turns out to be ["the spoils"]{.class_s2FW}; specifically in Achan's case, ["a goodly Babylonish garment, and two hundred shekels of silver, and a wedge of gold of fifty shekels weight"]{.class_s2FW} (7:21). The "curse" is not just connected with the [things]{.class_s2FX} either; it is connected with the violation of the tenth commandment (["then I coveted them"]{.class_s2FW}---7:21).

Now if you pick up nearly any modern translation ([ASV, RSV, NRSV, NIV, ESV,]{.class_s2FX} etc.), you will see the word ["accursed"]{.class_s2FW} translated as ["devoted."]{.class_s2FX} The reason for that is found in verse 19:

"But all the silver, and gold, and vessels of brass and iron, are CONSECRATED unto the LORD."

But the translation of ["devoted"]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cJ7.xhtml_page_102} misses something. Pensacola Christian College says they believe the [King James Version]{.class_s2FX} to be "AN accurate translation" (2013 Catalog under "Articles of Faith"), which means [nothing.]{.class_s2FX} The [ASV]{.class_s2FX} is considered to be "an accurate translation." The [NASV]{.class_s2FX} is considered to be "an accurate translation." The [ESV]{.class_s2FX} (the "Conservative" edition of the [RSV]{.class_s2FX}) is considered to be "an accurate translation." What you want is not just "an accurate translation," but one that is [complete]{.class_s2FX} and [perfect]{.class_s2FX} in the sense that it has [all]{.class_s2FX} the words the Holy Spirit wants you to have, the [way]{.class_s2FX} He wants you to have them.

The word ["devoted"]{.class_s2FX} doesn't tell you everything you need to know about the Hebrew word [heyrem.]{.class_s2FX} You see, the devotion was connected with [death]{.class_s2FX} (Lev. 27:28--29). And Jericho was not merely a ["devoted"]{.class_s2FX} city; a [real curse]{.class_s2FX} was put on it (vs. 26) and any of the people who took anything from it (vs. 18). Moreover, the only things "devoted" to the Lord were the gold, silver, brass, and iron (vs. 19); everything else was to be [destroyed ]{.class_s2FX}(vss. 21, 24).

What do you miss by getting rid of the word ["accursed"]{.class_s2FW} from verses 17--18? Well, you miss the fact that a [curse]{.class_s2FX} accompanies [covetousness:]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}["an heart they have exercised with COVETOUS PRACTICES; CURSED CHILDREN" ]{.class_s2FW}(2 Pet. 2:14). When those Israelites didn't give the tithe, they were [cursed]{.class_s2FX} (Mal. 3:8--9).

Now as a New Testament child of God, your [soul]{.class_s2FX} cannot be cursed because ["Christ hath redeemed us from the curse of the law, being made a curse for us"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 3:13). But you can bring a curse on your [body.]{.class_s2FX}

["For if ye live after the flesh, ye shall DIE"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:13).

["If any man defile the temple of God, him shall God destroy; for the temple of God is holy, which temple ye are"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 3:17).

When Ananias and Sapphira lied to the Holy Ghost out of covetousness, they both were [dropped dead]{.class_s2FX} (Acts 5:1--10). Covetousness of money ["is the root of all evil"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:10). Paul calls it idolatry (Col. 3:5) and says it will cause you to lose your Millennial inheritance (Eph. 5:5). So there is still a curse connected for the born-again believer.

Tell me something, Christian: what do you have that doesn't belong to God? I mean, He either created it or created the raw materials for you to make it. It's [His]{.class_s2FX} world and [His]{.class_s2FX} air and [His]{.class_s2FX} water (Psa. 24:1); it's [not yours.]{.class_s2FX} As a child of God, your [body]{.class_s2FX} is [His]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 6:19--20). Paul describes himself as a [bondslave]{.class_s2FX} of Jesus Christ (Rom. 1:1; Gal. 1:10; Tit. 1:1). A slave owns [nothing]{.class_s2FX} of his own; it all belongs to the [master.]{.class_s2FX}

You say, "Well, [I]{.class_s2FX} went out and worked, and [I]{.class_s2FX} earned the money to buy all this junk." You had better be careful there. Deuteronomy 8:1 says it is [God]{.class_s2FX} who gives you the ["power to get wealth."]{.class_s2FW} All the Lord has to do is take away your health and confine you to a hospital bed or a wheelchair, and you ain't gonna be earning "nuthin'."

Well, if everything you have belongs to God anyway, don't you reckon it might be a good idea to give Him what is His. Brethren, cheerful giving is the death of covetousness (2 Cor. 9:7). Do you want God's blessing instead of His curse? Then don't be a greedy, stingy tightwad. Don't get all you can and then sit on the can waiting for the undertaker. Learn to be a cheerful giver to the Lord and His work.

What is going on here in verses 17--18 is that when something is devoted to God and His service, it is [cursed]{.class_s2FX} if it is used for any other purpose. Belshazzar found that out the hard way when he hauled out the vessels from the Temple for use at his drunken orgy (Dan. 5:3--6).

Now consider again the connection of Jericho to Mystery Babylon prophetically. ["The accursed thing"]{.class_s2FW} was a BABYLONIAN garment, a wedge of gold, and a sack of silver. Prophetically speaking, that ["Babylonish garment"]{.class_s2FW} is the ["fine linen, and purple, and scarlet"]{.class_s2FW} in which the Whore is ["arrayed"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 17:4--5, 18:16). She is ["decked with gold"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 17:4, 18:16), and the first two items on the list of her ["merchandise"]{.class_s2FW} are ["gold, and silver"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 18:12). The city is not only built on harlotry (like Rahab; cf. Rev. 17:1--5, 18:3), but on covetousness as well (Rev. 18:12--14). Like Jericho (vs. 24), the future Babylon will be ["burned with fire"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 18:8--9).

There is more here than meets the eye, and I don't profess to know or understand everything about it. But the typology involved dictates that when Jesus Christ returns and destroys ["Babylon the great," ]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cJ7.xhtml_page_104}the spoil of that city belongs to the Lord. He gets whatever doesn't burn (the gold, silver, precious stones, pearls, brass, iron, and marble---see Rev. 18:12). That may be part of what is used to build the Millennial temple of Ezekiel 40--46. So what it looks like is that the Lord takes away the tangible wealth of the Roman Catholic Church (Rev. 17) and economic Babylon (Rev. 18) and makes it His own, for His own use and purposes. Right now, it is a [curse:]{.class_s2FX} the ["Vatican Billions"]{.class_s2FX} (see Avro Manhattan's work by that title) and the "Wall Street" billions (worldwide stock exchanges and banks) have damned billions in this present age (["the love of money is the root of all evil: which while some coveted after, they have ]{.class_s2FW}\
[. . . pierced themselves through with many sorrows"]{.class_s2FW}---1 Tim. 6:10), but when Jesus Christ returns, He takes it and finally puts it to good use: the glory and worship of God and His Messiah.

Back to Joshua 6:17---["Only Rahab the harlot shall live, she and all that are with her in the house, because she hid the messengers that we sent."]{.class_s2FW} Notice what the two spies are called in this verse:[ "the MESSENGERS that we sent."]{.class_s2FW} The two men weren't ["messengers"]{.class_s2FW}; they were [spies.]{.class_s2FX} They were sent ["to spy secretly" ]{.class_s2FW}(2:1). The word [messenger]{.class_s2FX} implies [public proclamation.]{.class_s2FX} The phrase ["the messengers that we sent"]{.class_s2FW} hearkens prophetically to the two witnesses sent to preach in the Tribulation (Rev. 11; see also our remarks under Josh. 2:1).             

Now this is in fulfillment of the oath the two spies swore to Rahab in 2:14--19. Rahab had been faithful to her word and had not betrayed the spies, and that scarlet line had hung out her window since the night the spies escaped (2:21).

As the Israeli army marched around that city each day, there was one part of that wall with a rope hanging from a window, and the thing that caught the eye of every Jewish soldier was the bright red thread woven down through it. Inside that house from which the scarlet cord hung sat Rahab with her family, huddled together, wondering what  was going to happen. But there was one thing they were counting on: if they were in the house with the scarlet thread hanging out the window, when the Jews went through the city slaughtering man, woman, child, and beast, they would be spared.

For seven days they stayed in that house and didn't go out. And []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_105}on the seventh day when the shout went up from the Jewish army and the walls of Jericho fell flat (vs. 20), the section of the wall with Rahab's house on it remained standing.

When the walls fell down flat, they didn't fall inward, as you would expect if an army were attacking the city with battering rams and war machines; they collapsed [outward.]{.class_s2FX} When Dr. John Garstang excavated the city in 1929--1936, he found that the outer wall fell outward, with the houses located on top of the walls (straddling the inner and outer walls) dragging the inner wall along with them. The Israelites were able to use the fallen walls like a ramp to invade the city, and wherever they were around the city, all they had to do was go straight up the ramp in front of them because the whole wall was down, except for the section with Rahab's house on it.

["And they utterly destroyed all that was in the city . . . with the edge of the sword"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 21). Verse 24 adds: ["And they burnt the city with fire, and all that was therein."]{.class_s2FW} Garstang found evidence of this. There were large layers of charcoal and ash, and the ruins of the walls were discolored by fire. The houses near the fallen walls were completely burned, with a layer of black debris, white ash, and burnt bricks where they once stood.

As I have pointed out several times now, this is a picture of the Second Advent, and if you want to see the parallels, turn to Joel 2.

Joel 2:1---["Blow ye the trumpet in Zion . . . ."]{.class_s2FW} There's that ["sound of the trumpet"]{.class_s2FW} back in Joshua 6:20 that brought down the walls of Jericho. [". . . and sound an alarm in my holy mountain: let all the inhabitants of the land tremble]{.class_s2FW} \[cf. Josh. 2:9--11\][: for the day of the LORD cometh . . . ."]{.class_s2FW} Second Advent.

Joel 2:2---["A day of darkness and of gloominess, a day of clouds and of thick darkness, AS THE MORNING spread upon the mountains . . . ."]{.class_s2FW} Joshua 6:12 says, ["And Joshua rose EARLY IN THE MORNING"]{.class_s2FW}; and further down in verse 15, it says, ["And it came to pass on the seventh day, that they rose EARLY ABOUT THE DAWNING OF THE DAY." ". . . a great people and a strong; there hath not been ever the like, neither shall be any more after it, even to the years of many generations."]{.class_s2FW} These are ["the armies"]{.class_s2FW} from Heaven which []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_106}follow Christ at the Battle of Armageddon (Rev. 19:14), which means this is a reference to the Church at the Second Advent.

Joel 2 is one of the great boo-boos in the [Scofield Reference Bible.]{.class_s2FX} Scofield got messed up in Joel 2:20 and assumed that the army of Joel 2:1--10 was the army of the [Antichrist.]{.class_s2FX} He didn't like the idea of the Church [burning]{.class_s2FX} anybody (Joel 2:3, 5--6). The problem he had was verse 11 in the passage, which reads, ["the LORD shall utter his voice before HIS army"]{.class_s2FW}---[not]{.class_s2FX} the [Devil's]{.class_s2FX} army or the army of the [Antichrist.]{.class_s2FX} So to enforce his own private interpretation on the passage, Scofield switched the paragraph mark in the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible from verse 12, where it [belongs,]{.class_s2FX} to verse 11, where it [doesn't.]{.class_s2FX} How do you know that to be so? Because that army is not like any one before it or after it (Joel 2:2), and those horsemen can't be wounded (Joel 2:8). Second Thessalonians 1:7--8 say that at the Second Coming, ["the Lord Jesus shall be revealed from heaven with his mighty angels, IN FLAMING FIRE taking vengeance on them that know not God."]{.class_s2FW} It is the armies from Heaven that bring the fire at the Second Advent, not the armies of the Antichrist.

Now don't misunderstand me. C. I. Scofield was a good man after he got saved; he was a great dispensational Bible teacher. The [Scofield Reference Bible]{.class_s2FX} is one of the best reference Bibles you can get; you won't go wrong on the fundamentals of the faith---including the Premillennial, pre-Tribulational return of the Lord Jesus Christ---if you get a [Scofield Reference Bible.]{.class_s2FX} But you can't have ["men's persons in admiration because of advantage"]{.class_s2FW} (Jude 16). When you get so ["heady"]{.class_s2FW} and ["highminded"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 3:4) that you think your scholarship equips you to mess with the [Authorized Version]{.class_s2FX} of the Holy Bible, you are in for trouble. That goes for C. I. Scofield, R. A. Torrey, "dear Dr. John \[R. Rice\]," your momma, your daddy, your grandparents, or [anyone else.]{.class_s2FX}

Do you know how I know that [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible is superior to [any]{.class_s2FX} scholarship, Fundamental or otherwise? Because of exactly what you see in Joel 2:12. Those Puritan and Anglican translators of the [King James Version]{.class_s2FX} weren't Premillennial; they were Postmillennial and Amillennial.
