Yet over and over again in their work, you find clear evidence of Premillennial theology (see the Introduction to Ezra in the []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_107}[Bible Believer's Commentary on Ezra, Nehemiah, Esther]{.class_s2FX} in regard to the Premillennial layout of 2 Chronicles, Ezra, Nehemiah, Esther, Job, and Psalms, for example). You can't explain that paragraph mark by the translators' theology.

You say, "Ruckman, are you saying the paragraph marks in a [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible are inspired?" I might not go that far. I believe the [AV]{.class_s2FX} is the Scriptures in English, and that ["ALL SCRIPTURE is given by inspiration of God"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 3:16). I believe ["every word"]{.class_s2FW} of God in the Scripture ["is given by inspiration of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 4:4; Prov. 30:5; John 6:63, 8:47). But while paragraph marks and punctuation marks like semicolons and commas may not be words, they certainly do show the marks of the supernatural leadership of the Holy Spirit on the [King James]{.class_s2FX} translators.

So Joel 2 is the prophetic fulfillment of the type you find in Joshua 6. Look at Joel 2:7 for one more example.

"They shall run like mighty men; they shall CLIMB THE WALL like men of war; and they shall MARCH EVERY ONE ON HIS WAYS, and they shall NOT BREAK THEIR RANKS."

It's all there: the trumpet, the marching, the ranks, the climbing up the wall, and the burning. [Joshua 6 is going to take place again.]{.class_s2FX}

We have already discussed the reasons for the genocide of verse 21 in the Introduction to this Commentary, which see. The spiritual application for the New Testament believer is found in Colossians 3:5.

"Mortify therefore your members which are upon the earth; fornication, uncleanness, inordinate affection, evil concupiscence, and covetousness, which is idolatry."

You are to commit [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} genocide on your flesh.

22 But Joshua had said unto the two men that had spied out the country, Go into the harlot's house, and bring out thence the woman, and all that she hath, as ye sware unto her.

23 And the young men that were spies went in, and brought out Rahab, and her father, and her mother, and her brethren, and all that she had; and they brought out all []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_108}her kindred, and left them without the camp of Israel.

24 And they burnt the city with fire, and all that was therein: only the silver, and the gold, and the vessels of brass and of iron, they put into the treasury of the house of the LORD.

25 And Joshua saved Rahab the harlot alive, and her father's household, and all that she had; and she dwelleth in Israel even unto this day; because she hid the messengers, which Joshua sent to spy out Jericho.

The passage is on the salvation of Rahab and her family. Here is a wicked woman, who under the laws of God and decent society, should have [died]{.class_s2FX} (Deut. 22:21; Gen. 38:24). She was a heathen under the curse of God (Deut. 7:1; Josh. 3:10), and yet, here she is being spared because of the "scarlet thread of redemption." What a wonderful picture of [grace]{.class_s2FX} and New Testament [salvation.]{.class_s2FX}

["And the young men that were spies went in, and brought out Rahab, and her father, and her mother, and her brethren, and all that she had; and they brought out all her kindred, and left them without the camp of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 23). Another picture of New Testament salvation. Hebrews 13:12--13 says:

"Wherefore Jesus also, that he might sanctify the people with his own blood, suffered without the gate. Let us go forth therefore unto him without the camp, bearing his reproach."

Interestingly, the verse on joining Christ ["without the camp"]{.class_s2FW} is followed by a statement that ["here have we no continuing city."]{.class_s2FW} That was certainly true of Rahab. She watched as her "hometown" was burned to the ground.

But look at verse 25 here in Joshua 6: ["And Joshua saved Rahab the harlot alive . . . and she dwelleth in Israel even unto this day ]{.class_s2FW}\[i.e., at the time Joshua was written\][."]{.class_s2FW} What started out as ["without the camp, bearing his reproach"]{.class_s2FW} ended up being ["accepted in the beloved"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:6). You see, Rahab, like Ruth after her, became a Jewish proselyte and married a Jew (["Salmon"]{.class_s2FW}---Matt. 1:5). She became the mother of Boaz and the []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_109}great great grandmother of King David (Matt. 1:5--6), and of course, that placed her in the line of the Lord Jesus Christ (Matt. 1:5--16).

Verse 24:[ "And they burnt the city with fire, and all that was therein: only the silver, and the gold, and the vessels of brass and of iron, they put into the treasury of the house of the LORD."]{.class_s2FW} Except for Achan's transgression, none of the other Israelites took anything. In Garstang's excavations, he found storerooms filled with enough food stuffs to withstand a long siege. Any normal invading force would have appropriated the supplies, but in this case, the conquerors left them alone.

26 And Joshua adjured them at that time, saying, Cursed be the man before the LORD, that riseth up and buildeth this city Jericho: he shall lay the foundation thereof in his firstborn, and in his youngest son shall he set up the gates of it.

27 So the LORD was with Joshua; and his fame was noised throughout all the country.

Verse 26 is not only a curse placed on the man who would rebuild Jericho, it was a prophecy as well. It was fulfilled to the letter 426 years later in 1 Kings 16:34.

"In his days did Hiel the Bethelite build Jericho: he laid the foundation thereof in Abiram his firstborn, and set up the gates thereof in his youngest son Segub, according to the word of the LORD, which he spake by Joshua the son of Nun."

We have discussed the importance of fulfilled prophecy many times in our works. Fulfilled prophecy is the main proof of the inspiration of the Bible as opposed to such amateurish trash as the [Shastas,]{.class_s2FX} the [Vedas,]{.class_s2FX} the [Puranas,]{.class_s2FX} the [Tripitaka,]{.class_s2FX} the [Zend Avesta,]{.class_s2FX} and the [Koran]{.class_s2FX} (Isa. 42:9, 43:9, 44:7, 46:9--10, 48:3--8). Revelation 19:20 says, ["the testimony of Jesus is the spirit of PROPHECY."]{.class_s2FW}

There is nothing in the "scriptures" of other religions like you find in the Bible. The Bible doesn't just tell you what's going to happen at "the Last Day" when time shall be no more (Rev. 10:6); it tells you what is going to happen [in history]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cJ7.xhtml_page_110} so you can check it out (e.g., see Isa. 44:28--45:1).

If Mohammed was such a "big boy" as a prophet, why couldn't he do what Joshua did here in verse 26? You won't find [anywhere ]{.class_s2FX}in the[ Koran]{.class_s2FX} or the [Hadith]{.class_s2FX} (the second most holy book in Islam) where Mohammed prophesies what would happen in 425 years or 400 years or 300 years or 200 years or 100 years or fifty years or even ten years. If he had, neither "holy book" could give you the fulfillment of such a prophecy since "revelation" [ceased]{.class_s2FX} with Mohammed.

One time in the [Koran,]{.class_s2FX} Mohammed [copied]{.class_s2FX} a prophecy given by Daniel, over 1,000 years before Mohammed was born, on the revived Roman Empire (Dan. 2, 7); but even then, Mohammed couldn't give you the details Daniel gave you. Another time, Mohammed hazarded a guess about the outcome of a battle, which as anyone knows has a fifty-fifty chance of being right: you will either win or you will lose. Mohammed just happened to hit it right, which is the "proof" of him being a prophet to a Moslem.

Being right on a 50% chance is nothing. If you want to see supernatural phenomena of divine revelation, get a Bible. The Holy Bible gives you [48 prophecies]{.class_s2FX} about [one man,]{.class_s2FX} written anywhere from [400--1,500 years]{.class_s2FX} before the fellow was born, and [every one of them comes through right on the money.]{.class_s2FX} Do you know what the chances are of that taking place?

Well, a mathematician and statistician named Peter Stoner, in his work [Science Speaks,]{.class_s2FX} calculated the odds of one man fulfilling 48 prophecies to be one out of ten with [157 zeroes]{.class_s2FX} after it. There are not that many electrons in three universes the size of our own. Moreover, according to another law of statistics and probability, if the chances of a thing taking place are over one out of ten with fifty zeroes after it, the event is statistically [impossible:]{.class_s2FX} it will [never]{.class_s2FX} take place. The life of Jesus Christ is the one sure proof that the Bible is the inspired word of God. Mohammed couldn't produce anything like it. If he were a "prophet," then kick him out of the office, because he couldn't prophesy his way out of a wet paper bag.

Verse 26 not only gives you proof that the book of Joshua ["is given by inspiration of God,"]{.class_s2FW} it also is further proof of Jericho []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_111}being a type of Mystery Babylon. The city was rebuilt under a type of the Antichrist---Ahab, the worst King the northern kingdom of Israel ever had (1 Kings 16:30--33). (On a passing note, when the city was rebuilt again the second time in the New Testament, it was built by another type of the Antichrist---[Herod.]{.class_s2FX} And it was set up as a [Roman]{.class_s2FX} town---cf. Rev. 17:9, 18.) It was rebuilt under a [Whore]{.class_s2FX} who was a [Queen]{.class_s2FX} (1 Kings 16:81; Rev. 2:20 cf. Rev. 17:1--5). It was rebuilt during a time of idolatry (1 Kings 16:31--32 cf. Rev. 13:14--15). Its rebuilding was connected with [human sacrifice]{.class_s2FX} (Psa. 16:4; Isa. 6:13). The part of the prophecy about the foundation being laid in the firstborn and the gates being set up in the youngest son could mean when the boys were born, but more than likely it means his sons were [killed,]{.class_s2FX} since such dedications among the heathen were accompanied by [child sacrifice]{.class_s2FX} (2 Kings 3:27, 16:3, 17:17; Jer. 32:35).

Like the Red Sea crossing and the defeat of the Amorite Kings on the other side of Jordan (see 2:10), it didn't take any time at all for the news of Joshua 4--6 to travel from "Dan to Beersheba." Joshua's victory was the headline of every newspaper and the lead story on every newscast.

Now the spiritual lesson of verse 27 for the Christian is given by Christ in John 12:26.

"If any man serve me, let him follow me; and where I am, there shall also my servant be: if any man serve me, him will my Father honour."

So if a man serves the Lord, God is with him and will honor him. That being the case, here are some spiritual lessons on serving God which can be gleaned from the chapter.

1. Anyone who serves God is going to be [peculiar to the world]{.class_s2FX} (Tit. 2:14; 1 Pet. 2:9). Joshua was given one of the most peculiar battle plans anyone ever had: march around your objective once a day for six days and then on the seventh day you march around it seven times. Then instead of attacking, you blow on trumpets and yell. What's that all about?!

Don't you know the soldiers on the walls of Jericho were wondering what was going on. Here they were shaking in their boots over a people who had walked through the Red Sea on dry ground, []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_112}had taken down two great Kings on the east side of Jordan, and then crossed the Jordan on dry ground. Now all they were doing was marching in review around the city. I bet you by the seventh day those Amorites in Jericho were mocking and jeering those Israelites for their peculiar behavior.

2. God's servants will [triumph over all obstacles.]{.class_s2FX} Over in Zechariah 4:7, the Lord was trying to encourage those Jews who returned from exile to rebuild the Temple, and they were facing opposition from the Samaritans, opposition from Arabs, and opposition from the Persian King. In the middle of all that, the Lord told the Governor:

"Who art thou, O great mountain? before Zerubbabel thou shalt become a plain: and he shall bring forth the headstone thereof with shoutings, crying, Grace, grace unto it."

If God has called you to do something, no obstacle will be able to stop you unless you give up. Of course, that doesn't mean you'll come through unscathed. You may get kicked, cussed, beaten, spat on, mocked, betrayed, etc.; but you will overcome all obstacles to accomplish the task God called you to do.

You take Paul. He went through gripings and complaining from the churches, accusations by false brethren, the Jews against him, the Romans against him, the weather against him, beatings, stonings, shipwrecks, and a thorn in the flesh (2 Cor. 11--12). If anyone had a reason to quit, Paul had it, but he kept going, and he overcame all the obstacles the Devil put before him. He could say at the end of his life, ["I have fought a good fight, I have finished my course, I have kept the faith"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 4:7).

3. The servants of Christ will be [daring in their faith.]{.class_s2FX} Those Jews had no fortress, no siege engines, no scaling ladders, no battering rams, no catapults, and they were on the enemy's ground. Yet they went ahead and did what God told them anyway, even though it seemed perfectly foolish.

4. The Lord's servants are [disciplined.]{.class_s2FX} The Israelites were told not to make a sound, and they didn't. If you are going to serve the Lord, Christian, you are going to have to be disciplined in your Bible reading, disciplined in your prayer life, and disciplined in your service. Paul said, []{#cJ7.xhtml_page_113}["And every man that striveth for the mastery is temperate in all things"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 9:25).

5. A complementary quality of the servants of God to discipline is their [self-denial. ]{.class_s2FX}God told the people to keep their hands off the spoils, and with the exception of one fellow, they did what they were told.

Over in 1 Samuel 15, Saul received the same instructions about the Amalekites that Joshua received about Jericho: "Go in there and kill everything that breathes; don't save any man, woman, child, or beast alive" (1 Sam. 15:3). Saul, though, couldn't deny himself a "war trophy," so he kept the King of the Amalekites alive to parade him around. The people under Saul couldn't deny themselves either; they kept all the best cattle alive (1 Sam. 15:9). When Samuel confronted Saul about his disobedience, Saul's excuse was all the best cattle were spared to sacrifice to the Lord (1 Sam. 15:15). Samuel told Saul:

["Hath the LORD as great delight in burnt offerings and sacrifices, as in obeying the voice of the LORD? Behold, to obey is better than sacrifice, and to hearken than the fat of rams"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Sam. 15:22).

Brethren, no amount of religious service can make up for not paying attention to what God says. God compared disregard for His words to [witchcraft]{.class_s2FX} and [idolatry]{.class_s2FX} (1 Sam. 15:23). In the New Testament, those sins are part of ["the works of flesh"]{.class_s2FW} that cause the believer to lose his inheritance in the Kingdom of God (Gal. 5:19--21). Saul lost a kingdom because he wouldn't [deny himself]{.class_s2FX} (cf. Luke 9:23 and comments in that Commentary).

[]{#cPS.xhtml}

# Chapter 7 {.heading_s2B}

7:1 But the children of Israel committed a trespass in the accursed thing: for Achan, the son of Carmi, the son of Zabdi, the son of Zerah, of the tribe of Judah, took of the accursed thing: and the anger of the LORD was kindled against the children of Israel.

This is a great chapter on revival, and when it is preached, the title of the sermon is nearly always "Sin in the Camp." It is a picture of how a church, school, or ministry can suffer because of one disobedient Christian. The principle is repeated over and over again in the Scripture.

["Wisdom is better than weapons of war: but one sinner destroyeth much good"]{.class_s2FW} (Eccl. 9:18).

["Dead flies cause the ointment of the apothecary to send forth a stinking savour; so doth a little folly him that is in reputation for wisdom and honour"]{.class_s2FW} (Eccl. 10:1).

["A little leaven leaveneth the whole lump"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:9).

Here the verse says, ["the children of Israel"]{.class_s2FW}---that's [corporately,]{.class_s2FX} as a group---["committed a trespass."]{.class_s2FW} Well, technically, no. It was just [one man: ]{.class_s2FX}["for Achan . . . took of the accursed thing."]{.class_s2FW} One man's sin was charged to the whole group.

That's what happened to David in 2 Samuel 24 and 1 Chronicles 21. In his pride, he numbered the men in Israel who were eligible to go to war so he could brag about the size of his army. As a result, thousands of his subjects died due to God's judgment. David prayed, ["I it is that have sinned and done evil indeed; but as for these sheep, what have they done?"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Chron. 21:17). Well, nothing, but David's sin involved the people.

You run into the same thing with Adam. Adam sinned and plunged the whole human race into sin.

["Wherefore, as by one man sin entered into the world, and death by sin; and so death passed upon all men, for that all have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 5:12).

That is what is known in systematic theology as "federal []{#cPS.xhtml_page_115}headship." A group is judged by the actions and decisions of its leaders. The chief priests rejected Christ and asked for a demon-possessed Roman dictator to be their King (John 19:15); as a result, those Jews have been under the thumb of Rome in one form or another for 2,000 years now. The people were judged by the decisions of their leaders.

Now just in case you think that's "not fair," just remember, the way you get into Heaven is on the righteousness of another.

["But not as the offense, so also is the free gift. For if through the offence of one many be dead, much more the grace of God, and the gift by grace, which is by one man, Jesus Christ, hath abounded unto many . . . . For if by one man's offence death reigned by one; much more they which receive abundance of grace and of the gift of righteousness shall reign in life by one, Jesus Christ.) Therefore as by the offence of one judgment came upon all men to condemnation; even so by the righteousness of one the free gift came upon all men unto justification of life. For as by one man's disobedience many were made sinners, so by the obedience of one shall many be made righteous"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 5:15--19).

2 And Joshua sent men from Jericho to Ai, which is beside Bethaven, on the east side of Bethel, and spake unto them, saying, Go up and view the country. And the men went up and viewed Ai.

3 And they returned to Joshua, and said unto him, Let not all the people go up; but let about two or three thousand men go up and smite Ai; and make not all the people to labour thither; for they are but few.

Now the Lord is angry with the whole nation, but Joshua doesn't know it. Joshua sends some men ahead to the next city to reconnoiter. The town of Ai is so small, population wise, that Joshua's men figure they won't have any trouble taking it after the victory at Jericho.

Notice the pride and arrogance displayed in verse 3: ["Let not []{#cPS.xhtml_page_116}all the people go up, but let about two or three thousand men go up and smite Ai; and make not all the people to labour thither; for they are but few."]{.class_s2FW}

They are so proud and puffed up that they are telling the commander-in-chief how to conduct the assault. Joshua is the supreme commander, not them. Their job was just to report on Ai, not to advise Joshua on what he ought to do.

They were [overconfident.]{.class_s2FX} The Bible says, ["Pride goeth before destruction, and an haughty spirit before a fall"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 16:18). They thought they could take Ai with a relatively small force; [they were about to lose their shirts.]{.class_s2FX}

The reason they had won at Jericho was not because of their own military prowess; it was because the battle had been ordered by the Captain of the Lord's host (5:14--6:5). God spoke to Joshua and told him what to do. There is [no prayer]{.class_s2FX} here, [no seeking God's face]{.class_s2FX} in the matter. Instead, Joshua follows the plans of [men.]{.class_s2FX}

4 So there went up thither of the people about three thousand men: and they fled before the men of Ai.

5 And the men of Ai smote of them about thirty and six men: for they chased them from before the gate even unto Shebarim, and smote them in the going down: wherefore the hearts of the people melted, and became as water.

6 And Joshua rent his clothes, and fell to the earth upon his face before the ark of the LORD until the eventide, he and the elders of Israel, and put dust upon their heads.

7 And Joshua said, Alas, O Lord GOD, wherefore hast thou at all brought this people over Jordan, to deliver us into the hand of the Amorites, to destroy us? would to God we had been content, and dwelt on the other side Jordan!

8 O Lord, what shall I say, when Israel turneth their backs before their enemies!

9 For the Canaanites and all the inhabitants of the land shall hear of it, and shall environ us round, and cut off our name from the earth: and what wilt thou do unto thy great name?

Three thousand men of Israel made a direct assault on the gate of Ai, expecting an easy victory, and instead were routed by the men of Ai (later on in 8:25, you will learn that the entire population of Ai, both men and women, was only 12,000, which means that the army of Ai was probably less than 6,000). Thirty-six men died as a result of Achan's sin. What Achan did affected innocent people.

["Shebarim"]{.class_s2FW} is more than likely the name of the valley that lay before Ai (see 9:11), as is indicated by the words ["in the going down"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5). The word means "breaks" or "ruins."

["Wherefore the hearts of the people melted, and became as water"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5): the Israelites are ready to quit. That is how we are. We presume on the grace of God. We get proud and puffed up; then when the Lord smacks us down, we are ready to quit.

Joshua was no exception. When he gets the bad news, he tears his clothes, puts dirt on his head, and falls face down on the ground before the Ark. All those things are Oriental gestures of [death.]{.class_s2FX} The idea is that it would have been better to die than to get this awful news.

Now this was the guy who was ready to take on the giants back there in Numbers 13--14. This is the fellow who challenged the Angel of the Lord back in chapter 5. Look at him now! He's flat on his face in the dirt, moaning and complaining, "Oh God, why did you ever bring us over Jordan if all you were going to do was let the Amorites kill us? We should just have stayed there in the plains of Moab with the Reubenites, Gadites, and Manassites. What can I say to the people when they are in full retreat before their enemies? All the Canaanites are going to hear about this and surround us and slaughter us, and when they do, Lord, your name is [mud."]{.class_s2FX}

Listen to that. He sounds just like those griping, murmuring Jews in Exodus 17:3 and Numbers 11:20, 14:2--3. That's the low point in Joshua's life. He has lost his faith. Right here in verses 7--9, Joshua is just as backslidden as the people God killed in the wilderness.

Now that's how the Bible deals with its "heroes." They are not perfect at all. Joshua here sounds just like Elijah does in 1 Kings 19:3--10 (which see). Lester Roloff used to describe it as "throwing a pity party in juniper jungle." James describes it as being men of ["like passions as we are"]{.class_s2FW} (James 5:17).

["O Lord, what shall I say, when Israel turneth their backs before their enemies!"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 8). There wasn't much he could say. When Paul talks about the armor of the Christian soldier, in Ephesians 6, he gives nothing for the [back;]{.class_s2FX} everything---the breastplate, the shield, and the sword---is for a [forward]{.class_s2FX} assault. Retreat should not be an option for the believer in Christ.

10 And the LORD said unto Joshua, Get thee up; wherefore liest thou thus upon thy face?

11 Israel hath sinned, and they have also transgressed my covenant which I commanded them: for they have even taken of the accursed thing, and have also stolen, and dissembled also, and they have put it even among their own stuff.

12 Therefore the children of Israel could not stand before their enemies, but turned their backs before their enemies, because they were accursed: neither will I be with you any more, except ye destroy the accursed from among you.

13 Up, sanctify the people, and say, Sanctify yourselves against to morrow: for thus saith the LORD God of Israel, There is an accursed thing in the midst of thee, O Israel: thou canst not stand before thine enemies, until ye take away the accursed thing from among you.

14 In the morning therefore ye shall be brought according to your tribes: and it shall be, that the tribe which the LORD taketh shall come according to the families thereof; and the family which the LORD shall take shall come by households; and the household which the LORD shall take shall come man by man.

15 And it shall be, that he that is taken with the accursed thing shall be burnt with fire, he and all that he hath: because he hath transgressed the covenant of the LORD, and because he hath wrought folly in Israel.

Joshua is in a prayer meeting, and the Lord tells him, "GET UP!" It wasn't time to pray; it was time to [move.]{.class_s2FX}

The Devil is subtle, boy. He will get you praying when you should be moving; he will get you moving when you should be praying. He will get you doing the [right thing]{.class_s2FX} at the [wrong time.]{.class_s2FX} It takes [spiritual discernment]{.class_s2FX} to be able to tell [when]{.class_s2FX} to do the right thing.

Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "Duties never conflict." In other words, duties need to be [prioritized.]{.class_s2FX} Don't go out witnessing when you ought to be studying your Greek grammar; don't be studying when you ought to be praying. That's the business.

I have had students come to me and ask me to let them out of Greek class because some special preacher like Ian Paisley was in town, and they wanted to go hear him preach. Well, who wouldn't get a blessing from Ian Paisley that he couldn't get from Greek grammar? I mean, it's always easy to do things that are a blessing. The question is, what is your [duty?]{.class_s2FX} Did God call you to school? Then stay in school and take the classes when they're assigned and do your homework when you ought.

Is it prayer meeting? Then don't be standing around studying for a test when you ought to be off somewhere praying. Duties never conflict. Amen, amen, amen!

["Wherefore liest thou thus upon thy face?"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 10). Don't you know Joshua had a good excuse for that one. "Well, Lord, you said, ['Humble yourselves therefore under the mighty hand of God,']{.class_s2FW} so I'm humbling myself. I'm down. You told me to call on your name, so I'm calling. You said to ask, seek, and knock. What do you think I'm doing?"

What was the problem, though? It was [sin:]{.class_s2FX}[ "Israel hath sinned"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11). Isaiah wrote, ["But your iniquities have separated between you and your God, and your sins have hid his face from you, that he will not hear"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 59:2).

Notice He said, ["ISRAEL hath sinned."]{.class_s2FW} He's not talking about the [individual]{.class_s2FX} in Israel who sinned (Achan); He's talking about the [nation corporately.]{.class_s2FX} Israel [as a nation]{.class_s2FX} was the son of God in the Old Testament (Exod. 4:22); outside of Adam and the angels as [created]{.class_s2FX} sons of God (see comments on Luke 3:38 in that Commentary), there were no individual sons of God in the Old Testament. So God is judging the nation as a whole here for the sins of one of its members.

Now although in the New Testament you are an individual son of []{#cPS.xhtml_page_120}God by faith in Jesus Christ (John 1:12), you still are a member of a corporate group: the Body of Christ. What you do as a member of that Body can affect it. Look at 1 Corinthians 12:25--27.

"That there should be no schism in the body; but that the members should have the same care one for another. And whether one member suffer, all the members suffer with it; or one member be honoured, all the members rejoice with it. Now ye are the body of Christ, and members in particular."

So what you do, Christian, can affect the Body of Christ for good or for ill. You see that all the time when some preacher falls due to a moral problem; that blackens the eye of the Church in general before an unsaved world. Those lost people out there don't distinguish between one church and another, or between one denomination and another. They lump all the professing Christians together in one group and say, "Yeah, that's 'Christians' for ya."

When one preacher sells out the Book, it affects the whole Body of Jesus Christ. He influences some student; that student becomes a professor in a Christian College and affects whole classes; those students go out as ministers and cause their congregations not to believe the Book. The first thing you know, churches all across the nation have no authority left. Apostasy is infectious.

When one man gives way in the ranks, the whole rank waivers and eventually falls to pieces. I never played football in College (I was too little for football and too short for basketball), but I know enough about the game to realize that if the linemen don't hold the line, there is going to be trouble for the men in the backfield. So every time some preacher or professor at a Christian College sells out the Book and substitutes some other authority for it, he damages the Body of Christ.

["They have also transgressed my covenant . . . for they have even taken of the accursed thing."]{.class_s2FW} In the first ten chapters of Joshua, there are [ten]{.class_s2FX} cities the Israelites attack. Jericho is the first of those ten cities, and God told them that the gold, silver, brass, and iron of that first city belonged to [Him]{.class_s2FX} (6:19). Everything else was to be destroyed because it was [cursed]{.class_s2FX} (see our comments on 6:26). The Israelites were able to take the spoil from the other nine cities, but the spoil of that first city belonged to [God.]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cPS.xhtml_page_121} So what you are dealing with here is the [tithe,]{.class_s2FX} the [tenth]{.class_s2FX} (see our comments on Gen. 14:20 in that Commentary). Those Jews were commanded to give God ["the firstfruits"]{.class_s2FW} (Lev. 23:10), and that included ["the firstfruits"]{.class_s2FW} of their conquests when they took the land of Canaan. Jericho was the [firstfruits;]{.class_s2FX} it was the [tithe.]{.class_s2FX}

Leviticus 27:30 says, ["all the tithe of the land . . . is the LORD'S: it is holy unto the LORD."]{.class_s2FW} When Achan took part of the spoils, he took the Lord's tithe and fell under the curse of Malachi 3:8--9.

"Will a man rob God? Yet ye have robbed me. But ye say, Wherein have we robbed thee? In tithes and offerings. Ye are cursed with a curse: for ye have robbed me, even this whole nation."

Notice the word ["stolen"]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}in verse 11. [Achan robbed God]{.class_s2FX} (Mal. 3:9). He ["dissembled"]{.class_s2FW}; that is, he [hid]{.class_s2FX} it, he [concealed]{.class_s2FX} it. And he put it with his own stuff: he treated it as [his]{.class_s2FX} when it belonged to [God.]{.class_s2FX} But the fact that he hid it showed that he [knew]{.class_s2FX} he was doing wrong.

Verse 12: ["Therefore the children of Israel could not stand before their enemies . . . because they were accursed."]{.class_s2FW} Now technically speaking, no Christian is ["accursed"]{.class_s2FW} because Christ took our curse for us on the cross (Gal. 3:13), but a Christian can bring [condemnation]{.class_s2FX} on himself.

["For if ye live after the flesh, ye shall die"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:13).

["If any man defile the temple of God, him shall God destroy; for the temple of God is holy, which temple ye are"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 3:17).

["For he that eateth and drinketh unworthily ]{.class_s2FW}\[talking about the Lord's Supper\][, eateth and drinketh damnation to himself, not discerning the Lord's body. For this cause many are weak and sickly among you, and many sleep"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 11:29--30).

Back to Joshua 7:12---["Neither will I be with you any more, except ye destroy the accursed from among you."]{.class_s2FW} Again, not technically true of the Christian. The promise to the believer in Christ is:

["I will never leave thee, nor forsake thee"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 13:5).

["]{.class_s2FW}\[Nothing\][]{#cPS.xhtml_page_122}[ shall be able to separate us from the love of God, which is in Christ Jesus our Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:38).

["Being confident of this very thing, that he which hath begun a good work in you will perform it until the day of Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 1:6).

Once Jesus Christ comes to live in you in the person of the Holy Ghost, He [won't]{.class_s2FX} leave you; He will [always]{.class_s2FX} be ["with you."]{.class_s2FW} But you can [grieve]{.class_s2FX} the Holy Spirit (Eph. 4:30) to the point where you lose your [fellowship]{.class_s2FX} with the Lord and you lose the [power of God]{.class_s2FX} in your life. That's why you have to ["destroy the accursed from among you."]{.class_s2FW} Individually in the Christian life, that's mortifying the deeds of the flesh (Rom. 8:13). We are to ["lay aside . . . the sin which doth so easily beset us"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 12:1). Corporately in the church, that's delivering an unrepentant believer involved in gross sin over to ["Satan for the destruction of the flesh, that the spirit may be saved in the day of the Lord Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 5:5). That has to be done so that one sinning Christian doesn't bring down the whole congregation; it has to be done to make the sinning Christian realize the severity of what he is doing so he will repent, if he will, and be restored (2 Cor. 2:5--8).

Now how was ["the accursed"]{.class_s2FW} to be destroyed from among the children of Israel? The first thing was [sanctification:]{.class_s2FX} ["Up, sanctify the people, and say, Sanctify yourselves against to morrow"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 13). That involved the people [cleaning up]{.class_s2FX} (see Exod. 19:10). For the Christian, that involves [confession of sin ]{.class_s2FX}(1 John 1:9) and ["the washing of water BY THE WORD"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 5:26). It's getting in the Book and letting the Holy Spirit use the word of God to clean you up on the inside.

The second part of destroying ["the accursed"]{.class_s2FW} was the Lord showing the whole congregation publicly who ["the accursed"]{.class_s2FW} was. This is a form of drawing the lot (as in a "lottery"). Representatives of all twelve tribes step forward, and the [tribe]{.class_s2FX} of the cursed individual is chosen. Then representatives of the families in the tribes step forward, and the [family]{.class_s2FX} is chosen. Then the individual [household]{.class_s2FX} in the family is chosen. And finally the individual who sinned is picked out of the household.

That's a picture of how things will run at the judgment. God calls []{#cPS.xhtml_page_123}out a nation to be judged, then a family out of that nation, then a household from that family, and finally the individuals in that household. "The nation of England step forward. The family of the Tudors come forth. The house of Henry VIII, you are up. Bloody Mary, you are first." That's how it will go.

Notice in verse 15 that it is not just the man who is burnt; it is ["all that he hath."]{.class_s2FW} It is the man himself, his family, and all his possessions. The fellow brings a curse on everything he has. It's a good thing we are not living under the Law now.

16 So Joshua rose up early in the morning, and brought Israel by their tribes; and the tribe of Judah was taken:

17 And he brought the family of Judah; and he took the family of the Zarhites: and he brought the family of the Zarhites man by man; and Zabdi was taken:

18 And he brought his household man by man; and Achan, the son of Carmi, the son of Zabdi, the son of Zerah, of the tribe of Judah, was taken.

19 And Joshua said unto Achan, My son, give, I pray thee, glory to the LORD God of Israel, and make confession unto him; and tell me now what thou hast done; hide it not from me.

20 And Achan answered Joshua, and said, Indeed I have sinned against the LORD God of Israel, and thus and thus have I done:

21 When I saw among the spoils a goodly Babylonish garment, and two hundred shekels of silver, and a wedge of gold of fifty shekels weight, then I coveted them, and took them; and, behold, they are hid in the earth in the midst of my tent, and the silver under it.

Now you can imagine how Achan felt standing there while his [tribe]{.class_s2FX} was taken, his [family]{.class_s2FX} was taken, and his father's [household]{.class_s2FX} was taken. I mean, he had a guilty conscience, knowing he stole and hid the stuff that belonged to God. He must have been sweating bullets as Joshua got closer to picking [him]{.class_s2FX} out of a crowd of 600,000 men.

There are two important lessons you can learn from verses 16--18. The first is: []{#cPS.xhtml_page_124}["The eyes of the LORD are in every place, beholding the evil and the good"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 15:3). There's no hiding anything from God. Jonah tried hiding in the bowels of a ship headed in the opposite direction from where God wanted him to go; it didn't work. David tried hiding his adultery by having Uriah killed, and the prophet stuck his finger right in David's face and said, ["Thou art the man"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 12:7). That Bible says, ["Thou hast set our iniquities before thee, our secret sins in the light of thy countenance"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 90:8).

The second lesson from this passage for the Christian is: ["So then every one of us shall give account of himself to God"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 14:12). That's not just written to lost people; Paul includes himself in the accounting. The context is the Judgment Seat of Christ (Rom. 14:10), and the Judgment Seat of Christ involves a [burning]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 3:13--15). Of course, unlike Achan, the Christian himself doesn't burn (1 Cor. 3:15), but the works of the flesh that brought condemnation on him do (Gal. 5:19--21 cf. Rom. 8:13).

Verse 19: ["And Joshua said unto Achan, My son, give, I pray thee, glory to the LORD God of Israel ]{.class_s2FW}\
[. . . ."]{.class_s2FW} Why? Because He's [omniscient]{.class_s2FX} (all-knowing); because He's the great Judge. In a court of law, the judge is addressed as "Your Honor." Even the criminals call him that, and if they don't, they are condemned on the charge of "contempt of court." If a human judge is granted such honor and glory, how much more so ["the Judge of all the earth."]{.class_s2FW}

[". . . and make confession unto him."]{.class_s2FW} Proverbs 28:13 says, ["He that covereth his sins shall not prosper: but whoso confesseth and forsaketh them shall have mercy."]{.class_s2FW} Achan covered his sin, literally---with [dirt.]{.class_s2FX} As a result, he didn't ["prosper."]{.class_s2FW} The silver, gold, and garment didn't profit him anything at all; in fact, he lost [everything]{.class_s2FX} because of them. The problem into which we are about to run, though, is that Achan confesses his sin, but if any ["mercy"]{.class_s2FW} was shown to him, it is certainly not evident in the text. Sometimes the confession comes too late; it did with Saul in 1 Samuel 15:24. Sometimes it is made with the wrong motives and ulterior plans in mind; that was the case with Balaam in Numbers 22:34 and Pharaoh in Exodus 9:27, 10:16. Sometimes confession is made to the wrong party; Judas confessed to a [priest]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cPS.xhtml_page_125} (Matt. 27:3--4).

In Achan's case, the confession came too late: he didn't confess till he was caught red-handed. But there was something more, for David didn't confess his adultery and murder until he was caught. David found mercy, unlike Achan. Achan was warned ahead of time that his sin would bring a curse on himself and Israel (6:18), and no amount of confession could lift that curse. We can only speculate as to any spiritual mercy he was shown for his confession, but as for the physical consequences of his curse, there was no mercy afforded him.

Now that was Old Testament, under the Law. In the New Testament, confession of sin is a condition of [fellowship,]{.class_s2FX} not [salvation.]{.class_s2FX} You can confess your sins to a Roman Catholic Priest all you want, and all it will do is wind you up in Hell like Judas Iscariot (Acts 1:25 cf. Matt. 27:3--5). Salvation has nothing to do with confession of sin, not even to [God.]{.class_s2FX} Salvation is conditioned on confessing Jesus Christ as your Saviour by faith (Rom. 10:9--10). [After salvation,]{.class_s2FX} confession of sin to restore fellowship with God is only made possible by the blood shed by the Lord Jesus Christ on the cross (1 John 1:7--9).

Verse 20: ["And Achan answered Joshua, and said, Indeed I have sinned against the LORD God of Israel."]{.class_s2FW} Two things about Achan's confession here: First, notice that Achan acknowledges that he sinned against [God.]{.class_s2FX} Do you know why that part of the confession is so important? Because Mohammed and "Allah" in the [Koran]{.class_s2FX} say it's a [lie.]{.class_s2FX} Sura 4:111 says, "And whoever commits a sin, he only commits it AGAINST HIS OWN SOUL." Whoever "the god" was (that's what the word [Allah]{.class_s2FX} means---"the god"), he certainly was not the God who wrote the Bible. In the [Holy Bible]{.class_s2FX} (not the ["Noble Koran"]{.class_s2FX}), sin is against [God.]{.class_s2FX} Joseph is worried about sinning against [God]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 39:9). David confessed, ["I have sinned against the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 12:13). The prodigal said, ["I have sinned against heaven"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 15:21). Even backslidden Jews like the ones in 1 Samuel 7:6 and Hell-bound pagans like Pharaoh in Exodus 10:16 had enough sense to realize they sinned against God. Only someone as stupid as Allah, "Gabriel" (the 600-winged demon who dictated the [Koran]{.class_s2FX} to Mohammed, [not]{.class_s2FX} the angel who appeared to Zacharias []{#cPS.xhtml_page_126}and Mary in Luke 1), and Mohammed wouldn't know that sin is against God. You might do yourself or someone else wrong, and the Bible certainly does use the phrase ["sinned against"]{.class_s2FW} in that respect from a [practical]{.class_s2FX} point of view (see Judg. 11:27; 1 Sam. 19:4, 24:11). But [theologically]{.class_s2FX} and [doctrinally]{.class_s2FX} speaking, for sin to be "sin," it has to be against God, because ["sin is the transgression of the law"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 3:4)---[God's ]{.class_s2FX}Law.

The second thing about Achan's confession in verse 20 is that you can't always tell what a man means when he says, "I have sinned." He might not mean "I want to get right with the Lord" at all. Here, Achan said, ["I have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} because he was caught red-handed. What else could he do? When Pharaoh said ["I have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} in Exodus 9:27, 10:16, what he meant was: "I am sick and tired of these plagues; now get off my back." When Saul said ["I have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Sam. 15:30), he meant: "Let me go on being King as if nothing ever happened." When Balaam said ["I have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 22:34), what he actually meant was: "Please don't kill me." I mean, the Angel of the Lord was standing right there in the way with a drawn sword ready to take off his head (Num. 22:31). When Judas said ["I have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 27:4), all he meant was: "I betrayed an innocent man, and my conscience is killing me over it."

Of course, not all confessions of sin in the Bible are like that. When the prodigal said, ["I have sinned"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 15:18--21), he intended to go home where he belonged and make things right with daddy. When David said ["Against thee, thee only, have I sinned, and done this evil in thy sight"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 51:4), he was down on his face getting right with God.

Brethren, the Lord knows what a man means when he says "I have sinned." I have the testimony of a Limey in World War I who got caught in the artillery zone between his own side and the Germans. He was lying there on his face in the mud, seeing pieces of men blown every place all around him. He said he confessed to God everything he could think of, and he said that all the time he was doing that, he had no intention of stopping any of it. He was just trying to cut a deal with God to save his worthless hide. His saying "I have sinned" didn't carry any weight. The Lord knows when the confession is real and when it isn't.

Verse 21 is one of the passages in the Scriptures that gives you the progression of sin. Another one is James 1:15. The progression of sin is first [presentation;]{.class_s2FX} here, ["when I SAW among the spoils."]{.class_s2FW} The next step is [illumination:]{.class_s2FX} the Holy Spirit gives light on the temptation on whether it is right or wrong. Achan had that illumination back in 6:18--19.

So far, so good. Sin does not come with the presentation or the illumination. Where sin enters is when you [debate]{.class_s2FX} the matter in your mind: should I do it or should I not? Debate shows a degree of [unbelief]{.class_s2FX} in the light God has given you on the matter. Debate is trying to figure out whether you can commit the sin with little or no consequences. Debate is where sin enters. I guarantee you that when Achan saw that beautiful Babylonian garment, that sack of silver, and that wedge of gold that he thought to himself, "Man, it's a shame I have to burn that nice coat. And look at all that money. All they ever talk about down at the Tabernacle is money, money, money. I can think of a few things I could spend that money on instead of those priests down at the Tabernacle." That's the kind of stuff that went through Achan's head. Sin enters with [debate.]{.class_s2FX}

Achan [looked;]{.class_s2FX} then he [coveted.]{.class_s2FX} The term is ["lust"]{.class_s2FW} in James 1:15---["Then when lust hath conceived, it bringeth forth sin."]{.class_s2FW} The sin Achan's lust brought forth was [theft]{.class_s2FX} (["then I coveted them, and took them"]{.class_s2FW}). And just like James 1:15 says, Achan's lust and sin lead to his [death]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 25).

There is an interesting cross-reference to the ["wedge of gold"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 21. It is found in Isaiah 13:12.

"I will make a man more precious than fine gold; even a MAN than the GOLDEN WEDGE of Ophir."

There, certain men are compared to [gold.]{.class_s2FX} The first time gold shows up in your Bible, it is connected to the place where [man was created]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 2:7--12). When you get to the end of Revelation, you find a city (the New Jerusalem) of ["pure gold"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 21:18, 21). That city is called ["the bride, the Lamb's wife"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 21:9--10). Why, in Ephesians 5:25--32, ["the Lamb's wife"]{.class_s2FW} is the [Church,]{.class_s2FX} the Body of Jesus Christ made up of [saved believers]{.class_s2FX} in this age. But if I were to tell you that in the resurrection in Eternity, your glorified body would be made of [living gold,]{.class_s2FX} some of the brethren would []{#cPS.xhtml_page_128}"blow a gasket" over "Ruckman's peculiar doctrines," so we will leave the discussion right there.

22 So Joshua sent messengers, and they ran unto the tent; and, behold, it was hid in his tent, and the silver under it.

23 And they took them out of the midst of the tent, and brought them unto Joshua, and unto all the children of Israel, and laid them out before the LORD.

24 And Joshua, and all Israel with him, took Achan the son of Zerah, and the silver, and the garment, and the wedge of gold, and his sons, and his daughters, and his oxen, and his asses, and his sheep, and his tent, and all that he had: and they brought them unto the valley of Achor.

25 And Joshua said, Why hast thou troubled us? the LORD shall trouble thee this day. And all Israel stoned him with stones, and burned them with fire, after they had stoned them with stones.

26 And they raised over him a great heap of stones unto this day. So the LORD turned from the fierceness of his anger. Wherefore the name of that place was called, The valley of Achor, unto this day.

Now the Babylonian garment and the wedge of gold were buried in the ground under Achan's tent, with the silver underneath them. Joshua sends some men to retrieve the stuff, and they bring it back and lay it out ["before the LORD"]{.class_s2FW}; that is, before the Ark or the Tabernacle. The gold and silver don't go into the Lord's treasury, though, as was originally intended, because now they are cursed. So they are taken, along with the garment, Achan, his family, and all his possessions, and are burned right along with everything else, and are buried under a heap of stones.

Verse 24 shows you that when Israel crossed over Jordan, more than just the 600,000 armed men crossed over. The [families]{.class_s2FX} of the nine-and-a-half tribes that would receive their inheritance in Canaan came over as well. So nearly a million-and-a-half people cross over Jordan on dry ground. A landslide (see our remarks under 3:13)?! Go []{#cPS.xhtml_page_129}kid your grandmother; we have better sense.

Now there are a couple of important lessons here. First, ["the love of money is the root of all evil"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:10). That has been changed in all the new "Bibles" to ["the love of money is a root of all kinds of evil."]{.class_s2FX} The excuse is that the definite article is not there in Greek. Of course, that is a "red herring" to get you to overlook the fact that [all]{.class_s2FX} translations add definite articles that aren't in the original Greek and Hebrew. You take 1 Corinthians 2:16---["But we have the mind of Christ."]{.class_s2FW} Why, there's no definite article in front of the Greek word for ["mind"]{.class_s2FW} ([noun]{.class_s2FX}), yet every translation adds one. Why? Because it would be nonsense to say "we have A mind of Christ." So don't accept the word of these hypocrites who will criticize the [King James]{.class_s2FX} for doing something and then turn right around and do the same thing themselves.

[In this age,]{.class_s2FX} ["the love of money is the root of all evil."]{.class_s2FW} That ["love of money"]{.class_s2FW} starts out in the Old Testament as the sin of [covetousness,]{.class_s2FX} and that sin certainly [is]{.class_s2FX} ["the root of all evil."]{.class_s2FW} The Devil started out [coveting]{.class_s2FX} the throne of God, and that covetousness turned into [pride,]{.class_s2FX} thinking he could actually do it. Covetousness is the basic root sin, and ["the love of money"]{.class_s2FW} springs from covetousness. Paul says, ["covetousness . . . is idolatry"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 3:5); that's because you are putting something you desire in the place of God and what God said. That's what Achan did.

The second important lesson here is that sin affects [innocents.]{.class_s2FX} Not only did 36 men die because of Achan's sin, Achan caused the death of his wife, his children, and his beasts also. Achan's sin affected people who had nothing to do with it: it affected the [congregation]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 13), it affected the [spiritual leader]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 7), and it affected Achan's [family]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 24).

But the most important lesson that we learn from this passage is that sin committed should be [judged]{.class_s2FX} and [confessed,]{.class_s2FX} not hidden away. The New Testament commentary on this point is: ["if we would judge ourselves, we should not be judged"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 11:31). If you don't want the Lord to judge you, you had better take care of the thing yourself.

Verse 25:[ "And Joshua said, Why hast thou troubled us? the LORD shall trouble thee this day."]{.class_s2FW} The word ["Achor"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. []{#cPS.xhtml_page_130}24) means "trouble." Over in 1 Chronicles 2:7, Achan is called ["Achar, the troubler of Israel"]{.class_s2FW}; ["Achar"]{.class_s2FW} means "troubler."

["And all Israel stoned him with stones, and burned them with fire, after they had stoned them with stones."]{.class_s2FW} Rough chapter. That's capital punishment for [stealing.]{.class_s2FX} The Old Testament prescribed capital punishment for more than just murder. There was capital punishment for adultery, for sexual perversion, for incorrigible disobedience to and disrespect for one's parents, for idolatry, and for involvement in the occult. If the whole Law were applied to America today, you wouldn't be able to travel from your home to your job without stepping on dead bodies.

Now there are a couple of reasons the punishment is so severe. The first is to show you just how [holy]{.class_s2FX} God is. Americans think God is akin to Santa Claus or a doting grandfather: all He wants to do is good to you, and He would never punish you for your sin, at least not in Hell. Listen, God is so holy that He would give you capital punishment for stealing fruit off a tree (Gen. 3). ["The wages of sin is death"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:23).

Second, God judged Achan's sin so severely because it made Israel's motive for conquering the land look suspect. The heathen looking at what Achan did would say that the Israelites were just marauders coming into the land to steal and pillage, like the barbarian tribes did to Rome or like what the Vikings did to England. No [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} purpose would be ascribed to the Israelites conquering the land; God would have nothing to do with it.

One of the reasons God didn't let His people take the spoils from Jericho was to show the heathen there in Canaan that He didn't call the Jews out of Egypt to steal somebody else's property. The conquest of the land of Canaan was divine judgment against the gross sins being committed by the heathen there (see our remarks in the Introduction). Jericho illustrated both the spiritual motive and power behind the conquest of the land, and the severity of the judgment against Achan's sin put the quietus on the heathen ascribing the motive to covetousness.

Now that is something to keep in mind in Christian work. What is the motivation for [more]{.class_s2FX} land, [more]{.class_s2FX} buildings,[ more]{.class_s2FX} TV or radio stations, etc.? You have to make sure that the motive is not the []{#cPS.xhtml_page_131}almighty dollar, because the world won't hesitate to judge you as mercenary in such matters. Christian work should be done in such a way that nobody can legitimately question its motivation.

Verse 26: ["And they raised over him a great heap of stones unto this day."]{.class_s2FW} A mound of stones was raised over the charred remains of Achan, his family, his beasts, and his goods. Years later at the end of the book of Joshua, anybody walking by could see that pile of rocks and remember why it was there and be warned not to covet and steal from God.

The pile of stones over Achan should be set in contrast with the pile of stones brought up from the River Jordan back in chapter 4 (see our remarks in that chapter). Those stones hauled out of the Jordan and stacked up on the bank signified death to the old life and resurrection to a new life. The stones piled over Achan are a picture that the old life should have been left dead and buried at the bottom of the Jordan, and shouldn't have been up parading around coveting this and coveting that. The New Testament commentary on this is Romans 8:13.

"For if ye live after the flesh, ye shall die: but if ye through the Spirit do mortify the deeds of the body, ye shall live."

Back to Joshua 7:26---["So the LORD turned from the fierceness of his anger. Wherefore the name of that place was called, The valley of Achor, unto this day."]{.class_s2FW} In fact, it's known as ["The valley of Achor"]{.class_s2FW} all the way up until 740 B.C., and although some of those Bible names for places have been lost through the passage of time, the Lord hasn't forgotten about them. You see, there are two other passages of Scripture that deal with this valley; both are connected with the [restoration of Israel at the Second Advent.]{.class_s2FX}

["Thus saith the LORD, As the new wine is found in the cluster, and one saith, Destroy it not; for a blessing is in it: so will I do for my servants' sakes, that I may not destroy them all. And I will bring forth a seed out of Jacob, and out of Judah an inheritor of my mountains; and mine elect shall inherit it, and my servants shall dwell there. And Sharon shall be a fold of flocks, and THE VALLEY OF []{#cPS.xhtml_page_132}ACHOR a place for the herds to lie down in, for my people that have sought me"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 65:8--10).

["Therefore, behold, I will allure her ]{.class_s2FW}\[talking about the nation of Israel that had been put away by God\][, and bring her into the wilderness, and speak comfortably unto her. And I will give her her vineyards from thence, and THE VALLEY OF ACHOR for a door of hope: and she shall sing there, as in the days of her youth, and as in the day when she came up out of the land of Egypt.]{.class_s2FW} \[When does that happen? Look at the next verse\][ And it shall be at THAT DAY]{.class_s2FW} \[a reference to the Second Advent---see Isa. 2:11, 17, 4:2, 10:20, 27, 11:10--11\][, saith the LORD, that thou shalt call me Ishi, and shalt call me no more Baali"]{.class_s2FW} (Hos. 2:14--16).

So in the place where a terrible judgment was executed to turn the Lord ["from the fierceness of his anger,"]{.class_s2FW} Israel will receive a blessing when Christ returns at the Second Advent. The Lord is able to take the worst circumstance and make something good out of it. The spiritual application to the born-again child of God is Romans 8:28.

"And we know that all things work together for good to them that love God, to them who are the called according to his purpose."

[]{#cUM.xhtml}

# Chapter 8 {.heading_s2B}

8:1 And the LORD said unto Joshua, Fear not, neither be thou dismayed: take all the people of war with thee, and arise, go up to Ai: see, I have given into thy hand the king of Ai, and his people, and his city, and his land:

2 And thou shalt do to Ai and her king as thou didst unto Jericho and her king: only the spoil thereof, and the cattle thereof, shall ye take for a prey unto yourselves: lay thee an ambush for the city behind it.

["And the LORD said unto Joshua"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1). Joshua has learned his lesson from chapter 7. Notice verse 3: ["So Joshua arose."]{.class_s2FW} Joshua is back on his face in prayer, getting his battle plan from the Lord. He's not presuming on God's grace and past victories like he did before at Ai (see our comments on 7:3). The lesson for you as a Christian is if you got your backside burned over something, don't jump into the same mess again. Be more cautious the next time and [pray]{.class_s2FX} about it for a while.

["Fear not, neither be thou dismayed."]{.class_s2FW} Sin once judged should be [forgotten.]{.class_s2FX} Joshua and the people had been through a terrible judgment on sin and had taken care of it. Now the Lord says, "OK; it's time to move on."

The trouble with some folks is that they live in the past. They dwell on something that happened five, ten, and even 25 years ago. There are Christians who get in a scuffle with the brethren and get hurt, and they sit down and don't do anything for the Lord from that point on. The thing to do is don't be dismayed over something that has happened in the past. If the sin has been confessed and judged, get up and [go on.]{.class_s2FX}

The Apostle Paul said, ["forgetting those things which are behind, and reaching forth unto those things which are before, I press toward the mark for the prize of the high calling of God in Christ Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 3:13--14).

Notice in verse 2 that the people were allowed to keep the spoil of Ai. Jericho was the "firstfruits" of their conquest; it was the []{#cUM.xhtml_page_134}"tithe"; it belonged to God (see our remarks under 7:11). After that, they were allowed to keep the spoils of the cities they conquered. If Achan had only waited, he could have had all he could carry off.

Christians are always worried about whether the tithe is for the New Testament believer or not, and I have discussed that under Malachi 3:8 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class_s2FX} Volume II. What they are really looking for when they bring up the subject is an excuse [not]{.class_s2FX} to tithe. But there is a more important principle to courageous giving than just giving 10% of your income. The principle is found in Proverbs 3:9.

"Honour the LORD with thy substance, and with the firstfruits of all thine increase."

The first part of whatever you get belongs to God. There are all kinds of alibis used to get out of that: "I'm in debt"; "Shouldn't I pay my bills off first"; etc. But I am here to tell you, by experience, that if you want God's blessing, if you want Him to take care of you when you need it, then you had better give Him ["the firstfruits of all thine increase."]{.class_s2FW}

I learned that the hard way. Before I was saved, I was tithing to the Catholic Church. After I trusted Christ, I figured I didn't need to tithe anymore since I wasn't trying to work my way to Heaven. I went off to school in Greenville and used all the alibis for not tithing: "I have to pay my school bill"; "I need milk for the babies"; "I have to pay the rent." Things got so lean, though, that I had to send the wife and kids back to the farm in Alabama because I had no money to buy food.

Things got so bad that I had nothing to eat for three days. Finally I found some old pancake flour the previous tenant had left in the back of a cupboard. I mixed it with water and made a blue paste and ate it. It made me sick. But that's when the Lord convicted me about tithing.

I decided then that no matter what, I would give the Lord the first tenth of whatever I got. I had a little cup in which I put the money. If I got five dollars, I would put fifty cents in the cup. When I started doing that, the Lord started blessing, and somebody left a couple of sacks of groceries on my doorstep. Soon I was able to bring the wife and kids back, and everything was fine. So I have been []{#cUM.xhtml_page_135}where you have been, and I speak as a fool (I mean, the Devil can always get in there to test your faith like he did with Job), but I can tell you from looking back over my life, that if you put the Lord first, the end will come out right.

3 So Joshua arose, and all the people of war, to go up against Ai: and Joshua chose out thirty thousand mighty men of valour, and sent them away by night.

4 And he commanded them, saying, Behold, ye shall lie in wait against the city, even behind the city: go not very far from the city, but be ye all ready:

5 And I, and all the people that are with me, will approach unto the city: and it shall come to pass, when they come out against us, as at the first, that we will flee before them,

6 (For they will come out after us) till we have drawn them from the city; for they will say, They flee before us, as at the first: therefore we will flee before them.

7 Then ye shall rise up from the ambush, and seize upon the city: for the LORD your God will deliver it into your hand.

8 And it shall be, when ye have taken the city, that ye shall set the city on fire: according to the commandment of the LORD shall ye do. See, I have commanded you.

9 Joshua therefore sent them forth: and they went to lie in ambush, and abode between Bethel and Ai, on the west side of Ai: but Joshua lodged that night among the people.

Now the Lord commands Joshua to set an ambush from behind Ai (vs. 2). Joshua stages a direct assault on the city so he can feign a retreat to draw all the men of Ai out. The ambushment would then invade the city and set it on fire to cut off the retreat of Ai's army to their fortress when Joshua turns and counterattacks.

A problem presents itself, though, involving the number of Israelites in the main assault and the number of men in the ambushment.

Verses 3--5 say, ["and Joshua chose out thirty thousand []{#cUM.xhtml_page_136}mighty men of valour, and sent them away by night. And commanded THEM, saying, Behold, YE shall lie in wait against the city, even behind the city . . . And I, and all the people that are with me, will approach unto the city."]{.class_s2GF}

Verses 11--13 say, ["And all the people, even the people of war that were with him ]{.class_s2FW}\[i.e., Joshua---vs. 12\][, went up, and drew nigh, and came before the city, and pitched on the north side of Ai . . . And he took about five thousand men, and set them to lie in ambush between Bethel and Ai, on the west side of the city. And when they had set the people, even all the host that was on the north of the city, and their liers in wait on the west of the city."]{.class_s2FW}

So were there 30,000 ["liers in wait,"]{.class_s2FW} or were there 5,000? Were they ["behind the city"]{.class_s2FW} or ["west of the city"]{.class_s2FW}?

There are three basic ways of handling the problem. The first is that of the "good, godly" Conservative and Fundamental [Bible correctors,]{.class_s2FX} and it is absolutely typical of such apostates.

Being too stupid (or infidelic) to deal with the passages as they stand, they drop back to the old chestnut that verse 3 is a "scribal error." Going to the "original Hebrew" does you no good at all, for it too says 30,000 in verse 3. The "original Hebrew" means nothing to these apostates; when necessary, they will change it just as quick as they will change the [AV]{.class_s2FX} text.

The second view is more faithful to the text, but it is not without its problems. It says that the 30,000 men of verse 3 were the total force sent against Ai. Out of those 30,000, ["about five thousand men"]{.class_s2FW} were sent to ambush Ai. The remaining 25,000 were the main assault force that drew the men of Ai out of their city. Verse 13 seems to support this by saying ["THEIR]{.class_s2FW} \[i.e., the main host's\][ liers in wait."]{.class_s2FW}

The problem with this view is that in Joshua's instructions to the ambushment in verse 4, the antecedent to ["them"]{.class_s2FW} and ["ye"]{.class_s2FW} is the ["thirty thousand mighty men of valour"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 3. They are distinguished from Joshua and the main force in verse 5. But it is a [possibility]{.class_s2FX} if you take verses 4--5 as Joshua briefing both groups together as to God's plan.

I think there are [two separate groups]{.class_s2FX} in verses 3 and 12. Why []{#cUM.xhtml_page_137}would that be? Look at verse 17.

"And there was not a man left in Ai or BETHEL, that went not out after Israel."

The ambushment lay in wait between Ai and Bethel, and the men of Bethel joined in the attack on the main host of Israel. The 5,000 additional men could have been reinforcements in case the men of Bethel discovered ["the liers in wait"]{.class_s2FW} and attacked them before they invaded Ai.

Also, though the details aren't given in Joshua, at some point the Israelites took Bethel as well (12:16). If Bethel were taken at the same time as Ai, the 5,000 men could have been part of the force that ambushed Bethel while the rest of the 30,000 men ambushed Ai.

As far as ["behind the city"]{.class_s2FW} and ["on the west side of the city,"]{.class_s2FW} ["behind"]{.class_s2FW} describes the relation of the ambushment to the main gate, and ["west"]{.class_s2FW} describes the relation of the ambushment to Bethel (vs. 12). If the main gate of Ai was on the north side from which Joshua and the main host attacked, ["the liers in wait"]{.class_s2FW} would have been on the southwest side of the city; that is, [behind]{.class_s2FX} it and to the [west]{.class_s2FX} of it.

Back to verse 3:[ "and Joshua chose out thirty thousand mighty men of valour, and sent them away by night."]{.class_s2FW} The men chosen for the ambushment are not just the rank and file ["people of war"]{.class_s2FW}; they are the elite "special forces" (Seals, Rangers, Green Berets, Delta Force). They are sent under cover of darkness to their position until Joshua draws out the men of Ai.

The plan is for Joshua and the main host to retreat before the men of Ai as the Israelis did back in 7:4 so that the men of Ai will pursue them as they did in 7:5. You talk about humiliating, boy! Because of Achan's sin and his own lack of prayer previously, Joshua now has to act like a coward and run before his enemies---that after the great victory at Jericho!

It is important to note that although God gives Joshua the battle plan for taking Ai, there is no supernatural intervention this time as there was at Jericho. The further you go in the Christian life, the fewer supernatural manifestations you will experience (see our remarks under 5:10--12). As you mature as a Christian, life becomes more and more of just trusting God and doing what He tells you in []{#cUM.xhtml_page_138}His Book.

Brethren, the life of faith isn't sitting around waiting for God to work a miracle for you. It is [believing]{.class_s2FX} and [doing]{.class_s2FX} what you read in the Scriptures and trusting God to provide for your needs as you do. That is the theme of a book entitled [The Silence of God]{.class_s2FX} by the British Bible teacher Sir Robert Anderson. Every Christian should get that book and read it. Anderson argues that in this "day of grace," God has pulled back from new revelation and supernatural intervention to get His children to live by faith in the written revelation He has given them. The rule for the child of God in this age is: ["Whatsoever is not of faith is sin"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 14:23).

It's taking life one day at a time with nothing but a Book to guide you. I know it's a drag, man. You want to pray and have God open the heavens for you; you want visions and angels flying around and an ecstatic feeling that gives you goose pimples. That's not the way it works, though. Once in a while you will get in a service where the Spirit is thick, but not often. That being the case, the best advice I can give you to get you through the day-to-day grind comes from Bob Jones Sr.: "The best preparation for tomorrow is to do what you ought to do today." There is no miraculous, sudden provision of your daily needs if you are disobeying God. If you are lazy and don't work, don't expect God to miraculously fill your refrigerator with food and pay all your bills.

["For they will come after us) . . . for they will say, They flee before us, as at the first"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). This time, it is the men of Ai who are proud, arrogant, and overconfident. They figured they would rout the Israeli army as they had before. They didn't figure that their previous victory was God punishing His people for their sin; they thought they had the better fighting force. They took Joshua's "bait" hook, line, and sinker.

["Then ye shall rise up from the ambush, and seize upon the city: for the LORD your God will deliver it into your hand"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 7). Notice, here, the two elements of [faith]{.class_s2FX} and [works.]{.class_s2FX} The faith was believing God would deliver the city to them; they had to take God at His word on the outcome of the battle. But while they were believing that, they had to implement a standard military tactic. It took [both]{.class_s2FX} to take Ai.

Another lesson we learn from the passage here is that sometimes you may have to strategically yield ground in order to gain it back. It is not a compromise if you are not yielding to temptation (especially the temptation to protect or advance yourself) or yielding to the Devil. You are temporarily yielding so you can gain footing and attack again, which is a proper military tactic. That is the principle behind the martial art of Aikido: you use a man's force against him.

That is a good tactic to use in soulwinning. If a lost man says, "I suppose you think you are good enough to get to Heaven," you go with the blow and reply, "No, as a matter of fact, I'm not; I would be just as good as dead and in Hell if it weren't for Jesus Christ." If a fellow gives you the excuse, "I can't live it," you give in to what he says and come back with: "You're right; you can't live it. Nobody can. That's why Jesus Christ lived it for you." You retreat just far enough to trap the sinner in his own words.

Verse 8: ["according to the commandment of the LORD shall ye do."]{.class_s2FW} Unlike what happened back in 7:3--4, the Israelites are back operating under ["the commandment of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} instead of the [advice of men.]{.class_s2FX} So this time, the attack is going to work. The application for the Christian is that he is to conduct himself according to what he reads in [the Book;]{.class_s2FX} not what he gets from Rick Warren, Robert Schuller, Joel Osteen, Rob Bell, Brian McLaren, Doug Pagitt, Liberty University, Hyles-Anderson College, Pensacola Christian College, Crown College, Tennessee Temple University, Bob Jones University, Moody Bible Institute, [Sword of the Lord, Christianity Today,]{.class_s2FX} Trinity Broadcasting Network, or denominational headquarters. Where they go by the Book, fine; but where they don't, drop them in "File 13" where they belong.

10 And Joshua rose up early in the morning, and numbered the people, and went up, he and the elders of Israel, before the people to Ai.

11 And all the people, even the people of war that were with him, went up, and drew nigh, and came before the city, and pitched on the north side of Ai: now there was a valley between them and Ai.

12 And he took about five thousand men, and set them to lie in ambush between Bethel and Ai, on the west side of the city.

13 And when they had set the people, even all the host that was on the north of the city, and their liers in wait on the west of the city, Joshua went that night into the midst of the valley.

14 And it came to pass, when the king of Ai saw it, that they hasted and rose up early, and the men of the city went out against Israel to battle, he and all his people, at a time appointed, before the plain; but he wist not that there were liers in ambush against him behind the city.

15 And Joshua and all Israel made as if they were beaten before them, and fled by the way of the wilderness.

16 And all the people that were in Ai were called together to pursue after them: and they pursued after Joshua, and were drawn away from the city.

17 And there was not a man left in Ai or Bethel, that went not out after Israel: and they left the city open, and pursued after Israel.

18 And the LORD said unto Joshua, Stretch out the spear that is in thy hand toward Ai; for I will give it into thine hand. And Joshua stretched out the spear that he had in his hand toward the city.

19 And the ambush arose quickly out of their place, and they ran as soon as he had stretched out his hand: and they entered into the city, and took it, and hasted and set the city on fire.

20 And when the men of Ai looked behind them, they saw, and, behold, the smoke of the city ascended up to heaven, and they had no power to flee this way or that way: and the people that fled to the wilderness turned back upon the pursuers.

21 And when Joshua and all Israel saw that the ambush had taken the city, and that the smoke of the city ascended, then they turned again, and slew the men of Ai.

22 And the other issued out of the city against them; so []{#cUM.xhtml_page_141}they were in the midst of Israel, some on this side, and some on that side: and they smote them, so that they let none of them remain or escape.

23 And the king of Ai they took alive, and brought him to Joshua.

24 And it came to pass, when Israel had made an end of slaying all the inhabitants of Ai in the field, in the wilderness wherein they chased them, and when they were all fallen on the edge of the sword, until they were consumed, that all the Israelites returned unto Ai, and smote it with the edge of the sword.

25 And so it was, that all that fell that day, both of men and women, were twelve thousand, even all the men of Ai.

26 For Joshua drew not his hand back, wherewith he stretched out the spear, until he had utterly destroyed all the inhabitants of Ai.

27 Only the cattle and the spoil of that city Israel took for a prey unto themselves, according unto the word of the LORD which he commanded Joshua.

28 And Joshua burnt Ai, and made it an heap for ever, even a desolation unto this day.

29 And the king of Ai he hanged on a tree until eventide: and as soon as the sun was down, Joshua commanded that they should take his carcase down from the tree, and cast it at the entering of the gate of the city, and raise thereon a great heap of stones, that remaineth unto this day.

Verse 3 says Joshua sent the first 30,000 men ["to lie in ambush" "by night"]{.class_s2FW} (cf. vs. 9). While they were doing that, ["Joshua lodged that night among the people"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 9). Verse 10 says, ["Joshua rose up early in the morning, and numbered the people"]{.class_s2FW}; he then sent 5,000 more men ["to lie in ambush"]{.class_s2FW} in addition to the first 30,000 (vs. 12) and set the main host on the north side of the city (vs. 11). But verse 13 says that after he had done this ["early in the morning"]{.class_s2FW} that ["Joshua went THAT NIGHT into the midst of the valley"]{.class_s2FW} that was between the main host and Ai (vs. 13 cf. vs. 11).

Now this can be confusing to modern readers unfamiliar with military tactics used against walled fortresses. Such attacks were often launched in the pre-dawn hours of the morning because it is generally the darkest part of the night; Santa Anna attacked the Alamo around 5:30 in the morning. The ["early in the morning"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 10 is during the morning watch of the Old Testament, which was between 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. (Judg. 7:19 cf. Luke 12:38). Most of the "morning watch" was [at night.]{.class_s2FX}

["And Joshua . . . went up, he and the elders of Israel, before the people to Ai"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 10). That's the "Supreme Commander"---the top General---and his "staff" leading the attack. They're not at the rear echelon directing the action; they're right up on the front lines.

In the spiritual warfare of the Christian, "the Captain of your salvation" (Heb. 2:10) is leading in the fight. I know it doesn't seem that way sometimes, but He's not just up in Heaven at the Father's right hand telling you what to do. [He's in your body,]{.class_s2FX} in the person of His Holy Spirit (Col. 1:27 cf. 1 Cor. 6:19). He said, ["Follow me"]{.class_s2FW} (see our comments on Luke 5:27 in that Commentary), which means He's out in front, leading in the attack.

If you are a pastor or spiritual leader in your local church (an elder---see 1 Pet. 5:1), that is to be your position as well. Paul told the Christians at Corinth, ["Be ye followers of me, even as I also am of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 11:1).
