You just don't [tell]{.class_s2FX} your congregation what to do; you [show]{.class_s2FX} them what to do by [example.]{.class_s2FX} Paul told the young preacher, ["be thou an example of the believers, in word, in conversation, in charity, in spirit, in faith, in purity"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 4:12). Peter told the elders to whom he wrote, ["Neither as being lords over God's heritage, but being ensamples to the flock"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 5:3).

["Now there was a valley between them and Ai . . . . Joshua went that night into the midst of the valley"]{.class_s2FY} (vss. 11, 13). The account is reminiscent of the scene in 1 Samuel 17, where the Israelites are in a "face-off" with the Philistines, and there is a valley between them (1 Sam. 17:2--3). In such instances, the "champion" on the offensive side goes into the valley to challenge the defenders to combat. The idea is: "I'm here; come on down and []{#cUM.xhtml_page_143}take me on if you're not a yellow-bellied coward." Joshua is provoking the King of Ai and "egging him on" into attacking the Israelites, and the ploy works (vs. 14).

There are some wonderful devotional applications here for the New Testament believer. There may be a "valley" between you and the objective the Lord wants you to conquer in your Christian life; that is, a low spiritual point where you don't feel you have the victory. Everyone loves the "mountain-top" experiences, but nobody wants to go through the "valley" experiences to get there. But even your Saviour had to go through low spots in His life. Don't you know that the Garden of Gethsemane was a "valley" for Him (see Matt. 26:37--38)? As a Christian, you aren't exempt from sorrow and trouble (John 16:33; Acts 14:22; 1 Thess. 3:4).

The thing to remember when you go through the valleys and the dark times of life is that the Lord Jesus is there with you to get you through them. He's called ["the lily of the valleys"]{.class_s2FW} (Song of Sol. 2:1); that's ["valleyS"]{.class_s2FW}---plural; as in [all]{.class_s2FX} of them, not just one. That Bible says He ["giveth songs in the night"]{.class_s2FW} (Job 35:10); that's why Paul and Silas could sing praises to God after being beaten and put in stocks (Acts 16:23--25). You can have the victory through the Lord Jesus Christ even in the "valleys" and the "night-times" of life.

Back to Joshua 8: ["And Joshua and all Israel made as if they were beaten before them, and fled by the way of the wilderness. And all the people that were in Ai were called together to pursue after them . . . and were drawn away from the city" ]{.class_s2FW}(vss. 15--16). The trick works: Ai is emptied of its defenders and left completely vulnerable (vs. 17). The men of Ai are so overconfident that [they leave the city gates open]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 17).

The Apostle Paul says, ["being crafty, I caught you with guile"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 12:16). ["Guile"]{.class_s2FW} is [trickery.]{.class_s2FX} Of course, he's speaking [spiritually]{.class_s2FX} and being [sarcastic]{.class_s2FX} as he does, but sometimes you have to use what seems like trickery to a lost man to get him to see his lost state and his need for Christ (see our remarks under vs. 7).

I was out door-knocking one time here in Pensacola, and a lady came to the door. I introduced myself and said, "I just stopped by to see if there are any Christians in the neighborhood." She said, "I am a Catholic." A Catholic is taught to say that to brush you off, but I []{#cUM.xhtml_page_144}didn't let it stop me. I said, "There are two kinds of Catholics: saved Catholics and lost Catholics. Which kind are you?"

You see, you don't have to be mean and nasty with them and tell them the Pope is the Antichrist. You're trying to get a chance to present the Gospel to them, so you "go with the flow."

The way I worded my question broke the ice with that woman, and she laughed and said, "I guess I'm the wrong kind." I said to her, "If you will give me a few minutes of your time, I'll show you how to be the right kind."

She let me and my partner in, and I asked her if she had a Bible. She brought out a [King James Version,]{.class_s2FX} and I sat down with her Bible and led her to the Lord in less than thirty minutes. ["Being crafty, I caught you with guile."]{.class_s2FW}

I was out on a downtown street one night witnessing and passing out tracts. A drunken soldier came by, and I offered him a tract. He glanced at it and said, "Yeah, what are you trying to sell, buddy?"

"Happiness," I replied, "you want some?"

That answer made him "back off" a bit, and he took the tract and asked, "Are you Catholic?"

I said, "Yes sir, I am." If I had told that fellow I was a Baptist preacher, he would have turned me off quicker than a radio. I simply used his own terminology against him. You are always told the word [Catholic]{.class_s2FX} means "universal." Well, sure, I'm a member of the "universal Church"---the [real]{.class_s2FX} one, the Body of Jesus Christ. So I said, "Yes, I am a Catholic, and your actions tonight are a disgrace to the Catholic Church."

That comment settled him down some more, and I started taking him down the "Roman's Road." After a bit, he said, "Are you sure you're Catholic?"

"Absolutely," I said, and I gave him some more Scripture.

Not being used to the Priest giving him that much Bible, he asked, "What kind of Catholic are you, anyway?"

["Apostolic,"]{.class_s2FX} I told him. Sure, man; I follow the teachings of the apostles who established the doctrine and practice for the "universal Church" here on this earth.

And finally he had his "out." "Oh, oh," he said as he handed me back the tract. "I'm ROMAN!"

I still didn't let that stop me, though. I got close to him and said, "Well, I don't know much about that religion . . . ." Now I must confess, that was the first outright lie I told that young man. I knew more about his church than he did. But what he needed right then was not for me to strut my knowledge or try to out argue him. "I don't know much about your religion, but let me ask you three questions. Will you give me a straight answer if I ask them?"

"Yes," he said.

"Here is my first question," I said, "and please tell me the truth. [Are you really happy with your religion?"]{.class_s2FX}

He hung his head and said, "No."

I asked my second question, "Do you know for certain that all of your sins are forgiven, and do you have the assurance [in writing?"]{.class_s2FX}

Again he had to admit, "No."

And for my third question, I asked, "If you dropped dead right this minute, do you know for certain that you would NOT go to Hell?"

"No," he said.

I put my arm around his shoulder and put the tract back in his hand, and said to him, "Well, buddy, I don't know much about your religion, but any religion that couldn't give me a 'Yes' answer to those three questions, [I wouldn't give you a dead horse for it."]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}And I slapped him on the back and walked off.

Now I didn't get to "land" that "fish" (see Matt. 4:10), but I got the "hook" in him. I watched as he walked away to catch a bus back to his base. He had that tract open and was reading it as he went. ["Being crafty, I caught you with guile."]{.class_s2FW}

Verse 18 here in Joshua 8:[ "And the LORD said unto Joshua, Stretch out the spear that is in thy hand toward Ai; for I will give it into thine hand."]{.class_s2FW} The lifting up of the spear is a symbolic picture of victory, but it means something else as well. The stretching out of Joshua's hand with the spear was a signal for the ambushment to begin its attack on Ai (vs. 19).

Now you may not realize it, but what Joshua did holding out that spear was quite a feat. Look at verse 26.

"For Joshua drew not his hand back, wherewith he stretched out the spear, until he had utterly destroyed all the inhabitants of Ai."

Joshua holds that spear out for the entire battle; conservatively, it couldn't have been any less than six hours. If you don't think that's something, go try it. Moses couldn't do it by himself. When Amalek attacked Israel in Exodus 17, whenever Moses held up his rod, the tide of battle turned in Israel's favor. But Moses couldn't hold his hands up the whole time. When he dropped them, Amalek gained the upper hand (Exod. 17:9--11). Moses had to sit down on a rock and have Aaron and Hur hold up his hands until Israel defeated the Amalekites (Exod. 17:12--13).

If you have ever hung up clothes on a clothesline, you know about what I'm talking. Your arms get tired from having to reach up the whole time to hang the clothes. That's why most women count on a dryer to take care of the job.

Back in the Army, when I trained men in bayonet fighting, I would make them rest the butt of the rifle on the forearm of their right hand and hold up the bayonet end with their left hand. That bayonet had to be pointing up in the air. The DIs would make the men stand there in that position to build up strength and endurance. But I don't care how strong a fellow was or how much weight he could lift, by the time he had been standing there ten minutes by the clock, the tip of his bayonet began to drop.

So Joshua either has help holding out that spear, or the Lord is giving him supernatural power to hold the thing up. No man is strong enough to hold a spear out and up for six hours by himself.

The lesson in verses 18 and 26, as applied to the Christian, should be apparent. A Christian should be [persistent.]{.class_s2FX} There's a word that's not in the dictionary, but it should be. It is [sticktuitiveness.]{.class_s2FX} You should "stick to" the task God has given you until it is [finished.]{.class_s2FX} The picture with Moses in Exodus 17 is [prayer.]{.class_s2FX} Is there something about which you are praying? Well, don't give up until you get a definite answer from the Lord on the matter. Paul said, ["Pray without ceasing"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Thess. 5:17). That doesn't mean pray 24 hours a day, seven days a week, 365 days a year. It means don't stop praying about a thing until you get your prayer answered.

Is there a sin or a bad habit in your life you need to get rid of? Well, don't stop fighting it until you've got the victory. You say, "Well, Bro. Ruckman, I just keep trying and trying, and it never seems to get better." Well, there's one thing for sure: you'll [never]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cUM.xhtml_page_147} get the victory if you [give up.]{.class_s2FX}

Proverbs 24:16, ["For a just man falleth seven times, and riseth up again: but the wicked shall fall into mischief."]{.class_s2FW} The man or woman who is trying to do right won't just stay down when he or she gets knocked down by sin and temptation. He or she gets up, repents, gets it under the blood (1 John 1:7--9), and goes at it one more round.

["And the ambush arose quickly out of their place . . . and they entered into the city, and took it, and hasted and set the city on fire"]{.class_s2G4-0}; verse 20 says, ["the smoke of the city ascended up to heaven."]{.class_s2G4-0} That's what happened to Sodom and Gomorrah (Gen. 19:28). That's what will happen to Babylon the Great in the Tribulation (Rev. 18:9, 18, 19:3). That's what the Bible says will happen to Edom in the Millennium (Isa. 34:6--19). That's what the Bible says about the [lost in Hell]{.class_s2G6} (Rev. 14:1).

What you are reading in Joshua 8:19--20 is the final destiny of [every]{.class_s2FX} city on earth. That includes New York, Chicago, Los Angeles, Jacksonville, Pensacola, Mobile, Atlanta, Miami, Washington, D.C., Beijing, Madrid, Lisbon, Moscow, London, Berlin, Paris, Rome, Manila, Mecca, Medina, Hyderabad, Johannesburg---the whole lot of them.

["But the day of the Lord will come as a thief in the night; in the which the heavens shall pass away with a great noise, and the elements shall melt with ferment heat, the earth also and the works that are therein shall be burned up"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Pet. 3:10).

The colored folk used to sing, "Oh my lovin' brother, when the world's on fire, don't you want God's bosom to be yo' pillow?" Yeah, I do. When the whole thing blows to "kingdom come," I'll be [in]{.class_s2FX} the One "pushing the button" ("pushing the plunger," "lighting the fuse," etc.). I [won't]{.class_s2FX} be on the [receiving end.]{.class_s2FX}

["And when the men of Ai looked behind them, they saw, and, behold, the smoke of the city ascended up to heaven, and they had no power to flee this way or that way"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 20). A description of a lost man. Job 11:20 says, ["But the eyes of the wicked shall fail, and they shall not escape, and their hope shall be as the giving up of the ghost."]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cUM.xhtml_page_148} When Jesus Christ returns to judge this earth, men are going to try to hide in caves and under mountains to get away from Him, and it won't work (Rev. 6:15--17).

But the ultimate "nowhere to run, nowhere to hide" scenario takes place at the White Throne Judgment. The Bible says ["the earth and the heaven"]{.class_s2FW} flee away from the One who sits on the throne, and the lost are hauled before that throne with no way of hiding or getting away. The lost man stands before the Lord in the filthy rags of his own self-righteousness (Isa. 64:6). He looks down, and there's no ground or anything holding him up. He can stare down a million light years into the Lake of Fire. For the first time in his life, he realizes it is [God]{.class_s2FX} holding him up (Col. 1:16--17). He tries looking up to the One on the Throne, the One who loved him enough to die for Him (John 5:22; Acts 17:31), and immediately hangs his head because he can't look at ["the light which no man can approach unto"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:16). Then he hears those terrible words---["Depart from me, ye cursed, into everlasting fire, prepared for the devil and his angels"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 25:41)---and down he goes, boy. There won't be a thing he can do about it. There will be no escape then; he will have ["no power to flee this way or that way."]{.class_s2FW}

Now the city being set on fire is the signal for Joshua and the main host to turn and counterattack the men of Bethel and Ai (vs. 21). And of course, the army of Ai can't retreat because the ambushers come out of the city and attack them from the rear (vs. 22). The men of Ai are completely surrounded and go down in defeat.

["And they smote them, so that they let none of them remain or escape . . . . And it came to pass, when Israel had made an end of slaying all the inhabitants of Ai in the field . . . that all the Israelites returned unto Ai, and smote it with the edge of the sword. And so it was, that all fell that day, both of men and women, were twelve thousand, even all the men of Ai"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 22, 24--25). Joshua does what Saul does not in 1 Samuel 15. Saul was commanded to kill every Amalekite from the King down to the newborn baby, and all the beasts too (1 Sam. 15:3). []{#cUM.xhtml_page_149}But Saul saved the King alive as a trophy (see Judg. 1:7), and the people saved all the best cattle (1 Sam. 15:9). Now verse 23 says the Israelites took the King of Ai alive, but it was not for the purpose of Joshua keeping him alive as a trophy of his victory over Ai. He took the King and hung him by the neck from a tree as a testimony of what happened to anyone who defied God and His armies (see Exod. 6:26).

Now as we discussed in the Introduction, it is passages like this that "shock" thin-skinned atheists and Liberals. What they don't realize, or don't want to acknowledge, was that the genocide commanded by God in the Old Testament was a [punishment on sin.]{.class_s2FX}[ "The iniquity of the Amorites"]{.class_s2FW} was finally ["full"]{.class_s2FW} (see Gen. 15:16). If you want to see how ["full,"]{.class_s2FW} read Leviticus 18; it's exactly what is being practiced in San Francisco, New Orleans, Pensacola, New York City, and Washington, D.C. in 2014. It is what God burned Sodom and Gomorrah to the ground for (Jude 7). It's what the Lord sent Nebuchadnezzar into the land to take His own people into captivity for (1 Kings 14:24 cf. Jer. 23:14; Ezek. 16:49--52). So you can expect God to do to America (both through nature and our enemies) what He did to Sodom and Gomorrah, and Judah.

The Liberals take passages like this one and compare them to: ["Blessed are the peacemakers: for they shall be called the children of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 5:9), and ["Suffer the little children to come unto me, and forbid them not: for of such is the kingdom of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Mark 10:14), and ["God is love"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 4:8). The dumb, stupid sapheads then figure that there are two different "Gods": there is the cruel, vicious, vengeful, murdering Bully of the Old Testament; and the sweet, loving, kind Heavenly Father of the New Testament who sent His Son down to this earth to show you how much He loves you.

Of course, that's a [lie.]{.class_s2FX} It was the God of the Old Testament who promised to send a ["seed"]{.class_s2FW} to redeem mankind (Gen. 3:15). It was the God of the Old Testament of whom David said, ["The LORD is my shepherd; I shall not want"]{.class_s2FW} and the rest of the sublime words of Psalm 23. Contrariwise, it was the sweet, kind, "gentle Jesus" who said, ["Ye serpents, ye generation of vipers, how can ye escape the damnation of hell?"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 23:33), and ["For []{#cUM.xhtml_page_150}the days shall come upon thee, that thine enemies shall cast a trench about thee, and compass thee round, and keep thee in on every side, And shall lay thee even with the ground, and thy children within thee; and they shall not leave in thee one stone upon another; because thou knewest not the time of thy visitation"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 19:43--44).

[Those are the same God.]{.class_s2FX} The problem that these infidels can't get is that He has [two sides.]{.class_s2FX} It's Law (Old Testament) and Gospel (New Testament). It's [holiness]{.class_s2FX} and [love.]{.class_s2FX} It's [wrath]{.class_s2FX} and [mercy.]{.class_s2FX} To the unbelieving, disobedient, and reprobate, He shows one side; to those who love Him, believe His words, and obey Him, He shows the other. A Gentile like Job who ["feared God, and eschewed evil"]{.class_s2FW} (Job 1:1) got one face of God, and the Canaanite tribes who practiced idolatry and sex perversion got another. Kings like David and Hezekiah got one side of God, and Kings like Saul and Ahab got the opposite side. In Jesus' day, the publicans and harlots experienced one side of Christ (Matt. 21:31--32), and the scribes and Pharisees experienced quite another (Matt. 23).

As a New Testament believer, do you know why you are going to end up in Heaven? Because when you got saved, the Holy Spirit placed you in Christ (1 Cor. 12:13), and when you die, you go to be where He is (2 Cor. 5:5--8; Phil. 1:23). But do you know that when a lost person dies, he finds out that he's in God too; he's just not in the part that ["loved us, and washed us from our sins in his own blood"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 1:5).

Can you imagine waking up in Hell and crying, "My God, where am I?!" And a voice comes out of the fire and the darkness and says, "You're in the Lord." You say, "How can that be?!" And the voice comes back, ["For our God is A CONSUMING FIRE"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 12:29). That lost man is a part of God too; he's just in the part in which he doesn't want to be.

Now in verse 27, the Israelites return from the battle to spoil the city, and in verse 28, the city is burned ["and made . . . an heap for ever."]{.class_s2FW} So the fire in verse 19 didn't burn the whole city down; it was just enough to send up the "smoke signal" for Joshua's counterattack. Once the battle was over and the city was spoiled, they finished the job.

["And the king of Ai he hanged on a tree until eventide: and as soon as the sun was down, Joshua commanded that they should take his carcase down from the tree, and cast it at the entering of the gate of the city, and raise thereon a great heap of stones, that remaineth unto this day"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 29). This is a picture of a lost man dying in his sins and being burned and going to Hell forever. The ["tree,"]{.class_s2FW} of course, is a picture of a cross (Gal. 3:13; 1 Pet. 2:24). The Law said, ["if a man have committed a sin worthy of death . . . and thou hang him on a tree: His body shall not remain all night upon the tree, but thou shalt in any wise bury him that day; (for he that is hanged is accursed of God;)"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 21:22--23). Jesus hung on a ["tree,"]{.class_s2FW} so He was under God's curse (Gal. 3:13), but He didn't hang for His own crimes or sins (1 Pet. 2:24). So Jesus Christ bore your [curse]{.class_s2FX} so you could receive His [blessing.]{.class_s2FX} What was that blessing? [The full righteousness of God Himself.]{.class_s2FX}

["For he ]{.class_s2FW}\[God\][ hath made him ]{.class_s2FW}\[Jesus Christ\][ to be sin for us, who knew no sin; that we might be made the righteousness of God in him"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:21).

When a lost man rejects Jesus Christ, he claims the curse Christ bore for him as his own. Spiritually speaking, he takes his place on the cross and has to die for his own sins. He is [buried]{.class_s2FX} (the type in Josh. 8 is the King of Ai's body being placed under ["a great heap of stones"]{.class_s2FW}). But unlike Jesus Christ, he doesn't come up from that grave. He remains there physically, and his soul is in Hell. He doesn't come up ["from the dead"]{.class_s2FW} (see our comments on Luke 20:35 in that Commentary). He goes from a state of ["death and hell"]{.class_s2FW} to ["the second death"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 20:14) with only the judgment in between (Rev. 20:12). And once he hits ["the second death,"]{.class_s2FW} the whole universe will be able to witness his torment every Sabbath day (Isa. 66:23--24). What was physically true of the cursed body of the King of Ai---["that remaineth unto this day"]{.class_s2FW}---will be spiritually and eternally true of the lost.

30 Then Joshua built an altar unto the LORD God of Israel in mount Ebal,

31 As Moses the servant of the LORD commanded the []{#cUM.xhtml_page_152}children of Israel, as it is written in the book of the law of Moses, an altar of whole stones, over which no man hath lift up any iron: and they offered thereon burnt offerings unto the LORD, and sacrificed peace offerings.

32 And he wrote there upon the stones a copy of the law of Moses, which he wrote in the presence of the children of Israel.

33 And all Israel, and their elders, and officers, and their judges, stood on this side the ark and on that side before the priests the Levites, which bare the ark of the covenant of the LORD, as well the stranger, as he that was born among them; half of them over against mount Gerizim, and half of them over against mount Ebal; as Moses the servant of the LORD had commanded before, that they should bless the people of Israel.

34 And afterward he read all the words of the law, the blessings and cursings, according to all that is written in the book of the law.

35 There was not a word of all that Moses commanded, which Joshua read not before all the congregation of Israel, with the women, and the little ones, and the strangers that were conversant among them.

What you are reading in this passage was commanded by Moses in Deuteronomy 11:29--30, 27:1--8. God commanded the people to build ["an altar of whole stones"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 31) that a chisel hadn't touched. God warned them about it in Exodus 20:25; Deuteronomy 27:5--6; and here. The reason is that there is something wrong with [iron]{.class_s2FX} throughout the Bible.

Iron is first mentioned in Genesis 4:22 in connection with the descendants of Cain. The name [Cain]{.class_s2FX} is connected with an [iron]{.class_s2FX} spear in Hebrew (see our comments on Gen. 4:1 in that Commentary). It was the giant [Goliath]{.class_s2FX} who had an iron spear (1 Sam. 17:4--7). Both Cain and Goliath were types of the [Antichrist]{.class_s2FX} (see chaps. 2--3 of [The Mark of the Beast]{.class_s2FX}). Iron is connected with the world Gentile power that crucified your Saviour (Dan. 2:40) and with the kingdom of the Antichrist as well (Dan. 2:41--45, 7:7--8, 19--25).

No iron was allowed in the construction of Noah's ark, and no iron appears in the Tabernacle. And while iron was used in the construction of Solomon's Temple (1 Chron. 22:3, 14, 16, 29:2, 7; 2 Chron. 2:7, 14), while the Temple was being built in Jerusalem, no ["tool of iron"]{.class_s2FW} was used in its construction (1 Kings 6:7). You can't miss the symbolism of Noah's ark (those [in the ark]{.class_s2FX} were saved from the judgment of God as those [in Christ]{.class_s2FX} are saved from God's wrath), and Jesus Himself likened His body to the Tabernacle and Temple (John 2:19--21).

Verse 31 is proof that Exodus and Deuteronomy were [real books,]{.class_s2FX} that they existed [before]{.class_s2FX} the conquest of Canaan, and that [Moses]{.class_s2FX} was the author. All three are denied by the infidels who came up with "higher criticism" (Astruc, Graf, Wellhausen, Eichhorn, Spinoza, et al.).

Now the construction of this altar is a great act of faith on Joshua's part. Ordinarily, men only set up an altar when they [own]{.class_s2FX} the land (see David buying the Temple mount before building his altar---2 Sam. 24:24--25). So when Joshua sets up this altar, it is not only an act of [obedience,]{.class_s2FX} but an act of [faith;]{.class_s2FX} he is as much as claiming the land when he hasn't taken any more than two or three cities.

["An altar of whole stones, over which no man hath lift up any iron: and they offered thereon burnt offerings unto the LORD, and sacrificed peace offerings"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 31). The typology points to the sacrifice of Jesus Christ. He is the ["stone . . . cut out without hands"]{.class_s2FW} (Dan. 2:23, 45), and His Church is made up of ["lively stones"]{.class_s2FW} that ["are built up a spiritual house, an holy priesthood, to offer up spiritual sacrifices, acceptable to God by Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:5). So the Church is made up of [God]{.class_s2FX}-made stones, not [man]{.class_s2FX}-made stones; it is through the sacrifice of Christ, and the New Birth that is imparted to us through faith in that sacrifice, that enables us to make ["spiritual sacrifices, acceptable to God."]{.class_s2FW} Outside of the sacrifice of Christ, any sacrifice made by any priest on this earth finds no more favor with God than Cain's produce stand (Gen. 4:3--7 and comments on the passage in that Commentary).

Verse 32: ["And he wrote there upon the stones a copy of the law of Moses."]{.class_s2FW}[]{#cUM.xhtml_page_154} According to the command given in Deuteronomy 27:4--8, Joshua plasters the sides of the stones that make up the altar and copies the Ten Commandments into the plaster. In keeping with the typology given above, the spiritual application to the New Testament believer is found in 2 Corinthians 3:2--9, and we refer you to our remarks on those verses in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on 1 & 2 Corinthians.]{.class_s2FX}

Now if you want to see what is going on in verses 33--34, then read Deuteronomy 27:11--26. In that passage, the Levitical priests who bear the Ark of the Covenant are standing there before the altar Joshua built on Mount Ebal, and at the foot of Mount Gerizim are six tribes and at the foot of Mount Ebal are six tribes. The tribes are divided according to the [mother]{.class_s2FX} from whom they came. On Mount Gerizim, there are the children of Rachel and Leah (Simeon, Levi, Judah, Issachar, Joseph \[Manasseh and Ephraim\], and Benjamin); and on Mount Ebal are the children of the two handmaids, Bilhah and Zilpah. The two notable exceptions on Mount Ebal are [Reuben]{.class_s2FX} and [Zebulun.]{.class_s2FX} Reuben was the firstborn son of Leah, but he was over on Ebal with the handmaids' sons because he committed adultery with his father's concubine, Bilhah, and lost the birthright (Gen. 35:22 cf. 1 Chron. 5:1). Zebulun was the last of Leah's sons, but there is no apparent reason given in Scripture as to why he was placed over with the handmaids' children.

What is going on in Joshua 8:33--34 is like a responsive reading that is practiced in some churches. Joshua reads the blessings and the curses recorded in Deuteronomy 28. When he reads a blessing, the tribes on Gerizim respond with "Amen!"; and when he reads a curse, the tribes on Ebal respond with "Amen!"

But what is interesting is those blessings and curses read by Joshua are preceded by the Levitical priests bearing the Ark reciting a litany of curses that are placed on any individual who breaks any one of the Ten Commandments. After each curse, [all]{.class_s2FX} the people are to respond with ["Amen."]{.class_s2FW} What is read by the priests bearing the Ark reveals the character of Old Testament salvation.

["Cursed be he that confirmeth not all the words of this law TO DO THEM"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 27:26).

The typical Fundamentalist teaching is that salvation in the Old []{#cUM.xhtml_page_155}Testament is the same as salvation in the New Testament---by grace through faith without works. They're [mad;]{.class_s2FX} they're [out of their minds;]{.class_s2FX} they're ready for the rubber room. In the Old Testament, God showed mercy to those who loved Him and KEPT HIS COMMANDMENTS (Exod. 20:6; Deut. 5:10)---WORKS!

Listen, brethren, if people were saved the same way in the Old Testament as they are in the New Testament, [why are there two Testaments?]{.class_s2FX} In the Old Testament, their sins weren't cleared or taken away (Exod. 34:7). In the Old Testament, there was no New Birth or adoption of the believer. Even under grace before the Law, redemption by the blood was only a [temporary]{.class_s2FX} thing; that's why they had to continually make sacrifices (see Heb. 9:7--12). ["For it is not possible that the blood of bulls and goats should take away sins"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 10:6). In the Old Testament, the blood of bulls and goats and sheep was the [only]{.class_s2FX} blood they had for redemption.

So the saints of the Old Testament were [not]{.class_s2FX} saved the same way as the saints in the New Testament are. Old Testament salvation involved both faith [and works.]{.class_s2FX} Look at the conclusion of this whole ["blessing and cursing"]{.class_s2FW} business. ["I call heaven and earth to record this day against you, that I have set before you life and death, blessing and cursing: therefore choose life, that both thou and thy seed may live: That thou mayest love the LORD thy God, and that thou mayest obey his voice ]{.class_s2FW}\[there's the [works]{.class_s2FX}\][, and that thou mayest cleave unto him ]{.class_s2FW}\[and there's the faith\][ for he is thy life"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 30:19--20).

If there is any doubt that [works]{.class_s2FX} were a part of Old Testament salvation, look at verses 15--16 there in Deuteronomy 30.

["See, I have set before thee this day life and good, and death and evil; In that I command thee this day to love the LORD thy God, to walk in his ways ]{.class_s2FW}\[[works]{.class_s2FX}\][, to keep his commandments and his statutes and his judgments]{.class_s2FW} \[[works]{.class_s2FX}\][, that thou mayest live."]{.class_s2FW}

Back to Joshua 8:[ "And all Israel, and their elders, and officers, and their judges stood on this side the ark and on that side before the priests the Levites, which bare the ark of the covenant of the LORD . . . that they should bless the people of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 33). Not only were the priests to pronounce []{#cUM.xhtml_page_156}the curses of Deuteronomy 27 as a warning to the people of what would happen if they broke the Ten Commandments, they were to convey a blessing on the people as well. That blessing is given in Numbers 6:22--27.

["And the LORD spake unto Moses, saying, Speak unto Aaron and unto his sons ]{.class_s2FW}\[those would be the priests who attended to the Ark\][, saying, On this wise ye shall bless the children of Israel, saying unto them, The LORD bless thee, and keep thee: The LORD make his face shine upon thee, and be gracious unto thee: The LORD lift up his countenance upon thee, and give thee peace. And they shall put my name upon the children of Israel; and I will bless them."]{.class_s2FW}

Verses 24--26 there in Numbers 6 are sometimes given as the benediction in more formal churches. They have even been set to music to be sung by a choir as a postlude to the service.

Now there are some lessons we as Christians can apply spiritually and devotionally from this blessing. First of all, the blessings come from the high priest and his sons. In the New Testament, that High Priest is Jesus Christ (Heb. 3:1), and we as believers are His sons (John 1:12; Heb. 2:10). So any blessings this sin-cursed earth still has are due to the Lord Jesus Christ keeping the door of salvation open and to the real Christians who are still here.

I know Christians---and I am talking about real, saved, Bible-believing Christians---can be a pretty sorry lot sometimes, but just wait until they all leave at the Rapture and see what happens. You talk about hell on wheels, that's exactly what it will be. If you think this place is a mess now, just wait until there are [no]{.class_s2FX} saved kids in the schools, [no]{.class_s2FX} saved cops on the police force, [no]{.class_s2FX} saved doctors in the hospitals, [no]{.class_s2FX} saved judges in the law courts, [no ]{.class_s2FX}saved players at all on the football teams. The lost crowd will finally get what they want: unrestrained license. There will be no one around to call to their minds what is right or remind them that what they are doing is wrong, no one to "shove religion down their throats"---just [moral anarchy.]{.class_s2FX}

Second, notice the Trinitarian nature of the blessing:

["The LORD bless thee, and keep thee"]{.class_s2FW}---the work of God the []{#cUM.xhtml_page_157}Father.

["The LORD make his face shine upon thee, and be gracious unto thee"]{.class_s2FW}---the work of the Holy Spirit.

["The LORD lift up his countenance upon thee, and give thee peace"]{.class_s2FW}---the work of God the Son (John 1:14, 18; Rom. 5:1).

The Trinity isn't a "Catholic" doctrine. It's found from Genesis 1--Revelation 22.

Third, note that ["name"]{.class_s2FW} put ["upon the children of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} in Numbers 6:27. In the Old Testament, that name is [Jehovah]{.class_s2FX} (Exod. 6:3); in the New Testament, that name is [Jesus Christ]{.class_s2FX} (1 John 5:20). It never was or will be "Allah." All "Allah" means is "the God," which begs the question---[which]{.class_s2FX} "God"? It is certainly [not]{.class_s2FX} ["the God and Father of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 11:31; Eph. 1:3; 1 Pet. 1:3), for one of the basic tenets of "Islam" is that "the God" (Allah) [has no Son]{.class_s2FX} (Sura 23:89, 37:150, 25:2, 17:111, 19:34). "Allah" is "the god" described in 2 Corinthians 4:4 and Daniel 11:38.

Finally, notice [again]{.class_s2G2} the emphasis the Bible puts on the [negative.]{.class_s2G2} The blessing in Numbers 6 is composed of [four]{.class_s2G2} verses; the curses the priests were to recite were comprised of [thirteen]{.class_s2G2} verses---over [three times]{.class_s2G2} as many. In the blessings and cursings of Deuteronomy 28 that are read in Joshua 8, there are fourteen positive statements followed by [54 negative statements.]{.class_s2G2} That's a proportion of three to one; God's idea of a "balanced" ministry is [75% negative.]{.class_s2G2} That is the same proportion as the Gospel in 1 Corinthians 15:34. ["Christ died]{.class_s2G3} \[negative\][ for our sins ]{.class_s2G3}\[negative\][ . . . And that he was buried ]{.class_s2G3}\[negative\][, and that he rose again the third day ]{.class_s2G3}\[positive\][." ]{.class_s2G3}Preacher, if all you are preaching is [positive]{.class_s2G2} thinking and [positive]{.class_s2G2} messages, [you don't have a Biblical ministry.]{.class_s2G2} If you want to be Scriptural in the matter, your preaching should be [75% negative.]{.class_s2G2}

Back to Joshua 8: ["And afterward he read all the words of the law, the blessings and cursings, according to all that is written in the book of the law. There was not a word of all that Moses commanded, which Joshua read not before all the congregation of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 34--35).

In the context, the reference is to Deuteronomy 27--28 (["the blessings and cursings"]{.class_s2FW}), which would take anywhere from []{#cUM.xhtml_page_158}twenty to thirty minutes, with the responses of the congregation. It could be a reference to the whole book of Deuteronomy, which would take about three hours to read. But if it were the entire ["book of the law"]{.class_s2FW}---Genesis through Deuteronomy---that would take anywhere from fourteen to sixteen hours to read. That would be from six in the morning to eight or ten at night. You have to admit, that would be one long "service." Not even Ezra did that in Nehemiah 8. He read [six hours]{.class_s2FX} at a time (["morning until midday"]{.class_s2FW}---Neh. 8:3) over a period of [seven days]{.class_s2FX} (Neh. 8:18).

The ["congregation"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 35 is more than just the 600,000 men of war; it includes the women and children as well. ["The strangers"]{.class_s2FW} are a reference to the Gentiles among the people who had become Jewish proselytes (cf. Acts 2:10, 13:43). That would include, of course, Rahab and her family.

The word ["conversant"]{.class_s2FW} is an old French word that means "to be associated with." It refers to the fact that those Gentiles lived among the Jews as Jews themselves. That is similar to how the word[ "conversation"]{.class_s2FW} is used in 2 Corinthians 1:12; Galatians 1:13; Ephesians 2:3, 4:22; Philippians 3:20; Hebrews 13:5, 7; etc. It's talking about the way you [live]{.class_s2FX} in those passages, not a dialogue between two people (see our comments on 1 Pet. 3:1 in that Commentary).

In the New Testament, Gentiles don't have to convert to Judaism to be part of ["the commonwealth of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 2:12). When you receive Christ,[ "ye are no more strangers and foreigners, but fellowcitizens with the saints, and of the household of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 2:13--19).

As far as your ["conversation"]{.class_s2FW} goes, you are to ["put off concerning the former conversation the old man, which is corrupt according to the deceitful lusts"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 4:22). You are to ["let your conversation be as it becometh the gospel of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 1:27) and ["be ye holy in all manner of conversation"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 1:15). Why? Because your ["conversation"]{.class_s2FW} isn't down here; it's "upstairs" (Phil. 3:20).

And one final thought about ["the book of the law"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 34: a Christian should carry his Bible in his [hand]{.class_s2FX} (Psa. 149:6), he should carry his Bible in his [heart]{.class_s2FX} (Deut. 6:6), and he should carry his Bible in his [mouth]{.class_s2FX}[]{#cUM.xhtml_page_159} (Josh. 1:8).

# Chapter 9 {.heading_s2B}

9:1 And it came to pass, when all the kings which were on this side Jordan, in the hills, and in the valleys, and in all the coasts of the great sea over against Lebanon, the Hittite, and the Amorite, the Canaanite, the Perizzite, the Hivite, and the Jebusite, heard thereof;

2 That they gathered themselves together, to fight with Joshua and with Israel, with one accord.

The first thing to notice in this passage is the word ["kings"]{.class_s2FW}---[plural.]{.class_s2FX} As we will see in chapter 12, there is no [one]{.class_s2FX} kingdom or empire or nation of "Palestinians." The ["kings,"]{.class_s2FW} here, are rulers of [City]{.class_s2FX}-States; that is, each city is its own independent political entity. There is no nation, politically or ethnically, of "Palestinians." There wasn't in 1913 B.C. (Abraham); there wasn't in 1450 B.C. (Joshua); there wasn't in 445 B.C. (Ezra and Nehemiah); there wasn't in A.D. 33 (Christ); there wasn't in A.D. 135 when the Romans changed the name of the land of Israel to "Palestine" (the Latin word for [Philistine]{.class_s2FX}); there wasn't in A.D. 638 when the Moslem [Arabs]{.class_s2FX} invaded; there wasn't between A.D. 750 and 1098 when [six different]{.class_s2FX} Moslem groups---[none]{.class_s2FX} of which were "Palestinians"---invaded the land; there wasn't in 1099 when the Catholic Crusaders took over the land; there wasn't in 1244 (Khwarezmian Tartars); there wasn't in 1260 (Mamelukes); there wasn't in 1517 (Ottoman Turks); there wasn't in 1831 (Egyptians); there wasn't in 1840 (Ottoman Turks again); there wasn't in 1917 when General Allenby took Jerusalem and the British Mandate of Palestine began; there wasn't in 1948 when Israel became a State again and five Arab nations attacked it; [and there's not one now]{.class_s2FX} (2014). "Palestinians" have historically been [Canaanites, Philistines, Amorites, Hittites, Hivites, Girgashites, Perizzites, Jebusites, Jews, Samaritans, Arabians, Romans, Greek Orthodox, Roman Catholics, Moslems, Egyptians, Turks, French, Russians, Germans, Italians, ]{.class_s2FX}and [English.]{.class_s2FX}

Now do you know what all that means as far as the One who [owns]{.class_s2FX} the land is concerned? Not one cotton-picking thing in the world! All those religions and nations EXCEPT ONE are [trespassers]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_161} on His land. God said that land belonged to [Him]{.class_s2FX} (Lev. 25:23; Num. 35:34; Deut. 32:43). God swore to give that land to the [Jews]{.class_s2FX}---the descendants of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob; NOT the descendants of Abraham, Ishmael, and Esau (Deut. 1:8, 21, 25, 35--39, 2:12, 24, 3:2, 20, 4:1, 21, 38, 40, 5:16, 31, 38, 6:10, 18, 23, and [fifty more verses in the same book]{.class_s2FX}). Those promises are not abrogated by [anything]{.class_s2FX} those Jews do or don't do because the covenant God made with that nation is [unconditional]{.class_s2FX} (Lev. 26:42--45) and it is [eternal]{.class_s2FX} (Psa. 105:7--11).

God drove the Jews out of that land once, and He brought them back again (2 Chron. 36--Ezra 1). God drove them out a second time in A.D. 70--135, and He promised to bring them back a second time (Isa. 11:11). [That's exactly what He did between 1917 ]{.class_s2FX}(the Balfour Declaration)[ and 1948]{.class_s2FX} (Israel becoming a State). You create a "Palestinian State" at your own peril (Zech. 14:1--3; Zeph. 3:8--13).

Once again I call to your attention that the nations listed in verse 1 are from [Ham]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 10:15--20 cf. 1 Chron. 1:8--16). That might not be "politically correct," but it is [so.]{.class_s2FX} The only nation that is missing from the list, that was given in Deuteronomy 7:1 and Joshua 3:10, is the [Girgashites.]{.class_s2FX} But when you get over to Joshua 24:11, you are told that the Girgashites were one of the nations that fought against the children of Israel when they took the land. Here in verse 1, the Girgashites are missing, and in Genesis 15:19--21, the Hivites are missing. All this has led the expositors and commentators to conclude that the Girgashites were an offshoot of the Hivites. I don't know if that's so or not, but you are about to read about an encounter Joshua had with a bunch of Hivites (vs. 7).

Now what's going on in this passage is that Joshua's enemies are all getting together in an "ecumenical movement." Before Joshua and Israel showed up, all those nations were fighting amongst themselves, but after Joshua took Jericho and then Ai, they decided they had better band together if they wanted to survive.

Note that expression in verse 2: ["with one accord."]{.class_s2FW} That's the same expression that's used of the early church in the book of Acts (Acts 1:14, 2:1, 46, 4:24, 5:12, 15:25). Paul told the Philippians: ["Fulfil ye my joy, that ye be likeminded, having the same love, being of one accord, of one mind"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 2:2).

The big thing in religious and political circles these days is []{#c100.xhtml_page_162}[unity.]{.class_s2FX} "Let's all get together with one leader in one united front." When the Pope talks about "one fold and one shepherd," he's talking about you becoming a part of [his]{.class_s2FX} church with [him]{.class_s2FX} in charge. Vatican II didn't change one plank of Catholic doctrine. Every Pope---including John Paul II, Benedict XVI, and "Francis"---still has to swear to "receive and profess all other things delivered, defined, and declared by the sacred canons, and general councils, and particularly THE HOLY COUNCIL OF TRENT."

That's called "the Tridentine Confession." For a Pope to become a Pope, he has to swear he believes everything that was "delivered, defined, and declared" by the Council of Trent (1545--1563). [The Council of Trent puts 125 curses on every Baptist, Methodist, Episcopalian, Lutheran, Presbyterian, Evangelical, Fundamentalist, etc.;]{.class_s2FX} that is, if you don't agree with the Catholic Church's teachings on justification, salvation, the Mass, the sacraments, prayers to dead saints, Purgatory, the superiority and infallibility of the Pope, etc., [you are damned to Hell.]{.class_s2FX} So no matter what the Roman Catholic Church claimed to have changed in 1965 (Vatican II), it still swears by what it declared in 1563.

That includes being cursed if you don't accept such pulp fiction as Tobit, Judith, Bel and the Dragon, 1 & 2 Maccabees, 1 & 2 Esdras, Ecclesiasticus, etc., to be ["the scripture of truth"]{.class_s2FW} (Dan. 10:21) and part of the Old Testament (Session 4 on the "Canonical Scriptures"). You are "anathema" (i.e., [damned to Hell]{.class_s2FX}) if you [print, distribute, read,]{.class_s2FX} or even [possess,]{.class_s2FX} without written permission of a Roman Catholic Bishop, any copy of the Bible which hasn't been approved by the Catholic Church and doesn't have the Roman Catholic doctrinal notes (Session 4 on the "Edition and Use of the Sacred Books").

You are accursed if you don't believe Christ's blood atonement is applied to you by Roman Catholic water baptism or that a Roman Catholic Priest sprinkling a baby removes that child's "original sin" (Session 5 on "Original Sin"). You are damned to Hell if you believe and teach that justification is by faith in Jesus Christ alone and that there is no saving grace conferred to you through the "sacraments" (Session 6, Canon IX).

You understand that a Pope has to swear he believes this. There is no ecumenicism in all this or "sweet spirit of Christian unity." It's the Pope's way or the highway. Anything different than that is just deceitful lying to bring you into bondage to a wino in Rome.

You are cursed if you believe you are justified without Roman Catholic sprinkling (Session 6, Canon XI). You are cursed if you believe you are saved by believing solely on Jesus Christ's blood atonement (Session 6, Canon XII). If you believe you are eternally secure in Jesus Christ, you are "anathema" (Session 6, Canon XVI). You are accursed if you believe the only sin in this age that can send you to Hell is rejecting Jesus Christ as your Saviour (Session 6, Canon XXVII). If you don't believe in Purgatory, you are headed for Hell (Session 6, Canon XXX).

Now that's nine curses put on you by the Roman Catholic Church; there are 116 more. And you think you are going to "get along" with that bunch? The only way you are going to get along with someone like that is if you [throw your Bible out the window.]{.class_s2FX}

The only "unity" the Bible teaches the born-again Christian is the [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} union of believers in the Body of Christ. When Paul says be ["of one accord, of one mind,"]{.class_s2FW} that fellowship is within the local church, and the ["one mind"]{.class_s2FW} is the [mind of Christ]{.class_s2FX} (Phil. 2:5; 1 Cor. 2:16). The only way you are going to think like Jesus Christ is to get into the Book. [That's ]{.class_s2FX}where God revealed His "mind." Unity in a local church has to be a unity of belief in and fidelity to the word of God, or it is not real unity. It's a [fake;]{.class_s2FX} it's just a [facade.]{.class_s2FX}

The problem is, the word of God [divides]{.class_s2FX} (Heb. 4:12). Jesus Christ didn't come to bring unity; He came to bring [division]{.class_s2FX} (Luke 12:51). The more you believe that Book, the greater the chasm between you and those who don't. The closer you get to Jesus Christ, the less you have in common with those who want nothing to do with Him.

The reason independent, Fundamental, Bible-believing Baptists have so much trouble in "getting along" is because they believe stronger about the Book than most groups. Catholics, Modernists, Liberals, "emergents," and "seeker sensitive" churches don't have the problems with church splits and church fights like Bible-believing Baptists do because those other churches don't believe anything. Oh, they'll make a profession of belief; they may even []{#c100.xhtml_page_164}recite a creed every Sunday. But they'll change the Book, correct the Book, and reinterpret the Book whenever necessary so they can "get along."

It is difficult for God's people who really believe the Book to be of ["one accord"]{.class_s2FW} on everything, but when it comes to the Devil's crowd, they can get together on two things: get rid of the [truth]{.class_s2FX} and get rid of [Jesus Christ.]{.class_s2FX} The heathen nations of Canaan that were fighting and bickering with each other all the time could come together to get rid of [Joshua.]{.class_s2FX} Things are no different with the New Testament "Joshua." Before Jesus Christ came along, Herod and Pilate were political enemies, but when it came to getting rid of the Prophet from Nazareth, they were able to set aside their animosity for one another and become [friends]{.class_s2FX} (Luke 23:11--12).

If you have a strong, militant Christian witness, you will find that groups that normally would have nothing to do with each other can "come together in the spirit of cooperation" to [stop you.]{.class_s2FX} They find they have something in common after all: get you off the street corner preaching or get you off the radio saying all those mean, nasty things about them. One of our graduates, when he was pastoring a church in Kentucky, had the Catholics, the Campbellites (Church of Christ), and the Southern Baptists all get together against him. If you are militantly proclaiming the truth, that sort of thing will happen to you: those who reject the truth will gang up together to [shut you up.]{.class_s2FX}

Now what you are looking at here in Joshua 9:2 is a prophetic picture of what God is going to do just before the return of Jesus Christ. The heathen Kings of Canaan think they are coming together to create a united front against Joshua (as one of the Founding Fathers said, "We must hang together . . . else, we shall most assuredly hang separately"), but God is getting them together to make it easier for Joshua to take them all down in one shot (see 11:1--8). That is what the Lord does before the Second Advent.

["Therefore wait ye upon me, saith the LORD, until the day that I rise up to the prey: FOR MY DETERMINATION IS TO GATHER THE NATIONS, that I may ASSEMBLE THE KINGDOMS ]{.class_s2FW}\[there is your United Nations Assembly\][, to POUR UPON THEM MINE INDIGNATION, even all my FIERCE []{#c100.xhtml_page_165}ANGER: for all the earth shall be DEVOURED WITH THE FIRE OF MY JEALOUSY"]{.class_s2FW} (Zeph. 3:8).

[The United Nations was created by God,]{.class_s2FX} but it wasn't created to be "mankind's last, best hope for peace" (see the insane madness put out by cussin' Harry Truman). The UN was created by God to [burn]{.class_s2FX} every nation that [despised Him, despised His Book, rejected His Son,]{.class_s2FX} and [oppressed His people]{.class_s2FX} (the Jews).

You think that's just the "vengeful, hateful God" of the Old Testament? Well, look at the "sweet gentle Jesus" of the New Testament.

["As therefore the tares are GATHERED and BURNED IN THE FIRE; so shall it be in the end of this world. The Son of man shall send forth his angels, and they shall GATHER out of his kingdom all things that offend, and them which do iniquity; And shall CAST THEM INTO A FURNACE OF FIRE: there shall be wailing and gnashing of teeth" ]{.class_s2FW}(Matt. 13:40--42).

[That ]{.class_s2FX}is the final ["one accord" ]{.class_s2FW}of the world system.

3 And when the inhabitants of Gibeon heard what Joshua had done unto Jericho and to Ai,

4 They did work wilily, and went and made as if they had been ambassadors, and took old sacks upon their asses, and wine bottles, old, and rent, and bound up;

5 And old shoes and clouted upon their feet, and old garments upon them; and all the bread of their provision was dry and mouldy.

6 And they went to Joshua unto the camp at Gilgal, and said unto him, and to the men of Israel, We be come from a far country: now therefore make ye a league with us.

7 And the men of Israel said unto the Hivites, Peradventure ye dwell among us; and how shall we make a league with you?

8 And they said unto Joshua, We are thy servants. And Joshua said unto them, Who are ye? and from whence come ye?

9 And they said unto him, From a very far country thy []{#c100.xhtml_page_166}servants are come because of the name of the LORD thy God: for we have heard the fame of him, and all that he did in Egypt,

10 And all that he did to the two kings of the Amorites, that were beyond Jordan, to Sihon king of Heshbon, and to Og king of Bashan, which was at Ashtaroth.

11 Wherefore our elders and all the inhabitants of our country spake to us, saying, Take victuals with you for the journey, and go to meet them, and say unto them, We are your servants: therefore now make ye a league with us.

12 This our bread we took hot for our provision out of our houses on the day we came forth to go unto you; but now, behold, it is dry, and it is mouldy:

13 And these bottles of wine, which we filled, were new; and, behold, they be rent: and these our garments and our shoes are become old by reason of the very long journey.

14 And the men took of their victuals, and asked not counsel at the mouth of the LORD.

15 And Joshua made peace with them, and made a league with them, to let them live: and the princes of the congregation sware unto them.

This is the account of the deception of the Gibeonites. Gibeon was a city of the Hivites (vs. 7, 11:19). Joshua 10:2 calls Gibeon ["a great city"]{.class_s2FW}: it was a city with a large population. Gibeon was also said to be ["as one of the royal cities" ]{.class_s2FW}(10:2); that is, it was the chief city of four cities of the Hivites in that area of Canaan (vs. 17).

There is something else about these Gibeonites: they are Hivites (vs. 7). Do you know where Israel encountered these Hivites before? Back in Genesis 34.

Back in that chapter, Shechem, the Prince of the Hivites, raped Dinah the daughter of Jacob. When her brothers Simeon and Levi heard about what happened, they tricked the Hivites into circumcising themselves in order to intermarry with Jacob's family. When those Hivites were healing, Simeon and Levi went in there by themselves and slaughtered the whole city. The Hivites here in Joshua 9 undoubtedly remember the last encounter their kin had []{#c100.xhtml_page_167}with the Jews and don't want to tangle with them again.

Now look at that thing. Two hundred and eighty-seven years earlier, Simeon and Levi had deceived those Hivites, and now their descendants are about to reap the deception practiced by their fathers 287 years ago. That Bible says, ["Be not deceived; God is not mocked: for whatsoever a man soweth, that shall he also reap"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 6:7). As God is my witness, I was reaping things in my 50s I had sown in my 20s. The Bookkeeper keeps long accounts.

Unlike the Kings of verse 1, the Gibeonites figure out really quickly what's going to happen to them if they try to fight against Joshua. They looked at what happened to Jericho and Ai and "read the handwriting on the wall." So they ["work wilily"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 4) and come up with a plan to trick Joshua into making ["a league"]{.class_s2FW} with them (vs. 6).

[Wilily]{.class_s2FX} is the adverbial form of the word [wily.]{.class_s2FX} It means "crafty," "tricky," "clever." It is not really an archaic word, but with the American education system in the shape in which it is today, some readers may not be familiar with it. The old storybooks used to talk about the "wily fox"; that's where Looney Toons got its idea for Wile E. Coyote. When a woman is trying to trap a man into marriage, she is said to use her "womanly wiles."

The Gibeonites' plan was to send some men to Joshua dressed up as ambassadors ["from a far country"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). In other words, [they professed to be something they weren't.]{.class_s2FX} The spiritual lesson for the Christian is to watch out for [false professors.]{.class_s2FX}

Paul said the apostles were ["ambassadors for Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:20). But there were fellows running around claiming to be apostles when they [weren't]{.class_s2FX} (Rev. 2:2). They were ["false apostles"]{.class_s2FW} pretending to be ["apostles of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 11:13); that is, they were [false ambassadors.]{.class_s2FX} They pretended to be ["ambassadors for Christ"]{.class_s2FW} when they were really [ministers of the Devil]{.class_s2FX} (2 Cor. 11:14--15).

The false ambassadors haven't gone away. They're still running around, causing trouble. They claim to have [apostolic succession]{.class_s2FX} from Matthew 16 when they [don't.]{.class_s2FX} They claim to have the [apostolic signs]{.class_s2FX} when they [don't.]{.class_s2FX} They claim to be God's "Apostle" ("Messenger," "Prophet," whatever) when the Bible says Jesus Christ is ["the Apostle and High Priest of our profession"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_168} (Heb. 3:1). Mark it down, in this day, if you run into someone calling himself an apostle, that bird is a [liar]{.class_s2FX} (Rev. 2:2).

The Gibeonites put on a good act. The "saddlebags" on their "mounts" (["sacks upon their asses"]{.class_s2FW}---vs. 4) were all ["old"]{.class_s2FW}; their wine skins were old and worn out (["old, and rent, and bound up"]{.class_s2FW}---vs. 4). The soles were coming off their shoes and were being held on by string (the word ["clouted"]{.class_s2FW} in vs. 5 is an archaic word meaning "patched" or "mended"). Their clothes were practically in rags, and their bread was all moldy and stale. Everything was made to look as if they had been on a long journey to get to Joshua when they had traveled [less than three days]{.class_s2FX} (vss. 16--17).

Now all of those things are perfect pictures of the man who poses as an "ambassador for Christ" when he [isn't.]{.class_s2FX} Jesus said, ["Beware of false prophets, which come to you in sheep's clothing, but inwardly they are ravening wolves"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 7:15). False ambassadors [counterfeit poverty]{.class_s2FX} (the ["old sacks"]{.class_s2FW}). They mess around with "old wine," like Christian Brothers Distillery. Their ["feet"]{.class_s2FW} aren't ["shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:15); they aren't ["beautiful"]{.class_s2FW} from preaching ["the gospel of peace"]{.class_s2FW} and bringing ["glad tidings of good things"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 10:15). They are shod in shoes that are old and patched from walking in the world. They are in the ["filthy rags"]{.class_s2FW} of their own self-righteousness, and their "preaching" is as dry as dust.

The Gibeonites claimed to be ["from a far country"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). In the Scriptures, the ["far country"]{.class_s2FW} can either be a picture of [Heaven]{.class_s2FX} (Prov. 25:25; Luke 19:12) or the Devil's country, [Babylon]{.class_s2FX} (Luke 15:13; Isa. 39:3). From an historical perspective, verse 6 refers to the latter. But from the spiritual viewpoint of the ["false apostles"]{.class_s2FW} of 2 Corinthians 11, it is a reference to those false ambassadors claiming to bring ["good news from a far country"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 25:25) when they are preaching ["another gospel"]{.class_s2FW} and perverting ["the gospel of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 1:6--7).

["Make ye a league with us."]{.class_s2FW} "Make an agreement with us; let's all just get along. Don't be a schismatic troublemaker; be kind and sweet. Let's all work together as one big, happy family." That's exactly what those Jews [weren't]{.class_s2FX} supposed to do.

["I will deliver the inhabitants of the land into your hand; and thou shalt drive them out before thee. Thou shalt make no covenant with them, nor with their gods"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 23:31--32).

["Take heed to thyself, lest thou make a covenant with the inhabitants of the land whither thou goest, lest it be for a snare in the midst of thee"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 34:12).

["And when the LORD thy God shall deliver them before thee; thou shalt smite them, and utterly destroy them; thou shalt make no covenant with them, nor shew mercy unto them"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 7:2).

The Jews weren't to make any agreement with those heathen nations in the land, because the Jews would be seduced into worshipping those pagan peoples' false gods and committing all the abominations that went along with that worship.

Verse 8:[ "And they said unto Joshua, We are thy servants."]{.class_s2FW} No, they weren't, but they are about to be. When Joshua does find out who they actually are, he makes them ["bondmen"]{.class_s2FW} to the Tabernacle (vs. 23). That Bible says, ["For by thy words thou shalt be justified, and by thy words thou shalt be condemned"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 12:37). Those Gibeonites receive the judgment they put on themselves with their words: ["We are thy servants."]{.class_s2FW}

Now Joshua asks two very important questions in verse 8: ["Who are ye? and from whence come ye?"]{.class_s2FW} But he doesn't follow through on them. He doesn't get any answer at all to the first question, and he doesn't check out the answer to the second question.

["Who are ye?"]{.class_s2FW} They never tell him, not even by a lie. They were [Hivites]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 7). But they gloss over that little detail, hoping that Joshua wasn't paying attention. [He wasn't.]{.class_s2FX} They didn't have to lie about their people because Joshua never insisted they answer his question: ["Who are ye?"]{.class_s2FW}

["Whence come ye?"]{.class_s2FW} They say, ["from a very far country."]{.class_s2FW} That was a lie; they were less than three days away from the camp at Gilgal (vs. 16---the whole army didn't move as fast as a small group of men could). But Joshua never asks [what]{.class_s2FX} country. They are lying to []{#c100.xhtml_page_170}save their own hides. They know that Joshua isn't going to spare any of the people of the land or make a league with any of them.

Notice in verses 9--10 that they mention what happened in Egypt nearly 43 years earlier and what happened to Sihon and Og on the other side of Jordan two years earlier. They [omit]{.class_s2FX} Jericho and Ai because those just took place. They wanted Joshua to think they had been making the trek from Babylon or Persia for the last two years (see the amount of time Herod allowed for the wise men to arrive at Jerusalem from the East---Matt. 2:16).

So the first thing they did to convince Joshua they were[ "from a very far country"]{.class_s2FW} was by something they [didn't]{.class_s2FX} say. Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn said that when the Communists took over Russia, they didn't mind the preachers saying that God is good; what they wouldn't let them say was that [the Devil is bad.]{.class_s2FX} The problem with Billy Graham and the New Evangelicals is not what they say; it's what they [won't say.]{.class_s2FX} They won't preach against particular sins. They won't say a sinner goes to Hell for rejecting Christ. If they do, they won't mention the fact that Hell is [eternal fire;]{.class_s2FX} it is just "separation from God." Those Gibeonites deceived Joshua by what they [didn't say.]{.class_s2FX}

Second, they present Joshua with something he can [see.]{.class_s2FX} They show him the dry, moldy bread, the torn, patched wine skins, and the ragged clothes. "See all this old, worn-out stuff? That's [proof]{.class_s2FX} we have been on a long journey." It was all a [lie.]{.class_s2FX} The idea was: "You can trust your eyes." No, he couldn't.

That's the argument the atheists, agnostics, and evolutionists use; and it is just as damnable from their lips as it was from the Gibeonites. "Look here, you can't see God, so He must not exist." Well, you can't see air or gravity either. Do you think [they]{.class_s2FX} don't exist? "Well, we know evolution is true; just look at this statue of a dinosaur." Those bones and models in museums don't mean evolution took place; all they prove is that someone is good with chicken wire, plaster of Paris, and paint.

You can't always trust your eyes. Just look at any stage magician: he performs [illusions]{.class_s2FX} made to make you [see]{.class_s2FX} one thing while he [does]{.class_s2FX} another. That's why the Bible says, ["we walk by faith, not by sight"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:7). ["Faith is the SUBSTANCE of things hoped for, the EVIDENCE of things not seen"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_171} (Heb. 11:1). In other words, when God gives you something to believe that you can't see, He gives you substantive evidence to believe it. When God wants you to believe His word, He gives you [fulfilled prophecy]{.class_s2FX} as the evidence of its truth (see our comments on 6:26).

Now what was Joshua's problem? Look at verse 14.

"And the men took of their victuals, and ASKED NOT COUNSEL AT THE MOUTH OF THE LORD."

There are two times Joshua messes up: here and at Ai. Both times were the result of him not praying about the matter. He should have gone over to the Ark and gotten down on his knees and said, "Lord, what about these fellows?" But he doesn't, and he ends up in what a friend of mine who was the director of a rescue mission called "an unscriptural situation." He made a league with a bunch of heathen idolaters, and that sowed the seeds for what took place in the book of Judges (see Judg. 1--2).

Now the lesson for the Christian is to watch out around whom he hangs. That Bible says:

["Be ye not unequally yoked together with unbelievers: for what fellowship hath righteousness with unrighteousness? and what communion hath light with darkness? And what concord hath Christ with Belial? or what part hath he that believeth with an infidel? And what agreement hath the temple of God with idols? for ye are the temple of the living God . . . Wherefore come out from among them, and be ye separate, saith the Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 6:14--17).

The Christian is to separate himself from this evil world system (Gal. 1:4) because ["evil communications corrupt good manners"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 15:33). If a good apple is thrown in a bushel basket of bad apples, it won't make the bad apples good; it will be turned bad by the bad apples. You are not to be in close fellowship with lost people or become involved with them in such a way where you have to go where they go or do what they do in violation of the Scriptures.

Now don't misunderstand me. You have to live in this lost world and do business in it; that is unavoidable. But there are certain situations in which you [don't]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_172} have to become involved. You don't have to marry an unsaved person; if you do, you have yoked yourself with that person so that wherever he or she goes and whatever he or she does, you are a part of it, whether you like it or not. You don't have to partner with or work for a business which has the [sole]{.class_s2FX} purpose of doing something or promoting something unscriptural.

I had a Christian tell me once, "I can't live a separated life, Bro. Ruckman, because I'd lose my job. I drive a beer truck for a living, and if I lived a separated life, I'd have to quit my job driving a beer truck." Well, if God can't give you any better job than driving a beer truck, [kick Him off the throne.]{.class_s2FX} That's a lack of faith on your part; that's not a lack of provision on God's.

Brethren, that Bible says, ["Can two walk together, except they be agreed?"]{.class_s2FW} (Amos 3:3). You may have trouble getting along with your mother, your father, your kids, your spouse, your relatives, and your friends; but there is one Person with whom it is essential to get along. If you can't get along with anybody else, you had better get along with [the Lord.]{.class_s2FX} One of these days, you are going to get yourself in a sure enough mess where the only Person who can help you is [God.]{.class_s2FX} When you get in a situation like that, you had better have a Partner with whom you can see eye to eye.

Now there are some important lessons we need to learn from the deception of the Gibeonites.

1. [The deadliest lie is one that is mostly true.]{.class_s2FX} You can't sell a bushel of bad apples without having some good ones on the top. What made the Gibeonites' lie so convincing was the [truth]{.class_s2FX} that was in it. They [did]{.class_s2FX} come to Joshua ["because of the name of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 9). They [did]{.class_s2FX} hear ["the fame of him, and all that he did in Egypt. And all that he did to the two kings of the Amorites"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 9--10). Everything in verse 11 was true: that was exactly what their leaders told them to do. They did take their bread hot out of the oven, and it was dry and moldy when they saw Joshua (vs. 12). All the rest of it, though, was a [lie.]{.class_s2FX} Eighty percent of what they said was the [truth,]{.class_s2FX} and it was all used to put across [a bald-faced lie.]{.class_s2FX}

In light of that fact, the deadliest "Bible" on the market is one that is most like the [real thing]{.class_s2FX} ([AV]{.class_s2FX} 1611). The worst Bible on the market is not the Liberal [RSV]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_173} that attacks the Virgin Birth in Isaiah 7:14. The [NASV, ESV,]{.class_s2FX} and [NIV]{.class_s2FX} are a little closer; but they come from the same text as the [RSV]{.class_s2FX} and the Jesuit [Rheims]{.class_s2FX} version of 1582. They will attack the Virgin Birth in Luke 2:33, the Trinity in 1 John 5:7, the Deity of Christ in 1 Timothy 3:16, etc., just like the [RSV]{.class_s2FX} does.

No, the deadliest "Bible" is the one that claims to come from the same Hebrew and Greek texts as the [real thing]{.class_s2FX} ([AV]{.class_s2FX} 1611): the ["New" King James Version.]{.class_s2FX} It won't attack the words of God by getting rid of 36,000--64,000 of them like the [NASV]{.class_s2FX} or the [NIV.]{.class_s2FX} Instead, it will attack the words of God in English by retranslating the words of the correct text according to the opinions of lost and apostate scholarship. The danger is that in many places it [sounds]{.class_s2FX} like the [King James]{.class_s2FX} without [being]{.class_s2FX} the [King James.]{.class_s2FX} It is actually just the readings of the [ASV]{.class_s2FX} smuggled into the [Authorized]{.class_s2FX} text (see our work on [About the New King James Version]{.class_s2FX}).

2\. [You should watch out when the lost world patronizes Christianity.]{.class_s2FX} In the days of Zerubbabel, the Samaritans tried pandering to the Jews: ["Let us build with you: for we seek your God, as ye do"]{.class_s2FW} (Ezra 4:2). That was a [half]{.class_s2FX} truth: they not only [feared God,]{.class_s2FX} they also [served idols]{.class_s2FX} (2 Kings 17:41). The [real]{.class_s2FX} truth was that they were ["the ADVERSARIES of Judah and Benjamin"]{.class_s2FW} trying to [stop]{.class_s2FX} the rebuilding of the Temple (Ezra 4:1). Christian, when the world tries to get on your good side, you had better take ["heed to the sword . . . in Joab's hand"]{.class_s2FW} (cf. 2 Sam. 20:10).

3. ["Religion" is often the futile works of lost sinners who fear God.]{.class_s2FX} There are lost folks who fear God; sure they do. They just don't fear Him [according to the truth of the Scriptures.]{.class_s2FX} Paul said those Christ-rejecting Jews of his day had ["a zeal of God, but not according to knowledge"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 10:2). They feared God enough to try to do something to please Him, but they weren't doing it according to the revelation He had given them through His Son (Heb. 1:1--2). That's how a lot of Roman Catholics are. They fear God; they are just trying to appease Him the [wrong way.]{.class_s2FX}

These Gibeonites heard the same stories Rahab did (see 2:9); they just weren't willing to make the same commitment Rahab did to that God (2:10). Instead, they decided to use their own devices to get into God's "good graces." That's what nearly all "religion" is: [man's]{.class_s2FX} ways of satisfying God's demands instead of [God's]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_174} ways.

4. [Local churches can become filled with an unregenerate membership.]{.class_s2FX} The Gibeonites wanted to "jine up" with the Israelites without accepting their God. A local church can get filled up with people who are just as lost as a goose in a horse race. They are there because of [ancestry:]{.class_s2FX} momma and daddy belonged to the church, so they do too. That thing sometimes goes back for [generations.]{.class_s2FX}

A church can become filled with unregenerate members through [relatives,]{.class_s2FX} especially through [marriage.]{.class_s2FX} My daddy was a vestryman in the Episcopalian Church. He didn't come from an Episcopalian family; all my dad's people were [Baptist]{.class_s2FX} farmers from Illinois. But my mother was a high-class Episcopalian from Pasadena, California, so my father attended the Episcopalian Church.

A lot of little country churches are controlled by one family. Everybody in the church is related to everybody else. Everybody attends because that's where the kin are. The New Birth doesn't factor into it at all.

5. [Then some lost folk join the church to have]{.class_s2FX} ["a form of godliness"]{.class_s2FW} [while]{.class_s2FX} ["denying the power thereof"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 3:5). In other words, they see the [activity]{.class_s2FX} and want to be part of it without ever committing to Jesus Christ. They join because they are taught the sacraments or the ordinances can do something for them, so they participate in the religious activity whether they believe it or not. If you have ever dealt with Catholics, you know the average Catholic either doesn't know or doesn't believe about half of what the Catholic Church teaches. But he has always been taught the church is the means of salvation, so he attends and gets sprinkled and takes the Mass and confesses to the Priest out of a kind of religious habit.

6.[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}[Lost sinners slip into the church because they pick up the language of the saved.]{.class_s2FX} That was a lot more prevalent when this country was a Bible-reading nation. It was easy to pick up the Christian vocabulary and pass off as a Christian when the person had never been born again at all.

7. [Unsaved people join Christian groups for what I call "vicarious philanthropy."]{.class_s2FX} They want to pay for their sins by being good to folks. There is many a businessman who joins a church or attends the Christian Businessman's Association to appease his []{#c100.xhtml_page_175}conscience. A lot of these Socialistic organizations like the "Department of Children and Families" (the old HEW) are staffed by unsaved people trying to atone for their sins by doing what they believe is good to their fellow man.

8. [You can get a church full of unsaved people who want to share in the social benefits of a group of religious folk.]{.class_s2FX} They want a program for their kids. If they are poorer folks, they want to hang around a congregation of people who will help them with their groceries, rent, and electric bills. If they are businessmen, they want the contacts to promote their business. They want access to the "Family Life Center." They want to participate in the softball program. They profess to be Christians to take advantage of the [social benefits.]{.class_s2FX}

9. [Then there are "upper-crust" folks who want to feel good about themselves by helping out the ones they scorn.]{.class_s2FX} Those are the doctors, lawyers, and bankers in town who join a church to help folks out while the whole time they look with disdain on real, Bible-believing Christians. They think hard Bible preaching [stinks,]{.class_s2FX} so if they can, they get in leadership positions like deacons, trustees, and on pulpit committees. They get them a "nice" little preacher whom they can keep like a canary in a cage and hear him "chirp" and "tweet" every Sunday morning. And that brings us to our last point.

10. [The unsaved join Christian works to gain control of them.]{.class_s2FX} You would be surprised how many Universities in the United States started out as [Christian]{.class_s2FX} works and were gradually taken over by unsaved professors. These guys study Christianity and sign their consent to professions of faith when they believe nothing of the kind. They get in the classroom and introduce their infidelity, and when a student complains, they hide behind "academic freedom." The administration doesn't want to look like a bunch of dogmatic, closed-minded "book burners," so they let the infidelity slide. Well, if you allow one infidel for "academic excellency," there's no reason not to allow more. So within a decade or two, the whole institution is shot through with professors and teachers who are no more "Christian" than Madalyn Murray O'Hair or Richard Dawkins. Pretty soon, all you have is a hot-bed of international Socialism. With "academic freedom" comes the liquor, the drugs, and the promiscuity until all []{#c100.xhtml_page_176}you have is a breeding ground for sot drunks, dopeheads, and whores and whoremongers.

You say, "What schools are you talking about, Ruckman?" Oh, the University of Chicago; it started out as a [Baptist]{.class_s2FX} school. Stetson University here in Florida was a [Southern Baptist]{.class_s2FX} school up until a few years ago. After "panty raids," rock concerts, dances, etc., it finally dropped the pretence. Princeton was a [Presbyterian]{.class_s2FX} school to train ministers. Harvard and Yale were set up to train ministers. Would you guess that of Harvard and Yale today? Those schools trained ministers, they trained church planters for the wilderness, and they trained missionaries to the Indians. Today, they are Liberal hellholes, along with Emory University ([Methodist]{.class_s2FX}), Wake Forest University ([Southern Baptist]{.class_s2FX}), Duke University ([Methodist]{.class_s2FX}), and Dartmouth College ([Puritan]{.class_s2FX}).

Here in Joshua 9, the Gibeonites are attempting to infiltrate the ranks of Israel to "get in on the blessing" without any commitment or obedience to Jehovah God. They are what the Scripture calls a ["mixed multitude."]{.class_s2FW} That was the problem when Israel came out of Egypt (Exod. 12:38), and that was the problem when they returned from captivity (Neh. 13:3). All the ["mixed multitude"]{.class_s2FW} wants is to "get in on the goodies" without ["bearing his reproach"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 13:13).
