16 And it came to pass at the end of three days after they had made a league with them, that they heard that they were their neighbours, and that they dwelt among them.

17 And the children of Israel journeyed, and came unto their cities on the third day. Now their cities were Gibeon, and Chephirah, and Beeroth, and Kirjathjearim.

18 And the children of Israel smote them not, because the princes of the congregation had sworn unto them by the LORD God of Israel. And all the congregation murmured against the princes.

19 But all the princes said unto all the congregation, We have sworn unto them by the LORD God of Israel: now therefore we may not touch them.

20 This we will do to them; we will even let them live, []{#c100.xhtml_page_177}lest wrath be upon us, because of the oath which we sware unto them.

21 And the princes said unto them, Let them live; but let them be hewers of wood and drawers of water unto all the congregation; as the princes had promised them.

22 And Joshua called for them, and he spake unto them, saying, Wherefore have ye beguiled us, saying, We are very far from you; when ye dwell among us?

23 Now therefore ye are cursed, and there shall none of you be freed from being bondmen, and hewers of wood and drawers of water for the house of my God.

24 And they answered Joshua, and said, Because it was certainly told thy servants, how that the LORD thy God commanded his servant Moses to give you all the land, and to destroy all the inhabitants of the land from before you, therefore we were sore afraid of our lives because of you, and have done this thing.

25 And now, behold, we are in thine hand: as it seemeth good and right unto thee to do unto us, do.

26 And so did he unto them, and delivered them out of the hand of the children of Israel, that they slew them not.

27 And Joshua made them that day hewers of wood and drawers of water for the congregation, and for the altar of the LORD, even unto this day, in the place which he should choose.

Joshua does what he wasn't suppose to do: he makes a league with the Gibeonites (vs. 15). He doesn't pray about it (vs. 14), and he swears ["by the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} to let them live (vs. 18).

Well, the Israelites travel down the road a three-day journey and find out the Gibeonites are ["right next door"]{.class_s2FX} to them (vss. 16--17). But by the time they find out the "ambassadors from a far country" are [Hivites living in the land,]{.class_s2FX} it is too late to do anything about it; the oath had already been taken (vs. 19). It couldn't be broken without the Lord punishing the Israelites for doing so (see 2 Sam. 21:1--2).

Numbers 30:2 says, ["If a man vow a vow unto the LORD, or []{#c100.xhtml_page_178}swear an oath to bind his soul with a bond; he shall not break his word, he shall do according to all that proceedeth out of his mouth."]{.class_s2FW}

The command in the Old Testament if you make a vow to the Lord or swear to do something by His name is you are to keep that vow, and if you don't, you are sinning.

["When thou shalt vow a vow unto the LORD thy God, thou shalt not slack to pay it: for the LORD thy God will surely require it of thee; and it would be sin in thee"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 23:21).

Now no one is [required]{.class_s2FX} to make a vow to the Lord.

["But if thou shalt forbear to vow, it shall be no sin in thee"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 23:22).

In fact, Solomon said that it is better not to vow than to vow and not pay (Eccl. 5:5). You need to keep that in mind when making promises to the Lord. You would be better off not making any promise at all than to make a promise and not follow through on it. Some Christians get under conviction in a sermon and make a commitment to do something without considering the cost (see our comments on Luke 14:28--32 in that Commentary). There's nothing wrong with responding to what you hear preached, but don't make any promise to God that you can't or have no intention to keep. That includes "faith-promise giving" and "stewardship pledges."

Now there was a provision in the Law if a person made a vow about something that was wrong without knowing it. Look at Leviticus 5:4--6.

["Or if a soul swear, pronouncing with his lips to do evil, or to do good, whatsoever it be that a man shall pronounce with an oath, and it be hid from him ]{.class_s2FW}\[i.e., he doesn't know what the Law says about the matter---Lev. 5:13\][; when he knoweth of it, then he shall be guilty in one of these]{.class_s2FW} \[the old saying is "ignorance of the law is no excuse"\][. And it shall be, when he shall be guilty in one of these things]{.class_s2FW} \[he made a rash oath without knowing all the facts and ends up sinning in his oath\][, that he shall confess that he hath sinned in that thing"]{.class_s2FW}; and Leviticus 5:6 gives you the offering the fellow was supposed to make to atone for his sinning by ignorance through his oath.

Now that is going to be pertinent when we get into Jephthah's rash vow in Judges 11. Jephthah had an "out" with his vow, but he didn't know the Scripture. In the days of the judges, ["every man did that which was right in his own eyes"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 17:6, 21:25). But Joshua was to go by ["the book of the law"]{.class_s2FW} (see our remarks under 1:8). So either what you are reading here in Joshua 9 is an example of not only Joshua's prayerlessness (vs. 14), but him not consulting the Book to find out what it said in the matter, or the command in Leviticus 5 was to [individuals]{.class_s2FX} and not to the nation [corporately.]{.class_s2FX}

If it is the former, then God made the vow to stand when the leaders committed themselves to it. A good example of that is Saul. Whenever Saul opened his mouth to swear by the Lord, God always held him to it. Saul never repented of any vow he ever swore, so God made it stick.

One time Saul swore a curse on any of his people who ate before he had overcome his enemies in battle, and his son Jonathan wasn't around when the vow was made and ended up eating some honey. Well, the people won the battle, but they were so famished that they ended up breaking the Law by eating the spoils of the battle raw with the blood. Saul blamed that on the person who broke his vow and swore again that that person would die even if it were his own son Jonathan. When God showed Saul by lot (see the process back in Josh. 7:16--18) that he and Jonathan were the guilty party, Saul was prepared to kill his own son for the consequences of his own rash oath, but the people wouldn't let Saul do it because it was Jonathan who led the people to victory. You will find that story in 1 Samuel 14. But because Saul had sworn without [any]{.class_s2FX} repentance, [any]{.class_s2FX} confession, or [any]{.class_s2FX} atonement, God followed through on Saul's oath; and Jonathan died along with his father in 1 Samuel 31.

In light of the above, the application to the New Testament believer is that he can't use his [ignorance of the Bible]{.class_s2FX} as an excuse for [sin.]{.class_s2FX} Christian, you are [responsible]{.class_s2FX} for what is in that Book whether you [know]{.class_s2FX} what is in the Bible or not. Christians can be really stupid sometimes, did you know that? They avoid reading the Bible thinking they won't be held accountable for what they don't know.

You wouldn't get away with that excuse if an officer pulled you over for running a stop sign. "Well, officer, I didn't see the stop sign." So he takes you back to it and makes you read it out loud. "I didn't see it." Well, you [could]{.class_s2FX} have seen it; you [should]{.class_s2FX} have seen it. It was your responsibility as a licensed driver to be [looking]{.class_s2FX} for it. If you can't get away with that excuse with a man, what makes you think you are going to get away with it with God?

The Lord gave you two commands in Scripture that strip you of the excuse of ignorance. Naturally they have been removed from all the new "Bibles" to make you think the Lord will give you a break for not knowing His word. They are John 5:39 and 2 Timothy 2:15.

John 5:39---["SEARCH THE SCRIPTURES; for in them ye think ye have eternal life: and they are they which testify of me."]{.class_s2FW}

The modern translations have all changed that verse so that it is no longer a command. They changed the [imperative]{.class_s2FX} to a [declarative:]{.class_s2FX} "You search the Scriptures because you think [by]{.class_s2FX} them you have eternal life." That completely "guts" the point of what Christ said. He wasn't making a mere observation of what the Jews did; He was telling them that if they thought they could get eternal life from the Scriptures (and they [could]{.class_s2FX}---John 6:63), then they had better search them because the Scriptures testified of [Him,]{.class_s2FX} and [He]{.class_s2FX} was the one who could give them eternal life.

Not content to stop you from [searching]{.class_s2FX} the Scriptures, the new "Bibles" also got rid of the command to [study]{.class_s2FX} the Bible in 2 Timothy 2:15. So with no command to [search]{.class_s2FX} the Scriptures and no command to [study]{.class_s2FX} the Scriptures, the Christian is relieved of his obligation to [know]{.class_s2FX} what God said so he can [obey]{.class_s2FX} it. [You better hadn't bet on it.]{.class_s2FX}

That [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible is still available here in the United States. No Christian will be able to stand before the Lord and say, "I didn't know." You [could]{.class_s2FX} have known, you [should]{.class_s2FX} have known, and it is your obligation as a child of God to [find out]{.class_s2FX} what He said and [do it]{.class_s2FX} (James 1:22).

Now there is something else in regard to this oath thing that every Christian should remember. If a man ever makes a rash oath that he has no business making---like a Masonic blood oath---and later, when he becomes a Christian, realizes he has made a fool of []{#c100.xhtml_page_181}himself, he is not obligated to keep such a thing as long as he follows 1 John 1:9.

"If we confess our sins, he is faithful and just to forgive us our sins, and to cleanse us from ALL unrighteousness."

The Christian doesn't need to sacrifice sheep or rams or goats or doves or pigeons; he already has his atonement. I mean, ["the blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanseth us from ALL sin,"]{.class_s2FW} brother (1 John 1:7). Confess the sin of making that rash oath, get it under the blood, and then get out of that unscriptural organization and live for God. Don't sit around moaning and beating yourself up over something for which Christ has forgiven you.

Back to Joshua 9: ["Now therefore ye are cursed, and there shall none of you be freed from being bondmen"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 23). This is the [literal]{.class_s2FX} fulfillment of Noah's prophecy in Genesis 9:25--26.

"Cursed be Canaan; a SERVANT OF SERVANTS shall he be unto his brethren . . . Blessed be the LORD God of Shem; and CANAAN SHALL BE HIS SERVANT."

There is no doubt about what the word ["servant"]{.class_s2FW} means in Genesis 9: it is a [slave.]{.class_s2FX} The Gibeonites were [Hivites]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 7), and the Hivites were descended from [Canaan]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 10:15--17). The Gibeonites were made ["bondmen"]{.class_s2FW} by Joshua for their deception. That's descendants of [Canaan]{.class_s2FX} being slaves to descendants of [Shem.]{.class_s2FX}

The Gibeonites were condemned forever to be ["hewers of wood and drawers of water for the house of my God."]{.class_s2FW} Now what is peculiar about that statement is, at the time, God had no ["house"]{.class_s2FW}; what He had was a [tent]{.class_s2FX}---the Tabernacle. But look at 1 Samuel 1:9.

"So Hannah rose up after they had eaten in Shiloh, and after they had drunk. Now Eli the priest sat upon a seat by a post of the TEMPLE of the LORD."

There was no ["temple"]{.class_s2FW} in 1 Samuel 1. That took place during the time of the judges before Samuel was born. The Temple wasn't built until the time of Solomon, nearly 171 years later. But the Tabernacle was referred to as the ["temple"]{.class_s2FW} in 1 Samuel 1:9, 3:3, 22:7 because it was patterned after the Temple in Heaven (Heb. 8:5 cf. Rev. 11:19, 14:17, 15:5).

Do you know why that is so significant? Because there will be a []{#c100.xhtml_page_182}Jewish temple rebuilt just before or during the Tribulation (2 Thess. 2:3--4). Well, right now, those Jews can't build anything on the Temple mount because there's a [Moslem mosque standing there]{.class_s2FX} (the Mosque of Omar, the Dome of the Rock). In 1968, the head of the supreme Moslem council in Jerusalem stated, "The Moslems will never permit [any]{.class_s2FX} Jew to pray in [this area.]{.class_s2FX} We are prepared to [die]{.class_s2FX} for this."

In order for a temple to be rebuilt, the Jews have five options:

1. [Tear down the Dome]{.class_s2FX} (Rabbi Levy, Tremont Temple, Bronx, New York, 1948). Of course, this would result in a Moslem ["jihad"]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}("holy war") against the Jews.

2. [Buy back the mount from the Moslems.]{.class_s2FX} Of course, this [ignores the fact]{.class_s2FX} that the mount had been [bought and paid for]{.class_s2FX} 1,500 years before Mohammed was born (2 Sam. 24:18--24; 1 Chron. 21:18--25). Unfortunately for the poor, oppressed, Stateless Palestinian "refugees," their own rulers had already turned down an offer of \$100 million for it in 1968.

3. [Wait for God to bring down the "Dome" with a natural]{.class_s2FX} (or [supernatural]{.class_s2FX}) [disaster.]{.class_s2FX} Eventually, this will happen (see Zech. 14:4--5), but for a Jewish temple to be rebuilt so that the Antichrist can sit in it during the Tribulation (Dan. 11:31; Matt. 24:15), it would have to occur at least four years before the Second Advent.

4. [Build the temple at a different site in Jerusalem.]{.class_s2FX} The problem with this is it would violate what the Scriptures say about the location of the future temple (see Isa. 2:2--3; Psa. 2:6).

5 [Try to rebuild it as a "joint project" with the Moslems.]{.class_s2FX}

Now regardless of how the Jews gain access to the Temple mount, the fact is that they would not necessarily have to erect a stone structure as they did in the days of Solomon, Zerubbabel, and Herod. Look at Amos 9:11.

"In that day will I raise up the TABERNACLE OF DAVID that is fallen, and close up the breaches thereof; and I will raise up this ruins, and I will build it as in the days of old."

["The tabernacle of David"]{.class_s2FW} was the tent David pitched for the Ark when he brought it to Jerusalem (2 Sam. 6:17). The fact of the matter is that the prophecies concerning a rebuilt temple during the Tribulation could be fulfilled with a reconstructed tabernacle of one []{#c100.xhtml_page_183}sort or another: either the full thing or a tent for the Ark. As we saw from 1 Samuel 1:9, that tabernacle could be considered a "temple."

Verse 27: ["And Joshua made them that day hewers of wood and drawers of water for the congregation, and for the altar of the LORD, even unto this day, IN THE PLACE WHICH HE SHOULD CHOOSE."]{.class_s2FW} The ["even unto this day"]{.class_s2FW} indicates an addition added to the book of Joshua around the time of Samuel or David (the Gibeonites show back up in 2 Sam. 21:1--9 during the reign of David).

But more importantly, notice the phrase ["in the place which he should choose."]{.class_s2FW} That's God choosing [one location ]{.class_s2FX}for the Ark, as He said He would back in Deuteronomy 12:5, 16:2, 6, 16. During the time of Joshua and the judges, that place was Shiloh (Josh 18:1 cf. Jer 7:12). The Bible says God ["forsook the tabernacle of Shiloh"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 78:60) because of ["the wickedness of my people Israel" ]{.class_s2FW}(Jer. 7:12). That was part of the judgment brought on the house of Eli about which you read in 1 Samuel 2--4.

The Ark was captured by the Philistines, and when it was brought back to Israel, it never did end up in the Tabernacle again. It was moved around until David finally brought it to [Jerusalem ]{.class_s2FX}in 2 Samuel 6. [Shiloh ]{.class_s2FX}was destroyed, and the Tabernacle, with the Brazen Altar, was moved around until it ended up at Gibeon where its slaves were (1 Chron. 16:39, 21:29; 2 Chron. 1:3, 13) until Solomon built the Temple at [Jerusalem.]{.class_s2FX}

The psalmist wrote, ["Moreover he refused the tabernacle of Joseph, and chose not the tribe of Ephraim ]{.class_s2FW}\[that's where Shiloh was located\][ : But chose the tribe of Judah, the mount Zion which he loved ]{.class_s2FW}\[[Jerusalem]{.class_s2FX}\][" ]{.class_s2FW}(Psa. 78:67--68).

God told David, ["But I have chosen JERUSALEM, that my name might be there; and have chosen David to be over my people Israel" ]{.class_s2FW}(2 Chron. 6:6). [That's ]{.class_s2FX}the city where God said He would live here on earth ["for ever" ]{.class_s2FW}(Psa. 132:13--14). One day when "God in the flesh" rules and reigns over this earth (1 Tim. 3:16 cf. Zech. 14:9), He will do it from [Jerusalem]{.class_s2FX} (Zech. 14:16--21), because it is ["the city of the great King"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 5:35). Mecca, Medina, Rome, Geneva, New York, London, Washington, D.C., etc., are all [out.]{.class_s2FX} That's O-U-T: OUT!

Jerusalem is [His]{.class_s2FX} city, where [He]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c100.xhtml_page_184} will one day rule. He is going to give every Moslem, European, American, Roman Catholic, and Greek Orthodox the boot.

[]{#c14V.xhtml}

# Chapter 10 {.heading_s2B}

10:1 Now it came to pass, when Adonizedek king of Jerusalem had heard how Joshua had taken Ai, and had utterly destroyed it; as he had done to Jericho and her king, so he had done to Ai and her king; and how the inhabitants of Gibeon had made peace with Israel, and were among them;

2 That they feared greatly, because Gibeon was a great city, as one of the royal cities, and because it was greater than Ai, and all the men thereof were mighty.

3 Wherefore Adonizedek king of Jerusalem sent unto Hoham king of Hebron, and unto Piram king of Jarmuth, and unto Japhia king of Lachish, and unto Debir king of Eglon, saying,

4 Come up unto me, and help me, that we may smite Gibeon: for it hath made peace with Joshua and with the children of Israel.

5 Therefore the five kings of the Amorites, the king of Jerusalem, the king of Hebron, the king of Jarmuth, the king of Lachish, the king of Eglon, gathered themselves together, and went up, they and all their hosts, and encamped before Gibeon, and made war against it.

Chapter 9 ends with ["the place which he should choose"]{.class_s2FW}; chapter 10 opens with ["Adonizedek king of JERUSALEM"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1). Jerusalem was ["the place"]{.class_s2FW} God chose to put His name (2 Chron. 6:6), but it certainly isn't here in Joshua 10.

The first time Jerusalem shows up in the Bible is in Genesis 14:18, where it is called ["Salem." "Salem"]{.class_s2FW} is the Hebrew word for [peace,]{.class_s2FX} so Jeru-salem is the "city of peace." That is an example of God's weird sense of humor. The "City of Peace" was attacked [33 times]{.class_s2FX} before 1949. "City of [Peace"]{.class_s2FX}---[what peace?!]{.class_s2FX}

When Joshua entered the land, that city was controlled by the [Amorites]{.class_s2FX} and the [Jebusites]{.class_s2FX} (10:5, 15:63) and was called ["Jebus"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 19:10; 1 Chron. 11:4) or ["Jebusi"]{.class_s2FW} (Josh. 18:28). The name []{#c14V.xhtml_page_186}means "trodden down," which is a more apt description of the place (see the Holy Spirit's commentary in Lam. 1:15; Dan. 8:13; Luke 21:24; Rev. 11:2).

The city was first taken from the Jebusites by Judah (Judg. 1:8) and then again by David (2 Sam. 5:6--9). Over the next 1,000 years, it was attacked by Shishak (2 Chron. 12:2--9), Jehoash (2 Kings 14:13--14), Rezin (2 Kings 16:5), three times by Nebuchadnezzar (2 Chron. 36:6; 2 Kings 24:10--12), and four more times during the intertestamental period.

After the close of the book of Acts, it was attacked twice by the Romans (A.D. 70, 135), then by the Persians (A.D. 614--Shahrbaraz), and then by the Byzantines (A.D. 629--Heradius). Between A.D. 638 and 1098, it was attacked by [seven]{.class_s2FX} different Moslem groups. The Catholics took it in the Crusades in 1099; the Moslem General Saladin took it back in 1187; Richard the Lionhearted recaptured the city in 1192; then the Khwarezmian Tartars took it from the Europeans in 1244. Between 1260 and 1840, it was attacked four more times by different Moslem groups (none of which were "Palestinians"), and it remained in the hands of the Ottoman Turks until 1917 when General Allenby liberated the city. [That's]{.class_s2FX} the "City of Peace." That doesn't include the "War of Liberation" in 1948 or the Six-Day War in 1967 or the [38 Moslem suicide bombings]{.class_s2FX} carried out by the "Intifada" between 1994 and 2004, or the rockets fired at the city by Saddam Hussein in 1991 and by the "Palestinians" in the Gaza Strip in 2012. "City of Peace"?! What are you talking about?!

But you see, there is a [reason]{.class_s2FX} why it is "the City of Peace." When God finally does send "peace on earth," He sends it [right there at that city]{.class_s2FX} (Hag. 2:7, 9; Psa. 76:2--3). The city awaits another battle. At that one, the entire military might of the UN gathers against Jerusalem (Zech. 12:2--3, 14:2), and when it does, the Creator Himself comes down to settle accounts with His creation (Zech. 14:7). He brings peace on earth the ultimate way: by mashing the opposition (200 million UN troops) into the ground until the blood runs up to the horses' bridles for 200 miles (Rev. 9:16--19, 14:18--20, 19:11--12; Isa. 63:1--6). Then it's bow down and kiss His feet or get smacked up side of the head with a two-inch galvanized iron pipe (Psa. 2:6--12).

Where does that happen? At [Jerusalem,]{.class_s2FX} []{#c14V.xhtml_page_187}["the city of the great King"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 5:35). [Nothing]{.class_s2FX} that Clinton (Hillary or Bill), Obama, Bush, Kerry, the UN, NATO, the EU, or the "Muslim Brotherhood" does (or will do) will alter one word of what you just read. It is more sure to take place than sunrise tomorrow morning (see Joel 3:15; Matt. 24:29; Rev. 6:12, 8:12, 16:10).

Back to Joshua 10:1. Notice the name of the King of Jerusalem: Adonizedek. The name means "Lord of righteousness" and should be set in contrast with the name of the first King of Jerusalem to show up in the Scriptures: Melchizedek (Gen. 14:18). The name Melchizedek means ["King of righteousness"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 7:2). Melchizedek was not only a King, he was a priest as well (Gen. 14:18; Heb. 7:1) and, as such, was a type of Christ (Heb. 7:3).

You would think with a name like "Lord of righteousness," Adonizedek would be a type of Christ too, but [he's not.]{.class_s2FX} In fact, he's just the [opposite.]{.class_s2FX} He's uniting a group of heathen Kings to [fight against]{.class_s2FX} the type of Christ here, and that's Joshua. So what you have here is a type of the Second Advent. Here is a King parading around as "Lord of righteousness" when he's working ["with all deceivableness of unrighteousness in them that perish"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Thess. 2:10). Adonizedek here is a picture of the [Antichrist.]{.class_s2FX}

In the Tribulation, ten Kings get together against the New Testament "Joshua" and the Jews. Out of those ten Kings comes a little King who rises up and knocks out three of the other Kings who were ahead of him. He takes over, and ten Kings reign with him. You can read about that in Daniel 7 and Revelation 17. That little King, of course, is the Antichrist. That's what Adonizedek and his buddies in verse 3 picture. They are types of the Antichrist and those ten Kings.

Now notice in verses 4--5 that the five Kings of verse 3 get together to wipe out the Gibeonites because they ["made peace with Joshua"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 4). There is a great spiritual lesson there for the Christian: [the lost world hates any friend of "Joshua,"]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}even a [neutral]{.class_s2FX} one. The Gibeonites weren't fighting; all they had done was declare a truce. When it came to the conquest of Canaan, the Gibeonites weren't helping Joshua and Israel; in that respect, they were [neutral.]{.class_s2FX}

But when it comes to Jesus Christ, there is no neutral ground. There are a lot of Christians who [are saved,]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_188} but when it comes to speaking up for the Lord Jesus Christ and being a testimony, they have decided to "lay low" and quietly let grace slip them into Glory. They think, "The world can't possibly have anything against me. I'm not 'rocking the boat'; I'm not 'making any waves.'"

[You're wrong.]{.class_s2FX} You can't straddle the fence between the Lord and the world. Both sides expect your loyalty. The world figures if you are not [for it]{.class_s2FX} and [loving it]{.class_s2FX} (1 John 2:15--17) and [conforming to it]{.class_s2FX} (Rom. 12:2) that you are for the other side, and the world [hates]{.class_s2FX} the other side (John 15:18--19; 1 John 3:13). The Lord Jesus Christ said, ["He that is not with me is against me; and he that gathereth not with me scattereth abroad"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 12:30). You are either on or off; you are either on one side or the other. There is no [neutrality.]{.class_s2FX}

If you try to get along with both sides, all you are going to do is take hits from both sides. You are like the fellow in the Civil War who didn't want to fight on either side, so he decided to wear a blue Union coat with gray Confederate pants. He figured that when the Union boys saw the coat, they wouldn't shoot him because they would think he was with the Union, and when the "Johnny Rebs" saw the pants, they wouldn't shoot him because they figured he was with the Confederacy. After the battle was over, that fellow was found dead on the battlefield with [Union bullets in the Confederate pants]{.class_s2FX} and [Confederate bullets in the Union jacket.]{.class_s2FX} All he did was make himself a target for [both sides.]{.class_s2FX} That's the way it will be with you if you try to get along with the world and your Saviour at the same time.

6 And the men of Gibeon sent unto Joshua to the camp to Gilgal, saying, Slack not thy hand from thy servants; come up to us quickly, and save us, and help us: for all the kings of the Amorites that dwell in the mountains are gathered together against us.

7 So Joshua ascended from Gilgal, he, and all the people of war with him, and all the mighty men of valour.

8 And the LORD said unto Joshua, Fear them not: for I have delivered them into thine hand; there shall not a man of them stand before thee.

9 Joshua therefore came unto them suddenly, and went []{#c14V.xhtml_page_189}up from Gilgal all night.

10 And the LORD discomfited them before Israel, and slew them with a great slaughter at Gibeon, and chased them along the way that goeth up to Bethhoron, and smote them to Azekah, and unto Makkedah.

11 And it came to pass, as they fled from before Israel, and were in the going down to Bethhoron, that the LORD cast down great stones from heaven upon them unto Azekah, and they died: they were more which died with hailstones than they whom the children of Israel slew with the sword.

Now the five Kings attack Gibeon, and the Gibeonites send a message to Joshua at Gilgal asking for help. They say, ["Slack not thy hand from thy servants"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6). The word ["slack"]{.class_s2FW} means "loose," or "slow" in this context. The idea is that a rider is loose with the reins so his horse doesn't run. The Gibeonites are telling Joshua, "Don't be [lax]{.class_s2FX} or [slow]{.class_s2FX} about it; ['come up to us QUICKLY, and save us, and help us.']{.class_s2FW}"

This is a picture of a [neutral]{.class_s2FX} Christian trying to get help from a brother who is [militant.]{.class_s2FX} I have seen it. A good case in Scripture is Obadiah and Elijah. In 1 Kings 17, Elijah confronts Ahab and tells him that there won't be any rain until he (i.e., Elijah) says so. Then he hides himself ["by the brook Cherith"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 17:3), and the ravens come and feed him twice a day. In the meantime, Obadiah stays in the King's household and doesn't let anyone there know he worships Jehovah instead of Baal. Three-and-a-half years later when the draught is so bad that Ahab sends Obadiah out to look for water to save the horses, Obadiah meets Elijah who is on his way to see Ahab. Obadiah is very anxious to give Elijah a testimony so Elijah would know what a fine "Christian" he was.

["Was it not told my lord what I did when Jezebel slew the prophets of the LORD, how I hid an hundred men of the LORD'S prophets by fifty in a cave, and fed them with bread and water?"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 18:13).

Elijah hadn't asked him about that; he had asked him to go tell Ahab he wanted to see him. Obadiah had wanted to stay neutral but []{#c14V.xhtml_page_190}still appear to be serving God. When Elijah had asked him to go fetch Ahab, Obadiah was scared Ahab would get so angry at him as the messenger that the King would have him killed. He was trying to get help from the man who had the power. Obadiah may have had [influence]{.class_s2FX} as the governor of Ahab's house (1 Kings 18:3), but Elijah had [power.]{.class_s2FX}

Back to Joshua 10:6---["for all the kings of the Amorites that dwell in the mountains are gathered together against us."]{.class_s2FW} Here is a good place to define what an [Amorite]{.class_s2FX} was. Amorites were not only a specific people descended from Canaan (Gen. 10:15--16), the name was also a descriptive term of any Canaanite people who lived in the hill country: ["the Amorites that dwell in the mountains."]{.class_s2FW} That's why the Jebusites of Jerusalem were referred to as ["Amorites."]{.class_s2FW} The word [Canaanite]{.class_s2FX} is used in a similar way in the Old Testament: it can either refer to a particular people in Canaan (Exod. 33:2, 34:11) or any race of people who lived in the land of Canaan (Josh 13:3).

Now consider, for a moment, how easy it would have been for Joshua to sit back and do nothing for the Gibeonites. It would have taken care of the problem of 9:18--20. Joshua could have let the Amorite Kings kill the Gibeonites and not have to worry about his oath not to kill them.

But it was because of the oath that Joshua went to their rescue. When David set up Uriah the Hittite to be killed in battle, the prophet Nathan told the King that he had ["slain him with the sword of the children of Ammon"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 12:9). David used the attack against the Ammonites as an opportunity to have Uriah slain. The fact that he was not the one wielding the sword did not absolve him of the guilt of [murder.]{.class_s2FX} That is the situation Joshua is in here. If he had let the Amorites kill the Gibeonites, he would have been guilty of their murder by his inaction. The lesson for the Christian here is found in Ezekiel 3:18.

"When I say unto the wicked, Thou shalt surely die; and thou givest him not warning, nor speakest to warn the wicked from his wicked way, to save his life; the same wicked man shall die in his iniquity; but his blood will I require at thine hand."

That's not just an Old Testament admonition; that's for the New Testament witness as well (see Acts 20:26--27). God has committed ["the word of reconciliation"]{.class_s2FY} to you, Christian (2 Cor. 5:19), and has commanded you to ["go . . . into all the world, and preach the gospel to every creature"]{.class_s2FY} (Mark 16:15). If you don't go or become actively engaged in some way in getting the Gospel out, God will require the blood of lost sinners at your hand. You can't just sit back and do nothing and expect everything to be all right with you at the Judgment Seat of Christ.

["So Joshua ascended from Gilgal, he, and all the people of war with him, and all the mighty men of valour . . . . Joshua therefore came unto them suddenly, and went up from Gilgal all night"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 7, 9). You will remember that the last time Joshua and the whole army made the trek from Gilgal to Gibeon that it took [three days]{.class_s2FX} (9:16--17). Here they make it in [one night.]{.class_s2FX} In military terms, that is known as a "forced march." The Jewish army made a journey of twenty miles in eight to ten hours; that's double-timing it, boy.

Nathan Bedford Forrest is a good example of that. Of course, he was cavalry, not infantry; but he is purported to have said that his military tactic was to "get there the firstest with the mostest" (the actual quote was "I got there first with the most men"). Those who knew him said that riding into an attack with Nathan Bedford Forrest was more like a steeplechase (a horse race) than a cavalry charge. I read an account of Forrest where he once chased a Union outfit for three nights and four days. When he finally caught up with it, the Union soldiers formed a circle to defend themselves; when they lay down on the ground to fire their rifles, they were so tired from the chase that they fell asleep with an attack coming in.

Perhaps the greatest forced march ever made was Mao Tse-tung's "Long March." "Chairman Mao" may have been a Communist and a mass murderer of his own people, but he was a good soldier. He escaped the Chinese Nationalist Army by traversing 8,000 miles in 370 days over some of the roughest terrain in western China.

Now Joshua and the army of Israel were able to do what they did in verse 9 because of what God said in verse 8.

["Fear them not: for I have delivered them into thine hand]{.class_s2FW} \[an [accomplished fact]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_192} even though they haven't fought the battle yet---see our remarks under 1:3\][; there shall not a man of them stand before thee."]{.class_s2FW}

If you could believe that, you would be some soldier, wouldn't you? You'd go into that fray with enthusiasm. That's what gave Joshua and those Jews the "get up and go" to make a trek of twenty miles in one night.

Now remember that, Christian, in your struggle against sin and the flesh. In God's eyes, your old man is dead, and you have the victory over it (Rom. 6). If you could get that, you would rival the Apostle Paul in your Christian life. That old boy had the victory through persecution, shipwrecks, travels, robbers, his own people out to kill him, the heathen out to kill him, some professing "Christians" out to kill him; he was hungry, tired, in pain a lot of the time, exposed to the elements, etc. Through all of that, he had the victory (see 2 Cor. 11). The same position, promises, and grace Paul had to make it through is available to every Christian if he will just believe them and follow through on them like Paul did.

["And the LORD discomfited them before Israel, and slew them with a great slaughter at Gibeon, and chased them along the way" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 10).[ ]{.class_s2FW}Look at that sentence. It's the Israelites doing the fighting (["whom the children of Israel slew with the sword"]{.class_s2FW}---vs. 11), but it is God who is "discomfiting" the Amorites. The word [discomfit ]{.class_s2FX}is an archaic word that means "to defeat or vanquish in battle," but it has come to be associated with the word [discomfort]{.class_s2FX}. If you want to see how "uncomfortable" God made those Amorites, just look at the following verses.

["And I will send hornets before thee, which shall drive out the Hivite, the Canaanite, and the Hittite from before thee" ]{.class_s2FW}(Exod. 23:28).

["Moreover the LORD thy God will send the hornet among them, until they that are left, and hide themselves from thee, be destroyed" ]{.class_s2FW}(Deut. 7:20).

["And I sent the hornet before you, which drave them out from before you, even the two kings of the Amorites; but not with thy sword, nor with thy bow" ]{.class_s2FW}(Josh. 24:12).

When those Jews fought those Canaanites and Amorites and []{#c14V.xhtml_page_193}Hivites and Hittites and Girgashites, etc., before they could ever lay into them with swords and spears and bows and arrows, God would send a swarm of hornets before the Israelites into the ranks of those heathen. Talk about uncomfortable! Can you imagine trying to block a sword slash or spear thrust while you're being stung all over your body by hornets three to five inches long? Why, you'd be driven to distraction, man!

But the Lord did something else here. When the Israelites routed the Amorite armies, as those Amorites were fleeing to Bethhoron, the Lord began dropping great hailstones on them. The largest hailstone on record fell in India on October 3, 2010. It weighed over 112 pounds. That's like the hailstones the Lord sends down in the Tribulation. In the Tribulation, God sends hailstones down weighing a talent apiece (Rev. 16:21); that's anywhere from [fifty]{.class_s2FX} to [120 ]{.class_s2FX}pounds, depending on whose measurement for the weight of a talent you accept.

Now the text doesn't say what size these hailstones were; it just says the hailstones were ["great stones"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11). Can you imagine a chunk of ice the size of a basketball and weighing around 25 pounds falling 20,000 feet out of the sky and hitting you? No wonder the text says ["they were more which died with hailstones than they whom the children of Israel slew with the sword."]{.class_s2FW} One of those hailstones would bash your skull in, boy.

12 Then spake Joshua to the LORD in the day when the LORD delivered up the Amorites before the children of Israel, and he said in the sight of Israel, Sun, stand thou still upon Gibeon; and thou, Moon, in the valley of Ajalon.

13 And the sun stood still, and the moon stayed, until the people had avenged themselves upon their enemies. Is not this written in the book of Jasher? So the sun stood still in the midst of heaven, and hasted not to go down about a whole day.

14 And there was no day like that before it or after it, that the LORD hearkened unto the voice of a man: for the LORD fought for Israel.

This is the account of "Joshua's Long Day." It is one of the most disbelieved miracles in the word of God by the skeptics. That it is an actual, historical event---and not a "myth" or "legend"---is attested to by the fact that the writer refers his readers to another work (["the book of Jasher"]{.class_s2FW}---vs. 13) for verification that he is telling the truth.

Now there are all sorts of things connected with this passage. We are not going to get into the arguments for and against either "geocentricity" (the universe revolves around the earth) or "heliocentricity" (the earth rotates on its axis and revolves around the sun). Suffice it to say that Joshua's command for the sun and moon to stand still was from the [perspective of the observer:]{.class_s2FX} note the words ["in the SIGHT of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 12.

Technically speaking, the sun does not "rise" or "set" in either system. It either goes around the earth (geocentricity), or the earth rotates creating the perception of movement across the sky (heliocentricity). "Rising" and "setting" are common, everyday terms we use of our observation in relationship to the horizon. From our vantage point, the sun "rises" up out of the eastern horizon and "sets" into the western horizon.

Joshua is not making a technical, "scientific" statement here on cosmic mechanics. He's using the common everyday language of anybody living from 4000 B.C.---A.D. 2014. A skeptic will say, "The Bible can't be right when Joshua told the sun to stand still, because the sun is always standing still; it is the earth that moves around the sun." Then the same jackass will pick up a newspaper to get the times of [sunrise]{.class_s2FX} and [sunset]{.class_s2FX} and have no problem with that. A little hypocritical there, aren't you, son? I mean, why hold the Bible to one standard and then give a break to the writings of [men]{.class_s2FX}?

There is a big difference between the highly technical jargon and "tradesman's terminology" of scientists and the practical observations and applications of the average person. For instance, take [painting.]{.class_s2FX} An artist's palette has seven to eight colors: red, yellow, blue, orange, green, purple, black, and sometimes white. If you have those colors, you can paint anything. Every time I say that, some smart aleck comes around to tell me, "Black is not a color; it's the lack of color." Someone else will say to me, "The real color is white; all the colors are in white." As proof of that, he will get out a []{#c14V.xhtml_page_195}spectrum and shine a white light through it, and the light will break down into the different colors.

Now tell me, what does that have to do with [painting?]{.class_s2FX} Not one cockeyed thing in the world! We are not talking about light or optics; we are talking about paint colors on a palette which the artist uses to produce images on a canvas. Some people get so impractical that they don't know where they're at, man.

Here in Joshua 10, Joshua is making a statement that any Israelite could look up and confirm with his eyes. The movements of the sun and moon across the sky were arrested, or at least [slowed,]{.class_s2FX} as we are about to see.

Now no matter what point of view you take, this is a major miracle. This is the Creator exercising authority over His creation. Joshua speaks to the Lord first in prayer, and then he commands the sun and moon to stand still (vs. 12). God responds to Joshua's words by causing the sun and moon to obey Joshua (vs. 14). One is reminded immediately of the New Testament "Joshua" speaking to the elements, and the storm becoming calm (Mark 4:39).

Writers like Immanuel Velikovsky (an atheist) and Donald Patten (a Christian) accept the event as historically true, but try to give a naturalistic explanation for why it occurred: a near collision between Earth and another planet (Velikovsky---Venus, Patten---Mars). While this all makes intriguing reading from the standpoint of astronomy, it has nothing to do with the Biblical text as you find it given to you by the Holy Spirit.

When it comes to explaining how the miracle took place, you could no more do it than you could explain how Jesus fed nearly 15,000 people (see our comments on Luke 9:14 in that Commentary) with five loaves of barley bread and two small fish (John 6:9). The whole point of a miracle is that God supernaturally overrides the laws of nature He set up. A clock or watch works consistently a certain way unless you manipulate it (set it forward or set it backward) with the means the watchmaker or clockmaker put in place for that purpose. If a man can do that, don't you know God has this universe set up to run the way He wants it to run when He wants it to run a particular way.

When it comes to this miracle of the sun and moon, this was a []{#c14V.xhtml_page_196}special thing that was nothing like anything before it or after it throughout the Old Testament (vs. 14). Isaiah 28:21 calls it the Lord's ["strange work"]{.class_s2FW} and His ["strange act."]{.class_s2FW} The next time the Lord does it, will be when the New Testament "Joshua" returns in power to this earth (see Hab. 3:11 and our comments on that verse in that Commentary), and we will discuss that a little further down here.

The thing to remember is that the Creator controls the heavens He made. God asked Job, ["Canst thou bind the sweet influences of Pleiades ]{.class_s2FW}\[a cluster of stars\][, or loose the bands of Orion]{.class_s2FW} \[a constellation\][? Canst thou bring forth Mazzaroth]{.class_s2FW} \[a reference to the Zodiac\][ in his season? or canst thou guide Arcturus with his sons ]{.class_s2FW}\[a particular star in a constellation with its associated stars\][?"]{.class_s2FW} (Job 38:31--32).

The obvious answer is: "No, you can't." [But God can.]{.class_s2FX} If God can keep track of something like ten octillion stars (that's ten with 27 zeros after it)---see Psalm 147:4---on a daily basis, do you think He's going to have any trouble controlling the movement of the sun and the moon? Of course not. The practical application of all this, which is lost to all unsaved Marxists and evolutionists in the American education system, is that you had better [seek the God who made and controls the heavens.]{.class_s2FX}

["Seek him that maketh the seven stars ]{.class_s2FW}\[that's the Pleiades of Job 38:31\][ and Orion, and turneth the shadow of death into the morning, and maketh the day dark with night, that calleth for the waters of the sea, and poureth them out upon the face of the earth: The LORD is his name"]{.class_s2FW} (Amos 5:8).

Now there have been some sincere but dubious attempts to "prove" the long day of Joshua. In the 1970s, a fellow named Harold Hill, in his book [How to Live Like a King's Kid]{.class_s2FX} (Bridge Publishing, South Plainfield, NJ, 1974), claimed when astronomers at the Goddard Space Flight Center in Greenbelt, Maryland were using computers to plot the positions of the sun, moon, and planets for future spacecraft trajectories that the computers supposedly found a "missing day" in their calculations. One scientist who had gone to Sunday school as a child reprogrammed the computers with []{#c14V.xhtml_page_197}information from Joshua 10 and the dial of Ahaz going back ten degrees (2 Kings 20:9--10)---that would be 23 hours and twenty minutes from Joshua 10 and forty minutes from 2 Kings 20---and the computers were able to work accurately from that information.

The problem was when the [Bible-Science Newsletter]{.class_s2FX} tried to confirm the story, it found out that the only thing Hill had to do with the project was that his company serviced some of the electrical generators at the facility. No one at the NASA office knew anything about Harold Hill or the "missing day" problem. When Hill was questioned about this, he admitted that what he wrote was [hearsay]{.class_s2FX} and that he couldn't remember his documentation.

The "original" of this story was published by Harry Rimmer back in 1936 ([The Harmony of Science and Scripture,]{.class_s2FX} Eerdman's, Grand Rapids, MI, pp. 269--270), who relates an account taken from a book by a Yale professor named C. A. L. Totten from 1890. Supposedly Totten got into correspondence with another professor at Yale who was an astronomer (the name of this astronomer is never given). This astronomer was a lost man who did not believe the Bible. He told Totten that he had discovered that the earth was 24 hours "out of schedule." Totten challenged him to read the Bible to see if the answer was there. The next time they met, the astronomer admitted to finding 23 hours and twenty minutes missing in Joshua 10, but that did not convince him the Bible was the inspired word of God because God wouldn't make a mistake of forty minutes. So Totten once more challenged him to keep on reading, and when the unsaved astronomer hit 2 Kings 20 and read about the shadow going back ten degrees on the sundial of Ahaz (forty minutes), he became a believer.

Now normally, Harry Rimmer has some good stuff, especially on "Creationism vs. Evolution," but Professor Robert Newman of Biblical Seminary in Hatfield, Pennsylvania noticed that Rimmer gave no documentation for anything he said, after claiming to be quoting directly from Totten's work. Newman did some research and found the book to which Rimmer referred: [Joshua's Long Day and the Dial of Ahaz.]{.class_s2FX} The problem Newman discovered with Rimmer's "synopsis" of Totten's work was that the story of the converted astronomer appeared nowhere in the book. Instead, Totten himself---who was a professor of [military science]{.class_s2FX} at Yale and [not]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_198} an astronomer---makes the argument that 24 hours [should be]{.class_s2FX} missing from past time, but through a series of calculations---which Totten did not give---he figured out that the "missing day" was [Tuesday, July 22.]{.class_s2FX} So both stories are rather suspect, but you can look up all the books involved on the computer (on "Google Books") if you are interested in reading them.

The best "proof" outside of the Bible that has been produced for this miracle is its attestation in the mythologies of other cultures. Just as the Flood is attested to by [270]{.class_s2FX} other cultures around the world, so is the account of a long day. References to a long day are found in ancient Greece and ancient Mexico. It is found in the Hindu and Buddhist literature. The Chinese had a record of it, as did the Incas in Peru, the Aztecs in Mexico, and the American Indians. The Babylonians, Persians, and Egyptians speak of it. Even the Polynesians of the South Pacific had an account of it. The universality of the account points to a real event that took place in history that has been imbedded on the memory of mankind; the Bible gives you the actual, factual record of what really took place, just as it did with the long ages of men before the Flood and the Flood itself.

Now what actually took place here in Joshua 10? The sun and moon didn't stop absolutely still in the sky and not move at all ["about a whole day"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 13). Look at the whole explanation there in verse 13:

"So the sun stood still in the midst of heaven, and HASTED NOT TO GO DOWN about a whole day."

So it [did]{.class_s2FX} go down, didn't it? It just took its time going down. It didn't put on the brakes and come to a screeching halt, and then drop like a lead weight after Joshua won the battle. What happened, from the standpoint of a scientist, was the Lord slowed down the rotation of the earth until the battle was over. According to Henry Morris ([Science and the Bible,]{.class_s2FX} Moody Press, Chicago, 1986, pg. 30), this would have affected the circulation of the atmosphere, which would account for the hailstorm of verse 11.

Be that as it may, the thing to remember is that any consequences of the Lord slowing down the earth's rotation would []{#c14V.xhtml_page_199}have been tempered by God in this instance so that Joshua could win the battle. Don't you worry, when the Lord wants to tear this sin-cursed world up, He'll tear it up. Look at Isaiah 24:19--20.

"The earth is utterly broken down, the earth is clean dissolved, the earth is moved exceedingly. The earth shall reel to and fro like a drunkard, and shall be removed like a cottage; and the transgression thereof shall be heavy upon it; and it shall fall, and not rise again."

That is what is going to happen the next time the Lord makes the sun and moon stand still. That takes place at the Second Advent. Verse 14 here in Joshua 10 says, ["for the LORD fought for Israel."]{.class_s2FW} With that in mind, look at Zechariah 14:3.

"Then shall the LORD go forth, and fight against those nations, as when he fought in the day of battle."

The context is the return of Jesus Christ in power at the Second Advent. When the Lord Jesus returns, the sun and moon stand still [again]{.class_s2FX} (Hab. 3:11). The context of Habakkuk 3 is [not]{.class_s2FX} the Exodus from Egypt, the wandering in the wilderness, or the conquest of Canaan under Joshua; it is the [Second Advent.]{.class_s2FX} The head of the seed of the serpent (Gen. 3:15) is being bruised in Habakkuk 3:13. The armies on white horses that follow Jesus Christ out of Heaven (Rev. 19:14) are in Habakkuk 3:15. ["The day of trouble"]{.class_s2FW} is in Habakkuk 3:16; that is ["the time of Jacob's trouble"]{.class_s2FW} in Jeremiah 30:7. That's a reference to the [Tribulation.]{.class_s2FX}

So what you are reading in Joshua 10 is a type of the Second Coming of the Lord Jesus Christ. That is why you have a hailstorm with it (see Rev. 16:21). "Atmospheric disturbances" are associated with the sun and moon standing still at the Second Advent just as they were in Joshua's time. When Jesus Christ comes back, the Lord sends a "whirlwind" around the globe that tears everything up. We will not take the time to go into all the Scriptures here, but I will list the major references for your own study--2 Kings 2:1, 11; Job 21:17--18, 38:1, 40:6; Psalm 58:9--10; Proverbs 1:26--27, 10:24--25; Isaiah 5:26--28, 17:13, 21:1, 40:23--24, 41:15--16, 66:15; Jeremiah 4:13, 23:19; Ezekiel 1:4; Hosea 13:3; Nahum 1:3; Habakkuk 3:14; Zechariah 9:14. All those passages are either [types ]{.class_s2FX}or [prophecies ]{.class_s2FX}of the Second Advent.

Back to Joshua 10--[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_200}["Is not this written in the book of Jasher" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 13). Here is a reference to a book not found in the canon of the Scripture; you will find it referenced again in 2 Samuel 1:18. This brings up the matter of "canonicity": what books belong in the Bible.

The current argument brought up by writers of pulp fiction like Dan Brown ([The DaVinci Code]{.class_s2FX}) is that you do [not ]{.class_s2FX}have all the books in your Bible that you are supposed to have. Brown says the Catholic Church excluded the Gnostic gospels like "The Gospel of Judas," "The Gospel of Thomas," "The Infancy Gospel of Jesus Christ," etc., written more than 100 years after the close of the New Testament canon. You can find more of these books in a work entitled [The Lost Books of the Bible. ]{.class_s2FX}The Catholics themselves add fifteen books to the canon of the Old Testament which Jesus Christ, the apostles, and orthodox Jewry [rejected]{.class_s2FX} (see our comments on Luke 24:44 in that Commentary). The dirty little secret of the modern perversions of the Scriptures is that the "oldest and best manuscripts" used by apostates like Westcott and Hort, Aland, Metzger, Eugene Nida, F. F. Bruce, and A. T. Robertson, et al., contain the Apocrypha as part of the inspired Old Testament. The publishers have [refused]{.class_s2FX} to print the contents of their own manuscripts. The reason that the [RSV, NASV, NIV, NRSV, ]{.class_s2FX}and [ESV ]{.class_s2FX}do not contain the apocryphal books that are in the manuscripts from which they come ([Sinaiticus, Vaticanus, Alexandrinus, ]{.class_s2FX}and [Ephraemi Rescriptus]{.class_s2FX}) is that it would "let the cat out of the bag" that those versions came from [Roman Catholic manuscripts ]{.class_s2FX}that match the [Roman Catholic canon ]{.class_s2FX}of the [Roman Catholic Council of Trent]{.class_s2FX} (see our remarks under 9:2).

The Liberal "higher critics" argue that since the Bible itself references other works, that those works should be part of the Scripture. So "scholars" are always digging around trying to find some piece of trash they can elevate above the 66 books the Holy Spirit inspired and preserved for you as ["holy scriptures" ]{.class_s2FW}(2 Tim. 3:15). These "lost books of the Bible" include:

["The book of the wars of the LORD" ]{.class_s2FW}(Num. 21:14).

Now what about these "lost books of the Bible"? Well, first of all, not everything [spoken]{.class_s2FX} or even [written ]{.class_s2FX}by the prophets and apostles was inducted into the canon of the Scripture that the Holy Spirit gave by inspiration. Jonah certainly prophesied [more ]{.class_s2FX}than the book bearing his name (e.g., see 2 Kings 14:25). God only deemed to give you [two]{.class_s2FX} instances of those prophecies. Paul certainly wrote more letters to more churches and pastors than you find in the thirteen books bearing his salutation in the New Testament (Romans--Philemon). What does that mean? [Absolutely nothing. ]{.class_s2FX}The Holy Spirit didn't put "The Epistle to the Laodiceans" in your New Testament.

Brethren, just as God [hid]{.class_s2FX} the particular activities of His Son when He was here on this earth from the ages of twelve to thirty because that information wasn't something  necessary for you to know, so the Holy Spirit deprived you of certain prophecies and writings because they were not pertinent to you for ["all things that pertain unto life and godliness, through the knowledge of him that hath called us to glory and virtue" ]{.class_s2FW}(2 Pet. 1:3).

Brethren, what you have in the Bible God has given you today is [exactly ]{.class_s2FX}what He wants you to have. If you were able to go back in time somehow and get the "originals," you would have [nothing]{.class_s2FX} in regards to [revelation;]{.class_s2FX} all you would have would be an [oddity]{.class_s2FX} and a [novelty]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_202} of which you could say, "Wow! Look at that!" Why do I say that? Because one time someone [did]{.class_s2FX} have an "original autograph," and he [burned it.]{.class_s2FX} You can read the account in Jeremiah 36. When the Holy Spirit "re-inspired" Jeremiah's writings (double inspiration!), He ["ADDED besides unto them many like words"]{.class_s2FW} (Jer. 36:32). If you were able to get the "original" of the book of Jeremiah, you would [not]{.class_s2FX} have what God wanted you to have for ["the scripture of truth"]{.class_s2FW} (Dan. 10:21) for that book.

Contrariwise, if you ever were able to find Paul's epistle he wrote to the Laodiceans, you would be [cursed by God]{.class_s2FX} if you tried to stick it into the canon of Scripture (Prov. 30:6; Rev. 22:18). Why? [Because God didn't want it in there.]{.class_s2FX}

That's why works like "The Book of Enoch" are a [horselaugh.]{.class_s2FX} Jude 14--15 never says Enoch [wrote]{.class_s2FX} anything. That is someone trying to "help God out" and [damning]{.class_s2FX} himself in the process just like Uzzah did in 2 Samuel 6:6--7.

That's what some jackass tried to do with ["the book of Jasher."]{.class_s2FW} There was no ["book of Jasher"]{.class_s2FW} anywhere in the Old Testament, so at least [five attempts]{.class_s2FX} were made to give you one long after God closed the canon of the New Testament. A Mormon publishing company out of Salt Lake City, Utah (J. H. Parry & Co.) translated one of these forgeries to cast doubt in your mind as to the completeness of the Old Testament so they could foist on you "Another Testament of Jesus Christ"---the [Book of Mormon.]{.class_s2FX} You can take [anyone's]{.class_s2FX} copy of "The Book of Jasher," published and distributed by [anyone]{.class_s2FX} (including Fundamental Creationists), and [throw it in the dumpster where it belongs.]{.class_s2FX} It has nothing to do with the canon of Scripture, the veracity of Scripture, or ["the book of Jasher"]{.class_s2FW} about which you read in Joshua 10:13 or 2 Samuel 1:18.

Now what is ["the book of Jasher"]{.class_s2FW}? Well, the word ["Jasher"]{.class_s2FW} is a Hebrew word that means "the upright." Well, in the context of Joshua 10, "the upright" would be a reference to [Joshua himself]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 14), so ["the book of Jasher"]{.class_s2FW} could be a reference to the book of Joshua itself.

You say, "But the book of Joshua hadn't been finished yet." We have already seen where things were added to the narrative at the end of Joshua's life (e.g., see 4:9, 5:9, 6:25, 7:26, 8:28--29, and 9:27). []{#c14V.xhtml_page_203}So this could be Joshua inserting this, or it could be someone adding the information after Joshua was dead. But it would be nothing odd in Scripture for the Holy Spirit to refer to the work as complete when it wasn't. Look at Jeremiah 25:13.

"And I will bring upon that land all my words which I have pronounced against it, even all that is written in this book, which Jeremiah hath prophesied against all nations."

Why, that was written during the reign of Jehoiakim. Jehoiachin and Zedekiah, the last two Kings of Judah, hadn't even come to the throne yet, and Jeremiah prophesied to both of them. Over half the book had yet to be written. But you see, that's the Lord treating the book as completed when it was still being written.

Now that may or may not be the case here. If it is, then it is much more than just the book of Joshua. The reference to the book in 2 Samuel 1:18 goes all the way up to the time of Saul and Jonathan. So what you have here is a collection of the historical books from Joshua---1 or 2 Samuel, or you have an extrabiblical work covering the same time period. The Old Testament often cites other historical works as a testimony to its own veracity (see the references to the chronicles of the Kings of Israel and Judah in the list of extracanonical works above).

15 And Joshua returned, and all Israel with him, unto the camp to Gilgal.

16 But these five kings fled, and hid themselves in a cave at Makkedah.

17 And it was told Joshua, saying, The five kings are found hid in a cave at Makkedah.

18 And Joshua said, Roll great stones upon the mouth of the cave, and set men by it for to keep them:

19 And stay ye not, but pursue after your enemies, and smite the hindmost of them; suffer them not to enter into their cities: for the LORD your God hath delivered them into your hand.

20 And it came to pass, when Joshua and the children of Israel had made an end of slaying them with a very great []{#c14V.xhtml_page_204}slaughter, till they were consumed, that the rest which remained of them entered into fenced cities.

21 And all the people returned to the camp to Joshua at Makkedah in peace: none moved his tongue against any of the children of Israel.

If you look on a map of Canaan at the time of Joshua, what takes place in this battle is that Joshua routs the armies of the five Kings attacking Gibeon. When that happens, they flee north and west to Beth-horon. That's when the Lord starts casting down the hailstones on top of their heads, so they turn and flee southward to Azekah and Makkedah.

Verse 15 doesn't actually take place between verse 14 and verse 16; it summarizes the successful completion of the campaign here in chapter 10 (see vs. 43). You know that is so because Joshua chases the five Kings to Makkedah where those Kings hide out in a cave. Joshua orders stones rolled over the entrance to the cave until the "mopping up" operation is completed. In the meantime, Joshua sets up a camp at Makkedah (vs. 21) and launches an attack against the city from there. If he had returned to Gilgal from the battle of verses 10--11, that would have given the five Kings plenty of time to get away, for Joshua would have left Makkedah to go to Gilgal, and then have to turn around and go right back. So verse 15 is actually what takes in verse 43; it is just given at the beginning of the narrative to let you know that the campaign was successful. In modern parlance, it would be called a "spoiler," since it gives the end of the story at the beginning.

Now outside of the historic application of the passage (i.e., these are five actual Kings of real cities in Canaan whom Joshua defeated in battle), there are a couple of other applications we can put on these verses. The first is the [prophetic]{.class_s2FX} application. This is still a picture of the Second Advent just as it was back in verses 11--14. When Jesus Christ returns in power to conquer the kingdoms of this world and make them His own (Rev. 11:15), there will be some Kings hiding out in caves then, too, to try to get away from Him.

["And the KINGS of the earth, and the great men, and the rich men, and the chief captains, and the mighty men, and []{#c14V.xhtml_page_205}every bondman, and every free man, HID themselves in the DENS and in the rocks of the mountains; And said to the mountains and rocks, Fall on us, and HIDE us from the face of him that sitteth on the throne, and from the wrath of the Lamb: For the great day of his wrath is come; and who shall be able to stand?"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 6:15--17).

But there is also [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} application to be made to the Christian's warfare. These "five Kings" are a picture for the believer of [hidden sins]{.class_s2FX} in his life. Our "Joshua" defeated these sins at Calvary, but they run away and hide, hoping to retain a foothold in you. They are hidden away in your body of sinful flesh just like those five Kings were hiding in that cave at Makkedah.

One of the best places for those sins to hide is your [mind,]{.class_s2FX} your [thoughts,]{.class_s2FX} your [imagination.]{.class_s2FX} A devil can get in you, Christian, and counterfeit your thoughts and counterfeit your imagination. The Devil did that with Peter in Matthew 16:22--23.

You had better check your thoughts, Christian, and not let them wander. It may not be you doing the thinking at all; it may be the Devil doing the thinking for you. Ask yourself, "Is this [me]{.class_s2FX} thinking or the [Devil]{.class_s2FX} thinking or the [Lord]{.class_s2FX} thinking? Does this thought agree with what God says in His word?" Don't take for granted that just because you are spiritual, love the Lord, and love the Book that the Devil and his demons can't get control of your thought life.

Some people have funny ideas about "demon possession." The standard cliché among Bible teachers and preachers is that a believer can be "demon oppressed" and "demon obsessed," but not "demon possessed." That's not true. A demon can get control of certain parts of your life, and those parts become his possession. Satan can "fill" a believer just like the Holy Spirit can (Acts 5:3 cf. Eph. 5:18).

There is a book which every Christian should read: it is [War on the Saints.]{.class_s2FX} It is a discourse on practical demonology in the life of a Christian. One of the main points of that book is that every inch of ground you yield to the Devil is possessed by his demons. Any place in your life where you disobey God and disobey the commands of Scripture is that much ground you have yielded to Satan.

To get back that yielded ground takes more than confessing the []{#c14V.xhtml_page_206}sin and pleading the blood of Christ against it. Confession takes care of [forgiveness]{.class_s2FX} (1 John 1:9), and the blood of Christ takes care of [cleansing]{.class_s2FX} (1 John 1:7). But when it comes to reclaiming captured territory, it takes an active [fight.]{.class_s2FX} It is going to involve [yielding]{.class_s2FX} that unyielded part of your life to the control of the Holy Ghost (Rom. 6:13, 16, 19). You are going to have to actively ["resist the devil"]{.class_s2FW} and [submit yourself to God]{.class_s2FX} (James 4:7). You must cast ["down imaginations, and every high thing that exalteth itself against the knowledge of God"]{.class_s2FW} and bring ["into captivity every thought to the obedience of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 10:5).

Now what was Joshua's solution for those hidden Kings. He had the entrance to that cave blocked up so they couldn't get out, and he put a guard on them to make sure they stayed in: he [contained]{.class_s2FX} them. That's what you need to do with sin: make every effort to [resist]{.class_s2FX} it and [oppose]{.class_s2FX} it. Box it in; shut it up. Don't let it get loose and run rampant so it can destroy you.

There are two basic philosophies of life: one is "let it all hang out," and the other is keep it under control. There is [hedonism]{.class_s2FX} and [temperance.]{.class_s2FX} One says, "Take the lid off the devilment and let it run its course"; the other says, "Keep the lid on that thing and don't let it out to wreak havoc." Your grandfathers and great-grandfathers were raised on the latter philosophy, and the last two or three generations have been raised on the former philosophy.

This country was founded on the philosophy that men were basically [evil;]{.class_s2FX} therefore, you had to put a [check]{.class_s2FX} on the government, a [check]{.class_s2FX} on your rulers, and a [check]{.class_s2FX} on [you.]{.class_s2FX} In schools, the children were taught to [control]{.class_s2FX} their minds, [control]{.class_s2FX} their flesh, and [control]{.class_s2FX} their words.

This modern bunch of egotistical, educated jackasses say, "They were hypocrites back then. They were just as wicked as we are today; they just pretended to be better." No, they didn't; they just [tried harder]{.class_s2FX} to keep the lid on their baser instincts. [This generation doesn't.]{.class_s2FX}

Brethren, if you want to know what went wrong with this country since about 1920 (and by now, the process is all but complete), it's the sick philosophy propagated by people like Bertrand Russell and John Dewey. The modern philosophy that has damned this nation is: []{#c14V.xhtml_page_207}don't try to control anything; just turn it loose.

You don't control the liquor, so you get a nation of drunks and eventually dope addicts. You don't control the pornography, so you have fornication and promiscuity all through your high schools and on your College campuses (accompanied by sky-rocketing VD rates, divorces, illegitimate births, and abortions), Lesbians and sodomites parading their filthy "lifestyle" in public and "demanding their rights" (the "right" God gave them in Jude 7 was to burn in ["eternal fire"]{.class_s2FW} for their sin), and your Supreme Court has just opened the door for any act of sexual deviancy to be practiced with the full approval of the State and Federal governments. You allow the teaching of evolution in schools and teach the kiddies they came from animals, so they end up acting like wild animals. That's why you have all those school shootings: it's the law of the jungle---kill or be killed.

You say, "I can't keep the standard." It's not the standard that's the problem; [you]{.class_s2FX} are the problem. [Try]{.class_s2FX} to keep the standard; don't get rid of it. Make people feel upset when they violate the standard. You say, "That doesn't do any good." Sure it does: it worries them; it makes them think twice before they violate the standard.

FDR and the Congress said in 1933, "Well, we can't control the liquor traffic, so we'll just let it go." You better hadn't. The death from alcohol-related deaths on the highways will be ten times as many as the murders the gangsters and mobsters committed during Prohibition. The money you shell out to prevent and treat alcoholism will be more than the "revenue" you bring in from taxing it. You had better shut it down.

You say, "That just does more damage than good." You even have Fundamental, Bible-believing Baptist pastors these days taking that attitude toward the legalization of marijuana and the drug traffic. "Making the drugs illegal and trying to keep them out of the country has failed, so just go ahead and make them legal."

You are a [fool]{.class_s2FX} even to think that way. Keeping depravity down is always better than turning it loose. Pressure on wrong-doing is always better than no pressure on it at all.

You say, "I can't control it." [Try]{.class_s2FX} to control it. If you try and fail, [try again.]{.class_s2FX} Don't think that it doesn't do any good to fight it, because []{#c14V.xhtml_page_208}it does. It builds backbone; it builds character. It shows you how weak you really are and makes you lean on the Lord more; it keeps you humble. Don't say it doesn't do any good.

Some pious hypocrite says, "Well, if you think it, that's just as bad as doing it." No, it isn't. I'll grant you that you are guilty of the sin if you entertain it in your heart, but it doesn't affect anyone else. I mean, ["Whosoever hateth his brother is a murderer"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 3:15), but you haven't committed the act. The other guy is still alive and walking around. If you live by the philosophy "I thought it, so I might as well do it," then when you hate your brother, you would blow his brains out. I guarantee you that is worse than just thinking about it.

Bob Jones Sr. said the trouble with this country is [the lowering of standards.]{.class_s2FX} As Christians, we need to keep the standards high. If you keep the standards high, you will always be better off than when you lower them.

Do you believe that Bible is the word of God? Then don't give an inch. You say, "Which Bible?" The one that built this nation; the one that built the ministries of Jonathan Edwards, George Whitefield, Charles Finney, D. L. Moody, Sam Jones, Billy Sunday, Bob Jones Sr., J. Frank Norris, Lee Roberson, and the great Fundamental works in this country---that old, black-backed, 66-caliber [Authorized Version]{.class_s2FX} of 1611 (and I [don't]{.class_s2FX} mean the ["New" King James Version]{.class_s2FX}).

The churches in America are now reaping the results of 100 years of Christian Colleges, Universities, and Seminaries teaching their ministerial students that only the original autographs were inspired. That means that [no]{.class_s2FX} Greek text, [no]{.class_s2FX} Hebrew text, [no]{.class_s2FX} translation, and [no]{.class_s2FX} version is the word of God, because [none]{.class_s2FX} of them were ["given by inspiration of God,"]{.class_s2FW} since 2 Timothy 3:16 only applies to the "originals."

Well, if they aren't the words of God, then they must be the words of [men.]{.class_s2FX} If they are the words of men, then that means they have [mistakes]{.class_s2FX} in them. That's what I was taught at Bob Jones University: [all]{.class_s2FX} texts;[ all]{.class_s2FX} versions, [all]{.class_s2FX} translations have mistakes in them; [none ]{.class_s2FX}of them are perfect. Who decides what God said and what He didn't say? [You do]{.class_s2FX} (or your teachers, scholars, professors, etc., do).

After 100 years of that, the ministers trained in those institutions finally figured out [it didn't matter what Bible they used,]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_209} because [they]{.class_s2FX} were the final authority. So gone are the days when the Fundamentalists and Conservatives "use" the [King James Version]{.class_s2FX} because they want to be "identified" with it. Bob Jones University finally dropped the pretense of "use only the [King James Version]{.class_s2FX} in this pulpit." They got rid of that sign and let the [NIV]{.class_s2FX} in.

The logical conclusion of it all was finally reached by the "purpose-driven," "seeker-sensitive," "emergent" crowd: [get rid of any part of that Book that makes your congregation feel uncomfortable.]{.class_s2FX} After all, the goal is "being relevant" and "reaching out to others" and "being culturally sensitive to the needs of those around us"; it's not [fidelity to God and His words. That's]{.class_s2FX} why your country is in the shape it is in today: the standard was dropped and trodden under foot.

Verse 19: ["And stay ye not, but pursue after your enemies, and smite the hindmost of them."]{.class_s2FW} To appropriate the complete victory provided to you in Christ, it takes constant persistence. You can't be lax. Groups like the Nazarenes talk about "a second work of grace"; the Charismatics talk about "being slain in the Spirit"; the Holiness talk about "the eradication of the old nature." The idea is that after salvation, there is a second work the Holy Spirit performs in you where He gets rid of all sin in your life. Those people are [blind.]{.class_s2FX}

Fighting sin is a [lifetime]{.class_s2FX} battle. The greatest Christian who ever lived fought against it all his life (Rom. 7:15--20). After all, folks, why would Paul command you to ["mortify therefore your members which are upon the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 3:5) if it was a one-time act never to be repeated. Paul practiced what he preached; he said, ["I die DAILY"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 15:31).

I have been saved 64 years now, and I can tell you that I have seen every sin in that Bible come up in my life; if not in deed, then in thought. If you have been saved any substantial length of time at all, and you expose yourself constantly to that Book, then you have given up hope of being "good," if you are honest. Like Solomon told old Shimei, ["Thou knowest all the wickedness which thine heart is privy to"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 2:44). If you don't know that about yourself, brother, sister, [I sure do.]{.class_s2FX} It takes a constant fight to put []{#c14V.xhtml_page_210}that wickedness down.

Now look at what happened in verse 20. Joshua told the people, ["suffer them not to enter into their cities"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 19). Why? Because they would "hole up" in a fortified city, and it would be harder to get them out. That's what happened. The Israelites didn't pursue quickly enough, and there were some of those Amorites who got away and ["entered into fenced cities"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 20).

The practical lesson for Christian warfare is that if you are not persistent in pressing the attack on the sin in your life, it will gain a stronghold and be harder for you to get rid of.

Verse 21: ["And all the people returned to the camp to Joshua at Makkedah in peace: none moved his tongue against any of the children of Israel."]{.class_s2FW} The Lord had performed such a mighty work for Joshua and those Jews that none of those Hivites was going to say anything against them at all (see Exod. 11:7 for a similar situation). That Bible says, ["When a man's ways please the LORD, he maketh even his enemies to be at peace with him"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 16:7).

22 Then said Joshua, Open the mouth of the cave, and bring out those five kings unto me out of the cave.

23 And they did so, and brought forth those five kings unto him out of the cave, the king of Jerusalem, the king of Hebron, the king of Jarmuth, the king of Lachish, and the king of Eglon.

24 And it came to pass, when they brought out those kings unto Joshua, that Joshua called for all the men of Israel, and said unto the captains of the men of war which went with him, Come near, put your feet upon the necks of these kings. And they came near, and put their feet upon the necks of them.

25 And Joshua said unto them, Fear not, nor be dismayed, be strong and of good courage: for thus shall the LORD do to all your enemies against whom ye fight.

26 And afterward Joshua smote them, and slew them, and hanged them on five trees: and they were hanging upon the trees until the evening.

27 And it came to pass at the time of the going down of the sun, that Joshua commanded, and they took them down off the trees, and cast them into the cave wherein they had been hid, and laid great stones in the cave's mouth, which remain until this very day.

Joshua orders the mouth of the cave opened and those five Kings brought out to [him]{.class_s2FX} so they can be dealt with as he dealt with the King of Ai back in 8:29. The devotional application for you as a Christian is to bring your hidden sins to [Jesus Christ]{.class_s2FX} for disposal. An old song entitled "O For a Closer Walk With God" says, "The dearest idol I have known, Whate'er that idol be, Help me to tear it from Thy throne, and worship only Thee."

One time, a teenage boy put up a bunch of pictures of rock stars and pin-ups from girlie magazines on the wall of his room. His mother didn't say a word to him; she just took one of those big "blue ribbon" family Bibles and cut out a full-color picture of Jesus Christ on the cross and hung it up in the middle of all those other pictures in the boy's room. The next time she went in there to clean up her son's room, she noticed all the other pictures were down and the only picture left was that picture of Christ. "What happened to your pictures?" she asked her son. The boy replied, "Well, when Christ goes up, everything else has to come down."

Amen! That's right. Once Jesus Christ [goes up]{.class_s2FX} in your life, everything else should [come down.]{.class_s2FX}

Joshua has those five Kings hauled out of the cave and lays them out flat on the ground. Then he has the elders of Israel come and put their feet on the necks of the Kings. That's a symbol of [conquest]{.class_s2FX} and [victory.]{.class_s2FX} That was to give the leaders of those Jews [confidence]{.class_s2FX} in the upcoming battles in verses 28--43.
