The spiritual lesson for the Christian is: ["sin shall not have dominion over you"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:14) and ["let not sin therefore reign in your mortal body, that ye should obey it in the lusts thereof"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:12). Gaining victory over a particular sin in your life will give you confidence in fighting the other sins you face.

One of the greatest blessings you will ever get in your Christian life is to see a sin which has dogged you and bothered you and []{#c14V.xhtml_page_212}harmed you all your life down under your feet. Of course, it is like stepping on [yourself:]{.class_s2FX} you are mortifying the deeds of your body (Rom. 8:13). The thing to remember is when the "King" gets up from under your foot, knock it down again and keep knocking it down until it stays down.

Robert Shuler---the old-time Methodist evangelist and pastor of Trinity Methodist in Los Angeles, not Robert Schuller the "televangelist" who operated that "Graumen's Chinese Theater" out there in Garden Grove, California---used to tell a story about a boy he knew back in the mountains of Virginia. That kid was known as "Puddn'Head Wilson." Puddn'Head Wilson was the boy no one wanted to fight, but Puddn'Head would fight anybody. He very seldom won, though. He was short and skinny as a rail, and any fight he was in usually ended with him getting knocked flat on the ground.

The trouble with Puddn'Head was that he couldn't be kept down. One guy knocked him down one time and thought he had knocked him out cold, but when he turned around to walk away, Puddn'Head came up behind the fellow with a knife and cut his stomach open. Another fellow knocked Puddn'Head down, and when he walked away, he hadn't taken fifteen steps before Puddn'Head threw a rock and hit the kid in the back of the head. When Shuler and Puddn' got into it, Shuler ended up biting off part of Puddin' Head's ear.

Well, Shuler and Puddn'Head Wilson both grew up and over the years lost track of each other. One day, Shuler went down to a bank to borrow some money for a building program. He asked to see the president of the bank and was ushered into the bank president's office.

Shuler noticed the bank president's name was Wilson, and at one point when the bank president turned his head, Shuler saw that a piece of his ear was missing. Sure enough, that bank president was old Puddn'Head Wilson.

Well, the two of them had a hugging session there in that office and got to talking about their lives after they parted ways. "How in the world did you ever become president of a bank?" asked Shuler, "You never finished high school." Wilson said, "Well, Bob, I got a job here as a messenger boy, and after that, there was nothing to it."

Puddn'Head Wilson had a quality that you as a Christian would do well to emulate: [he wouldn't stay down.]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c14V.xhtml_page_213} Even as an adult, he didn't let a "dead-end job" like being a messenger boy keep him down. He kept getting up and going on until he became a success. This modern generation quits if they don't get what they think they have coming to them, and they keep on quitting the rest of their lives.

Verse 25: ["And Joshua said unto them, Fear not, nor be dismayed, be strong and of good courage."]{.class_s2FW} Back when Joshua took command of the people back in chapter 1, the people encouraged Joshua with these same words: ["be strong and of a good courage"]{.class_s2FW} (1:18). Now Joshua encourages the leaders of the people. New Testament Christians are commanded, in this regard, to ["comfort one another"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Thess. 4:18), ["edify one another"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Thess. 5:11), and ["exhort one another"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 3:13, 10:25).

["For thus shall the LORD do to all your enemies against whom ye fight."]{.class_s2FW} Notice the Lord's part and your part in the battle. The Lord doesn't do everything for you; you have to put forth the effort and [fight.]{.class_s2FX} One of the temptations the Devil will put before you is to sit around on your dead can and let the Lord do everything for you while you do nothing. That's not how it works. Of course, you have to ["be strong in the LORD, and in the power of HIS might"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:10). You're not going to win the battle in your own strength and might, but you still have to do [something,]{.class_s2FX} and that's FIGHT.

Paul said, ["I have fought a good fight"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 4:7). The roughest fight you will ever have in your life is against the sin in your own life. Amen! You will never be in a greater fight than that this side of the Rapture.

I heard Bob Jones Sr. say one time, "When you boys get out in the ministry, and get in the word and try to minister it to people, you're going to get in a bloody battle that will make all the battlefields of this world look like nothing." I grinned to myself at the time; I knew some things about combat. I could think of a lot of things that I considered to be worse than the ministry and the Christian life. I thought to myself, "That's stretching things a bit." But I was a young Christian and kind of naive about those things.

You see, you can get out of regular combat. They'll carry you off []{#c14V.xhtml_page_214}on a stretcher or in a body bag, or you'll do your time and get out, or the war will end and you'll muster out. But you won't get out of the fight against sin. The Bible says, ["There is no discharge in that war"]{.class_s2FW} (Eccl. 8:8). You will fight it every day of your life.

Now notice that victory over sin has to be connected with the crucified Christ. Joshua takes these five Kings and hangs them on five trees. As we saw back in 8:28, that is a picture of the crucifixion of Jesus Christ. Then he takes the bodies of those dead Kings and sticks them back in the cave where they hid and seals the entrance with ["great stones"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 27). That obviously is a picture of Christ's burial. So positionally in Christ, your sins are dead and buried with Him, and what comes out of the "grave" at salvation is a new man in Christ that is free from sin (Rom. 6:3--7).

Paul wrote, ["I am crucified with Christ: nevertheless I live; yet not I, but Christ liveth in me: and the life which I now live in the flesh I live by the faith of the Son of God, who loved me, and gave himself for me"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 2:20).

So through Christ's death and burial, sin has been conquered in the life of a Christian. The problem is, it still remains in the body; it is just dead. You can't deny it's there; after all, John wrote, ["If we say that we have no sin, we deceive ourselves, and the truth is not in us"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 1:8). But the only power sin has over you is the power you give it. If you ["yield . . . your members as instruments of unrighteousness unto sin"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:13), you become a slave to a rotting corpse. That's why you have to ["reckon ye also yourselves to be dead indeed unto sin, but alive unto God through Jesus Christ our Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:11). If you are dead to sin and sin is dead to you, then there is no communion between the two: two dead men can't do too much to get along together.

28 And that day Joshua took Makkedah, and smote it with the edge of the sword, and the king thereof he utterly destroyed, them, and all the souls that were therein; he let none remain: and he did to the king of Makkedah as he did unto the king of Jericho.

29 Then Joshua passed from Makkedah, and all Israel []{#c14V.xhtml_page_215}with him, unto Libnah, and fought against Libnah:

30 And the LORD delivered it also, and the king thereof, into the hand of Israel; and he smote it with the edge of the sword, and all the souls that were therein; he let none remain in it; but did unto the king thereof as he did unto the king of Jericho.

31 And Joshua passed from Libnah, and all Israel with him, unto Lachish, and encamped against it, and fought against it:

32 And the LORD delivered Lachish into the hand of Israel, which took it on the second day, and smote it with the edge of the sword, and all the souls that were therein, according to all that he had done to Libnah.

33 Then Horam king of Gezer came up to help Lachish; and Joshua smote him and his people, until he had left him none remaining.

34 And from Lachish Joshua passed unto Eglon, and all Israel with him; and they encamped against it, and fought against it:

35 And they took it on that day, and smote it with the edge of the sword, and all the souls that were therein he utterly destroyed that day, according to all that he had done to Lachish.

36 And Joshua went up from Eglon, and all Israel with him, unto Hebron; and they fought against it:

37 And they took it, and smote it with the edge of the sword, and the king thereof, and all the cities thereof, and all the souls that were therein; he left none remaining, according to all that he had done to Eglon; but destroyed it utterly, and all the souls that were therein.

38 And Joshua returned, and all Israel with him, to Debir; and fought against it:

39 And he took it, and the king thereof, and all the cities thereof; and they smote them with the edge of the sword, and utterly destroyed all the souls that were therein; he left none remaining: as he had done to Hebron, so he did to Debir, and to the king thereof; as he had done also to []{#c14V.xhtml_page_216}Libnah, and to her king.

40 So Joshua smote all the country of the hills, and of the south, and of the vale, and of the springs, and all their kings: he left none remaining, but utterly destroyed all that breathed, as the LORD God of Israel commanded.

41 And Joshua smote them from Kadeshbarnea even unto Gaza, and all the country of Goshen, even unto Gibeon.

42 And all these kings and their land did Joshua take at one time, because the LORD God of Israel fought for Israel.

43 And Joshua returned, and all Israel with him, unto the camp to Gilgal.

This is what is known as the "southern campaign"; that is, Joshua is conquering the cities in the south of Canaan (vs. 40). Verse 41 gives you the extent of the campaign. It goes from Gibeon up above Jerusalem down to Kadesh-barnea where they should have entered the land back in Numbers 13--14, and from the "Gaza Strip" by the sea coast to Goshen over by the Dead Sea (note: this is a different Goshen than the one in Egypt).

The passage lists six major cities Joshua took: Makkedah, Libnah, Lachish, Eglon, Hebron, and Debir. Some cities were taken in a day, like Makkedah (vs. 28). A city like Lachish was a little harder, and it took two days to conquer it (vs. 32). And at Lachish, the king of Gezer brought over his army to help out the King of Lachish (see our comments on 9:1--2). On a couple of the cities, you are given no time element for the conquest. What you do know is that it took much longer than a week or a month or even a year to take all those cities. Joshua 11:18 says, ["Joshua made war a long time with all those kings."]{.class_s2FW}

Once more, the Christian is reminded that the fight against sin is a lifetime battle. There is no "second blessing" or being "slain in the Spirit" that eradicates the old Adamic nature in the believer.

Now I know passages like this aren't particularly exciting reading, but the Holy Spirit put these verses in there for a reason. First of all, it shows you the [historical nature]{.class_s2FX} of the Bible. The Bible isn't primarily a religious book; it's first and foremost a [history]{.class_s2FX} book. []{#c14V.xhtml_page_217}The Lord records the history of how He works in the lives of men and nations so that we up here in the Twenty-first Century can learn from what happened to those folks back there in 4000, 1500, 1000, and 400 B.C. (1 Cor. 10:11).

Of course, the problem is: "the only thing men learn from history is that men don't learn from history." Who cares what happened to the King of Makkedah or ["Horam king of Gezer"]{.class_s2FW} or a bunch of people in Eglon, Hebron, and Debir? Well, you had better pay attention to what happened to those people, because the same thing will happen to [you]{.class_s2FX} and [your country]{.class_s2FX} if you don't get right (see our comments on Luke 13:3 in that Commentary).

Second, the reason the Lord repeats things so many times in the Scriptures is so you will [get what He is saying.]{.class_s2FX} I know it's a drag to read a passage like this where the same material is gone over again and again, but one of the keys to learning anything is to go over it again and again until you get it. When I was in school, the teachers made you recite your "times tables," recite poetry, recite famous speeches, etc., until you could give them by memory. I don't reckon the public schools do that today; they're too busy making sure your kids know how to fornicate and commit sodomy. But if you want to learn something, you repeat it until it becomes second nature.

The advertising world knows that. You will see all kinds of signs and billboards, and commercials on TV and radio, that say, "Have a Coke, have a Coke, have a Coke." There's nothing particularly thirst-quenching about a Coke; if you want your thirst quenched, drink water. But the Coca Cola company keeps repeating that over and over to you so that when you get thirsty, your first response is: "Have a Coke." Well, you should so familiarize yourself with what's in that Book so that whatever circumstance arises, your first response is [what God says.]{.class_s2FX}

The Lord's people forget so easily, so the Holy Spirit says something over and over again so you won't forget. The old song says, "Count your blessings, name them one by one." Why? Because we forget God's blessings, so we should constantly rehearse them so we won't forget. The Lord says the same things over and over again to ram it into you so you'll remember what He says.

Now before closing this chapter, let's pick up a couple of lessons []{#c14V.xhtml_page_218}from these seemingly boring, dull verses that just give you a litany of Joshua's southern conquests. First, note that he ["smote"]{.class_s2FW} each city ["with the edge of the sword."]{.class_s2FW} Now we know Joshua and those Israelites had other weapons like slings and spears, but remember that what you are reading here is a type of the believer's spiritual warfare. The weapon of the Christian is a ["twoedged sword"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 4:12) that is called ["the sword of the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:17). Your weapon, Christian, is the word of God, the Scriptures. If you are going to get the victory over sin and temptation, you are going to have to use the word of God against the Devil like Christ used it when He was tempted (see Matt. 4:1--10; Luke 4:1--12).

Second, notice the Old Testament use of the word [soul]{.class_s2FX} here in Joshua 10 (vss. 28, 30, 32, 35, 37, 39). In the Old Testament, the word [soul]{.class_s2FX} was equated with [physical life]{.class_s2FX} (note how it is used of [animals]{.class_s2FX} in Num. 31:28). That's because, before Calvary and the Resurrection, the soul of man is [stuck to the body of flesh]{.class_s2FX} (Rom. 7:1--5) so that whatever the flesh does affects the soul (e.g., Lev. 5:2, 7:18, 20--21, 25, 27, 17:10, 12, 15, 22:6).

When a sinner comes to Christ for salvation, the Holy Spirit cuts the soul loose from the flesh by an ["operation"]{.class_s2FW} that is a [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} circumcision (Col. 2:11--12). In that way, no sin committed in the flesh can affect the eternal destiny of the new man in Christ (Isa. 55:3; Acts 13:34; Rom. 8:1--2, 29, 38--39 cf. Ezek. 4:14). Of course, you will reap what you sow in the flesh (Gal. 6:8), and you can lose rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ (2 Cor. 5:10 cf. 1 Cor. 3:13--15), but you will never again become ["dead in trespasses and sins"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 2:1) as Adam became when he sinned.

[]{#c1BA.xhtml}

# Chapter 11 {.heading_s2B}

11:1 And it came to pass, when Jabin king of Hazor had heard those things, that he sent to Jobab king of Madon, and to the king of Shimron, and to the king of Achshaph,

2 And to the kings that were on the north of the mountains, and of the plains south of Chinneroth, and in the valley, and in the borders of Dor on the west,

3 And to the Canaanite on the east and on the west, and to the Amorite, and the Hittite, and the Perizzite, and the Jebusite in the mountains, and to the Hivite under Hermon in the land of Mizpeh.

4 And they went out, they and all their hosts with them, much people, even as the sand that is upon the sea shore in multitude, with horses and chariots very many.

5 And when all these kings were met together, they came and pitched together at the waters of Merom, to fight against Israel.

Chapter 11 deals with what is known as the "northern campaign." In chapter 10, Joshua took all the cities in the south of Canaan; here in chapter 11, he takes the cities in the north of Canaan going all the way up just below Mt. Hermon in Lebanon (vs. 17). Look at the cities involved: ["Hazor"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1) is up above the Sea of Galilee going toward Lake Huleh; ["Madon"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1) lies just west of the Sea of Galilee; ["Shimron"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1) is over near the Kishon River; ["Achshaph"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1) is just below Mt. Carmel and to the east; ["Dor"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2) is on the sea coast below Mt. Carmel; and ["Chinneroth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2) is another name for the Sea of Galilee (12:3 cf. 21:32; Isa. 9:1).

Now what you are reading in this passage is the biggest confederacy yet. Look at verse 4.

"And they went out, they and all their hosts with them, much people, even as the sand that is upon the sea shore in multitude, with horses and chariots very many."

This was alluded to back in 9:1--2, and you can see our comments on that passage. Again I draw your attention to the fact that it is [God]{.class_s2FX} who brings the nations together to [destroy ]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c1BA.xhtml_page_220}them.

["For, behold, in those days, and in that time ]{.class_s2FW}\[a reference to the end of the Tribulation---Rev. 16:12--16\][, when I shall bring again the captivity of Judah and Jerusalem, I ]{.class_s2FW}\[the speaker is [the Lord]{.class_s2FX}\] [will also GATHER ALL NATIONS, and will bring them down into the valley of Jehoshaphat, and will plead with them there for my people and for my heritage Israel, whom they have scattered among the nations, and parted my land . . . . Assemble yourselves ]{.class_s2FW}\[the United Nations Assembly---Zeph. 3:8\][, and come, all ye heathen, and gather yourselves together round about: thither cause thy mighty ones to come down, O LORD. Let the heathen be wakened, and come up to the valley of Jehoshaphat: for there will I sit to judge all the heathen round about"]{.class_s2FW} (Joel 3:1--2, 11--12).

That's the Lord gathering the nations together to wipe them out at the Second Advent. When the New Testament "Joshua" returns, He has a "southern campaign" at Sinai, Edom, and Jerusalem, and a "northern campaign" involving a much larger force at Armageddon. So what you read in Joshua 9, 10, and 11 is a picture of the Second Advent, like we have taught you time and time again.

Now the practical lesson for the Christian---and we have mentioned this before under our remarks on 8:3 (which see)---is that the further along you get in the Christian life, the less "divine intervention" you get in the fight against sin, the world, and the Devil, and the harder the fight gets because you have to rely on the word of God and prayer. The first battle in which the Israelites were involved they didn't have to do much of anything. All they had to do was march around Jericho and shout and God brought down the walls. And although the next battle went badly because of sin, the Lord intervened miraculously in the battle with the five Kings. In each battle, though, God's people had to take more responsibility. In the battle against this huge confederacy, there are no miracles from God; it is just pure fighting. It is just faith in the promise of God (vs. 6) and hard work.

That is how the Lord deals with us in the Christian life. If you got saved later in life like I did, you come into the Christian life with a []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_221}certain amount of "baggage." There are some things that God will initially take out of your life immediately. It's kind of deceptive in a way because you think getting rid of the rest of your sins will be that easy. The Lord will give you deliverance from some things He knows you can't handle, and He will let you fight the things He knows you need to handle through prayer and the word.

The old saying is: "Every dog should have just enough fleas to remind him that he's a dog"; in the same way, every Christian has just enough sin left over after salvation to remind him that's he's a [saved sinner.]{.class_s2FX} About the time you think you've got it whipped because you don't drink, you don't smoke, you don't cuss, you got your hair cut right, you dress right, you witness, you read your Bible, you pray, etc.; about that time you run into things like pride and laziness and jealousy and temper and misrepresentation and prevarication and drawing judgment before you know the facts and taking somebody's word for something because you are already prejudiced to start with and believing something you heard because it is to your benefit to believe it, etc.

These Charismatics and Holiness folk who claim to be wholly sanctified and to be sinless because their old natures have been "eradicated" are [liars.]{.class_s2FX} I have a dissertation in my files called "the Holiness nightmare"; you can read the full text under our remarks on Romans 15:1 in that Commentary. The gist of it is that once you think you have taken care of all the sin in your life, you have to deal with things like secret pride, bitterness, an unyielding spirit, self-centeredness, lust, deceit, a vengeful spirit, excusing sin in your life, stinginess, vanity, partiality, an unmerciful attitude, fake humility, apathy toward the things of God, etc. No Charismatic or Holiness could pass that test, not if he were honest with himself. Those are the kinds of things you will have to fight your whole life, long after the drugs, alcohol, cigarettes, and filthy language are gone.

Back to Joshua 11: ["And to the Canaanite on the east and on the west"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3)---that's east and west of the Jordan up above the Sea of Galilee. ["Under Hermon"]{.class_s2FW} is Mt. Hermon just above Dan in southern Lebanon. ["The land of Mizpeh"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3) and ["the valley of Mizpeh eastward"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 8) are a region north of Lake Huleh just below Mt. Hermon, so this is a different Mizpeh than the []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_222}one in Gilead on the east side of Jordan (Gen. 31:23--25, 48--49; Judg. 10:17, 11:1).

Verse 4: ["And they went out, they and all their hosts with them, much people, even as the sand that is upon the sea shore in multitude, with horses and chariots very many."]{.class_s2FW} Israel is facing a seemingly hopeless situation. They are facing a superior force with mounted cavalry. Humanly speaking, there seems to be no hope of victory. But that Bible says, ["Some trust in chariots, and some in horses: but we will remember the name of the LORD our God"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 20:7); and ["The horse is prepared against the day of battle: but safety is of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 21:31). [No]{.class_s2FX} army is delivered or victorious because of the multitude of chariots or horses; or in the case of the United States, tanks, bombers, carriers, cruise missiles, etc. Salvation, even [physical]{.class_s2FX} salvation, is [of the Lord.]{.class_s2FX}

Here is an army with more soldiers and superior armament, and they are about to [lose their shirts.]{.class_s2FX} The United States goes around the world and throws its weight around because (so far) it has a better trained army and better equipment than its enemies. But you let God have a grievance against this country (like a bunch of faggots, queers, Lesbians, dykes, and Moslems leading your army), and all the nuclear missiles, aircraft carriers, tanks, cruise missiles, fighter jets, "drones," etc., will mean [absolutely nothing.]{.class_s2FX}

["The waters of Merom"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5), where the northern confederacy has its "staging area" (the encampment where they plan to launch their attack), is a river that flows into the Sea of Galilee from the town of Merom, which is north and west of the Sea of Galilee.

Now this is a tremendous confederation Joshua faces. I don't know if you as a believer will ever face that much opposition or not. Some of your brethren in the Dark Ages did. The Catholics launched a [crusade]{.class_s2FX}---I mean a [military crusade]{.class_s2FX} just like they launched against the Moslems in Palestine---against the Albigenses of southern France. Martin Luther faced down the combined religious and political might of the Roman Catholic Church and said at the Diet of Worms, "Here I stand. I can do no other. God help me. Amen."

I must confess, up to this point in my life, I have never been up []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_223}against that much opposition. I have had the faculty members at fifteen Christian schools cut me down in class, but that doesn't amount to much. I have had Roman Catholics threaten to bomb the work here, but nothing ever came of that. I have had people sue me in court about eight times, but that is small potatoes. I have had the police stop me while I was street preaching and threaten to haul me off to the "pokie" in the squad car, but that doesn't really count either; they didn't do it.

But if you have to face the HEW (HRS, "Department of Children and Families") like Lester Roloff did, or the Roman Catholic Church and the IRA, the European Parliament, and the British Broadcasting Company like Ian Paisley, that is a different story. You are about to get into a situation in this country (and by the time of publication of this book, it may already be here) where you face the combined forces of the news media; the faggots, butches, Lesbians, and transvestites; and Federal, State, and local governments about the queers trying to get into churches and force Christians to "accept" them and [promote]{.class_s2FX} their perversion. When that time comes, all I can tell you to do is [stand fast on the Book]{.class_s2FX} and [pray.]{.class_s2FX} You don't have a promise of physical deliverance like Joshua had, but you do have the promise of a reward in Heaven (2 Tim. 4:7--8; James 1:12; Rev. 2:10). Just keep on doing what God wants you to do and don't give an inch. Remember, though, that you won't be able to handle the battle in the flesh; you will have to go forward [on your knees.]{.class_s2FX}

6 And the LORD said unto Joshua, Be not afraid because of them: for to morrow about this time will I deliver them up all slain before Israel: thou shalt hough their horses, and burn their chariots with fire.

7 So Joshua came, and all the people of war with him, against them by the waters of Merom suddenly; and they fell upon them.

8 And the LORD delivered them into the hand of Israel, who smote them, and chased them unto great Zidon, and unto Misrephothmaim, and unto the valley of Mizpeh eastward; and they smote them, until they left them none remaining.

9 And Joshua did unto them as the LORD bade him: he houghed their horses, and burnt their chariots with fire.

Now Joshua is facing the largest army he has ever faced, and the Lord comes to him and reaffirms what He told him all the way back in 1:9---["Be not afraid because of them."]{.class_s2FW} Moses told the people, ["When thou goest out to battle against thine enemies, and seest horses, and chariots, and a people more than thou, be not afraid of them: for the LORD thy God is with thee, which brought thee up out of the land of Egypt"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 20:1).

I know that's easy to say, but it's not always easy to believe. I mean, when you've got the Catholics against you, the Charismatics against you, the Southern Baptists against you, the Campbellites against you, the Liberals against you, a bunch of lukewarm Laodicean Christians against you, the press against you, the TV and radio news stations against you, the queers against you, and the government against you, you are up against a "northern confederacy," boy, I kid you not. And trying to take care of a wife and kids on a living that pays "peanuts" adds to the discouragement and apprehension, doesn't it? It makes you wonder if God is really going to take care of you.

But I can say, without fear of contradiction, that when you get in those circumstances, you don't [need]{.class_s2FX} the support of the Catholics, the Campbellites, the Charismatics, the Liberals, the news media, the sex perverts, the government, or even the brethren. [You need God.]{.class_s2FX} If you have the Lord, and the Lord and you are together, you can get through. Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "One man and God are a majority." Now [that's]{.class_s2FX} a "confederacy."

Do you know about what you need to worry? You need to worry about [fellowship with God.]{.class_s2FX} All these people who compromise with the world to get the money, or to keep from getting shut down or shot, end up with [nothing ]{.class_s2FX}spiritually. If you stay in fellowship with God, eventually you will wind up on top. It may take a while, but that's where you'll end up. I mean, it took Noah 120 years, but when he stepped out of the ark, he was King of the world, boy. I don't know what the Lord may do for you in this life, but if you stay in fellowship with the Lord and serve Him the way He wants, one day you will rule []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_225}and reign with Him as a King and a priest.

One old saint said, "Anything with Thy smile; nothing with Thy frown." That means as long as you and the Lord get along and you make Him happy, you can take anything. And the opposite is true: if you and the Lord are at odds with each other, you won't make it no matter how you fare materially or financially. When you are in fellowship with the Lord, a bowl of pea soup and a hunk of black bread with a glass of water are better eating than sirloin or lobster served with champagne when you are out of fellowship with Him. Amen, amen, amen!

Back to verse 6: [". . . for to morrow about this time will I deliver them up all slain before Israel."]{.class_s2FW} How much difference a day can make. That northern confederation didn't know it, but they only had 24 hours to live. There's an account like that over in 2 Kings 7. Samaria was under siege by the Syrians, and the famine was so bad in the city that the women were eating their children (2 Kings 6). The King of Israel blamed Elisha and God, but when he sent a messenger to execute Elisha, Elisha gave this prophecy:

["Then Elisha said, Hear ye the word of the LORD; Thus said the LORD, To morrow about this time shall a measure of fine flour be sold for a shekel, and two measures of barley for a shekel, in the gate of Samaria"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Kings 7:1).

In other words, the famine would be broken, and food would be sold "dirt cheap." The King's adviser mocked Elisha: ["Behold, if the LORD would make windows in heaven, might this thing be?"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Kings 7:2). Bad move---God [did]{.class_s2FX} make ["windows in heaven"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 7:11). Because of his unbelief, Elisha told that fellow, ["Behold, thou shalt see it with thine eyes, but shalt not eat thereof."]{.class_s2FW}

Now, we are not going into the whole story; you can read it in 2 Kings 7. The next day when the food became available, that adviser lay dead, trodden under foot by all the people trying to get to the food. That fellow thought he had a full life and career ahead of him; he only had 24 hours to live. He was like that rich fool in Luke 12:20.

That Bible says, ["Boast not thyself of to morrow; for thou knowest not what a day may bring forth"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 27:1). That's why Paul said, ["behold NOW is the accepted time; behold, NOW is the day of salvation"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c1BA.xhtml_page_226} (2 Cor. 6:2). If you are lost, the best time to get saved is RIGHT NOW; you may not be alive tomorrow. If you are saved and there is something you need to do for the Lord Jesus Christ, don't wait until tomorrow to do it; tomorrow may be too late.

["Thou shalt hough their horses, and burn their chariots with fire."]{.class_s2FW} Joshua takes the horses and cuts the hamstrings to cripple them (vs. 9); David does the same thing in 2 Samuel 8:4. This was done for two reasons: first because the horses were dedicated to the idolatrous worship of the sun god (2 Kings 23:11), and second because the horses were used in the practice of [bestiality.]{.class_s2FX} Look at Leviticus 18:23--25.

"Neither shalt thou lie with any beast to defile thyself therewith: neither shall any woman stand before a beast to lie down thereto: it is confusion. Defile not ye yourselves in any of these things: FOR IN ALL THESE THE NATIONS ARE DEFILED WHICH I CAST OUT BEFORE YOU: And the land is defiled: therefore I do visit the iniquity thereof upon it, and the land itself vomiteth out her inhabitants."

[That's]{.class_s2FX} where America is [right now.]{.class_s2FX} Even though God Almighty called all the sexual depravity mentioned in Leviticus 18 (including "gay marriage"---Lev. 18:22) ["abominations"]{.class_s2FW} (Lev. 18:27) and ["abominable customs"]{.class_s2FW} (Lev. 18:30), your first Hamite President (and all the nations in Canaan that practiced this filth were [Hamites]{.class_s2FX}) sees no difference in two men shacking up together (or two women shacking up together) and eating lobster, shrimp, or catfish (Lev. 11:10). [The Bible never says a land vomits out its inhabitants for eating clams, oysters, and scallops.]{.class_s2FX} Someone is so eaten up with [perverse lust]{.class_s2FX} that he [can't read.]{.class_s2FX}

Do you know what you can expect here in the United States for practicing (and teaching your kids in the public schools to practice) all the sexual abominations in which those Canaanites, Perizzites, Hittites, Hivites, Amorites, Girgashites, and Jebusites were involved? You can expect the land to [vomit out]{.class_s2FX} its citizens. "America the Beautiful" is going to [puke out]{.class_s2FX} all these fairies, fruits, faggots, butches, dykes, Lesbians, queers, double-breasted finks, transvestites, crossdressers, and "transgenders," right along with []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_227}everyone who put up with them, promoted them, "accepted" them, and gave "aid and comfort" to them. God is going to treat this nation just like He treated Sodom and Gomorrah, and those seven heathen nations in Canaan. Don't think America is going to get out of it just because it started out as a Bible-believing, Bible-reading nation and still has a population of 75% professing "Christians."

Bob Jones Sr. said, "God is going to require more of this nation than He does other nations because this nation started out right." America is the only Gentile nation that didn't start out with paganism or Roman Catholicism. It started out with God and the Bible, and it has now dumped both for money, sex, and education---just about in that order. Jesus said, ["For unto whomsoever much is given, of him shall be much required"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 12:48). This country has had more Bible, more Gospel, more preaching, and more real Biblical Christianity than any other country on earth; so when the axe falls, it's going to fall hard.

Now there is one more reason the Lord told Joshua to hamstring those horses and burn the chariots. If those Jews had captured all those horses and chariots, they would have had a cavalry second to none; then they would put their trust in their horses and chariots instead of the Lord. The Lord warned them, ["Woe to them that go down to Egypt for help; and stay on horses, and trust in chariots, because they are many; and in horsemen, because they are very strong; but they look not unto the Holy One of Israel, neither seek the LORD!"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 31:1).

That was one of Solomon's problems. God told those Jewish Kings that they weren't to multiply to themselves horses, wives, or gold (Deut. 17:16--17); and Solomon violated all three prohibitions. Solomon had 4,000 chariots (2 Chron. 9:25) with ten horses per chariot (1 Kings 4:26). David numbered the people so he could boast about the size of his army, which is why ["the LORD sent a pestilence upon Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 24:15). God wanted those Jews trusting [Him,]{.class_s2FX} not their army or cavalry (Psa. 20:7).

It doesn't do any good for the United States military to count their soldiers, sailors, Marines, ships, submarines, tanks, intercontinental ballistic missiles, cruise missiles, etc. When the Lord decides to judge this nation, all those things won't matter one []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_228}bit. The national motto on your coins and money says, "In God We Trust" (of course now it has been put on the [edge]{.class_s2FX} of the coins where you won't notice it and where it will wear off quicker). Americans don't trust God any more; they trust the things the coins and money can buy.

Verse 7 in Joshua 11 is the military tactic called "the element of surprise." Joshua and the army of Israel do another forced march (see our comments on 10:9) and catch the northern confederation off guard when they weren't ready for an attack. Other examples in military history are Stonewall Jackson at Chancellorsville (Civil War), Hitler's invasion of Poland and the Japanese attack on Pearl Harbor (WWII), the use of tanks at Cambrai (WWI), and Al Quaeda flying two jets into the Twin Towers in New York City (Sept. 11, 2001).

Now Joshua and the Israelites take the northern confederation by surprise, and the Lord gives Israel the victory over them. What's left of the northern confederacy's army flees in three directions (vs. 8): towards ["Zidon"]{.class_s2FW} on the sea coast in northern Lebanon, towards ["Misrephoth-maim"]{.class_s2FW} which is on the sea coast below Tyre at the southernmost border of Lebanon (13:6), and towards  ["the valley of Mizpeh"]{.class_s2FW} which is north and east of Merom above Lake Huleh. According to Joshua 13:6, all of Lebanon clear up to Sidon and Mt. Hermon belonged to Israel. If the present State of Israel got just the land God gave Joshua, it would be four or five times larger than it is now. There would be no "Jordan" or "Gaza Strip" or "West Bank" or "Southern Lebanon"; all those places would be Israeli territory. Don't worry; when Jesus Christ comes back, those Jews are not only getting all of that, they are going to get the Sinai Peninsula, the Nile Delta in Egypt, and all of Syria and Iraq up to the Euphrates River (Gen. 15:18).

We have already commented on verse 9 under our remarks on verse 6 (which see).

10 And Joshua at that time turned back, and took Hazor, and smote the king thereof with the sword: for Hazor beforetime was the head of all those kingdoms.

11 And they smote all the souls that were therein with []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_229}the edge of the sword, utterly destroying them: there was not any left to breathe: and he burnt Hazor with fire.

12 And all the cities of those kings, and all the kings of them, did Joshua take, and smote them with the edge of the sword, and he utterly destroyed them, as Moses the servant of the LORD commanded.

13 But as for the cities that stood still in their strength, Israel burned none of them, save Hazor only; that did Joshua burn.

14 And all the spoil of these cities, and the cattle, the children of Israel took for a prey unto themselves; but every man they smote with the edge of the sword, until they had destroyed them, neither left they any to breathe.

15 As the LORD commanded Moses his servant, so did Moses command Joshua, and so did Joshua; he left nothing undone of all that the LORD commanded Moses.

Joshua does the same thing in this passage as he did in the "southern campaign" (see chap. 10): after dispensing with the main host, he turns back, and one by one, he takes all the cities involved. The first city he takes is the ["head"]{.class_s2FW} city, Hazor (vs. 10), the city that organized the northern confederacy (vs. 1). Joshua takes the chief city first and burns it to the ground to demoralize the rest of the cities in the confederation (vs. 13).

We have already commented on the Old Testament use of the word ["souls"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 11) under our remarks on 10:28--39 (which see). As with all the cities from Ai onward, the Israelites were allowed to keep the spoils of the cities, and we have already commented on that under our remarks on 7:11 and 8:2 (which see).

Verses 12 and 15 show you Joshua's chain of command and his perfect obedience in the matters at hand. Now by perfect obedience, I am not talking about either Moses or Joshua being sinlessly perfect because neither of them were. Moses lost his temper and struck the rock when he should have spoken to it (Num. 20:8--11), and twice Joshua forgot to pray about something and got himself and the people in trouble (chaps. 7 and 9). But when it came to the matter of destroying the heathen people of the land, Joshua did what Moses []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_230}told him to do (Deut. 7:2, 20:16--17), and of course, Moses got his "marching orders" from God (Deut. 7:23--24).

The spiritual application, of course, is to the Christian's battle against sin. Once more you should note the relation between faith and works in this matter. In this chapter, Joshua has faith in what the Lord told him in verse 6. But suppose Joshua, having believed God would give him the victory, went up against that northern confederation with no sword, no spear, no shield, saying, "The Lord's delivered all of them into my hand; I've got it made. I've got this thing whipped." What would have happened? Why, he would have gotten slaughtered, of course. The victory depended on Joshua doing his part: [fighting.]{.class_s2FX}

It is the same in the Christian fight against sin. Positionally you are dead to sin and ["a new creature" "in Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:2--4; 2 Cor. 5:17). You have been born again spiritually, and ["that which is born of the Spirit is spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (John 3:6). So you have a new spiritual life you didn't have before, and ["the flesh lusteth against the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:17). As long as you are in this body of sinful flesh, there is going to be a conflict. You have to practically work out what is positionally true. That is the difference between [standing]{.class_s2FX} and [state.]{.class_s2FX} If you just sit back and do nothing based on your doctrinal standing in Christ, the flesh is going to mop the floor with you. You have to use the new weapons, the [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} weapons (2 Cor. 10:3--6) God has given you---the [word of God]{.class_s2FX} and [prayer]{.class_s2FX} (Eph. 6:17--18)---to put down the desires of the flesh. So it is not just living in the Spirit positionally; it is walking in the Spirit and crucifying the lusts of the flesh (Gal. 5:24--25). It takes [active warfare]{.class_s2FX} on your part to appropriate the victory Christ has promised you.

16 So Joshua took all that land, the hills, and all the south country, and all the land of Goshen, and the valley, and the plain, and the mountain of Israel, and the valley of the same;

17 Even from the mount Halak, that goeth up to Seir, even unto Baalgad in the valley of Lebanon under mount Hermon: and all their kings he took, and smote them, and slew them.

18 Joshua made war a long time with all those kings.

19 There was not a city that made peace with the children of Israel, save the Hivites the inhabitants of Gibeon: all other they took in battle.

20 For it was of the LORD to harden their hearts, that they should come against Israel in battle, that he might destroy them utterly, and that they might have no favour, but that he might destroy them, as the LORD commanded Moses.

21 And at that time came Joshua, and cut off the Anakims from the mountains, from Hebron, from Debir, from Anab, and from all the mountains of Judah, and from all the mountains of Israel: Joshua destroyed them utterly with their cities.

The passage is a summary of the conquest of Canaan: it includes both the southern and the northern campaigns. As we pointed out back in 10:41, ["the land of Goshen"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 16) is not the land where Israel settled when they were in Egypt (Gen. 47:27; Exod. 9:26); this Goshen is a region in the mountainous region of Judah near the Dead Sea. You will see that time and time again in the Scriptures. Carmel is not only a mountain in northern Israel (1 Kings 18); it is also a location in Judah (1 Sam. 25). You see the same thing today; 32 States have a city named "Greenville."

["The mountain of Israel, and the valley of the same"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 16) is probably a reference to Mount Ephraim, which is actually a mountainous region in the center of Canaan intersected by valleys. In verse 21, ["the mountain"]{.class_s2FW} is [plural]{.class_s2FX}---["mountains."]{.class_s2FW} This is a figure of speech known as "heterosis," which Bullinger defines as "an exchange of one voice, mood, tense, person, NUMBER, degree, or gender for another" ([Figures of Speech Used in the Bible,]{.class_s2FX} 1898); in this case, a singular is used for a plural.

Verse 17 gives you the southernmost and northernmost extremes of Joshua's conquests. ["Mount Halak"]{.class_s2FW} is south of the Dead Sea bordering on Edom (["Seir"]{.class_s2FW}), and ["Baal-gad"]{.class_s2FW} is north of Dan in central Lebanon at the western foot of Mt. Hermon.

Now up to this point, you have been given the narrative of []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_232}Joshua's conquest of Canaan, but no time element has been given. Verse 18 gives you the first indication of how long it took: ["Joshua made war A LONG TIME with all those kings."]{.class_s2FW} If you use the age of Caleb as given in 14:6--10 as an indicator, the ["long time"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 18 is at least five years, and perhaps longer.

We covered verse 19 in chapter 9. Verse 20 is a favorite verse of the Calvinist. The teaching is that there are certain people chosen before Genesis 1:1 called "the elect," whom God has predestinated to Heaven against their will ("Irresistible Grace"). Then everybody else is "reprobate"; that is, God [rejected]{.class_s2FX} them before Genesis 1:1 based solely on His good pleasure. To ensure those people will end up in Hell, the Lord hardens their hearts to reject the Gospel. As an example, Calvinists will pull out Pharaoh from Romans 9:17--18 and Exodus 4:21.

That's the kind of theological and philosophical nonsense you get from sniffing Calvin's TULIPs too long. Calvinists depend on the Biblical ignorance of their students and congregations to perpetuate such baloney. Election isn't based on God's ["good pleasure."]{.class_s2FW} It's based on His [foreknowledge:]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}["Elect according to the foreknowledge of God the Father"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 1:2).

Before God ever said He would harden Pharaoh's heart, He said, ["And I am sure that the king of Egypt will not let you go, no, not by a mighty hand"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 3:19). And as far as the actual hardening goes, the Lord didn't harden Pharaoh's heart until Pharaoh had rejected what God said in Exodus 5 and had defied Him with the magicians in Exodus 7:11--12 (see Exod. 7:13--14). In other words, Pharaoh acted [of his own free will]{.class_s2FX} before the Lord ever did anything to him.

As for the heathen people of Canaan, they weren't predestinated for Hell. God didn't arbitrarily harden their hearts; He hardened their hearts because they had been living like the devil for 400 years. He let ["the iniquity of the Amorites"]{.class_s2FW} fill up and overflow the cup (Gen. 15:16) before He hardened their hearts. The Lord will not harden any sinner's heart until that sinner messes up first. The warning is for a man not to harden [himself.]{.class_s2FX}

["But exhort one another daily, while it is called To day; lest any of you be hardened through the deceitfulness of sin"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c1BA.xhtml_page_233} (Heb. 3:13).

Now, the spiritual lesson for the Christian is that the Lord will allow the flesh to rise up against the spirit for the express purpose of putting down the flesh, humiliating it, and defeating it. A good example of that in the New Testament is Simon Peter. Peter got proud and cocky in his discipleship; and when the Lord told the disciples that they would all forsake Him and run away in the Garden of Gethsemane, Peter bragged, ["Though all men shall be offended because of thee, yet will I never be offended"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 26:33). When the Lord told Peter, "The Bible says, ['I will smite the shepherd, and the sheep of the flock shall be scattered abroad']{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 26:31)," Peter replied, "It doesn't say that in the original text; it says all the sheep will be scattered [except me.]{.class_s2FX}"

Well, the Lord let Peter's old flesh rise up out there in the Garden of Gethsemane, and when Peter tried to defend Christ with a sword, Jesus told him to put it away. Peter got scared and ran away, and he got mad at the Lord because of that. That's why he cussed and denied Christ there by the fire: he was mad at Jesus for putting him in the position where he looked like a coward.

Peter is there by the fire cussing a blue streak, and the Lord comes out of that interrogation before Annas and looks straight at Peter. He doesn't have to say a word; He just looks him straight in the eyes. About that time, the rooster sounds off, and Peter remembers Jesus telling him he would deny Christ three times before the cock crew. That was too much for Peter to take. He ran out of that judgment hall back to the garden and fell on his knees weeping and praying. That was Simon Peter's flesh being allowed to rise up until it got smacked down so the spirit could get back on top.

Now if you are saved, you can't lose. The Christian has the promise of God that the Lord will get him through.

["And we know that all things work together for good to them that love God, to them who are the called according to his purpose"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:28).

["Being confident of this very thing, that he which hath begun a good work in you will perform it until the day of Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 1:6).

When sin has got you down and it looks like it has you whipped, remember: []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_234}["greater is he that is in you, than he that is in the world"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 4:4). The same God who gave Joshua the victory over that massive army of the northern confederacy [lives in you,]{.class_s2FX} if you are a believer, and can give you the victory over sin if you will fight with the weapons He has given you in the way He told you to do it (read Rom. 6).

22 There was none of the Anakims left in the land of the children of Israel: only in Gaza, in Gath, and in Ashdod, there remained.

23 So Joshua took the whole land, according to all that the LORD said unto Moses; and Joshua gave it for an inheritance unto Israel according to their divisions by their tribes. And the land rested from war.

["The Anakims"]{.class_s2FW} are the giants that scared off the ten spies in Numbers 13:33. Joshua faces them after he has put down all the Hittites, the Hivites, the Girgashites, the Perizzites, the Amorites, the Canaanites, and the Jebusites in the land: the giants are the last group with whom he deals. That just goes to show you that the toughest battles are the ones toward the [end;]{.class_s2FX} the last battle is the hardest.

That's why no Christian should brag or boast about what he is going to do or what he thinks he would do in a particular situation, like Peter did there in Matthew 26 (see our remarks above under vs. 20). Paul warned you, ["Wherefore let him that thinketh he standeth take heed lest he fall"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 10:12).

One time the King of Syria was bragging to the King of Israel about how many soldiers he had to come down and whip the Israelites (1 Kings 20:10). Even though the King of Israel at that time was a pagan idolater, he had a word of sage advice for the Syrian King: ["Let not him that girdeth on his harness boast himself as he that putteth it off"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 20:11). In other words, don't be bragging about by how much you are going to win the game when you are back in the locker room and haven't even put on your uniform yet. All kinds of things can happen before the game is over. The old saying is: "Don't count your chickens before they're []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_235}hatched."

Now there is nothing wrong with claiming the victory ahead of time by faith, but it has to be [faith in what God says,]{.class_s2FX} not faith in your own abilities and aspirations. That's what Joshua and Caleb did back in Numbers 13--14. While the other ten spies were bemoaning the fact that they were like grasshoppers in comparison to the giants, Caleb said, "We can take 'em" (Num. 13:30), but that was based on the promises and blessings of God.

["If the LORD delight in us, then he will bring us into this land, and give it us . . . Only rebel not ye against the LORD, neither fear ye the people of the land; for they are bread for us: their defence is departed from them, and the LORD is with us: fear them not"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 14:8--9).

So after 45 years (see 14:10), Joshua and Caleb are finally taking the ground they both claimed by faith back in Numbers 13--14. But again, they claimed it by faith because God promised it to them (Num. 14:24, 30). This modern "name it and claim it" theology isn't found anywhere in Scripture; it's just asking for something to consume on your own lusts (James 4:3).

Now let that be a lesson to you in faith. If the Lord has called you to do something for Him, He's going to show you some of the fruit like He did those spies in Numbers 13:23--24. At the same time, He's going to let you see some of the "giants," the [obstacles]{.class_s2FX} to doing what God has called you to do. Why does He do that? To see if you'll [quit.]{.class_s2FX} He wants to see if you'll claim the promise by faith or give up. If you give up, you spend your time wandering aimlessly in your Christian life like the children of Israel did in the wilderness for forty years.

This country is filled with "forty-year" Christians wandering in the wilderness. They gave up in a business meeting or in some hassle with a pastor, deacon, or another Christian. They got "miffed," as the saying goes, and just quit serving God. If you do any personal work at all, you've run into them: they [used to]{.class_s2FX} go to church, but they don't anymore.

Now the next thing you learn from Joshua and Caleb is if you claim the promises of God by faith, the end may not be in sight. It can take a long time for the promise to be fulfilled. With Joshua and Caleb it took 45 years. The Lord might not make you wait that long, []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_236}but He could make you wait a pretty good clip. Some of those old-time missionaries like William Carey and Adoniram Judson labored for [years]{.class_s2FX} before they even saw their first convert, but they finally saw the "land" God promised them. Before everything was said and done, Carey saw the word of God translated into over forty languages, and Judson not only saw the Bible translated into Burmese but Baptist churches all over Burma. It just took a while to get there---a whole lifetime of service.

There has been many a young man graduate from PBI to go out into the work. They bang away one year, two years, four years, sometimes more, with no members but their family or a handful of folks meeting in garages and living rooms before the work takes off and the Lord gives them a decent-size congregation and a building. The key was they [didn't quit;]{.class_s2FX} they kept at it until the Lord blessed.

Back to Joshua 11: ["There was none of the Anakims left in the land of the children of Israel: only in Gaza, in Gath, and in Ashdod, there remained"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 22). So Joshua destroyed the giants in the land which the Israelites already possessed; then you are given the exceptions. The exceptions are Gaza, Gath, and Ashdod. That was Philistine territory (Josh. 13:3; 1 Sam. 6:17). You will remember that Goliath was a Philistine from Gath (1 Sam. 17:23). In the Bible, Goliath and his four sons are the last of the giants, and they are slain by David and his men (2 Sam. 21:16--22).

Verse 23 is a closing summary on the conquest of Canaan and an introduction to what is about to take place in the upcoming chapters where the land is divided by lot to the twelve tribes. Here is an example---one of many in the Bible---where there is a difference between "all without distinction" and "all without exception." Joshua conquered ["the whole land"]{.class_s2FW} within the boundaries laid down in verses 16--17; that's "all without distinction." But there were [exceptions,]{.class_s2FX} and those exceptions are given in 13:1--6. The chapter ends with: ["And the land rested from war."]{.class_s2FW} But look at Judges 3:1--4.

"Now these are the nations which the LORD left, to prove Israel by them, even as many of Israel as had not known all the wars of Canaan; Only that the generations of the children of Israel might know, to teach them war, at []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_237}the least such as before knew nothing thereof; Namely, five lords of the Philistines, and all the Canaanites, and the Sidonians, and the Hivites that dwelt in mount Lebanon, from mount Baal-hermon unto the entering in of Hamath. And they were to prove Israel by them, to know whether they would hearken unto the commandments of the LORD, which he commanded their fathers by the hand of Moses."

So the Lord let a few of those heathen peoples survive for a couple of reasons. First, He left a few of them around to teach the next generation [war.]{.class_s2FX} I know that is contrary to this modern philosophy that says war is the greatest evil there is on this earth. The fact is, war is just [one]{.class_s2FX} way to die; there are all kinds of other ways like disease, disasters, murder, old age, etc.

The Bible says God is ["a man of WAR"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 15:3), and that doesn't set well with the ["God is love"]{.class_s2FW} crowd either, but it is so. Brethren, the wars don't stop until the Captain of our salvation (Heb. 2:10) returns in power to put down all His enemies. [That's]{.class_s2FX} when ["neither shall they learn war any more"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 2:4), and not until.

The spiritual lesson is that each generation has to learn to fight sin; it can't rest on the laurels of its predecessors. If you want to know why this present generation is practically worthless when it comes to [character,]{.class_s2FX} it is because it had everything handed to it on a silver platter. My generation came up through the Depression and World War II; we had to [fight]{.class_s2FX} for food, [fight]{.class_s2FX} for a job, and [fight]{.class_s2FX} to survive the Germans and the Japanese.

When it comes to the fight against sin and the flesh, it doesn't matter what the Pilgrims did, what Jonathan Edwards or David Brainerd or Charles Finney did, what D. L. Moody or R. A. Torrey did, what Billy Sunday or Mordecai Ham did, or what Bob Jones Sr., John R. Rice, Lee Roberson, or Lester Roloff did. You have to "learn war" [yourself.]{.class_s2FX}

The second reason God left some of those heathen people around was to see if the next generation would follow Him like Joshua and his generation did. You read back in verse 15 here in Joshua 11:

"As the LORD commanded Moses his servant, so did []{#c1BA.xhtml_page_238}Moses command Joshua, and so did Joshua; he left nothing undone of all that the LORD commanded Moses."

Joshua did everything the Lord commanded him to do, and as long as Joshua lived, the Israelites served God.

["And the people served the LORD all the days of Joshua, and all the days of the elders that outlived Joshua, who had seen all the great works of the LORD, that he did for Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 2:7).

But after Joshua's generation died out, the Bible says, ["there arose another generation after them, which knew not the LORD, nor yet the works which he had done for Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 2:10). So God left those heathen peoples to get that generation of Israelites to follow Him (Judg. 2:21--23).

So each generation of Christians is going to have its own battles against the world, the flesh, and the Devil. The new generation can't just sit back and rely on the victories of the previous generation. That is what this present bunch of Laodiceans are doing. They've given up the fight to "get along" with the world, and except for a few isolated groups here and there, nearly the whole of American Christianity has fallen into apostasy. They need to "learn war" and ["hearken unto the commandments of the LORD."]{.class_s2FW}

[]{#c1ET.xhtml}

CHAPTER 12

12:1 Now these are the kings of the land, which the children of Israel smote, and possessed their land on the other side Jordan toward the rising of the sun, from the river Arnon unto mount Hermon, and all the plain on the east:

2 Sihon king of the Amorites, who dwelt in Heshbon, and ruled from Aroer, which is upon the bank of the river Arnon, and from the middle of the river, and from half Gilead, even unto the river Jabbok, which is the border of the children of Ammon;

3 And from the plain to the sea of Chinneroth on the east, and unto the sea of the plain, even the salt sea on the east, the way to Bethjeshimoth; and from the south, under Ashdothpisgah:

4 And the coast of Og king of Bashan, which was of the remnant of the giants, that dwelt at Ashtaroth and at Edrei,

5 And reigned in mount Hermon, and in Salcah, and in all Bashan, unto the border of the Geshurites and the Maachathites, and half Gilead, the border of Sihon king of Heshbon.

6 Them did Moses the servant of the LORD and the children of Israel smite: and Moses the servant of the LORD gave it for a possession unto the Reubenites, and the Gadites, and the half tribe of Manasseh.

The chapter enumerates the Kings conquered on both sides of Jordan and the territory they ruled. The first six verses give the conquests on the east side of Jordan, and you can read the accounts of those battles in Numbers 21. ["The river Arnon"]{.class_s2FW} is the southernmost border, and Mount Hermon is the northernmost border (vs. 1).

This territory, along with the Biblical lands of Moab and Ammon, became known as "Transjordan" in 1921, when the unsaved [Druid,]{.class_s2FX} []{#c1ET.xhtml_page_240}Winnie the Pooh Churchill, bragged about creating Transjordan "with a stroke of a pen"; it is known today as "the Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan." It is an [Arab]{.class_s2FX} kingdom, not "Palestinian." In other words, Churchill turned over the territories belonging to Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh (vs. 6)---[Jewish]{.class_s2FX} tribes­---to [Arab Moslems.]{.class_s2FX} Israel lost half of its land to Mohammed before World War II ever started. For a full account of this, see chapter ten of [Israel: A Deadly Piece of Dirt.]{.class_s2FX}

Churchill trampled all over the Bible with his "White Papers." That land wasn't "Transjordan"; it was [Gilead]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 2) and [Bashan]{.class_s2FX} (vss. 4--5). It wasn't just [Moses]{.class_s2FX} who gave it to the tribes of Reuben, Gad, and half of Manasseh (vs. 6); it was [God]{.class_s2FX} (Deut. 3:18). Churchill stole [Jehovah God's]{.class_s2FX} land and turned it over to an [Arab moon god]{.class_s2FX} (Allah). No wonder England ended up as a sixth-rate world power after World War II. The old saying was: "the sun never sets on the British Empire." [It set in 1921.]{.class_s2FX} God took away every major colonial holding Britain had.

Now we are not going to go into all the places mentioned in verses 2--5; you can look them all up in a Bible atlas. Briefly, ["the sea of Chinneroth"]{.class_s2FW} is the Sea of Galilee, and ["the salt sea"]{.class_s2FW} is the Dead Sea (vs. 3). Sihon's kingdom went from the northern border of Moab at the Arnon River to the Jabbok River half way between the Dead Sea and the Sea of Galilee. Og's kingdom ran from the Jabbok River up to Mt. Hermon on the east side of Jordan. Og was the last of the giants to rule on the east side of Jordan (Deut. 3:11).

Now I know all these places and names seem boring to you reading them up here in the Twenty-first Century. After all, who cares about cities covered over in the dust of time like Heshbon, Aroer, Beth-jeshimoth, Ashdoth-pisgah, Ashtaroth, and Edrei? You're more concerned with New York, Washington, D.C., Atlanta, Nashville, Chicago, Los Angeles; and maybe London, Paris, Rome, Mecca, Damascus, Islamabad, Benghazi, Bagdad, and Tehran. But these cities here in Joshua 12 have to do with the land your Lord and Saviour is coming back to rule over one day.

From a [spiritual, devotional]{.class_s2FX} standpoint, it is a good thing to keep a list of specific victories the Lord has given you and prayers He has answered. How are you to "count your many blessings, name them []{#c1ET.xhtml_page_241}one by one, and it will surprise you what the Lord hath done" if you can't remember what they are? I keep a list. I've got the books and tracts the Lord let me get printed, the cars He has given me, the house paid for, my boys' tonsils taken out without any hospital bills, three Bibles that had been lost and were found in impossible situations, in-laws saved, opposition to the ministry removed, victories in court trials, etc. If you don't make a list, you'll forget, and then you'll get to griping and complaining about the Lord not doing anything for you.

7 And these are the kings of the country which Joshua and the children of Israel smote on this side Jordan on the west, from Baalgad in the valley of Lebanon even unto the mount Halak, that goeth up to Seir; which Joshua gave unto the tribes of Israel for a possession according to their divisions;

8 In the mountains, and in the valleys, and in the plains, and in the springs, and in the wilderness, and in the south country; the Hittites, the Amorites, and the Canaanites, the Perizzites, the Hivites, and the Jebusites:

9 The king of Jericho, one; the king of Ai, which is beside Bethel, one;

10 The king of Jerusalem, one; the king of Hebron, one;

11 The king of Jarmuth, one; the king of Lachish, one;

12 The king of Eglon, one; the king of Gezer, one;

13 The king of Debir, one; the king of Geder, one;

14 The king of Hormah, one; the king of Arad, one;

15 The king of Libnah, one; the king of Adullam, one;

16 The king of Makkedah, one; the king of Bethel, one;

17 The king of Tappuah, one; the king of Hepher, one;

18 The king of Aphek, one; the king of Lasharon, one;

19 The king of Madon, one; the king of Hazor, one;

20 The king of Shimronmeron, one; the king of Achshaph, one;

21 The king of Taanach, one; the king of Megiddo, one;

22 The king of Kedesh, one; the king of Jokneam of Carmel, one;

23 The king of Dor in the coast of Dor, one; the king of the nations of Gilgal, one;

24 The king of Tirzah, one: all the kings thirty and one.

This passage gives the conquests on the west side of the Jordan, and verse 7 once more gives you the northernmost and southernmost limits of the land God gave Joshua. Notice it was given to ["the tribes of Israel for a possession."]{.class_s2FW} So this is a picture of the Millennial inheritance (see Ezek. 47--48).

Now that is not only for the tribes of Israel; it is for the Christian as well. If you are a Christian in the Body of Christ right now and you ["fight the good fight of faith"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:12), you receive a Millennial inheritance with your Lord and Saviour as well (2 Tim. 4:7--8). The Apostle Paul said, ["If we suffer, we shall also reign with him"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:12); that's in the same context as:[ "endure hardness, as a GOOD SOLDIER of Jesus Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:3).

Once more I draw your attention to the fact that there never was and never has been a nation or kingdom of "Palestinians." The land had [31 Kings]{.class_s2FX} (vs. 24), each one ruling over a city as an independent political State. The Moslems who conquered the land in the Middle Ages were [not]{.class_s2FX} "Palestinians"; they were Arabians, Egyptians, and [Turks.]{.class_s2FX} When General Allenby liberated Jerusalem in 1917, he took it from the [Ottoman Turks,]{.class_s2FX} not the "Palestinians." Outside of the [Philistines]{.class_s2FX} who inhabited the "Gaza Strip" (the term [Palestine]{.class_s2FX} was the Roman name for the land of the Philistines, to whom 90% of the land of Canaan [never]{.class_s2FX} belonged), there never has been a political State of "Palestinians"; that's a figment of the imagination of a murderous Egyptian terrorist (Yassir Arafat). The only political State ever to rule all of "Palestine" from Lebanon to the Sinai was the political State of [Israel,]{.class_s2FX} and Israel took the land of Canaan [by the commandment of God Almighty]{.class_s2FX} from [31 separate]{.class_s2FX} Kings.

Now verses 9--13 give you the first three major battles Joshua fought: Jericho first, Ai second, and then the five Kings in chapter 10 (Jerusalem, Hebron, Jarmuth, Lachish, and Eglon). Verses 13--16 give the rest of the conquests of the southern campaign. Notice that not every city Joshua took in the south was given in Joshua 10: Geder, Hormah, Arad, and Adullam were not among the battles of []{#c1ET.xhtml_page_243}Joshua 10, even though Joshua took them in the southern campaign.

Verse 17 obviously is part of Joshua's northern campaign, since the places listed in verses 17--18 are north of the borders given for the southern campaign in 10:41. But the Kings associated with the northern confederacy in 11:1 aren't given until verses 19--20 here in chapter 12. Tappuah, Hepher, Aphek, and Lasharon (known as Sharon---Isa. 35:2) are in central Canaan, in and to the west of Mt. Ephraim. This [might]{.class_s2FX} mean that Joshua began his northern campaign [before]{.class_s2FX} the formation of the confederacy of 11:1--3. Except for Tirzah in verse 24, which was at the northern end of Mt. Ephraim, the rest of the cities of verses 19--23 seem to be associated with the northern confederacy.

It should be noted that the ["Gilgal"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 23 is [not]{.class_s2FX} where Joshua had his encampment (see our remarks under 4:19--20). This Gilgal is a location in northern Canaan, probably around Dor and Carmel (vss. 22--23). Because the text here in verse 23 says ["the nations of Gilgal,"]{.class_s2FW} expositors have associated it with ["Harosheth of the Gentiles"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 4:2, 13, 16).

Now, anyone familiar with the Old Testament recognizes some of the cities listed in this chapter as associated with other important events in Scripture. It was between Bethel and Ai (vs. 9) where Abraham set up his first altar when he entered Canaan (Gen. 12:8) and where he got right when he returned from Egypt (Gen. 13:3). We have commented on Jericho (vs. 9) under 6:26.

Hebron (vs. 10) was where Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob were buried (Gen. 23:19, 49:29--31, 50:13). For his faith in Numbers 13--14, Caleb was given Hebron as his inheritance (Josh. 14:13--14). Hebron was a city of refuge (Josh. 20:7--9). Hebron was where David first reigned when he became King (2 Sam. 2:3--11). Hebron was where Joab slew Abner in revenge for killing his brother Asahel in battle (2 Sam. 3:27), even though Hebron was a city of refuge where Abner should have been safe (Num. 35:11--12). Hebron was also where Absalom began his rebellion against his father (2 Sam. 15:9--10).

Bethel (vs. 9), of course, is "the house of God" where Jacob saw the ladder that reached up to Heaven (Gen. 28:10--19), and it is the place where Jacob got right when he returned to the land (Gen. []{#c1ET.xhtml_page_244}35:1--6). But Bethel is where Jeroboam set up one of the golden calves when he led the northern kingdom into apostasy (1 Kings 12:26--33; Amos 3:14, 4:4, 5:5), and instead of being "the house of God," it became ["the king's chapel"]{.class_s2FW} (Amos 7:13).

Adullam is where David hid out from Saul (1 Sam. 22:1) and the Philistines (2 Sam. 23:13). Megiddo (vs. 21) is the Armageddon of prophecy (Rev. 16:16). Carmel (vs. 22) is Mt. Carmel (see 1 Kings 18). And Tirzah (vs. 24) was the first capital of the northern kingdom (1 Kings 15:33, 16:8, 15, 23) before Omri built Samaria (1 Kings 16:24); it was known for its beauty (Song of Sol. 6:4).

Now the thing to remember is that even though Joshua conquered these cities, because the Israelites didn't immediately occupy them, in whole or in part, the inhabitants of the land entrenched themselves back in their cities, and those cities had to be retaken. For example, Joshua killed the King of Jerusalem in Joshua 10, but in Judges 1, after the death of Joshua, Judah has to fight against the city again, and it is burnt to the ground (Judg. 1:8). But even then they weren't able to drive out the Jebusites who lived there (Josh. 15:63; Judg. 1:21), so David has to finish taking the city when he becomes King (2 Sam. 5:5--9). Bethel has to be retaken after Joshua's death (Judg. 1:22--25). The cities of Taanach, Dor, Megiddo, Gezer, and Aphek all were repopulated by heathen peoples after Joshua took them (Judg. 1:27--31).

This incomplete obedience in possessing the land Joshua had conquered is what resulted in the apostasy of Judges 2--3. The spiritual lesson for the New Testament believer is that if we don't "possess the land" our "Joshua" conquered for us (Rom. 6:1--10), then we are doomed to a life of servitude to sin (Rom. 6:16) and condemnation in the flesh (Rom. 8:1--13).

[]{#c1GA.xhtml}

# Chapter 13 {.heading_s2B}

13:1 Now Joshua was old and stricken in years; and the LORD said unto him, Thou art old and stricken in years, and there remaineth yet very much land to be possessed.

2 This is the land that yet remaineth: all the borders of the Philistines, and all Geshuri,

3 From Sihor, which is before Egypt, even unto the borders of Ekron northward, which is counted to the Canaanite: five lords of the Philistines; the Gazathites, and the Ashdothites, the Eshkalonites, the Gittites, and the Ekronites; also the Avites:

4 From the south, all the land of the Canaanites, and Mearah that is beside the Sidonians, unto Aphek, to the borders of the Amorites:

5 And the land of the Giblites, and all Lebanon, toward the sunrising, from Baalgad under mount Hermon unto the entering into Hamath.

6 All the inhabitants of the hill country from Lebanon unto Misrephothmaim, and all the Sidonians, them will I drive out from before the children of Israel: only divide thou it by lot unto the Israelites for an inheritance, as I have commanded thee.

["Now Joshua was old and stricken in years"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1). Again, using the age of Caleb in 14:10 as a guide, Joshua is over 85 years old at this point, since this is after the conquest of the Anakim in Hebron and Debir (11:21 cf. 15:13--15); an estimate based on 23:1 and 24:29 would probably place Joshua between 90 and 100 years old here.

["There remaineth yet very much land to be possessed."]{.class_s2FW} After reading about everything Joshua did in chapters 11--12, the reader might wonder what the Lord means here. After all, you've been reading where Joshua goes in and takes all those cities and kills all the inhabitants. What do you mean, ["there remaineth yet very much land to be possessed"]{.class_s2FW}?

Well, any military commander understands what's going on here. Just because you [conquer]{.class_s2FX} a land and [temporarily]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c1GA.xhtml_page_246} drive out the inhabitants, doesn't mean you ["possess"]{.class_s2FX} the land. Sometimes the people you whip in war end up owning more of the land you took in battle than they did before you took it away from them. The Japanese own more of the island of Oahu today than the Americans do. The Japanese didn't need to bomb Pearl Harbor to "possess" Oahu; they simply lost the war and [bought it out.]{.class_s2FX} The children of Israel have conquered the land and have it under military occupation; but they haven't "possessed" it yet in the sense of moving in, building houses and cities, plowing the ground and raising crops, etc.

Now the Christian is involved in [spiritual]{.class_s2FX} conquest. Jerry Falwell used to talk about "taking a city for Christ." Well, if you mean getting the Gospel and the truths of the Scripture to every person in the town, you might have something there. But in the New Testament, there is no such thing as Christians taking over physical territory to enforce "Christian laws" on a lost populace, like John Calvin tried to do in Geneva. You might have Christians ban together in a community and adopt laws based on the Scriptures like the early settlers and the founders of this country did, but the job of New Testament believers is not to "Christianize" a country. It's to [evangelize]{.class_s2FX} a country.

The Christian [spiritually]{.class_s2FX} "conquers" now and [physically]{.class_s2FX} "possesses" later in the Millennium. In the Parable of the Pounds, the "conquest" was the servants "occupying" until their Lord's return (Luke 19:13); that is, trading and making a profit with the money he left them. The "possession" was the cities they were given to reign over by their lord as a reward for their faithfulness. In Pauline terms, ["If we suffer]{.class_s2FW} \[there's the "conquest"\][, we shall also reign with him]{.class_s2FW} \[and there's the "possession"\]["]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:12).

Again, ["And whatsoever ye do, do it heartily, as to the Lord, and not unto men]{.class_s2FW} \[conquest\][; knowing that of the Lord ye shall receive the reward of the inheritance]{.class_s2FW} \[possession\]["]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 3:23--24).

No Christian is in the Millennium reigning now, like some Preterists, Postmillennialists, and Amillennialists teach; and no Christian is going to before the Rapture. The reigning and the inheritance are [future,]{.class_s2FX} when your Lord returns. It's the []{#c1GA.xhtml_page_247}[cross now]{.class_s2FX} and the [crown later.]{.class_s2FX}

Now we have already discussed some of these exceptions of verses 2--5 under our remarks on 11:22--23. Something important to note in verse 2 here in chapter 13 is that there are [two]{.class_s2FX} ["Geshuri."]{.class_s2FW} There is one in the south of Canaan on the west side of Jordan, and that is the one here in verse 2 (see also 1 Sam. 27:8). The other land of the ["Geshurites"]{.class_s2FW} is located up in Bashan in the north, on the east side of Jordan, and that is the one in verse 13 (see also 12:5; Deut. 3:14). It was from this second ["Geshur"]{.class_s2FW} that one of the greatest types of the Antichrist came---Absalom (2 Sam. 3:3, 13:37, 15:8).

["Sihor, which is before Egypt"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3) is a river ["in the way of Egypt"]{.class_s2FW} (Jer. 2:18; Isa. 23:3); that is, the ["Via Maris,"]{.class_s2FX} what Exodus 13:17 calls ["the way of the land of the Philistines."]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}It was the ancient trade route that connected Egypt with Canaan through northern Sinai. Some expositors have identified it with the Nile, others with the so-called "river (or brook) of Egypt" in the north of the Sinai Peninsula.
