Just to confuse the critics of the Bible, there are [three]{.class_s2FX} Hazors in the same region (vss. 32, 25). ["Ziklag"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 31) was a city controlled by the Philistines in the day of David; the King of Gath gave it to David when he was on the run from Saul (1 Sam. 27:6). ["Beersheba"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 28) is the southernmost city in all the land of Israel (Judg. 20:1; 1 Sam. 3:20; 2 Sam. 3:10; 1 Kings 4:25; 1 Chron. 21:2).

The most noteworthy city in the first group, though, is ["Kerioth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 25). There are [two]{.class_s2FX} Kerioths in Scripture: one is in Judah, and the other is in Moab (Jer. 48:21, 41; Amos 2:2). The reason this is significant is because [Judas]{.class_s2FX} was from Kerioth: [Iscariot]{.class_s2FX} means "man of Kerioth." As far as the Gospel record goes, he was the only one of the twelve apostles not to come from Galilee. So he was either from Judah or Moab. I take it that he was from Moab because  Jeremiah 48:24--25, where the Kerioth of Moab is mentioned, is about the Son of Perdition (see the ["little horn"]{.class_s2FW} of Dan. 7:8, 8:9 there in Jer. 48:25).

In the second group, Samson grew up between ["Eshtaol, and Zoreah"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 13:25, 16:31). ["Adullam"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 35) is where David []{#c1NT.xhtml_page_284}hid out in the cave with his 400 men when he was on the run from Saul (1 Sam. 22:1--2); it is also connected with the Second Advent in Micah 1:15.

Now there is a discrepancy in the count in the first group (vs. 32) and the second group (vs. 36). This is easily explained by the fact that Simeon received his inheritance out of the cities of Judah (19:9), so several of the cities in verses 21--36 are also found in 19:2--8.

In the third group, there is a different ["Mizpeh"]{.class_s2FW} than the ones we discussed in our comments on 11:3; this is a city in southern Judah. ["Joktheel"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 38 means "subdued by God"; later on in 2 Kings 14:7, Amaziah applies the name to the rock city of Selah-Petra in Edom where the Jews will flee from the Antichrist during the Tribulation.

One will recognize ["Jarmuth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 35), ["Lachish"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 39), ["Eglon"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 39), and ["Makkedah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 41) as cities connected with the Battle of the Five Kings in chapter 10. ["Bethdagon"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 41) means "house of Dagon" (the fish god of the Philistines---Judg. 16:23; 1 Sam. 5:1--5) just as [Bethel]{.class_s2FX} means "house of God."

Verses 45--47 cover the major Philistine cities that were supposed to be part of Judah's inheritance, but Judah didn't go in there and drive them out. As a result, they have trouble with the Philistines all the way up to the end of David's reign. That was over 300 years of trouble because of disregarding what God told them to do. The area is still giving Israel trouble today; it is from the "Gaza Strip" that the "Palestinians" are launching rocket attacks against Israeli cities. When Israel uses its military to try to stop them, the European Union, the Arab League, the United Nations, and the [United States]{.class_s2FX} have a fit. They want Israel to put up with what [none of them would stand for.]{.class_s2FX}

Notice the city of ["Cain"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 57. That's a town named after an Old Testament character. There's nothing unusual about that. You have cities all over this country named after people; like Jacksonville (named after Andrew Jackson), Washington, D.C. (named after George Washington), Lincoln, Nebraska (named after Abraham Lincoln), Austin, Texas (named after Stephen Austin), Houston, Texas (named after Sam Houston), etc. What that shows you is that even the Canaanite people understood Cain from before []{#c1NT.xhtml_page_285}the Flood to be an historic figure.

According to some expositors, ["the city of Salt"]{.class_s2FW} is supposed to be Zoar, where Lot fled when he left Sodom (Gen. 19:22--23). Deuteronomy 34:3 confirms the existence of Zoar at the time of Moses and Joshua. ["Engedi"]{.class_s2FW} was another place David hid out while on the run from Saul (1 Sam. 23:29); according to 2 Chronicles 20:2, it also had another name---["Hazazontamar."]{.class_s2FW}

Keep that in mind when you hear these infidels and agnostics talk about "contradictions in the Bible." A lot of so-called "contradictions" can be explained by the fact that both people and places in the Bible have two names, and sometimes there are even four. Pensacola is called "the City of Five Flags" and "the Cradle of Naval Aviation." Once the queers and faggots decided to invade the place during Memorial Day weekend, it got called "the Gay \[i.e., [Sex Pervert]{.class_s2FX}\] Riviera."

["As for the Jebusites the inhabitants of Jerusalem, the children of Judah could not drive them out: but the Jebusites dwell with the children of Judah at Jerusalem unto this day"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 63). Judah had the same trouble Manasseh had back in 13:13 (see our comments on the verse). They didn't get rid of the Jebusites altogether, and it caused them terrible trouble later on.

Take a moment and go read Judges 19, and you will see why God commanded genocide against all those Canaanite peoples. It wasn't just a matter of not accepting the Jews' "religion," like Mohammed practices with his religion. Mohammedans are commanded to kill anybody who won't accept their religion.

"Fight therefore against them \[i.e., the [infidels]{.class_s2FX}---Sura 2:191\] until there be no more civil discord, [and the only worship be that of Allah"]{.class_s2FX} (["Holy" Koran,]{.class_s2FX} Sura 2:192).

That's not what's going on here in Joshua at all. The offer to "convert" is not even given by Joshua. Those Canaanites were practicing things for which God burned Sodom and Gomorrah to the ground. Those Jebusites in Judges 19 are doing the same thing the Sodomites did back in Genesis 19. Don't believe me? READ THE TWO PASSAGES! The only difference between the Jebusites in Judges 19 and the Sodomites in Genesis 19 was the Jebusites had not []{#c1NT.xhtml_page_286}completely lost their "sexual preference" (I believe that is the modern "double-speak" for it) for women. They were "bi" (bisexual) and not total faggots; but it is obvious from what you read in Judges 19 that they were headed that way. The reason God prescribed the death penalty for sodomy in the Old Testament is that if you don't kill them, [they will kill you.]{.class_s2FX} I am not telling anyone to "kill a queer for Jesus." In the Bible, that is something the civil government is supposed to do, NOT ANY INDIVIDUAL (Rom. 13:3--4). But any society that puts up with that filth is doomed to destruction.

If the faggots don't kill you with their diseases (Exod. 15:26 cf. Lev. 18:3, 22), they will eventually grow in numbers until they become emboldened to kill you directly. For all their talk of "tolerance," it is the "gay community" that makes the death threats when Christians won't "knuckle under" to their demands. Just wait until the government not only takes their side but is run by them and watch what will happen. The United States under Obama, "Hillary," and the Democrats is headed that way [right now.]{.class_s2FX} You can expect God to do to America exactly what He did to Sodom and Gomorrah, and to [His own chosen people]{.class_s2FX} for doing the same thing (Amos 4:11; Isa. 3:8--9; 1 Kings 14:24).

# Chapter 16 {.heading_s2B}

16:1 And the lot of the children of Joseph fell from Jordan by Jericho, unto the water of Jericho on the east, to the wilderness that goeth up from Jericho throughout mount Bethel,

2 And goeth out from Bethel to Luz, and passeth along unto the borders of Archi to Ataroth,

3 And goeth down westward to the coast of Japhleti, unto the coast of Bethhoron the nether, and to Gezer: and the goings out thereof are at the sea.

4 So the children of Joseph, Manasseh and Ephraim, took their inheritance.

The passage introduces the inheritance of Joseph's two sons, Manasseh and Ephraim. We have already discussed the double portion of Joseph in our comments on 14:4, which see.

The eastern border of Ephraim went from the spring of Jericho over to Jordan (vs. 1; Jericho proper belonging to Benjamin---18:21) and up to ["Ataroth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2; called ["Atarothaddar"]{.class_s2FW} in vs. 5). The southern border went from the spring of Jericho up to ["Bethel"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2) and westward over to ["Bethhoron"]{.class_s2FW} (the lower and the upper---vss. 3, 5), and then down to ["Gezer"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3).

["The water of Jericho"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1) was the bitter spring of the city that was later healed by Elisha (2 Kings 2:19--21). ["Bethel to Luz"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2) is peculiar wording since Bethel [was]{.class_s2FX} Luz (Judg. 1:23). But in Genesis 28:19, the distinction is made between the [place]{.class_s2FX} where Jacob slept on the stone and had the vision of the ladder up to Heaven (Bethel) and the [city]{.class_s2FX} near the place (Luz).

["Archi"]{.class_s2FW} is the town from which David's counselor Hushai, who acted as a "double agent" during Absalom's rebellion, came (2 Sam. 16:16). According to 1 Chronicles 7:22--24, the two Bethhorons (vss. 3, 5) belonged to the tribe of Ephraim because it was Ephraim's [daughter]{.class_s2FX} (["Sherah"]{.class_s2FW}) who founded the cities.

5 And the border of the children of Ephraim according []{#c1TH.xhtml_page_288}to their families was thus: even the border of their inheritance on the east side was Atarothaddar, unto Bethhoron the upper;

6 And the border went out toward the sea to Michmethah on the north side; and the border went about eastward unto Taanathshiloh, and passed by it on the east to Janohah;

7 And it went down from Janohah to Ataroth, and to Naarath, and came to Jericho, and went out at Jordan.

8 The border went out from Tappuah westward unto the river Kanah; and the goings out thereof were at the sea. This is the inheritance of the tribe of the children of Ephraim by their families.

9 And the separate cities for the children of Ephraim were among the inheritance of the children of Manasseh, all the cities with their villages.

10 And they drave not out the Canaanites that dwelt in Gezer: but the Canaanites dwell among the Ephraimites unto this day, and serve under tribute.

["Michmethah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6) was a place on the northern boundary of Ephraim that bordered Manasseh (17:7). ["Taanathshiloh"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 6) is a fuller name for Shiloh where the Tabernacle was set up (18:1).

["Tappuah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 8) was both the name of a [region]{.class_s2FX} and a [city]{.class_s2FX} within that region. ["The land of Tappuah"]{.class_s2FW} belonged to Manasseh, but the city of Tappuah belonged to Ephraim (17:8). At Tappuah, the northern border of Ephraim ran along the Kanah River all the way to the Mediterranean (vs. 8). According to 17:9, all the cities south of the Kanah belonged to Ephraim, all the cities north of the river belonged to Manasseh. And as we saw with Tappuah above, there were certain cities within the boundaries of Manasseh that actually belonged to Ephraim (vs. 9).

Verse 10 gives you the incomplete obedience of Ephraim in not driving out the Canaanites in Gezer (see our comments on 13:13 and 15:63). In fact, when God finally gets rid of the Canaanites in Gezer, He has to use a heathen King to do it (1 Kings 9:16). Ephraim doesn't do it (Judg. 1:29); none of the judges do it; Saul doesn't do it; David doesn't do it; and Solomon doesn't do it. It is [Pharaoh]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c1TH.xhtml_page_289} who does it, and he does it as a "wedding gift" for his daughter who married Solomon.

The spiritual lesson for the Christian's warfare is to deal with sin and worldliness. Fight against it. Don't give it "aid and comfort"; don't allow it a place in your life. When the Holy Spirit exposes an idol in your life, break it down (2 Cor. 10:5). If you don't, it's going to keep popping up and bothering you, and eventually get control of you if you let it. There isn't any way of dealing with it other than [fighting.]{.class_s2FX}

I wish every Christian could read some of the anecdotes I have read from military history. There is account after account, and story after story, of brave men who fought, sometimes against impossible odds, and for what? [Absolutely nothing.]{.class_s2FX}

Those Germans in World War II fought for a demon-possessed madman. The average German solder wasn't a Nazi; he was just fighting for the "Fatherland." But there were a lot of brave soldiers who fought for Hitler at places like Stalingrad, where only one in ten made it back alive. Our boys in Vietnam fought for a fornicating Catholic (JFK). You have young Americans dying and being maimed right now (as of this writing) for a Marxist Moslem (Obama). Well, they're not Marxist or Moslem, for the greater part; a lot of them are brave young men just following orders. But they [fight.]{.class_s2FX}

Now if someone can do that for a lost, Hell-bound sinner, what's your excuse, Christian? Haven't you got a better Commander? I think so! Haven't you got a better cause! I think so! THEN FIGHT!

[]{#c1UC.xhtml}

# Chapter 17 {.heading_s2B}

17:1 There was also a lot for the tribe of Manasseh; for he was the firstborn of Joseph; to wit, for Machir the firstborn of Manasseh, the father of Gilead: because he was a man of war, therefore he had Gilead and Bashan.

2 There was also a lot for the rest of the children of Manasseh by their families; for the children of Abiezer, and for the children of Helek, and for the children of Asriel, and for the children of Shechem, and for the children of Hepher, and for the children of Shemida: these were the male children of Manasseh the son of Joseph by their families.

These verses introduce the inheritance of the other half of the tribe of Manasseh. Notice how the name ["Gilead"]{.class_s2FW} is used in verse 1. When it says Gilead ["was a man of war,"]{.class_s2FW} the reference isn't to the [individual;]{.class_s2FX} it's talking about the [people]{.class_s2FX} named after the individual. You see the same thing with the name [Jacob]{.class_s2FX} over and over again in the prophets where it's referring to the [nation of Israel,]{.class_s2FX} not the patriarch (e.g., Isa. 9:8, 10:21, 17:4, 27:9, 29:22, 40:27, 41:8, 43:1, 44:1--2, 48:12). Gilead [the man]{.class_s2FX} would have been long since dead by the time the Israelites took the lands of Gilead and Bashan, for he was ["brought up on Joseph's knees"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 50:23 cf. Num. 26:29), and no one over the age of twenty at the time the spies gave the evil report made it into the Promised Land but Joshua and Caleb (Num. 14:29--30). When you read the account of Jephthah and the Gileadites whipping Ephraimites in battle in Judges 12, you can understand why ["Gilead . . . was a man of war."]{.class_s2FW}

["The male children of Manasseh"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2) turn out to be [great]{.class_s2FX} [grandchildren]{.class_s2FX} (see vs. 3). The line runs Manasseh, Machir, Gilead, and then Gilead's sons: Jeezer (Abiezer here in Josh. 17:2), Helek, Asriel, Shechem, Shemida, and Hepher (Num. 26:29--32). It is the families of these great grandchildren of Manasseh who settle in Canaan. (1 Chron. 7:15--17 lists some other sons of Gilead, and these [may]{.class_s2FX} have been the ones who settled on the east side of Jordan.)

Now the use of the word "son" or "children" is something to keep in mind when talking about apparent "contradictions" in the Bible. A "son" or a "child" may not be the immediate offspring of a father at all. It can be used of a grandson, a great grandson, a distant descendant, a son-in-law, an adopted or foster son, or anyone in a line of succession. You say, "Well how do I know which one it is?" [Read the context,]{.class_s2FX} and [compare Scripture with Scripture.]{.class_s2FX} Give the Holy Spirit the benefit of the doubt that He knew what He wanted recorded instead of you sitting in judgment of God's words.

Here is a good spot to look at something on which the Bible puts a lot of emphasis (just by sheer numbers of [mention]{.class_s2FX}) into which you may not put too much thought. Usually you read right over this stuff without thinking about its import. But look at the number of times these things are said just in these two verses:

"The FIRSTBORN[ ]{.class_s2G0-1}of Joseph."

"The FIRSTBORN of Manasseh."

"The CHILDREN[ ]{.class_s2G0-1}of Manasseh."

"The CHILDREN[ ]{.class_s2G0-1}of Abiezer."

"The CHILDREN[ ]{.class_s2G0-1}of Helek."

"The CHILDREN[ ]{.class_s2G0-1}of Asriel.

"The CHILDREN of Shechem."

"The CHILDREN of Hepher."

"The CHILDREN of Shemida."

"The male CHILDREN of Manasseh the SON of Joseph."

The Lord is always talking about [sons, children, birth,]{.class_s2FX} and [begetting]{.class_s2FX} all the way through the Book. The first command given to man in the Bible is: ["Be fruitful, and multiply, and replenish the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 1:28). Why is that?

Because everyone belongs to one family or another. You are either a child of disobedience, a child of wrath, with the Devil as your father (Eph. 2:2--3; John 8:44); or you have been born again by incorruptible seed and are a child of God by faith in the Son of God, with God as your Father (1 Pet. 1:23; Gal. 3:26, 4:6). God is concerned with [lineages]{.class_s2FX} (there are more than fifty chapters of genealogies in the Bible). The question arises, then, in [what family are you?]{.class_s2FX}

["For through him we both have access by one Spirit []{#c1UC.xhtml_page_292}unto the Father. Now therefore ye are no more strangers and foreigners, but fellowcitizens with the saints, and of the household of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 2:18--19).

["And again, I will put my trust in him. And again, Behold I and the children which God hath given me"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 2:13).

3 But Zelophehad, the son of Hepher, the son of Gilead, the son of Machir, the son of Manasseh, had no sons, but daughters: and these are the names of his daughters, Mahlah, and Noah, Hoglah, Milcah, and Tirzah.

4 And they came near before Eleazar the priest, and before Joshua the son of Nun, and before the princes, saying, The LORD commanded Moses to give us an inheritance among our brethren. Therefore according to the commandment of the LORD he gave them an inheritance among the brethren of their father.

5 And there fell ten portions to Manasseh, beside the land of Gilead and Bashan, which were on the other side Jordan;

6 Because the daughters of Manasseh had an inheritance among his sons: and the rest of Manasseh's sons had the land of Gilead.

This passage deals with the resolution of a problem that came up in Numbers 27. There were six families of the Manassites that inherited territory on the west side of Jordan in Canaan. The problem arose that the inheritance passed from father to son, and Hepher only had one son, Zelophehad, who had no sons himself. But Zelophehad did have five daughters, so what was to be done with the inheritance of the family of Hepher?

When the girls brought their predicament to Moses, the Lord admitted they had a case. The judgment that was given in Numbers 27:8--11 was that in the case where a man had no son, the daughter could receive the land; where a man had no children at all, his brothers could get the land; and where he was an "only child," his next of kin got the land. From this judgment came the law of the []{#c1UC.xhtml_page_293}kinsman redeemer (Deut. 25:7--10) which plays such a pivotal role in the book of Ruth as a type of New Testament redemption. So what seems like a boring technical matter for a probate court turns out to be an important type of your salvation as a New Testament believer.

Now look at a couple of those names. How would you ladies like a name like ["Hoglah"]{.class_s2FW}? I know it has nothing to do with a hog (the name in Hebrew actually means "partridge"), but it's funny how words come out in a different language; it makes you wonder how some of our names must sound in some other language.

Notice also the name ["Noah."]{.class_s2FW} In the context, it's a woman's name, but everyone is more familiar with the [man]{.class_s2FX} of that name. So some names can be for either a man or a woman. Isn't [Francis]{.class_s2FX} a woman's name? Well, it's a man's name too (e.g., Francis Scott Key and St. Francis of Assissi). If you wanted to see a motion picture with "Marion" in it, would you look for a French actress (Marion Cotillard) or "The Duke" (Marion Morrison aka [John Wayne]{.class_s2FX})? It could be either one. Wasn't JFK's nickname "Jack"? Well, his wife's name was [Jackie.]{.class_s2FX} And you can have the female country singer Bobbie Gentry or the male baseball player Bobby Richardson.

Do you know why that is so important? Because there is a famous "contradiction" in the Bible where ["Timna"]{.class_s2FW} is Esau's concubine in Genesis 36:12 but his son in 1 Chronicles 1:36. Why it never occurred to these infidels (Liberal or Fundamental---take your pick) that it could be [both]{.class_s2FX} is beyond reason, given what you just read above. Two different "Timnas" in the same family: one the man's wife and the other his son. What was so hard to figure out about that? Some people do have a time of it, don't they?

I got a letter one time from a Seminary student at Bob Jones University where he told me my position on the [King James]{.class_s2FX} was "untenable" because of the "numerous contradictions" in it. Then for examples, he enclosed five sheets of material written by a Liberal in the National Council of Churches. What's a ministerial student at a Fundamental institution that's supposed to be a "bastion of orthodoxy" doing taking the position of an unsaved Liberal on the Bible? [And why is his professor giving him the material to destroy his faith in the word of God?]{.class_s2FX}

I wrote the kid back in my own "nice, sweet" way and told him his []{#c1UC.xhtml_page_294}professor was so stupid that he couldn't solve a grade-school problem, and that if he were sitting under someone that dumb, he might as well get out of there and stop blowing his money down a rat hole. Listen, people, I have students here at PBI who never finished high school who could handle a matter like you read above, so don't waste my time.

I answered four of that Seminary student's "contradictions" and told him if his professor couldn't answer the rest of them in the next class, get rid of him; give the bum "the boot." A fellow like that has no business teaching Bible to a DVBS, much less in a Seminary. Brethren, what is the point of a man teaching the Bible when he doesn't believe it, thinks it is filled with contradictions, and cannot explain the problems in the Scriptures that an eighteen-year-old kid could with a little tutoring?

Back to the text: Manasseh ended up with ["ten portions"]{.class_s2FW} in Canaan (vs. 5) because the five families with male heirs got a portion each and the five daughters of Zelophehad each got a portion (vs. 6).

7 And the coast of Manasseh was from Asher to Michmethah, that lieth before Shechem; and the border went along on the right hand unto the inhabitants of Entappuah.

8 Now Manasseh had the land of Tappuah: but Tappuah on the border of Manasseh belonged to the children of Ephraim;

9 And the coast descended unto the river Kanah, southward of the river: these cities of Ephraim are among the cities of Manasseh: the coast of Manasseh also was on the north side of the river, and the outgoings of it were at the sea:

10 Southward it was Ephraim's, and northward it was Manasseh's, and the sea is his border; and they met together in Asher on the north, and in Issachar on the east.

11 And Manasseh had in Issachar and in Asher Bethshean and her towns, and Ibleam and her towns, and the inhabitants of Dor and her towns, and the inhabitants of Endor and her towns, and the inhabitants of Taanach []{#c1UC.xhtml_page_295}and her towns, and the inhabitants of Megiddo and her towns, even three countries.

These are the borders and towns of the tribe of Manasseh on the west side of Jordan. We have already commented on the southern border it shared with Ephraim under 16:6--9, which see. On the north, it shared its border with Asher and Issachar (vs. 10), with the Kishon River and the Valley of Jezreel being the boundaries; the western border was the Mediterranean coast (vs. 10). Like Ephraim, Manasseh had cities in other tribes: in Asher it had Dor; and in Issachar it had Beth-shean, Ibleam, Endor, Taanach, and Megiddo (vs. 11).

Bible readers will recognize the town of Endor as the place where Saul sought the services of a witch to bring up the spirit of Samuel (1 Sam. 28:7--14). Megiddo, of course, is the site of the Battle of Armageddon at the Second Advent (Rev. 16:14--16; Zech. 12:11).

12 Yet the children of Manasseh could not drive out the inhabitants of those cities; but the Canaanites would dwell in that land.

13 Yet it came to pass, when the children of Israel were waxen strong, that they put the Canaanites to tribute; but did not utterly drive them out.

This is the incomplete obedience of the western Manassites, but notice the compromise. They couldn't drive the Canaanites out, so they put them to tribute---a subjugation tax like the Moslems put on Christians and Jews when they conquer a land (the [jizya]{.class_s2FX}). (Mohammed never had an original thought in his life. He stole the "jizya" from here in the Old Testament just as he stole "holy war," praying five times a day toward Mecca, obeying him like you would obey God, alms-giving, etc. If Mohammed ever did have an original thought, it died of loneliness.) The problem was that wasn't what God told them to do: they were to wipe them out. Just having them under tribute left them open to infect Israel with false gods and idolatry (Deut. 20:17--18), which is exactly what happened in the book of Judges (read Judg. 1--2).

14 And the children of Joseph spake unto Joshua, saying, Why hast thou given me but one lot and one portion to inherit, seeing I am a great people, forasmuch as the LORD hath blessed me hitherto?

15 And Joshua answered them, If thou be a great people, then get thee up to the wood country, and cut down for thyself there in the land of the Perizzites and of the giants, if mount Ephraim be too narrow for thee.

16 And the children of Joseph said, The hill is not enough for us: and all the Canaanites that dwell in the land of the valley have chariots of iron, both they who are of Bethshean and her towns, and they who are of the valley of Jezreel.

17 And Joshua spake unto the house of Joseph, even to Ephraim and to Manasseh, saying, Thou art a great people, and hast great power: thou shalt not have one lot only:

18 But the mountain shall be thine; for it is a wood, and thou shalt cut it down: and the outgoings of it shall be thine: for thou shalt drive out the Canaanites, though they have iron chariots, and though they be strong.

Through verses 1--13, you have been reading about the tribe of Manasseh, but now both Ephraim and Manasseh come together to Joshua. Notice[ "the children of Joseph"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 14; that's both Manasseh and Ephraim (vs. 17).

["Why hast thou given me but one lot and one portion to inherit . . ."]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 14). That wasn't true. Ephraim got one portion, and Manasseh got another portion just above it. And if that weren't enough, Manasseh got a second portion on the east side of Jordan, so that was [three]{.class_s2FX} portions for Joseph's tribes.

[". . . seeing I am a great people."]{.class_s2FW} That's pride operating there. If it's a reference to the tribes' numbers, it's absolutely [false.]{.class_s2FX} According to the census taken back in Numbers 26, Manasseh had a smaller population than either Issachar or Zebulun to the north that received much less territory; Ephraim had fewer people than Benjamin, which had a smaller inheritance than Ephraim.

Now what was the problem? They weren't appreciative of the blessings God had given them. They admit, []{#c1UC.xhtml_page_297}["forasmuch as the LORD hath blessed me hitherto."]{.class_s2FW} That's the first true thing they've said, but they aren't talking about the land God just gave them in the lot. They're talking about their [stuff:]{.class_s2FX} the spoils they took in battle. They're like that rich fool in Luke 12:16--17. They had more territory (and arguably[ better]{.class_s2FX} land) than any of the other tribes, but they wanted more.

The picture, of course, is of Christians complaining of their lot in life. Paul says God ["hath blessed us with all spiritual blessings in heavenly places in Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 1:3), and all they can see is [what they don't have.]{.class_s2FX} The problem is [covetousness;]{.class_s2FX} it's being [unthankful.]{.class_s2FX} The answer is to [be content.]{.class_s2FX}

["Not that I speak in respect of want: for I have learned, in whatsoever state I am, therewith to be content"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 4:11).

["Let your conversation be without covetousness; and be content with such things as ye have: for he hath said, I will never leave thee, nor forsake thee"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 13:5).

["But godliness with contentment is great gain"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:6).

Back to Joshua 17: ["And Joshua answered them, If thou be a great people]{.class_s2FW} \[he takes them at their word and uses it against them\][, then get thee up to the wood country, and cut down for thyself there in the land of the Perizzites and of the giants."]{.class_s2FW} In other words: "GET OFF YOUR LAZY DUFFS AND GET TO WORK! Go clear out some woods and build you some new cities if the ones you were given aren't enough. But you'll have to deal with them giants."

Look at their response---verse 16: ["The hill]{.class_s2FW} \[i.e., Mt. Ephraim\][ is not enough for us: and all the Canaanites that dwell in the land of the valley have chariots of iron."]{.class_s2FW} Instead of claiming the promises of God like Caleb did back in chapter 14, they continue to whine and make excuses: "We can't drive those Canaanites out of the cities you gave us because they have better equipment and better armament than we do." Those chariots meant nothing back in Joshua 11, and later on in Judges 4 they won't mean anything either. Those Israelites had something better than iron chariots; [they had God on their side]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c1UC.xhtml_page_298} if they had just claimed the promises He made back in chapter 1.

[". . . both they who are of Bethshean and her towns, and they who are of the valley of Jezreel."]{.class_s2FW} Well, then, give them back to Issachar and see if he has any better luck than you do.

Of course Joshua doesn't say that. He tries to motivate them to take action. ["And Joshua spake unto the house of Joseph . . . thou are a great people, and hast great power: thou shalt not have one lot only: But the mountain shall be thine . . ."]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 17--18). Joshua has the faith that they will ["drive out the Canaanites"]{.class_s2FW} even when they don't. He says, "I don't care if it is a mountain; I don't care if they are giants; I don't care if their chariots are iron. If you are such a great people and have such great power, you will go in there and whip 'em. The proof is in the pudding."

Now Christian, when it looks like the odds are stacked against you and victory is impossible, you have some promises that will get you through if you [claim]{.class_s2FX} them and [act]{.class_s2FX} on them (and of course, I am talking about in your war against sin, the flesh, the world, and the Devil; I am not talking about "health and wealth").

["What shall we then say to these things? If God be for us, who can be against us?"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:31).

["Nay, in all these things we are more than conquerors through him that loved us"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:37).

["So that we may boldly say, the Lord is my helper, and I will not fear what man shall do unto me"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 13:6).

The key to those promises is to [do]{.class_s2FX} something about them. You will never win the battle if all you do is sit around and whine and complain. GET UP AND FIGHT!

[]{#c1WK.xhtml}

# Chapter 18 {.heading_s2B}

18:1 And the whole congregation of the children of Israel assembled together at Shiloh, and set up the tabernacle of the congregation there. And the land was subdued before them.

2 And there remained among the children of Israel seven tribes, which had not yet received their inheritance.

3 And Joshua said unto the children of Israel, How long are ye slack to go to possess the land, which the LORD God of your fathers hath given you?

4 Give out from among you three men for each tribe: and I will send them, and they shall rise, and go through the land, and describe it according to the inheritance of them; and they shall come again to me.

5 And they shall divide it into seven parts: Judah shall abide in their coast on the south, and the house of Joseph shall abide in their coasts on the north.

6 Ye shall therefore describe the land into seven parts, and bring the description hither to me, that I may cast lots for you here before the LORD our God.

7 But the Levites have no part among you; for the priesthood of the LORD is their inheritance: and Gad, and Reuben, and half the tribe of Manasseh, have received their inheritance beyond Jordan on the east, which Moses the servant of the LORD gave them.

8 And the men arose, and went away: and Joshua charged them that went to describe the land, saying, Go and walk through the land, and describe it, and come again to me, that I may here cast lots for you before the LORD in Shiloh.

9 And the men went and passed through the land, and described it by cities into seven parts in a book, and came again to Joshua to the host at Shiloh.

10 And Joshua cast lots for them in Shiloh before the LORD: and there Joshua divided the land unto the children []{#c1WK.xhtml_page_300}of Israel according to their divisions.

Now verses 1--5 lay the foundation for the jealousy and competition that existed between the northern ten tribes and the two southern tribes. The first thing is the placement of the Tabernacle in a permanent place of worship.

Remember, all throughout the wilderness wanderings the Tabernacle was moved from place to place as the pillar of cloud and the pillar of fire indicated the new encampment of the children of Israel. When Joshua entered the land, the Tabernacle was set up at Gilgal where Joshua's headquarters were. But after the warfare ended, the Tabernacle was moved up to Shiloh in Ephraim where Joshua had his inheritance (19:49--50) and where Eleazar and Phinehas the high priests had their inheritance (24:33). Although the Tabernacle was occasionally moved from time to time (see our remarks under 24:26), Shiloh was its main location until the Philistines took the Ark of the Covenant in 1 Samuel 1. Because of the sin of Hophni and Phinehas, the Bible says God ["forsook the tabernacle of Shiloh"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 78:60; see also Jer. 7:12, 26:6) and ["refused the tabernacle of Joseph, and chose not the tribe of Ephraim"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 78:67).

It goes on in that same chapter to say, ["But chose the tribe of Judah, the mount Zion which he loved"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 78:67). First Chronicles 5:2 says ["Judah prevailed above his brethren"]{.class_s2FW} even though ["the birthright was Joseph's"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Chron. 5:2). David came from [Judah;]{.class_s2FX} when he brought back the Ark, he brought it back to [Jerusalem;]{.class_s2FX} when Solomon built the Temple, he built it in [Jerusalem.]{.class_s2FX}

Psalm 132:13 says, ["For the LORD hath chosen Zion; he hath desired it for his habitation."]{.class_s2FW} Psalm 87:2 says, ["The LORD loveth the gates of Zion more than all the dwellings of Jacob."]{.class_s2FW} So Ephraim is [out.]{.class_s2FX}

When Jesus Christ spoke to that Samaritan woman, she said, ["Our fathers worshipped in this mountain; and ye say, that in Jerusalem is the place men ought to worship"]{.class_s2FW} (John 4:20). She's talking about Mt. Gerizim in [Mt. Ephraim.]{.class_s2FX} So the controversy between Ephraim and Judah over worship goes all the way up into the New Testament. God established Judah and []{#c1WK.xhtml_page_301}Jerusalem, and He dumped Ephraim and Shiloh.

The second thing that fostered the division between the northern tribes and the southern tribes was the basic division laid out in chapters 14--17. The basic division was Judah and Joseph (Manasseh and Ephraim)---see verse 5.  The reason Manasseh and Ephraim talked about only getting one portion in Canaan was because they were only counted as one son of Jacob---Joseph.

When the Lord divides the kingdom during the time of Rehoboam, He gives one tribe to Judah (Benjamin, based on Judah laying down his life for Benjamin back in Gen. 44), and together, Judah and Benjamin make up the kingdom of [Judah.]{.class_s2FX} The rest of the tribes are identified with Ephraim, the son of Joseph who was put first by Jacob (Gen. 48:20). Look at Isaiah 7:2, 5, 8--9; Jeremiah 31:9, 18, 20; Ezekiel 37:16, 19; Hosea 5:3, 5, 9, 11--14, 6:4, 10, 11:8, 12, 13:1; and Zechariah 9:10, 13; in all those references, Ephraim is used of the northern ten tribes and the northern tribes started right here in Joshua 18.

Now, Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh had received their inheritances on the east side of Jordan; and Judah, Ephraim, and the rest of Manasseh had gotten their inheritances in the land. But the other seven tribes had not stepped up yet to claim any of the land that was left. So Joshua said, ["How long are ye slack]{.class_s2FW} \[i.e., loose\][ to go to possess the land"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 3). They had conquered the land, but since then, they had done nothing to take possession of it. They were just standing around waiting for God to give them a swift kick in the seat of the britches to get them moving, I guess.

Three men from each of the remaining seven tribes are selected to go and ["describe"]{.class_s2FW} the land and divide it into seven parts to be parsed out by lots. The "survey" is recorded ["in a book,"]{.class_s2FW} and we have that record today as part of the book of Joshua.

11 And the lot of the tribe of the children of Benjamin came up according to their families: and the coast of their lot came forth between the children of Judah and the children of Joseph.

12 And their border on the north side was from Jordan; and the border went up to the side of Jericho on the north []{#c1WK.xhtml_page_302}side, and went up through the mountains westward; and the goings out thereof were at the wilderness of Bethaven.

13 And the border went over from thence toward Luz, to the side of Luz, which is Bethel, southward; and the border descended to Atarothadar, near the hill that lieth on the south side of the nether Bethhoron.

14 And the border was drawn thence, and compassed the corner of the sea southward, from the hill that lieth before Bethhoron southward; and the goings out thereof were at Kirjathbaal, which is Kirjathjearim, a city of the children of Judah: this was the west quarter.

15 And the south quarter was from the end of Kirjathjearim, and the border went out on the west, and went out to the well of waters of Nephtoah:

16 And the border came down to the end of the mountain that lieth before the valley of the son of Hinnom, and which is in the valley of the giants on the north, and descended to the valley of Hinnom, to the side of Jebusi on the south, and descended to Enrogel,

17 And was drawn from the north, and went forth to Enshemesh, and went forth toward Geliloth, which is over against the going up of Adummim, and descended to the stone of Bohan the son of Reuben,

18 And passed along toward the side over against Arabah northward, and went down unto Arabah:

19 And the border passed along to the side of Bethhoglah northward: and the outgoings of the border were at the north bay of the salt sea at the south end of Jordan: this was the south coast.

20 And Jordan was the border of it on the east side. This was the inheritance of the children of Benjamin, by the coasts thereof round about, according to their families.

21 Now the cities of the tribe of the children of Benjamin according to their families were Jericho, and Bethhoglah, and the valley of Keziz,

22 And Betharabah, and Zemaraim, and Bethel,

23 And Avim, and Parah, and Ophrah,

24 And Chepharhaammonai, and Ophni, and Gaba; twelve cities with their villages:

25 Gibeon, and Ramah, and Beeroth,

26 And Mizpeh, and Chephirah, and Mozah,

27 And Rekem, and Irpeel, and Taralah,

28 And Zelah, Eleph, and Jebusi, which is Jerusalem, Gibeath, and Kirjath; fourteen cities with their villages. This is the inheritance of the children of Benjamin according to their families.

The first of the last seven tribes to receive their inheritance is Benjamin, the tribe that went with Judah in the division of the kingdom. So it's Judah first to receive its inheritance between Judah and Joseph, and it's Benjamin first between it and the other tribes that go with Joseph. Benjamin becomes a "buffer zone" between Judah and Joseph because he was the brother of Joseph through the same mother, Rachel, but it was Judah who saved him back in Genesis 44.

The northern border goes up to Jericho and then over to Gilgal to Jordan on the east. Then it goes westward to Bethel and then down just south of the lower Bethhoron. ["Compassed the corner of the sea"]{.class_s2FW}  (vs. 14) is a Hebrew idiom talking about the border of Benjamin nearest the Mediterranean Sea, the [seaward]{.class_s2FX} border. So the western border is south of Bethhoron and goes down south to Kirjathjearim that belongs to Judah (vs. 14 cf. 15:9, 60). The southern border of Benjamin was, of course, the northern border of Judah (vss. 15--19 cf. 15:6--9).

Of the cities Benjamin received, the most notable include Jericho, the first city to be conquered by the Israelites when they entered the land. Of course, this is not the walled city destroyed by Joshua (see our comments on 6:26). This would be the villages associated with the city (vs. 28).

["Bethel"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 22) is where Jacob saw the vision of the ladder up to Heaven (Gen. 28:11--19). The name means "house of God," and it is where Jacob goes to get right when he returns from Haran (Gen. 35:1--7). When Jeroboam sets up the two golden calves in the northern kingdom in opposition to the Temple in Jerusalem, he sets []{#c1WK.xhtml_page_304}up one in Bethel (1 Kings 12:28--33), and the city ceases to be the "house of God." It is just ["the king's chapel,"]{.class_s2FW} and the word of God is forbidden to be preached there (Amos 7:13).

The "moral of the story" is that when God is not in a place, it is no longer the house of God. That happened in Bethel, it happened in Shiloh, and it happened at the Temple in Jerusalem. Remember that the next time you hear a preacher call a church building "the house of God." Maybe it is and [maybe it isn't.]{.class_s2FX} The only time a church building can be considered a "house of God" is when it is filled with saved people whose [bodies are the temples of the Holy Ghost]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 6:19) and where the word of God is being preached and taught [in truth]{.class_s2FX} (1 Tim. 3:15). Where that is not the case, it is not a house of God. It may be a "chapel," a meeting house, a "sanctuary," a cathedral, an auditorium, etc.; but a house of God it is NOT.

["Chepharhaammonai"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 24) is the third longest word in the Bible. ["Chushanrishathaim"]{.class_s2FW} (Judg. 3:8) is longer by one letter, and ["Mahershalalhashbaz"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 8:1) is the longest.

["Gibeon"]{.class_s2FW} and ["Beeroth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 25) and ["Chephirah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 26) are three of the cities of the Gibeonites (Judg. 9:17). ["Mizpeh"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 26) was one of the cities, along with Bethel, where Samuel judged Israel (1 Sam. 7:16).

["Zelah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 28) is where Saul and Jonathan were eventually buried (2 Sam. 21:14). ["Gibeath"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 28) is also known as ["Gibeah of Benjamin"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Sam. 13:15--16) and was the hometown of Saul (1 Sam. 10:26, 11:4). We have already commented on Jerusalem and the Jebusites under 15:8, 63 (which see).

[]{#c1Y6.xhtml}

# Chapter 19 {.heading_s2B}

The chapter finishes up the allotments given to the last six tribes to receive their inheritances. Those are the six tribes associated with the tribes of Joseph in the north (see our remarks under 18:11). The inheritance of Simeon is in verses 1--9, the inheritance of Zebulun in verses 10--16, Issachar's in verses 17--23, Asher's in verses 24--31, Naphtali's in verses 32--39, and Dan's in verses 40--48.

19:1 And the second lot came forth to Simeon, even for the tribe of the children of Simeon according to their families: and their inheritance was within the inheritance of the children of Judah.

2 And they had in their inheritance Beersheba, or Sheba, and Moladah,

3 And Hazarshual, and Balah, and Azem,

4 And Eltolad, and Bethul, and Hormah,

5 And Ziklag, and Bethmarcaboth, and Hazarsusah,

6 And Bethlebaoth, and Sharuhen; thirteen cities and their villages:

7 Ain, Remmon, and Ether, and Ashan; four cities and their villages:

8 And all the villages that were round about these cities to Baalathbeer, Ramath of the south. This is the inheritance of the tribe of the children of Simeon according to their families.

9 Out of the portion of the children of Judah was the inheritance of the children of Simeon: for the part of the children of Judah was too much for them: therefore the children of Simeon had their inheritance within the inheritance of them.

Now Simeon doesn't get a prescribed tract of land; it gets cities within the territory of Judah. We gave you the reason for this back in our comments on 14:4, which see. But once Simeon gets in the land, the tribe gets swallowed up by Judah; you read little to nothing about it.

Their only "claim to fame" during the days of David was that they had 7,100 ["mighty men of valour for the war" ]{.class_s2FW}(1 Chron. 12:25). First Chronicles 4:24--43 gives you a few of their exploits. In 1 Chronicles 4:39--41, during the days of Hezekiah, some of them took the pasture land of the Hamites that lived at ["the entrance of Gedor," ]{.class_s2FW}a city that belonged to Judah (Josh. 15:58). About that same time, 500 of them went down to Mt. Seir in Edom and killed off the remaining Amalekites Saul let escape back in 1 Samuel 15, and they lived in those cities (1 Chron. 4:42--43).

Those things took place during the Assyrian captivity of the northern kingdom. Simeon, of course, went with the northern tribes when the kingdom divided under Rehoboam, so it had cities up in the northern kingdom of Israel at that time (2 Chron. 34:6). So the natural thing for any Simeonites who escaped that invasion and didn't want to live under Assyrian rule would be to move back to the old "homestead."

This migration of tribes in the land is important when we get to the tribe of Zebulun in a few verses. Over Israel's history in the land, some of the tribes (e.g., Dan) don't always stay in the allotment given to them by Joshua. Some move into other tribes' territories and take cities with which those tribes did nothing.

As an illustration of that, look at ["Ziklag"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 5. It was originally given to Judah (15:31), and here it is one of the cities in Judah given to Simeon. By the time of David, it has come under the control of the Philistines, who give it to David (1 Sam. 27:6), so it comes back under the control of Judah. The Simeonites either didn't drive the Philistines out, or they couldn't keep the Philistines from taking it over. Either way, they lost Ziklag.

["And they had in their inheritance Beersheba, or Sheba"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 2). This is a famous "error" in the [King James Version ]{.class_s2FX}at which all the apostates at the Christian Colleges, Universities, and Seminaries will grasp to destroy your faith in the Holy Bible. You see, some editions of the [AV ]{.class_s2FX}read ["AND Sheba" ]{.class_s2FW}instead of ["OR Sheba."]{.class_s2FW}

That's suppose to be a "gross" error. That is said by the same ones who give you two gods in John 1:18, slap the Deity of Christ out of a sinner's mouth as he is getting saved (Luke 23:42; Acts 9:6), and []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_307}pervert the clearest verses in the Bible on the Incarnation and the Trinity (1 Tim. 3:16; 1 John 5:7). Ain't that the pot calling the kettle black? After perverting the Scriptures, changing them to bring them down to their own level of ignorance, and removing words, clauses, and whole verses in some instances, these hypocrites will complain about an ["or" ]{.class_s2FW}being an ["and."]{.class_s2FW} You never met a bunch of sorrier rascals in your life.

You say, "Well, Ruckman, they can't both be right." Can't they? Haven't you ever heard of a [hendiadys]{.class_s2FX}? You say, "A what?" A hendiadys: it's "the expression of a single idea by two words connected with the conjunction [and.]{.class_s2FX}" You see it in Titus 2:13­ -- ["the great God and our Saviour Jesus Christ." ]{.class_s2FW}That's not two different persons of the Godhead returning at the Rapture; ["Jesus Christ" ]{.class_s2FW}[is ]{.class_s2FX}["the great God" ]{.class_s2FW}whose ["glorious appearing" ]{.class_s2FW}is our ["blessed hope."]{.class_s2FW}

The same thing is going on here in verse 2. ["Sheba"]{.class_s2FW} is the abbreviated form of ["Beersheba," ]{.class_s2FW}so it can be ["Beersheba, or Sheba" ]{.class_s2FW}(you can call it one or the other), or it can be ["Beersheba, and Sheba" ]{.class_s2FW}(a hendiadys -- both names referring to the same city). That is the "gross error" raised by those apostate hypocrites who would attack every fundamental of the faith after telling you their changes "affect no major doctrine."

10 And the third lot came up for the children of Zebulun according to their families: and the border of their inheritance was unto Sarid:

11 And their border went up toward the sea, and Maralah, and reached to Dabbasheth, and reached to the river that is before Jokneam;

12 And turned from Sarid eastward toward the sunrising unto the border of Chislothtabor, and then goeth out to Daberath, and goeth up to Japhia,

13 And from thence passeth on along on the east to Gittahhepher, to Ittahkazin, and goeth out to Remmonmethoar to Neah;

14 And the border compasseth it on the north side to Hannathon: and the outgoings thereof are in the valley of []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_308}Jiphthahel:

15 And Kattath, and Nahallal, and Shimron, and Idalah, and Bethlehem: twelve cities with their villages.

16 This is the inheritance of the children of Zebulun according to their families, these cities with their villages.

This is the inheritance of Zebulun, and it poses a problem. If you look at any map of the tribes in the land, you will see Zebulun "landlocked" by Asher on the west, Manasseh to the south, Issachar on the east, and Naphtali on the north. You say, "So? What's the problem?" The problem is Genesis 49:13.

"Zebulun shall dwell at the haven of the sea; and he shall be for an haven of ships; and his border shall be unto Zidon."

Not here in Joshua 19 it isn't, to all appearances. It is Asher that gets the northern coastal cities clear up to Zidon (vss. 28--29 cf. Judg. 1:31). Deborah said, ["Asher continued on the sea shore" ]{.class_s2FW}(Judg. 5:17). It is [Asher's ]{.class_s2FX}territory, not Zebulun's, that borders Manasseh at the Mediterranean coast (17:7--10).

Now to solve this problem, we are not going to go to the "original Hebrew" or to the Greek [Septuagint]{.class_s2FX}, written 200 years after the birth of Christ. ["An haven of ships" ]{.class_s2FW}doesn't mean "access to distant seaports where ships find haven" as Delitzsch would lead you to believe. It means ["an haven of ships" ]{.class_s2FW}just as the text says.

Now you know me. When it comes to a choice between the Bible ([AV ]{.class_s2FX}1611) and Christian scholarship, I am going to take the Book over the opinions of a bunch of egotistical stuff-shirts (no matter how "good" and "godly" they are) every time. Just because you may be an expert in the Hebrew language doesn't mean you have the sense of a brass monkey when it comes to [belief in the Book.]{.class_s2FX} The Pharisees and Sadducees of Christ's day were native Hebrew-speaking Jews, and they rejected everything their Hebrew "originals" said about the Lord Jesus Christ. Mastery of the Biblical languages is no substitute for [honesty and common sense, ]{.class_s2FX}and it never will be.

When it comes to this matter of Zebulun being ["at the haven of the sea," ]{.class_s2FW}what evidence do we have that the Bible is right and the []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_309}Hebrew scholars don't know about what in the world they are talking? Well, Josephus locates the eastern border of Zebulun at the southern end of the Sea of Galilee and the western border at the Mediterranean near Mt. Carmel ([Antiquities of the Jews, ]{.class_s2FX}Book V, Chapter 1, Paragraph 22). That would give Zebulun two places for ["an haven of ships." ]{.class_s2FW}That being the case, what you have is a clear case of the archaeologists being [wrong ]{.class_s2FX}about the locations of some of the cities in verses 11--15.

Take, for example, ["Nahallal" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 15). After complaining about the [AV ]{.class_s2FX}misspelling the word (it is ["Nahalol" ]{.class_s2FW}in Judg. 1:30 with the same Hebrew word there as here in vs. 15), the scholars place it east over near the border of Issachar, completely ignoring the context where it is grouped with western cities like Shimron and Bethlehem. The [Jewish Encyclopedia ]{.class_s2FX}places it south and west of Nazareth away from Issachar's border. The [Oxford Bible Atlas]{.class_s2FX} (1989, pg. 61) places it near the mouth of the Kishon River on the north side of Carmel, giving Zebulun ["a haven of the sea." ]{.class_s2FW}The [Jewish Encyclopedia ]{.class_s2FX}even says the [tomb of Zebulum ]{.class_s2FX}is located just outside of Sidon, showing that someone took Jacob's prophecy in Genesis 49:13 seriously.

Now what's going on with Zebulun's western border? Well, as we have seen before, the lines between tribes were not always clear cut; some tribes, like Ephraim and Manasseh, had cities in other tribes. Although that it is not stated here in Joshua 19, over time, it could have very well come to be the case. Asher didn't drive out the inhabitants of four of its coastal cities: Accho, Zidon, Ahlab, and Achzib (Judg. 1:31). Zebulun had the larger army under David (1 Chron. 12:33, 36), and those scholars who take Genesis 49:13 literally believe the verse to have been fulfilled during the reigns of David and Solomon (cf. 1 Kings 4:21).

During the captivity of the northern tribes, Zebulun still had a significant presence in the land (2 Chron. 30:10--11, 18), and the tribe stands out prominently in the prophecy concerning Christ's First Advent (Isa. 9:1 cf. Matt. 4:13--15). During Christ's ministry, Jews from ["Tyre and Sidon"]{.class_s2FW} came to hear Christ preach (Luke 6:17), and if we are to take Jacob's words at face value, undoubtedly those Jews were connected with the tribe of Zebulun. So we will believe the words in the [King James]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_310} Bible as they stand and let the Hebrew scholars play around in the "kiddie corral." You will always get more truth out of [believing the Book]{.class_s2FX} than you will fiddling around with Hebrew (or Greek) grammar and syntax (see [The Full Cup,]{.class_s2FX} 1998, pp. 202--203).

Before leaving this passage on Zebulun, there are a couple of other things you need to notice. The first is ["Gittah-hepher"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 13. That is ["Gathhepher"]{.class_s2FW} in 2 Kings 14:25---Jonah's hometown. Do you know why that is so significant? Because when the Pharisees and the Sadducees get to arguing in John 7 about whether Jesus was the Prophet like unto Moses (Deut. 18:15), they tell Nicodemus, ["Search, and look: for out of Galilee ariseth no prophet"]{.class_s2FW} (John 7:52).

[We did.]{.class_s2FX} We did what those Jewish leaders [didn't do.]{.class_s2FX} They said, ["Search, and look,"]{.class_s2FW} and then they all turned around and went home (John 7:53). [Jonah]{.class_s2FX} was a prophet from Galilee:[ Gathhepher is in Galilee.]{.class_s2FX} When Jesus Christ wanted to compare Himself to a prophet, do you know with whom He compared Himself? [Jonah,]{.class_s2FX} the prophet from Galilee. Jonah signified Christ's death, burial, and resurrection (Matt. 12:39--40).

The second thing you want to notice is ["Bethlehem"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 15. This is not the Bethlehem in Judah; this is a second Bethlehem up north in Zebulun. Now why is that so important? Because when it comes to prophecy, the Bible is not slipshod. It doesn't speak in generalities that can be taken any way the reader wants to take them, like the nonsense put out by Jeane Dixon and Nostradamus. It is very [exact.]{.class_s2FX} It will [name]{.class_s2FX} a fellow over 200 years before he is born (1 Kings 13:2 cf. 2 Kings 23:16; Isa. 44:28--45:1 cf. Ezra 1:1--4). In the case of Christ's birthplace, look at the prophecy in Micah 5:2 and notice the wording carefully.

"But thou, Bethlehem Ephratah, though thou be little among the thousands OF JUDAH, yet out of thee shall he come forth unto me that is to be ruler in Israel; whose goings forth have been from of old, from everlasting."

The Holy Spirit not only told you the name of the town, He told you where the town was located so you would not mistake it for another town of the same name­---Bethlehem OF JUDAH, not the one []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_311}in Zebulun. You won't find anything like that in 114 chapters of the [Koran. ]{.class_s2FX}Mohammed being a "prophet" is just too funny for words.

17 And the fourth lot came out to Issachar, for the children of Issachar according to their families.

18 And their border was toward Jezreel, and Chesulloth, and Shunem,

19 And Hapharaim, and Shion, and Anaharath,

20 And Rabbith, and Kishion, and Abez,

21 And Remeth, and Engannim, and Enhaddah, and Bethpazzez;

22 And the coast reacheth to Tabor, and Shahazimah, and Bethshemesh; and the outgoings of their border were at Jordan: sixteen cities with their villages.

23 This is the inheritance of the tribe of the children of Issachar according to their families, the cities and their villages.

This is Issachar's inheritance. Its western border is found in verse 18, its northern border was Tabor, its eastern border the Jordan, and the valley of Jezreel separated it from Manasseh in the south. ["Jezreel"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 18) is where Ahab had a "home away from home"; i.e., a palace away from the capital in Samaria (1 Kings 18:45, 21:1). It's where the mess with Naboth took place (1 Kings 21:1--13), and where God judged Jezebel and the house of Ahab for Naboth's murder (2 Kings 9:10--37, 10:1--11). ["Shunem"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 18) was the hometown of the ["great woman" ]{.class_s2FW}who took care of Elisha (2 Kings 4:8).

["Tabor"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 22) is the mountain city (Jer. 46:18) where Barak launched his attack against Sisera in Judges 4 and where the kings of the Midianites slew Gideon's brothers (Judg. 8:18--19). The ["Bethshemesh" ]{.class_s2FW}of verse 22 is a different one than the one in Judah (see our comments on 15:10); this one is in Issachar near the Jordan. There is a third Bethshemesh in Naphtali (vs. 38).

24 And the fifth lot came out for the tribe of the children of Asher according to their families.

25 And their border was Helkath, and Hali, and Beten, and Achshaph,

26 And Alammelech, and Amad, and Misheal; and reacheth to Carmel westward, and to Shihorlibnath;

27 And turneth toward the sunrising to Bethdagon, and reacheth to Zebulun, and to the valley of Jiphthahel toward the north side of Bethemek, and Neiel, and goeth out to Cabul on the left hand,

28 And Hebron, and Rehob, and Hammon, and Kanah, even unto great Zidon;

29 And then the coast turneth to Ramah, and to the strong city Tyre; and the coast turneth to Hosah; and the outgoings thereof are at the sea from the coast to Achzib:

30 Ummah also, and Aphek, and Rehob: twenty and two cities with their villages.

31 This is the inheritance of the tribe of the children of Asher according to their families, these cities with their villages.

This is the inheritance of Asher, and as we said under our comments on Zebulun's inheritance, it ran along the seashore. It goes from ["Shihor-libnath" ]{.class_s2FW}(a river south of Dor) up to Mt. Carmel (vs. 26). It shares common ground with Zebulun at Nahalol at the mouth of the Kishon (see our remarks about ["Nahallal" ]{.class_s2FW}under vs. 15) and runs along the coast all the way up to Zidon in Lebanon (vs. 28). Its inland cities from the south to the north were ["Helkath" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 25) along the Kishon, ["Beten" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 28), ["Aphek" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 30), ["Cabul" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 27), ["Bethemek" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 27), and ["Kanah" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 28).

Bible readers are familiar with Mt. Carmel where Elijah had his contest with the prophets of Baal (1 Kings 18). Carmel is by the Mediterranean (Jer. 46:18), which explains where Elijah got the water to drench his sacrifice during a drought (1 Kings 18:33--35).

["Cabul" ]{.class_s2FW}is the location of twenty cities which Solomon gave to Hiram King of Tyre (1 Kings 9:11--13). Evidently Hiram didn't think much of the cities (1 Kings 9:13); the name [Cabul ]{.class_s2FX}means "how little; as nothing."

The ["Hebron" ]{.class_s2FW}of verse 28 is, of course, a different Hebron than the one taken by Caleb back in chapter 14. The ["Kanah" ]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_313}of verse 28 is a different one than the Cana of Galilee in John 2:1 where Christ performed His first public miracle; this Kanah is inland and south of Tyre.

["Tyre" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 29) and ["Zidon" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 28) are the two major cities of Phoenicia (modern day Lebanon) and still exist today. Jezebel was from Zidon (1 Kings 16:31). It was Zidon that was responsible for spreading Baal and Ashtoreth worship throughout the Mediterranean (1 Kings 11:5, 33, 16:31). Asher doesn't go in and destroy the people of Tyre and Zidon (Judg. 1:31), so the worship of Baal and Ashtoreth plagues Israel all the way through the book of Judges (Judg. 1:31, 10:6) and into the reigns of Solomon (1 Kings 11:33), Ahab (1 Kings 16:31), Athaliah (2 Kings 11:18), and Manasseh (2 Kings 21:3). It is this Zidonian worship that ends up bringing down both the northern kingdom of Israel (2 Kings 17) and the southern kingdom of Judah (Jer. 44). Note that last reference. It is from Zidon from which the Roman Catholic Mary, the "Queen of Heaven," comes, so the disobedience of Asher is still damning billions of people even today.

32 The sixth lot came out to the children of Naphtali, even for the children of Naphtali according to their families.

33 And their coast was from Heleph, from Allon to Zaanannim, and Adami, Nekeb, and Jabneel, unto Lakum; and the outgoings thereof were at Jordan:

34 And then the coast turneth westward to Aznothtabor, and goeth out from thence to Hukkok, and reacheth to Zebulun on the south side, and reacheth to Asher on the west side, and to Judah upon Jordan toward the sunrising.

35 And the fenced cities are Ziddim, Zer, and Hammath, Rakkath, and Chinnereth,

36 And Adamah, and Ramah, and Hazor,

37 And Kedesh, and Edrei, and Enhazor,

38 And Iron, and Migdalel, Horem, and Bethanath, and Bethshemesh; nineteen cities with their villages.

39 This is the inheritance of the tribe of the children of Naphtali according to their families, the cities and their villages.

This is Naphtali's inheritance. It is bordered by Zebulun on the south, Asher on the west, and the Sea of Galilee and the Jordan on the east (vss. 34--35). ["Zaanannim" ]{.class_s2FW}(vs. 33) is the ["Zaanaim" ]{.class_s2FW}of Judges 4:11, where Sisera was slain (Judg. 4:17--22).

["Judah upon Jordan" ]{.class_s2FW}is a peculiar expression, seeing as how Judah's territory was nowhere near Naphtali's. The [Septuagint]{.class_s2FX}, being wrong as usual, solves the "problem" by using Jehudi's penknife (Jer. 36:23) to cut ["Judah" ]{.class_s2FW}out of the text. Not being quite as ignorant (or as lazy) as Origen, who wrote the [Septuagint]{.class_s2FX} about a hundred years after the close of the New Testament, we will search the Scriptures for the answer.

Naphtali shared a border with Manasseh on the east side of Jordan. It was Jair who settled that area (see our comments on 13:30). Jair was not only counted as a ["son of Manasseh" ]{.class_s2FW}(Num. 32:41; Deut. 3:14), being Manasseh's great, great grandson; he was also the great, great grandson of [Judah.]{.class_s2FX} In 1 Chronicles 2:3--5, 21--23, the line runs Judah, Pharez, Hezron (who married the daughter of Machir, the son of Manasseh), Segub, Jair. So Jair's territory in Bashan was ["Judah upon Jordan."]{.class_s2FW}

["Chinnereth" ]{.class_s2FW}is a city on the north of the Sea of Galilee, after which the sea was named in the Old Testament (see our remarks under 13:27). The ["Hazor"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 36 was the city that formed the northern confederacy against Joshua back in 11:1 (which see). Because the people of Naphtali didn't go in and possess the city, it was rebuilt by the Canaanites and oppressed Israel during the time of the judges (Judg. 4:2). Over and over again, we see the Israelites paying for their incomplete obedience in these chapters.

Once again there is a discrepancy in the count of cities in verse 38. There are [sixteen]{.class_s2FX} ["fenced cities"]{.class_s2FW} listed in verses 35--38, three less than the nineteen given. If you add the proper names in verse 33, that would give you 23, four over the nineteen of verse 38. The answer is that not every name in verse 33 is a city; four of them, like ["Allon"]{.class_s2FW} and ["Adami,"]{.class_s2FW} are names of [places]{.class_s2FX}. Of the remaining five names, only the ["fenced cities"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_315} would be included in the count of verse 38.

40 And the seventh lot came out for the tribe of the children of Dan according to their families.

41 And the coast of their inheritance was Zorah, and Eshtaol, and Irshemesh,

42 And Shaalabbin, and Ajalon, and Jethlah,

43 And Elon, and Thimnathah, and Ekron,

44 And Eltekeh, and Gibbethon, and Baalath,

45 And Jehud, and Beneberak, and Gathrimmon,

46 And Mejarkon, and Rakkon, with the border before Japho.

47 And the coast of the children of Dan went out too little for them: therefore the children of Dan went up to fight against Leshem, and took it, and smote it with the edge of the sword, and possessed it, and dwelt therein, and called Leshem, Dan, after the name of Dan their father.

48 This is the inheritance of the tribe of the children of Dan according to their families, these cities with their villages.

Dan is the last tribe to receive its inheritance. As we have seen on other occasions, Dan shares some of its territory with other tribes. ["Zorah, and Eshtaol"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 41) were part of Judah's territory as well as Dan's (see 15:33). ["Ekron"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 43) was part of Judah's inheritance (15:45). Some expositors make ["Irshemesh"]{.class_s2FW} the same as the Bethshemesh in Judah (15:10).

["Ajalon"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 42) is where the moon stood still back in 10:12. Judges 1:35 records the incomplete obedience of the Danites in not driving the Amorites from Ajalon and Shaalabbin.

["Thimnathah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 43) is supposed to be another name for Timnath (see our remarks on Timnah under 15:57). ["Gibbethon"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 44) was the site of some civil conflict in the northern kingdom (1 Kings 15:27, 16:15). ["Japho"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 46) is supposed to be another name for Joppa (Jon. 1:3; Acts 9:43).

Now Dan had a large population (64,400 in the census given in []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_316}Num. 26:42--43), but it only received a relatively small inheritance. So they go up north near the headwaters of the Jordan and take a town called ["Leshem"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 47; called ["Laish"]{.class_s2FW} in Judg. 18) and renamed it after the patriarch of their tribe. You can read the full account in Judges 18.

But there is some important information behind this verse at the end of a long, boring list of names. Tucked quietly away in this story, where no one who does not ["search the scriptures"]{.class_s2FW} (John 5:39) and ["study to shew thyself approved unto God"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:15) (both verses have been changed in the corrupt modern versions) will find them, are the [origins of the Roman Catholic Church.]{.class_s2FX} In Judges 17--18 is the first time a priest is called a "father" (Judg. 17:10, 18:19). He takes a "vow of poverty" and is provided only his necessities (Judg. 17:10). And he uses images as "aids to worship" (Judg. 18:18--20). Right there is where the basic elements of the Roman Catholic priesthood get their start. Later on it will add ["vestments"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Kings 10:22), a worship service at twelve o'clock noon on Sunday (1 Kings 18:26), and praying to the Queen of Heaven (Jer. 44:17--19). But it gets its start right there in Joshua 19 and Judges 17--18.

Now this is where Dan goes into apostasy, and it never gets out. From Joshua 19:47 all the way until the Assyrians take the northern tribes into captivity in 2 Kings 17, Dan is involved in false worship (Judg. 18:30--31). Those Danites are worshipping those images they took from Micah there in Judges 18 all the way through the book of Judges and into the beginning of 1 Samuel. They have a family of priests operating outside of the normal Levitical priesthood. When Jeroboam comes along, he sets up one of his golden calves in Dan, and that's where all the people go to worship instead of in Jerusalem (1 Kings 12:29--30). That idolatry becomes such a snare to Dan that in the Tribulation the tribe becomes connected with the Antichrist and his image (see our comments on Gen. 49:16--17 in that Commentary), and is missing from the tribes sealed in the Tribulation (Rev. 7).

49 When they had made an end of dividing the land for inheritance by their coasts, the children of Israel gave an []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_317}inheritance to Joshua the son of Nun among them:

50 According to the word of the LORD they gave him the city which he asked, even Timnathserah in mount Ephraim: and he built the city, and dwelt therein.

51 These are the inheritances, which Eleazar the priest, and Joshua the son of Nun, and the heads of the fathers of the tribes of the children of Israel, divided for an inheritance by lot in Shiloh before the LORD, at the door of the tabernacle of the congregation. So they made an end of dividing the country.

All twelve tribes have now divided up the land, and the last one to get his inheritance is Joshua. Like Caleb, he gets the city of his choice because he gave a good report back there in Numbers 14. Being from the tribe of Ephraim (Num. 13:8), he gets ["Timnathserah in mount Ephraim"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 50), which is called ["Timnathheres"]{.class_s2FW} in Judges 2:9. It is where Joshua is buried (24:30).

Now notice God's way of doing things in verse 51. This is a nation started and preserved by [God,]{.class_s2FX} so [God]{.class_s2FX} is supposed to be running things. That's called a "theocracy." In a theocracy, religion and politics are right together. [God]{.class_s2FX} chooses the [leader, God]{.class_s2FX} chooses the [high priest,]{.class_s2FX} and [God]{.class_s2FX} gives them a [Book]{.class_s2FX} by which to run things.

That's not your case as a New Testament Christian. While it is true that Christians founded the United States and based its laws on the Bible, and that even today the majority of Americans are professing Christians, there is no such thing as a "Christian nation" where God is running it.

America is a [republic;]{.class_s2FX} it's not a [democracy.]{.class_s2FX} Democracy is mob rule; a republic is rule by representation. The Founding Fathers considered America a "Christian nation" in the sense that they represented a professing Christian populace. The first Chief Justice of the Supreme Court, John Jay, said, "Providence has given to our people the choice of their rulers, and it is the duty, as well as the privilege and interest of our Christian nation, to select and prefer Christians for their rulers."

In the New Testament, God is supposed to run the [individual,]{.class_s2FX} []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_318}and if God gives that individual the privilege of selecting his rulers and making his laws---as He has [not]{.class_s2FX} to believers in India, Saudi Arabia, Iran, Syria, Egypt, Vietnam, Red China, North Korea, etc.---the saved believer is to choose those leaders and laws that best reflect the moral principles of the word of God and give Christians the freedom to live and witness for their Saviour. But he is [not]{.class_s2FX} to enforce his religious beliefs and practices on others by the law.

That's exactly why your forefathers came over to this country---to get away from governments that forced them by law to worship a certain way. In Italy, Spain, France, and Austria, they were forced to take the Mass, sprinkle babies, and follow the Pope; or they were burned at the stake. In Germany, they were forced to be Lutherans; in Switzerland, they were forced to be Reformed; in England, they were forced to be Anglican. The Church and the State were right together; and if you didn't worship as the State dictated, you were fined, imprisoned, whipped, had your property confiscated, and sometimes executed. So when the Founding Fathers set up your Constitution, a bunch of Connecticut Baptists wanted a guarantee that what they just left in Europe wouldn't be repeated over here. That's why you have a First Amendment to the Bill of Rights that says Congress isn't to pass a law establishing a religion or prohibiting the free exercise thereof.

When Thomas Jefferson talked about the separation of Church and State, it had nothing to do with Christians not being able to tell the government what to do; it had to do with the government not telling local churches what to do. Reading the Bible and praying in the public schools are not "establishing a religion" because the Bible and prayer are not a "church." What your district and Supreme Court judges, and your government bureaucrats, are doing today is exactly the opposite of what the men who wrote the Constitution and Bill of Rights intended. The government is "establishing," by judicial and regulatory fiat, the [religion]{.class_s2FX} (and that's exactly what it is according to the Supreme Court ruling in Torcaso vs. Watkins in 1961) of [secular, atheistic humanism.]{.class_s2FX}

Now in a theocracy, God runs things. There has only been one legitimate theocracy in the 6,000 years of human history, and that is the one set up in Exodus and Deuteronomy. The difference []{#c1Y6.xhtml_page_319}between the theocracy of Israel and, say, a theocracy set up by Mohammed in Islam, is that the Jewish theocracy had the [right Book]{.class_s2FX} and the [right God.]{.class_s2FX} All other theocracies (like Islam, Hinduism, Buddhism, Shintoism, Catholicism, etc.) are either man-made or demoniac systems.

There will be no legitimate theocracy until Jesus Christ comes back. When Christ returns, He is [God's King,]{.class_s2FX} ruling from [God's capital,]{.class_s2FX} in [God's house,]{.class_s2FX} as [God's High Priest]{.class_s2FX} (Isa. 2; Zech. 14). Until that happens, you can expect "hell on wheels" from the governments of this world (the UN, the EU, NATO, the Vatican, the Arab League, the Muslim Brotherhood, and the [United States]{.class_s2FX}).

[]{#c21J.xhtml}

# Chapter 20 {.heading_s2B}

20:1 The LORD also spake unto Joshua, saying,

2 Speak to the children of Israel, saying, Appoint out for you cities of refuge, whereof I spake unto you by the hand of Moses:

3 That the slayer that killeth any person unawares and unwittingly may flee thither: and they shall be your refuge from the avenger of blood.

4 And when he that doth flee unto one of those cities shall stand at the entering of the gate of the city, and shall declare his cause in the ears of the elders of that city, they shall take him into the city unto them, and give him a place, that he may dwell among them.

5 And if the avenger of blood pursue after him, then they shall not deliver the slayer up into his hand; because he smote his neighbour unwittingly, and hated him not beforetime.

6 And he shall dwell in that city, until he stand before the congregation for judgment, and until the death of the high priest that shall be in those days: then shall the slayer return, and come unto his own city, and unto his own house, unto the city from whence he fled.

The chapter deals with the ["cities of refuge"]{.class_s2FW} God commanded Moses back in Numbers 35. Premeditated murder was absolutely forbidden under the Law, and the penalty for it was death---[before the Law]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 9:6), [under the Law]{.class_s2FX} (Num. 35:30--34), and [under grace]{.class_s2FX} (Rom. 13:4; Acts 25:11). But where the killing was unintended or an accident, God provided protection: the ["cities of refuge."]{.class_s2FW}

We would call the crime today "manslaughter." You're driving down the road, and some kid runs out in front of you. You can't stop in time and run over him and kill him. That's manslaughter, see. You weren't lying in wait to run over the kid; it just happened. There was a rule in the Mosaic Law for that sort of thing.

When the Bible says ["Thou shalt not kill"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 20:13), you []{#c21J.xhtml_page_321}don't apply that law uniformly across all forms of taking life. The Bible defines its own terms. Jesus called it ["murder"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 19:18). The commandment gives you the generality; and other parts of Exodus, Numbers, and Deuteronomy give you the specifics. God's not talking about going to war; wars are necessary from time to time. If the Japanese bomb your naval base with the intention of invading your country, you had better kill them before they kill you.

I wish people would get that thing straight. Nobody wants war; there's nothing nice about it. But in war, you are trained to kill the enemy because if you don't, he's going to kill you. And yeah, sometimes that involves women and children. Claude Eatherley, the pilot of the weather reconnaissance aircraft that supported the atomic bombing of Hiroshima, had to get psychiatric treatment from worrying about all the children that died when the bomb was dropped. That's bad, see, but I guarantee you that if the bomb hadn't been dropped, more Americans and Japanese would have died in a land invasion than died at Nagasaki and Hiroshima combined. There are all kinds of horror stories from the Japanese going though Manchuria and the Philippines. Who worried about those kids? A soldier shouldn't worry about killing the enemy in war when it is necessary.

I had a woman write me one time from her Christian school about her roommate who was attending a church pastored by a Tennessee Temple graduate.
