That preacher would correct the [AV]{.class_s2FX} from the pulpit, and when the woman's roommate would try to talk to the man about the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible being the perfect word of God, he would laugh at her.

That Tennessee Temple graduate would tell that woman, "The [King James]{.class_s2FX} has many mistakes in it." "For example," he said, "the [King James]{.class_s2FX} Bible says, ['Thou shalt not kill,']{.class_s2FW} and then the Lord tells those Jews to kill those Canaanites and kill those Amalekites. That reading in Exodus 20:13 is a mistake."

That's the kind of education ministerial students are getting in these Christian Colleges and Universities. That graduate of a [Fundamental]{.class_s2FX} Bible school was giving one of his church members arguments [against]{.class_s2FX} the Old Testament put forth by Celsus and Marcion, two [heretics]{.class_s2FX} from the Second Century A.D. Those were [infidelic]{.class_s2FX} arguments, [1800 years out of date,]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c21J.xhtml_page_322} being taught to ministerial students at a Fundamental Christian College because faculty members like Fred Afman couldn't stand the [authority of that Book.]{.class_s2FX}

Now, according to the Bible, there are crimes ["worthy of death"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 1:32), and one of those crimes is [murder]{.class_s2FX} (Rom. 1:29). If a guy is found guilty by a jury of his peers of murdering someone and he has had every legal opportunity to prove he is not guilty, don't put him in an air-conditioned cell for thirty years and give him access to cable television and feed him three square meals a day and take care of all his health and dental needs. Hook him up to "old sparky" and let him "ride the lighting," and don't be ashamed to pull the switch either. Sure man! I mean, give the guy a chance to trust Christ first, but if you don't kill the murderer for his crime, that Bible says you pollute the land and defile it, and the only way it can be cleansed is by shedding the blood of the murderer---Numbers 35:37; look it up and READ IT!

Listen, people, if that Book is true, don't bother asking God to bless America, because [it ain't gonna happen.]{.class_s2FX} There are about 15,000 murders in this country every year. Since 1976, only 1,362 murderers have been executed for their crimes. If that Book is so, this country is defiled beyond repair.

The pro-life crowd claims abortion is murder. Well, if that's so, do you think God is going to bless any nation that kills over a million babies a year, approximately sixty million since the Supreme Court legalized abortion back in 1973? Abortion is murder, and you don't believe in executing the doctors who commit it? Then don't pray, sing, or say "God bless America" because ["the land cannot be cleansed of the blood that is shed therein, but by the blood of him that shed it"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 35:33).

Now if you kill somebody by accident or without your knowledge, that's not murder, see; it's manslaughter. But something still has to be done about it. In the Old Testament, the kinfolk of the one killed had a right to hunt the manslayer down and kill him. Every few years Hollywood comes out with a movie like "Death Wish" where the husband has to avenge the death of his wife or the daddy has to avenge the death of his child. You won't get away from a [King James]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c21J.xhtml_page_323} Bible; it will run your courts and entertainment whether they like it or not.

In the Old Testament, if you killed somebody without intending to, you had better get to the nearest city of refuge just as quick as you could get, because if you didn't, the kinfolk out for revenge could kill you with impunity. It was taken for granted that if you weren't guilty of premeditated murder, you wouldn't try to hide the body and get away with it; you would go present your case to the elders of the city of refuge. Of course, if the avenger had clear evidence and eyewitness testimony that you committed murder, the city of refuge did you no good at all; you were turned over to the victim's kinfolk for execution. Sure man! Why feel sorry for the murderer? He didn't take any pity on his victim.

But if you killed by accident, you were safe as long as you stayed in the city of refuge, and you had to stay there until the death of the high priest. That's a wonderful picture of salvation. Whether you know it or not, you are guilty of murder. You say, "I am not, Dr. Ruckman. I have never killed anybody, not even in war." Yes, you are. You are guilty of [the death of God's Son: ]{.class_s2FX}your [sins]{.class_s2FX} put Him on the cross.

["Who his own self bare our sins in his own body on the tree, that we, being dead to sins, should live unto righteousness: by whose stripes ye were healed"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:24).

["For Christ also hath once suffered for sins, the just for the unjust, that he might bring us to God, being put to death in the flesh, but quickened by the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 3:18).

The sentence for "Deicide" is eternal death, and the one who has been given ["the power of death"]{.class_s2FW} is the Devil (Heb. 2:14). But God has provided a place of refuge where Satan can't touch us.

["That by two immutable things, in which it was impossible for God to lie, we might have a strong consolation, who have FLED FOR REFUGE to lay hold upon the hope set before us"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 6:18).

What is ["the hope"]{.class_s2FW} to which we have ["fled for refuge"]{.class_s2FW}? It's Jesus Christ acting as our High Priest to obtain eternal salvation for us (Heb. 6:19--20, 5:8--10). That hope was accomplished by His []{#c21J.xhtml_page_324}resurrection from the dead (1 Pet. 1:3, 21) so that the One we murdered by our sins becomes the One to whom we flee for refuge and deliverance. If you are [in Him,]{.class_s2FX} your sins are not imputed to you, and you are reconciled to God (2 Cor. 5:19). The blood that was shed because of your sins is the same blood that draws you nigh to God (Eph. 2:13). And as long as my High Priest (Heb. 3:1) lives, the Devil can't touch me, and I am not subject to the penalty of the Law (Heb. 7:19--25). WELL GLORY!

7 And they appointed Kedesh in Galilee in mount Naphtali, and Shechem in mount Ephraim, and Kirjatharba, which is Hebron, in the mountain of Judah.

8 And on the other side Jordan by Jericho eastward, they assigned Bezer in the wilderness upon the plain out of the tribe of Reuben, and Ramoth in Gilead out of the tribe of Gad, and Golan in Bashan out of the tribe of Manasseh.

9 These were the cities appointed for all the children of Israel, and for the stranger that sojourneth among them, that whosoever killeth any person at unawares might flee thither, and not die by the hand of the avenger of blood, until he stood before the congregation.

These are the cities of refuge. According to Numbers 35:13--14, there were to be six in number: three on the east side of Jordan and three in Canaan. They are situated so that on each side there is one in the north, one in the middle, and one in the south. In other words, no matter where you lived in Israel, a city of refuge was available to you.

Notice they are all on high ground: ["MOUNT Naphtali . . . MOUNT Ephraim . . . the MOUNTAIN of Judah . . . Golan]{.class_s2FW} \[that's the Golan HEIGHTS\]["]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 7--8). That's so they can be easily seen and located; they're not in some hidden valley like Shangri La or El Dorado.

Jesus said, ["A city that is set on a hill cannot be hid"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 5:14). The reference is to these cities of refuge about which you are reading here. So the spiritual application for the Christian is he is to be a light (["Ye are the light of the world"]{.class_s2FW}---Matt. 5:14) to point []{#c21J.xhtml_page_325}lost sinners to Jesus Christ to whom they can flee for refuge (see comments above).

Now verse 7 gives the three cities in Canaan, and verse 8 gives the ones on the east side of Jordan. ["Kedesh in Galilee"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 7) is up near Lake Huleh. ["Shechem"]{.class_s2FW} was a town in Mt. Ephraim in the tribe of Manasseh (17:7). ["Hebron"]{.class_s2FW} was the town given to Caleb for his inheritance (14:13--15). ["The mountain of Judah,"]{.class_s2FW} in this case, is the mountain Caleb took from the Anakim (14:12).

Something to note when it comes to Hebron as a city of refuge is the story of Joab slaying Abner in 2 Samuel 3. Abner had slain Joab's brother Asahel in battle (2 Sam. 2:18--23)---which was NOT murder or manslaughter---and Joab and his brother Abishai never forgave him for it. When Abner came to Hebron to turn the northern kingdom of Israel over to David, Joab came to the city after David had sent Abner away ["in peace"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 3:23). Joab suspected Abner of deceit, but he was more concerned with taking vengeance on him for the death of his brother (2 Sam. 3:25). Joab called Abner back to Hebron---[a city of refuge]{.class_s2FX}---and slew him treacherously (2 Sam. 3:27). Because of that, David put a curse on Joab's house and descendants (2 Sam. 3:29), and when David died, he left instruction to Solomon to execute Joab because he had ["shed the blood of war in peace"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 2:5--6).

There are two lessons from that account. The first is found in 2 Samuel 3:30.

"So Joab AND ABISHAI his brother slew Abner, because he had slain their brother Asahel at Gibeon in the battle."

Why was Abishai guilty of Abner's murder? He wasn't even there. But like Saul of Tarsus in Acts 8:1, Abishai was ["consenting"]{.class_s2FW} in the murder of Abner. He wanted it and he approved of it; the modern term is he was an "accessory" to it.

Jesus said, ["Ye have heard that it was said by them of old time, Thou shalt not kill; and whosoever shall kill shall be in danger of the judgment: But I say unto you, That whosoever is angry with his brother without a cause shall be in danger of the judgment"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 5:21--22). John wrote, ["Whosoever hateth his brother is a murderer"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 3:15).

You don't have to shoot or stab someone to be a murderer; all []{#c21J.xhtml_page_326}you have to do is hate the person in your heart without a just cause.

The second lesson is that religion can't save you. When Solomon sent Benaiah to slay Joab, Joab ran to the Tabernacle ["and caught hold on the horns of the altar"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 2:28). He figured anything that touched that altar was holy (Exod. 30:28--29), and he wouldn't be killed in that case. But God told Moses:

["Moreover ye shall take no satisfaction for the life of a murderer, which is guilty of death: but he shall be surely put to death. And ye shall take no satisfaction for him that is fled to the city of his refuge"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 35:31--32).

The altar couldn't save the murderer any more than a city of refuge could. There was no sacrifice in the Levitical Law to atone for murder. That's why David said when he was confronted with the murder of Uriah the Hittite: ["Deliver me from bloodguiltiness, O God]{.class_s2FW} \[he was guilty of the blood of Uriah\][ . . . For thou desirest not sacrifice; else would I give it: thou delightest not in burnt offering"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 51:14, 16).

If it had not been for[ "the sure mercies"]{.class_s2FW} God gave to David (Isa. 55:3 cf. 2 Sam. 7:11--16; Psa. 89:28, 35--37), David would have died. Because of the promise He made to David, God didn't impute the sin to him (Psa. 32:1--2 cf. Rom. 4:7--8), but if that had not been the case, David would have been put to death. As it was, David still had to pay for his sin in his family (2 Sam. 12:11--14).

Now you should be glad you live this side of the Resurrection. In the New Testament, you have something those people in the Old Testament didn't have: [you have a sacrifice for murder.]{.class_s2FX} Listen, brother, sister, that Bible says, ["the blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanseth us from ALL SIN"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 1:7).

I had a meeting one time in a women's penitentiary in Wetumpka, Alabama. It was one of the best meetings I ever had; of all the places I had ever preached up to that point, I had never had as much liberty as I had there. I had never preached in any congregation that was more open and receptive, and responded better, than those women in that prison.

I remember one night eight of those ladies got saved. As I was going out the door, they stopped me and talked to me. But I noticed off to the side a big, old, fat colored woman standing there with tears []{#c21J.xhtml_page_327}just streaming down her face and running down all over her dress. She said, "Preacha, is deah any hope fo' a murderah?"

That woman was in there for murder, and she knew she was guilty. She wasn't claiming to be "framed" or justify what she had done. She wanted to know if God could save a murderer like her.

I said, "Yeah, the blood of Jesus Christ, God's Son, cleanses us from [all]{.class_s2FX} sin."

She said, "Yeah, but is there any hope for a murderah?"

I said it again more emphatically, "The blood of Jesus Christ, God's Son, cleanses us from ALL sin, sister; and if it doesn't cleanse from murder, it doesn't cleanse from nothin'." And down she went to that altar, and she got saved.

Now I never know who reads these Commentaries. It may be that a copy of this ends up in the hands of a murderer or the hands of someone on death row; you never know. If that is your case, I have some good news for you. If you murdered someone, you deserve to die. If you aren't dead yet, it is because God has been awfully good to you. If you aren't dead yet, God is giving you a chance (and probably [another]{.class_s2FX} chance) to be saved, and if that's the situation you are in, ["the blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanseth us from ALL SIN"]{.class_s2FW}---even murder. You had better get to Jesus Christ just as quick as you can get before you end up in the Lake of Fire (Rev. 21:8).

[]{#c239.xhtml}

# Chapter 21 {.heading_s2B}

21:1 Then came near the heads of the fathers of the Levites unto Eleazar the priest, and unto Joshua the son of Nun, and unto the heads of the fathers of the tribes of the children of Israel;

2 And they spake unto them at Shiloh in the land of Canaan, saying, The LORD commanded by the hand of Moses to give us cities to dwell in, with the suburbs thereof for our cattle.

3 And the children of Israel gave unto the Levites out of their inheritance, at the commandment of the LORD, these cities and their suburbs.

4 And the lot came out for the families of the Kohathites: and the children of Aaron the priest, which were of the Levites, had by lot out of the tribe of Judah, and out of the tribe of Simeon, and out of the tribe of Benjamin, thirteen cities.

5 And the rest of the children of Kohath had by lot out of the families of the tribe of Ephraim, and out of the tribe of Dan, and out of the half tribe of Manasseh, ten cities.

6 And the children of Gershon had by lot out of the families of the tribe of Issachar, and out of the tribe of Asher, and out of the tribe of Naphtali, and out of the half tribe of Manasseh in Bashan, thirteen cities.

7 The children of Merari by their families had out of the tribe of Reuben, and out of the tribe of Gad, and out of the tribe of Zebulun, twelve cities.

8 And the children of Israel gave by lot unto the Levites these cities with their suburbs, as the LORD commanded by the hand of Moses.

Now all twelve tribes have received their inheritance, but there is one tribe that was not counted among the twelve. It was Levi, and we have discussed the reasons for this under 12:14 and 14:3--11 (which see). Those Levites were separated from the rest of the tribes []{#c239.xhtml_page_329}in the place of the firstborn of the rest of Israel (Num. 8:16--18).

The Levites were to receive 48 cities out of the other twelve tribes (vs. 41 cf. Num. 35:7), and those cities included the ["suburbs"]{.class_s2FW} which extended a total of 5,500 feet out from the city wall (see our remarks on Num. 35:4--5 in[ The "Errors" in the King James Bible,]{.class_s2FX} 1999, pg. 115). ["The villages"]{.class_s2FW} connected with those cities remained with the tribes out of which those cities were taken (e.g., see vs. 12).

The tribe of Levi was divided into three families: Kohath, Gershon, and Merari (Num. 26:57); Aaron was part of the family of Kohath through his father Amram (Num. 26:58--59). Aaron's part of the Kohathites got thirteen cities out of the tribes of Judah, Simeon, and Benjamin (vs. 4); the rest of the Kohathites got ten cities out of the tribes of Ephraim, Dan, and the western half of Manasseh (vs. 5). The Gershonites got thirteen cities out of Issachar, Asher, Naphtali, and Manasseh on the east side of Jordan (vs. 6); the Merarites got twelve cities out of Reuben, Gad, and Zebulun (vs. 7).

9 And they gave out of the tribe of the children of Judah, and out of the tribe of the children of Simeon, these cities which are here mentioned by name,

10 Which the children of Aaron, being of the families of the Kohathites, who were of the children of Levi, had: for theirs was the first lot.

11 And they gave them the city of Arba the father of Anak, which city is Hebron, in the hill country of Judah, with the suburbs thereof round about it.

12 But the fields of the city, and the villages thereof, gave they to Caleb the son of Jephunneh for his possession.

13 Thus they gave to the children of Aaron the priest Hebron with her suburbs, to be a city of refuge for the slayer; and Libnah with her suburbs,

14 And Jattir with her suburbs, and Eshtemoa with her suburbs,

15 And Holon with her suburbs, and Debir with her suburbs,

16 And Ain with her suburbs, and Juttah with her []{#c239.xhtml_page_330}suburbs, and Bethshemesh with her suburbs; nine cities out of those two tribes.

17 And out of the tribe of Benjamin, Gibeon with her suburbs, Geba with her suburbs,

18 Anathoth with her suburbs, and Almon with her suburbs; four cities.

19 All the cities of the children of Aaron, the priests, were thirteen cities with their suburbs.

This first passage deals with the cities Aaron's part of the Kohathites received. As with the division of the tribes, Judah is dealt with first. Notice in verses 11--13, the Levites get the city of Hebron, which was given to Caleb for an inheritance (14:14). We saw back in 20:7 that Hebron was chosen as a city of refuge. All the cities of refuge were Levitical cities (Num. 35:6). The way Hebron was divided between the Levites and Caleb was that the Levites got the city proper and the suburbs, and Caleb got the fields and villages associated with the city (vs. 12). The Levites also got Caleb's other city, Debir (vs. 15 cf. 15:15--19).

["Bethshemesh"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 16) was the city to which the Philistines returned the Ark of the Covenant in 1 Samuel 6, and the reason it was returned there was because it was the nearest Levitical city to Philistine territory (1 Sam. 6:15--16). Aaron's kin got the city of Gibeon (vs. 17), and that is where the Tabernacle and Brazen Altar ended up before Solomon built the Temple (1 Chron. 16:39, 21:29 cf. 1 Kings 3:4; 2 Chron. 1:3--6). ["Anathoth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 18) was the hometown of Abiathar the high priest (1 Kings 2:26) and, many years later, of Jeremiah (Jer. 29:27).

20 And the families of the children of Kohath, the Levites which remained of the children of Kohath, even they had the cities of their lot out of the tribe of Ephraim.

21 For they gave them Shechem with her suburbs in mount Ephraim, to be a city of refuge for the slayer; and Gezer with her suburbs,

22 And Kibzaim with her suburbs, and Bethhoron with her suburbs; four cities.

23 And out of the tribe of Dan, Eltekeh with her suburbs, Gibbethon with her suburbs,

24 Aijalon with her suburbs, Gathrimmon with her suburbs; four cities.

25 And out of the half tribe of Manasseh, Tanach with her suburbs, and Gathrimmon with her suburbs; two cities.

26 All the cities were ten with their suburbs for the families of the children of Kohath that remained.

This passage is a list of the cities received by the rest of the Kohathites. The first city in this section is the city of refuge Shechem (20:7). ["Gezer"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 21) is a city the Levites were "sharing" with Ephraimites and Canaanites (see our comments on 16:10).

Now there are a couple of "discrepancies" between the list here and the list in 1 Chronicles 6. ["Kibzaim"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 22 is called ["Jokmeam"]{.class_s2FW} in 1 Chronicles 6:68, and ["Beeshterah"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 27) is ["Ashtaroth"]{.class_s2FW} in 1 Chronicles 6:71 (you can see the same thing between vs. 25 and 1 Chron. 6:70). But as we saw back in 14:15 and 15:15, cities can have[ more than one name.]{.class_s2FX} Moreover, who doesn't know that over a period of 900 years a city can [change names:]{.class_s2FX} New York started off as New Amsterdam; Byzantium changed to Constantinople under the Romans and Istanbul under the Moslems; the Communists renamed St. Petersburg in Russia "Leningrad" and Saigon in Vietnam "Ho Chi Minh City."

Another "discrepancy" is that the allotment out of Dan in verses 23--24 is missing from 1 Chronicles 6; the cities of verse 24 are given as coming out of Ephraim (1 Chron. 6:66--69). The reason for this is found back in 19:47. By the time 1 Chronicles was written, Dan had long since forsaken its southern inheritance in favor of its northern holdings; Ephraim had taken over the cites of verse 24.

27 And unto the children of Gershon, of the families of the Levites, out of the other half tribe of Manasseh they gave Golan in Bashan with her suburbs, to be a city of refuge for the slayer; and Beeshterah with her suburbs; two cities.

28 And out of the tribe of Issachar, Kishon with her suburbs, Dabareh with her suburbs,

29 Jarmuth with her suburbs, Engannim with her suburbs; four cities.

30 And out of the tribe of Asher, Mishal with her suburbs, Abdon with her suburbs,

31 Helkath with her suburbs, and Rehob with her suburbs; four cities.

32 And out of the tribe of Naphtali, Kedesh in Galilee with her suburbs, to be a city of refuge for the slayer; and Hammothdor with her suburbs, and Kartan with her suburbs; three cities.

33 All the cities of the Gershonites according to their families were thirteen cities with their suburbs.

These are the cities given to the Gershonites. As with the other two lists, the first city given is the city of refuge; in this instance, ["Golan in Bashan"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 27 cf. 20:8). ["Kadesh in Galilee"]{.class_s2FW} is the other city of refuge belonging to Gershon (vs. 32 cf. 20:2).

Like Gezer back in verse 21, ["Rehob"]{.class_s2FW} is one of those cities out of which the Asherites didn't drive out the Canaanites (Judg. 1:31).

34 And unto the families of the children of Merari, the rest of the Levites, out of the tribe of Zebulun, Jokneam with her suburbs, and Kartah with her suburbs,

35 Dimnah with her suburbs, Nahalal with her suburbs; four cities.

36 And out of the tribe of Reuben, Bezer with her suburbs, and Jahazah with her suburbs,

37 Kedemoth with her suburbs, and Mephaath with her suburbs; four cities.

38 And out of the tribe of Gad, Ramoth in Gilead with her suburbs, to be a city of refuge for the slayer; and Mahanaim with her suburbs,

39 Heshbon with her suburbs, Jazer with her suburbs; four cities in all.

40 So all the cities for the children of Merari by their []{#c239.xhtml_page_333}families, which were remaining of the families of the Levites, were by their lot twelve cities.

41 All the cities of the Levites within the possession of the children of Israel were forty and eight cities with their suburbs.

42 These cities were every one with their suburbs round about them: thus were all these cities.

Now unlike the other families, the cities of Merari don't begin with a city of refuge. ["Ramoth in Gilead"]{.class_s2FW} (20:8) doesn't even show up until five verses into the passage. ["Bezer"]{.class_s2FW} in Reuben (vs. 26) isn't even identified as a city of refuge even though it is one (20:8). With Reuben, one is reminded again of the fact that the tribe was rejected because of his sin of fornication with his father's concubine (1 Chron. 5:1).

["Ramoth in Gilead"]{.class_s2FW} was taken by the Syrians in 1 Kings 22:3. It is where both Ahab and his son Joram were mortally wounded in battle (1 Kings 22:29--37; 2 Kings 8:28), and it is also where Jehu was anointed to be King (2 Kings 9:1--10).

43 And the LORD gave unto Israel all the land which he sware to give unto their fathers; and they possessed it, and dwelt therein.

44 And the LORD gave them rest round about, according to all that he sware unto their fathers: and there stood not a man of all their enemies before them; the LORD delivered all their enemies into their hand.

45 There failed not ought of any good thing which the LORD had spoken unto the house of Israel; all came to pass.

Now given all the incidents of incomplete obedience we have read in chapters 13--19, the statements in this passage seem to contradict those. But remember, this is a general summary of what the Lord accomplished for the children of Israel through Joshua (see our comments on 11:23). To affirm this interpretation, the Holy Spirit gives you this commentary on verse 44:

["For if Jesus had given them rest, then would he not afterward have spoken of another day. There remaineth therefore a rest to the people of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 4:7--8).

Israel faced plenty of enemies and plenty of warfare after verses 43--45. God hadn't yet enlarged their borders as He promised back in Deuteronomy 12:20. All of that awaits fulfillment when the second "Joshua" returns. But everything God promised Joshua back in chapter 1 had been accomplished.

The problem with what follows in the book of Judges is that God kept His part, [but the Israelites didn't keep theirs.]{.class_s2FX} That's the problem with the Christian's spiritual warfare. The problem is not with the promises of God; the problem is with [us]{.class_s2FX} (and I include myself here). Whenever sin has gotten the upper hand in my life, it is because I have not followed what the Holy Spirit said to get the victory. The same is true for you. If you claim the promises God gives in passages like Romans 6 and do what the Scriptures say in those passages, you [will]{.class_s2FX} get the victory.

["For whatsoever is born of God overcometh the world: AND THIS IS THE VICTORY THAT OVERCOMETH THE WORLD, EVEN OUR FAITH"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 5:4).

["This I say then, Walk in the Spirit, AND YE SHALL NOT FULFILL THE LUST OF THE FLESH"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:16).

["Submit yourselves therefore to God. Resist the devil, AND HE WILL FLEE FROM YOU"]{.class_s2FW} (James 4:7).

[]{#c25F.xhtml}

# Chapter 22 {.heading_s2B}

22:1 Then Joshua called the Reubenites, and the Gadites, and the half tribe of Manasseh,

2 And said unto them, Ye have kept all that Moses the servant of the LORD commanded you, and have obeyed my voice in all that I commanded you:

3 Ye have not left your brethren these many days unto this day, but have kept the charge of the commandment of the LORD your God.

4 And now the LORD your God hath given rest unto your brethren, as he promised them: therefore now return ye, and get you unto your tents, and unto the land of your possession, which Moses the servant of the LORD gave you on the other side Jordan.

5 But take diligent heed to do the commandment and the law, which Moses the servant of the LORD charged you, to love the LORD your God, and to walk in all his ways, and to keep his commandments, and to cleave unto him, and to serve him with all your heart and with all your soul.

6 So Joshua blessed them, and sent them away: and they went unto their tents.

7 Now to the one half of the tribe of Manasseh Moses had given possession in Bashan: but unto the other half thereof gave Joshua among their brethren on this side Jordan westward. And when Joshua sent them away also unto their tents, then he blessed them,

8 And he spake unto them, saying, Return with much riches unto your tents, and with very much cattle, with silver, and with gold, and with brass, and with iron, and with very much raiment: divide the spoil of your enemies with your brethren.

9 And the children of Reuben and the children of Gad and the half tribe of Manasseh returned, and departed from the children of Israel out of Shiloh, which is in the land of Canaan, to go unto the country of Gilead, to the land of []{#c25F.xhtml_page_336}their possession, whereof they were possessed, according to the word of the LORD by the hand of Moses.

Verses 1--4 are the fulfillment of the commission given to the armed fighters from the tribes of Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh who settled on the east side of Jordan (see our remarks under 1:12--15). Those tribes saw the conquest of the land all the way to the end as they promised; now Joshua allows them to go home with his blessing (vs. 6). They fulfilled what Moses told them to a "T" (vs. 2 cf. Deut. 3:20).

But in being sent away, they are given a warning: ["But take diligent heed to do the commandment and the law, which Moses the servant of the LORD charged you"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 5). Being separated from the other tribes by the Jordan didn't separate them from the Law of God. This was the heart of the Mosaic covenant (Exod. 15:26)---[works.]{.class_s2FX} Those three tribes end up going into captivity first because they ignored Joshua's warning (1 Chron. 5:25--26).

["To love the LORD your God."]{.class_s2FW} That is ["the first and great commandment"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 22:37--38). It, along with the command to love your neighbor, is the summation of the LAW, not the Gospel (see our comments on Luke 10:27 in that Commentary). The New Testament Gospel is that God loved us first through the sacrifice of His Son (1 John 4:10; Rom. 5:8). For [us]{.class_s2FX} this side of Calvary, ["The love of God . . . is IN CHRIST JESUS OUR LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:39), not in the keeping of the Law.

["And to walk in all his ways"]{.class_s2FW}: an Old Testament commandment that is all about commandment-keeping and works (Deut. 5:33, 8:6, 13:4, 26:17, 28:9, 30:16; Psa. 119:1). The commands for the New Testament believer are:

["Walk in newness of life"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:4).

["Walk in the Spirit"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 5:16, 25; Rom. 8:1, 4).

["Walk by faith, not by sight"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 5:7).

["Let us walk honestly"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 13:13).

["Walk worthy of the vocation wherewith ye are called"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 4:1).

["Walk as children of light"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 5:8).

["Walk worthy of God"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Thess. 2:12).

["Walk in wisdom"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c25F.xhtml_page_337} (Col. 4:5).

["As ye have therefore received Christ Jesus the Lord, so walk ye in him"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 2:6).

The Christian doesn't walk in good works to [get]{.class_s2FX} saved; he walks in good works because he [is]{.class_s2FX} saved (Eph. 2:8--10). Good works are the fruit of walking ["worthy of the Lord unto all pleasing"]{.class_s2FW} (Col. 1:10).

When Jesus said ["If ye love me, keep my commandments"]{.class_s2FW} (John 14:15), those ["commandments"]{.class_s2FW} have nothing to do with the Decalogue, and certainly not keeping the Sabbath as the Seventh-day Adventists try to put on you (Rom. 13:9; Col. 2:16--17). Those are [new]{.class_s2FX} commandments given by the Holy Spirit [after]{.class_s2FX} the Resurrection (John 14:25--26), and you can find a discussion of them under our remarks on John 14:15 and 1 John 2:3--4, 3:23--24 in those Commentaries (which see).

["And to cleave unto him."]{.class_s2FW} The word ["cleave"]{.class_s2FW} here doesn't mean "to sever or cut in two," as in "to cleave wood"; it means "to stick to or cling to; adhere firmly, closely, or loyally to." But you could have figured that out by the preposition that followed the word: ["unto."]{.class_s2FW} If you ["cleave unto"]{.class_s2FW} something, you aren't splitting it apart.

Now cleaving to the Lord is a good command for the New Testament believer. When Barnabas met with the first Gentile church at Antioch, he ["exhorted them all, that with purpose of heart they would cleave unto the Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 11:23). Of course, a born-again child of God cannot be separated ["from the love of God, which is in Christ Jesus our Lord"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 8:39), but in his daily walk of fellowship and service, he certainly can get away from the Lord. That is why the walk and the cleaving go right together here in Joshua 22:5.

["And to serve him with all your heart and with all your soul."]{.class_s2FW} Notice how love and service go hand in hand. ["The first and great commandment"]{.class_s2FW} is to love the Lord ["with ALL THY HEART, and with ALL THY SOUL, and with all thy mind"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 22:37--38). Jesus said, ["No SERVANT can SERVE two masters: for either he will hate the one and LOVE the other"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 16:13). That is why the Christian is commanded not to love the world, because sooner or later, you will [serve]{.class_s2FX} what you []{#c25F.xhtml_page_338}[love]{.class_s2FX} (1 John 2:15--17).

Back to Joshua 22: ["And when Joshua sent them away also unto their tents, then he blessed them, And he spake unto them saying, Return with much riches unto your tents, and with very much cattle, with silver, and with gold, and with brass, and with iron, and with very much raiment"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 7--8). Everything they weren't allowed to have at Jericho (see 6:18--19) they now have; if Achan had only waited, he could have had much more than 200 shekels of silver, a gold wedge, and a nice Babylonian garment.

Let that be a lesson to you, Christian. What you are reading here is reward for faithful service, like the believer receives at the Judgment Seat of Christ. Notice the gold and silver in verse 8, and the ["much riches"]{.class_s2FW} matching the ["precious stones"]{.class_s2FW} of 1 Corinthians 3:12; note ["much raiment"]{.class_s2FW} matching ["the fine linen"]{.class_s2FW} which ["is the righteousness of saints"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 19:8). The "goodies" come after a life of serving Christ; you don't get them down here. It's not "your best life now" (Joel Osteen); the "dessert" comes at the [end of the meal.]{.class_s2FX}

Now if the Lord gives you money in this life, OK. But that should not be your goal as a believer. Paul said:

["But they that will be rich fall into temptation and a snare, and into many foolish and hurtful lusts, which drown men in destruction and perdition. For the love of money is the root of all evil: which while some coveted after, they have erred from the faith, and pierced themselves through with many sorrows"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:9--10).

The Christian's treasures are to be "upstairs" (Matt. 6:20), and when you lay up treasures down here for yourself, you are ["not rich toward God"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 12:21).

Back to verse 8: ["divide the spoil of your enemies with your brethren."]{.class_s2FW} This was a law laid down by the Lord in Numbers 31:27 and reaffirmed by David:

["But as his part is that goeth down to the battle, so shall his part be that tarrieth by the stuff: they shall part alike. And it was so from that day forward, that he made it a statute and an ordinance for Israel unto this day"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c25F.xhtml_page_339} (1 Sam. 30:24--25).

What this means for the believer in the Body of Christ is that when you support the Lord's work with a cheerful, willing heart (2 Cor. 9:7), you will get the same reward as those doing the work. If you give to the spread of the Gospel overseas, you will "split even" with the missionary on the field at the Judgment Seat of Christ.

Jesus said, ["For whosoever shall give you a cup of water to drink in my name, because ye belong to Christ, verily I say unto you, he shall not lose his reward"]{.class_s2FW} (Mark 9:41).

Paul wrote to the Hebrews, ["For God is not unrighteous to forget your work and labour of love, which ye have shewed toward his name, in that ye have ministered to the saints, and do minister"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 6:10).

Verse 9 here in Joshua 22 is self-explanatory.

10 And when they came unto the borders of Jordan, that are in the land of Canaan, the children of Reuben and the children of Gad and the half tribe of Manasseh built there an altar by Jordan, a great altar to see to.

11 And the children of Israel heard say, Behold, the children of Reuben and the children of Gad and the half tribe of Manasseh have built an altar over against the land of Canaan, in the borders of Jordan, at the passage of the children of Israel.

12 And when the children of Israel heard of it, the whole congregation of the children of Israel gathered themselves together at Shiloh, to go up to war against them.

13 And the children of Israel sent unto the children of Reuben, and to the children of Gad, and to the half tribe of Manasseh, into the land of Gilead, Phinehas the son of Eleazar the priest,

14 And with him ten princes, of each chief house a prince throughout all the tribes of Israel; and each one was an head of the house of their fathers among the thousands of Israel.

15 And they came unto the children of Reuben, and to []{#c25F.xhtml_page_340}the children of Gad, and to the half tribe of Manasseh, unto the land of Gilead, and they spake with them, saying,

16 Thus saith the whole congregation of the LORD, What trespass is this that ye have committed against the God of Israel, to turn away this day from following the LORD, in that ye have builded you an altar, that ye might rebel this day against the LORD?

17 Is the iniquity of Peor too little for us, from which we are not cleansed until this day, although there was a plague in the congregation of the LORD,

18 But that ye must turn away this day from following the LORD? and it will be, seeing ye rebel to day against the LORD, that to morrow he will be wroth with the whole congregation of Israel.

19 Notwithstanding, if the land of your possession be unclean, then pass ye over unto the land of the possession of the LORD, wherein the LORD'S tabernacle dwelleth, and take possession among us: but rebel not against the LORD, nor rebel against us, in building you an altar beside the altar of the LORD our God.

20 Did not Achan the son of Zerah commit a trespass in the accursed thing, and wrath fell on all the congregation of Israel? and that man perished not alone in his iniquity.

Now when the Reubenites, Gadites, and the half tribe of the Manassites return to their homes on the east side of the Jordan, they stop at the crossing on their side and build a big altar for anyone passing by to see: ["To see to"]{.class_s2G4-0} (vs. 10) may look like an odd construction, but it is still used that way today: "see to it," "see to that." In other words, pay attention to it; take care of it. In a few verses, we will get the full purpose for building the altar, but in verse 10, we know it was built for "show" (to look at), [not for use.]{.class_s2G6}

Why was that such an important point? Because the Israelites were only to make burnt offerings on the Brazen Altar at the Tabernacle (Lev. 17:8--9; Deut. 12:5--6, 27). The other tribes think the three eastern tribes have set up an altar for themselves on their side of Jordan in opposition to ["the altar of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 19). []{#c25F.xhtml_page_341}They are ready to go to war with the Reubenites, Gadites, and the Manassites on the other side of Jordan (vs. 12) because they believe God will bring a curse on all the people like He did over the sin at Baal-peor and Achan's trespass (vss. 17, 20).

Now the western tribes may have jumped to a conclusion, but they handled the matter right. They sent a "committee" over to inquire what was going on and to give the other three tribes a chance to repent if they were guilty. Those western tribes have righteous indignation because they are [zealous for the truth;]{.class_s2FX} that is, they are angry about the [right thing.]{.class_s2FX} That Bible says, ["Be ye angry, and sin not"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 4:26). In other words, be angry for the right reason, and when you do, follow through on that anger the right way.

The western tribes were concerned about righteousness according to [what the Law said.]{.class_s2FX} Later on in the book of Judges, they weren't: ["every man did that which was right IN HIS OWN EYES" ]{.class_s2FW}(Judg. 21:25), not according to [what God said in His Book.]{.class_s2FX}

When a nation doesn't operate according to God's righteousness as defined in God's Book, you don't have [liberty;]{.class_s2FX} you have [license.]{.class_s2FX} Liberty is the freedom to do what is [right; ]{.class_s2FX}license is the freedom to do [whatever you want.]{.class_s2FX} And what the unsaved man wants, whose Adamic nature is not restrained in any way by the word of God or God's Law, is to indulge the flesh in whatever manner he sees fit. When a society gets to that point, you either have anarchy or a totalitarian dictatorship to keep everything under control.

The reason this country is in the mess in which it is right now is because people, even Christians, are no longer zealous for the word of God. Hardly anybody is concerned with God's opinion about anything. That's not "progress" (evolution); that's [regression.]{.class_s2FX} It's moving back to a [jungle]{.class_s2FX} culture, with [jungle]{.class_s2FX} morals, operating under the law of the [jungle]{.class_s2FX}---me first, you next; dog eat dog.

I have something I read to my congregation from time to time. It's a "want ad" for an employee by a general store owner back in the Nineteenth Century. The employer asks for a man who can work twelve hours a day, dress properly, not gamble, not drink, attend church on Sunday, and lead his family in daily Bible reading and prayer. The government came along and one by one over time, through regulations and legislation, told employers they couldn't []{#c25F.xhtml_page_342}require those things for their businesses because they infringe on others' religious and civil "rights." The employer can't set up the standards for his store. Do you know how that ended up? It ended up with Obama telling companies they have to support sex perversion and abortion against their wishes or be closed down by the Federal government. In other words, it ended up with [enslavement;]{.class_s2FX} your liberty is completely gone.

Now the delegation sent to the eastern tribes is headed up by ["Phinehas the son of Eleazar the priest"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 13--14). There was a reason for that. Look at verse 17.

"Is the iniquity of Peor too little for us, from which we are not cleansed until this day, although there was a plague in the congregation of the LORD."

That is not a coincidental reference. It was [Phinehas]{.class_s2FX} who ended the plague God brought on Israel for the sin of Baal-peor.

["And when Phinehas, the son of Eleazar, the son of Aaron the priest, saw it, he rose up from among the congregation, and took a javelin in his hand; And he went after the man of Israel into the tent, and thrust both of them through, the man of Israel and the woman through her belly. So the plague was stayed from the children of Israel"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 25:7--8).

The Lord said Phinehas[ "was zealous for my sake among them]{.class_s2FW} \[see our comments above\][" ]{.class_s2FW}(Num. 25:11). Because of that, the Lord gave Phinehas ["and his seed after him"]{.class_s2FW} a ["covenant of peace"]{.class_s2FW} that gave him and his descendants ["an everlasting priesthood"]{.class_s2FW} (Num. 25:12--13). That priesthood runs all the way into the Millennium (1 Chron. 6:4--8 cf. Ezek. 40:46, 43:19, 44:15, 48:11).

In addition, Phinehas will forever stand out as one of the clearest examples in the Bible of the difference between Old Testament salvation and New Testament salvation. Look at Psalm 106:30--31.

"Then stood up Phinehas, and executed judgment: and so the plague was stayed. AND THAT WAS COUNTED UNTO HIM FOR RIGHTEOUSNESS unto all generations for evermore."

The same thing is said of Phinehas as was said of Abraham in []{#c25F.xhtml_page_343}Romans 4:3, except in Phinehas' case there was no faith involved. Phinehas received imputed righteousness based on pure works: being zealous enough to stab two fornicating idolaters through the belly with a javelin. [That's not salvation by grace through faith at all.]{.class_s2FX} You receive the imputed righteousness of God based on your faith in the substitutionary death of Jesus Christ on the cross for you and in His resurrection from the dead (Rom. 4:24--25). Salvation under the Old Testament is not the same as salvation under the New Testament, no matter what any "good, godly" Fundamentalists says. Moral of the story: when a good, godly Fundamentalist crosses that Book, just cross him off at that point.

21 Then the children of Reuben and the children of Gad and the half tribe of Manasseh answered, and said unto the heads of the thousands of Israel,

22 The LORD God of gods, the LORD God of gods, he knoweth, and Israel he shall know; if it be in rebellion, or if in transgression against the LORD, (save us not this day,)

23 That we have built us an altar to turn from following the LORD, or if to offer thereon burnt offering or meat offering, or if to offer peace offerings thereon, let the LORD himself require it;

24 And if we have not rather done it for fear of this thing, saying, In time to come your children might speak unto our children, saying, What have ye to do with the LORD God of Israel?

25 For the LORD hath made Jordan a border between us and you, ye children of Reuben and children of Gad; ye have no part in the LORD: so shall your children make our children cease from fearing the LORD.

26 Therefore we said, Let us now prepare to build us an altar, not for burnt offering, nor for sacrifice:

27 But that it may be a witness between us, and you, and our generations after us, that we might do the service of the LORD before him with our burnt offerings, and with our sacrifices, and with our peace offerings; that your children may not say to our children in time to come, Ye []{#c25F.xhtml_page_344}have no part in the LORD.

28 Therefore said we, that it shall be, when they should so say to us or to our generations in time to come, that we may say again, Behold the pattern of the altar of the LORD, which our fathers made, not for burnt offerings, nor for sacrifices; but it is a witness between us and you.

29 God forbid that we should rebel against the LORD, and turn this day from following the LORD, to build an altar for burnt offerings, for meat offerings, or for sacrifices, beside the altar of the LORD our God that is before his tabernacle.

This is the explanation of the eastern tribes for their altar, and they preface it with: ["if it be in rebellion, or if in transgression against the LORD, (save us not this day,)"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 22). They are telling the other tribes the same thing Paul told Festus: ["if I be an offender, or have committed any thing worthy of death, I refuse not to die"]{.class_s2FW} (Acts 25:11). In other words, "If we are guilty of rebellion or transgression in this matter, go ahead and kill us."

Now the explanation is that once the next generation or two comes along, they might forget about the agreement Moses made with the Transjordanian tribes in Numbers 32, and they would ostracize the eastern tribes from the covenant God made with Israel. They were afraid of being "excommunicated" from the worship at the Tabernacle because they weren't in the Promised Land proper.

The tendency is for the next generation to forget what their fathers went through to make things better for them. You see that in Exodus 1:8 where ["a new king"]{.class_s2FW} arose[ "over Egypt, which knew not Joseph."]{.class_s2FW} That was a fellow who knew nothing about the most important man in Egyptian history, the one who saved Egypt, and the whole Middle East, from being wiped out by famine. After Joshua died, and all the elders who lived with him, there were generations of Israelites who knew nothing about the wars their fathers fought to take the land (Judg. 3:1--2). As a result, they had settled in with the heathen people left in the land and adopted their false gods (Judg. 3:5--7). So the fears of the Transjordanian tribes are well founded.

The altar they built wasn't for sacrifice; it was for a witness that []{#c25F.xhtml_page_345}they worshipped the same God as the tribes in Canaan did. We have the same thing today in local churches. There is usually a place down front where those who respond to an invitation can come and pray: [a prayer altar.]{.class_s2FX} That's not an altar for burning literal sacrifices, but it is a place where saints can come and present their ["bodies a living sacrifice"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 12:1).

Of course, we understand that is not the only place a Christian can go to get right, but it is a good place to pray in the church building. Every once in a while we get some Hyperdispensational kook come through who says, "There's no prayer altar in the New Testament. Where do you get a prayer altar?" We got it from the same place you get toilets, light bulbs, Sunday schools, and church buses---and church buildings, for that matter.

Now don't misunderstand what I am saying. There is nothing wrong with any of those things. What you have to realize is that there are plenty of things in our local churches today that you won't find in the New Testament. Where did you ever read Paul writing about a PA system? That doesn't mean those things are [unscriptural]{.class_s2FX} just because you can't find those things in the Bible. The rule of thumb is if it is not [contrary to Scripture]{.class_s2FX}---i.e., something definitely [wrong]{.class_s2FX} with it---you can use it for God's glory, the evangelism of sinners, and the edification of saints.

30 And when Phinehas the priest, and the princes of the congregation and heads of the thousands of Israel which were with him, heard the words that the children of Reuben and the children of Gad and the children of Manasseh spake, it pleased them.

31 And Phinehas the son of Eleazar the priest said unto the children of Reuben, and to the children of Gad, and to the children of Manasseh, This day we perceive that the LORD is among us, because ye have not committed this trespass against the LORD: now ye have delivered the children of Israel out of the hand of the LORD.

32 And Phinehas the son of Eleazar the priest, and the princes, returned from the children of Reuben, and from the children of Gad, out of the land of Gilead, unto the land []{#c25F.xhtml_page_346}of Canaan, to the children of Israel, and brought them word again.

33 And the thing pleased the children of Israel; and the children of Israel blessed God, and did not intend to go up against them in battle, to destroy the land wherein the children of Reuben and Gad dwelt.

34 And the children of Reuben and the children of Gad called the altar Ed: for it shall be a witness between us that the LORD is God.

Phinehas and his delegation accept the explanation, and the Bible says, ["it pleased THEM"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 38). Look at verse 33: ["And the thing pleased THE CHILDREN OF ISRAEL."]{.class_s2FW} Did you notice when you read the passage that it doesn't say [God]{.class_s2FX} was particularly pleased with it.

Now the passage doesn't say the Lord was upset about the matter either, but did you notice the [lack of prayer]{.class_s2FX} on both sides? The Reubenites, Gadites, and the Manassites didn't ask the Lord what He thought about putting up an altar of witness. On the other side, Phinehas and the representatives of the ten tribes on the west of Jordan didn't ask the Lord what He thought of it either or what should be done about the matter; neither did the whole congregation back at Shiloh. The whole thing was human expediency from start to finish. Brethren, prayer shouldn't be a [last resort;]{.class_s2FX} it should be a [first necessity.]{.class_s2FX}

Verse 34:[ "And the children of Reuben and the children of Gad called the altar Ed: for it shall be a witness between us that the LORD is God."]{.class_s2FW}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}First of all notice the italicized words. In the [King James]{.class_s2FX} text, the words ["Ed"]{.class_s2FW} and ["shall be"]{.class_s2FW} are in italics.

The Fundamentalists and the Conservatives are always complaining about the italicized words in the [AV]{.class_s2FX} because they are not in the "originals." That may be true, but look at how the sentence would read without the italics:[ "And the children of Reuben and the children of Gad called the altar: for it a witness between us that the LORD is God."]{.class_s2FX}

What kind of nonsense is that? They ["called the altar"]{.class_s2FX}---they called it what? ["For it a witness"]{.class_s2FX}---what's a sentence doing with no predicate? It's almost as bad as the [ASV]{.class_s2FX}[]{#c25F.xhtml_page_347} reading for 1 Timothy 3:16 where there is no subject for ["was manifest in the flesh"]{.class_s2FW} (see our comments on the verse in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on the Pastoral Epistles]{.class_s2FX}).

The [King James]{.class_s2FX} supplies the Hebrew word for witness here (["Ed"]{.class_s2FW}) because that is the style of the Hebrew text: the Hebrew word is given and then defined. For examples, see the naming of Jacob's sons in Genesis 29:32--35, 30:6--24. If the [King James]{.class_s2FX} hadn't added ["shall be,"]{.class_s2FW} you would have a subject with  no verb, and that wouldn't be good English. So the [King James]{.class_s2FX} adds words where necessary, and it puts them in italics to let you know those words weren't in the Hebrew or Greek texts. In other words, the [Authorized Version, ]{.class_s2FX}unlike the modern translations, is an [honest text.]{.class_s2FX} The new versions will add words without identifying them and then complain about the [King James']{.class_s2FX} italics. They're a bunch of [apostate hypocrites.]{.class_s2FX}

The next thing is this matter of setting up stones as a witness. Jacob does it in Genesis 31:45--48, and Joshua does it in Joshua 24:27, and we will cover the subject when we get to that latter passage.

[]{#c28G.xhtml}

# Chapter 23 {.heading_s2B}

23:1 And it came to pass a long time after that the LORD had given rest unto Israel from all their enemies round about, that Joshua waxed old and stricken in age.

2 And Joshua called for all Israel, and for their elders, and for their heads, and for their judges, and for their officers, and said unto them, I am old and stricken in age:

3 And ye have seen all that the LORD your God hath done unto all these nations because of you; for the LORD your God is he that hath fought for you.

4 Behold, I have divided unto you by lot these nations that remain, to be an inheritance for your tribes, from Jordan, with all the nations that I have cut off, even unto the great sea westward.

5 And the LORD your God, he shall expel them from before you, and drive them from out of your sight; and ye shall possess their land, as the LORD your God hath promised unto you.

Joshua is up in years now, around 110 years old (24:29). The old song goes, "Old soldiers never die; they just fade away." If a fellow can get through combat for six months, he can get through sixty years. If he can survive his first three or four initial actions, the chances are he won't die in combat; he'll just get old and die.

That's an ironic kind of thing, but it is nearly always true. Most guys who die in battle get shot in their first or second action. If they can make it past three or four, they usually go on and on. And in a way, it is pitiful, because, at least in the old days, they want to die fighting.

My dad used to teach my brother and me that the highest honor any man can have is to die in combat leading troops for his country. With the way this country has treated God and His word in the last sixty years, I don't believe that anymore. I believe the greatest honor any man can have is to [die doing what God has called him to do.]{.class_s2FX} But with a lot of these battle-scarred veterans---whether []{#c28G.xhtml_page_349}physically or spiritually---that's usually not how it ends.

At one time, my daughter Diana had four pictures hanging in her bedroom; they represented four generations of my family who were all in the military. One was a picture of my great granddaddy in his General's uniform from the Civil War. The next was a picture of my granddaddy in his General's uniform from the Philippine Insurrection. The third was a picture of my dad who ended World War II as a Colonel, and on his uniform, he had three battle stars from World War I. The last one was a picture of me, but she couldn't get one of me in my uniform. I was a Second Lieutenant at the end of World War II. All those old soldiers in my family all died of old age.

My dad had three campaigns under his belt. He was up around sixty somewhere when World War II broke out, and the Army put him in the ordnance corps (weapons development). That just about broke his heart. As a combat man, he wanted to be in a line company in the infantry. He wanted the chance to die in combat, but that's not what happened. He retired, and his final years were filled with taking walks on Rehoboth Beach (Delaware), playing bridge, and going to the movies. "Old soldiers never die; they just fade away."

MacArthur came home from Korea, gave his farewell address to Congress, and then faded into the background. He grew older and older until he was asked to speak at West Point; then two years later was dead. That guy made it through Veracruz, World War I, World War II, Korea; and died in a hospital back here in the States of a rare liver disease. Patton would lead attacks in the front tank with a brace of six shooters. He didn't die in combat; he died in a car accident after the war was over. Rommel would walk through a hail of bullets in an attack and make fun of the guys lying flat on the ground trying to survive the gunfire; he would make fun of them and tell them to get up and look around. He didn't die in combat; he was forced to commit suicide by taking poison after an unsuccessful assassination attempt on Hitler. "Old soldiers never die; they just fade away.

["Joshua waxed old and stricken in age"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 1). He got up in years and couldn't handle the sword or spear like he used to. His eyesight got bad; his chest fell into his stomach; he wasn't in shape to go out to battle like the young men anymore. David got up in years and still tried leading in the attack, but when you get to a certain point, you can't do what you used to do. The Bible says, []{#c28G.xhtml_page_350}["David waxed faint"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 21:15) and almost got killed by a giant (2 Sam. 21:16). His men had to tell him, "No more" (2 Sam. 21:17). "Old soldiers never die; they just fade away."

One of the dangers of old age is defeatism. The longer you live, the more friends you lose to death, and you become very lonely. Your body becomes frail, and you are afraid of falling and breaking something that won't heal well. You can't do what you used to do, so you feel useless. I have had many an elderly person tell me, "Nobody needs me; I'm of no use to anybody."

I know how discouraging old age can be. I can't play hockey anymore; I can't fish anymore; I can't run anymore; I can't work out in the garden as long as I used to anymore. I've got macular degeneration in both eyes, so my eyesight is going out on me. The memory is going; the hearing is going. The Bible says Joshua was ["STRICKEN in age."]{.class_s2FW} That's being struck and hit by old age. I know exactly what that means: old age will knock you down, boy.

But there are some blessings to getting old. You have less trouble with the flesh, the old nature. You won't be tempted by much because you can't do anything about it anymore. If you put me in a car and turned on the radio to a "rock" station, it wouldn't bother me a bit anymore, because [I can't hear it.]{.class_s2FX}

I have found that the older I get, the easier it is to trust God because [that's all I can do.]{.class_s2FX} I have never had that much faith, but when I can't do anything about a thing, I just trust God and stop worrying about it. You young fellows try to figure out what to do and then try to handle it yourself. That's because you have the strength and mental sharpness of youth. When that's gone, you don't try to do "nuthin'" but leave it in the Lord's hands.

Some of you retired folk are missing some great opportunities to witness. Some of you grandmothers could go down to the mall, find some young man or young woman sitting around doing nothing, put your arm around the kid, and say, "How do you do? I just want to tell you the Lord loves you, and I love you, and I want you to go to Heaven some day. Would you please read this tract about the Lord Jesus Christ?" That young person will think twice before turning down someone who reminds him of his grandma.

Are you a shut-in? Then get you a telephone book, pick up a phone, and go through the white pages and witness to anyone who will talk to you. Someone in Tom Malone's church did that and went through the phone book [four times.]{.class_s2FX} On one of those calls, he stopped someone who was about to commit suicide when the phone rang and was able to lead the person to Christ.

Are you afraid to talk? Then mail out tracts. I know a guy up in Tennessee who literally got sick if he had to talk to anyone. He wanted to witness but was literally too shy to engage in a conversation. He asked, "What can I do, Dr. Ruckman?" I told him, "Mail tracts out to addresses in the phone book." He got a bunch of these booklets the Bookstore puts out entitled [Millions Disappear]{.class_s2FX} and mailed them out with a return address card if the person got saved. That guy got [500 decision cards]{.class_s2FX} back of folks who accepted Christ after reading that booklet. If you are old and can't get out, you can do that.

Back to Joshua 23. We have already discussed how Joshua could speak to nearly two million people (vs. 2) under our comments on 1:10-11, which see. We have also discussed how God fought for Israel (vs. 3) under our comments on 10:14 (which see). Remember that in your fight against sin in your life and against the world, the flesh, and the Devil. It's not just you doing the fighting; the Lord is in you in the person of the Holy Ghost fighting too. You get the victory as you ["yield yourselves unto God"]{.class_s2FW} (Rom. 6:13). You have to ["be strong in THE LORD, and in the power of HIS MIGHT"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:10). David said, ["GOD is my strength and power"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Sam. 22:33).

Notice the [military]{.class_s2FX} victory in verse 4 (["I have cut off"]{.class_s2FW}) and the future [political]{.class_s2FX} victory in verse 5 (["ye shall possess their land, as the LORD your God hath promised you"]{.class_s2FW}). Every military victory has to be followed up by a political victory, or else everything accomplished in battle is undone. After World War I, the Allied nations got together in the League of Nations and undid all four years of the war by putting war reparations on Germany. That set up everything for Adolf Hitler and World War II. The same thing happened after World War II. Everybody got together in the United Nations and gave the Russian and the Chinese Communists a seat at []{#c28G.xhtml_page_352}the table, which created the wars in Korea, Vietnam, and the "Cold War."

So the victory [after]{.class_s2FX} is just as important as the victory [before.]{.class_s2FX} The Israelites whip the armies of those heathen nations, but they don't follow through and go in and finish off the ones who are left. They try to "get along," and that's from where all the troubles recorded in Judges come.

6 Be ye therefore very courageous to keep and to do all that is written in the book of the law of Moses, that ye turn not aside therefrom to the right hand or to the left;

7 That ye come not among these nations, these that remain among you; neither make mention of the name of their gods, nor cause to swear by them, neither serve them, nor bow yourselves unto them:

8 But cleave unto the LORD your God, as ye have done unto this day.

9 For the LORD hath driven out from before you great nations and strong: but as for you, no man hath been able to stand before you unto this day.

10 One man of you shall chase a thousand: for the LORD your God, he it is that fighteth for you, as he hath promised you.

11 Take good heed therefore unto yourselves, that ye love the LORD your God.

Notice ["the book of the law of Moses"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 6 is called ["the book of the law of God"]{.class_s2FW} in 24:26 (see the same thing in Luke 2:22--23). Some Seventh-day Adventists try to make a distinction between the two, which is nonsense. The two are synonymous. [God]{.class_s2FX} was the ["lawgiver"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 33:22; James 4:12), but so was [Moses]{.class_s2FX} (Num. 21:18; John 1:17). The Bible, the written word, is like Jesus Christ, the living Word (John 1:1, 14, 7:19): 100% God; 100% man.

So Joshua 23:6 and 24:26 are a claim for the divine inspiration of the first five books of the Bible. Verse 6 is also a claim for the Mosaic authorship of the Pentateuch; this is reaffirmed by Jesus Christ in Mark 1:44, 7:10, 10:3--8, 12:26; John 5:46. The J, E, P, D, H, R []{#c28G.xhtml_page_353}writers of the higher critics are just so much "alphabet soup" cooked up by German rationalists looking for an excuse to [reject what God said;]{.class_s2FX} but ["Thy word is true from the beginning: and every one of thy righteous judgments endureth for ever"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 119:160).

Verse 6 is the charge the Lord gave to Joshua back in 1:7, and now Joshua gives it to the people. It is also a repeat of the admonition Moses gave to the people back in Deuteronomy 5:32.

["Neither make mention of the name of their gods, nor cause to swear by them"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 7; see also Exod. 23:13). Those Jews weren't even to talk about the false gods of those nations there in Canaan before them. The old saying is: "Speak of the Devil, and he appears." The name is associated with the worship: ["their drink offerings of blood will I not offer, nor take up their names into my lips"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 16:4). That last reference is connected prophetically with the worship of the Antichrist and his image in the Tribulation, and when the Lord Jesus Christ comes back at the Second Advent, He says, ["For I will take away the names of Baalim out of her mouth]{.class_s2FW} \[i.e., Israel's mouth\][, and they shall no more be remembered by their name"]{.class_s2FW} (Hos. 2:17). During the Millennium, no one's going to remember who Baal, Ashtoreth, Mithras, Jupiter, Mercury, Diana, Thor, Odin, Shiva, Brahma, Kali, Vishnu, Ganesh, Allah, Santa Claus, Mary, St. Peter, St. Michael, St. Joseph, St. Jude, St. Bernadette, "Blessed Pius IX," etc., were.

We have already commented on the material in verses 8 and 11 under 22:5, which see. Of course, when we talked about loving the Lord back in 22:5, we discussed the [doctrinal]{.class_s2FX} aspects, but love is also a very [practical, personal]{.class_s2FX} thing. Nearly every problem in the local church is a [love]{.class_s2FX} problem. Christians don't give because they don't love the Lord enough to give. They don't witness because they don't love the Lord enough to talk about Him. The Lord told the Ephesian church there in Revelation 2:4, ["Nevertheless I have somewhat against thee, because thou hast left thy first love."]{.class_s2FW}

Now if you can get things patched up between you and the Lord, that will straighten up a lot of other problems. If there is a controversy or grievance between you and Him, it is going to spill []{#c28G.xhtml_page_354}out into other relationships and other parts of your life. You have got to keep that love between you and God warm and fervent, and you can't do that if sin or resentment or bitterness or covetousness stands between you and Him.

Verse 10 is a promise to the nation based on it keeping the Law (Lev. 26:3--8), but the reverse was true as well.

["But if ye will not hearken unto me, and will not do all these commandments; And if ye shall despise my statutes, or if your soul abhor my judgments, so that ye will not do all my commandments, but that ye break my covenant . . . I will set my face against you, and ye shall be slain before your enemies: they that hate you shall reign over you; and ye shall flee when none pursueth you"]{.class_s2FW} (Lev. 26:14--15, 17).

["But it shall come to pass, if thou wilt not hearken unto the voice of the LORD thy God, to observe to do all his commandments and his statutes which I command thee this day; that all these curses shall come upon thee, and overtake thee . . . The LORD shall cause thee to be smitten before thine enemies: thou shalt go out one way against them, and flee seven ways before them: and shalt be removed into all the kingdoms of the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 28:15, 25).

["How should one chase a thousand, and two put ten thousand to flight, except their Rock had sold them, and the LORD had shut them up?"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 32:30).

The promise was that if those Jews would keep God's Law, they would never lose a battle; God would rout their enemies before them. But if they didn't keep the Law and they worshipped other gods, they would be the ones put to flight before their enemies until they ended up being taken into captivity. When God sent Judah into captivity, He told them, ["For though ye had smitten the whole army of the Chaldeans that fight against you, and there remained but wounded men among them, yet should they rise up every man in his tent, and burn this city with fire"]{.class_s2FW} (Jer. 37:10). In other words, even if those Jews managed to wound everyone in Nebuchadnezzar's army down to the last man, God said He would raise up that bunch of cripples, amputees, maimed, and []{#c28G.xhtml_page_355}casualties, and let them take Jerusalem and burn it to the ground. That's how upset the Lord got with His chosen people.

That is a picture of the United States in its present condition if you ever saw it. The world used to tremble when American troops showed up. Back during the Spanish-American War, an American got in trouble down in Cuba and was about to be killed. He wrapped an American flag around himself and said, "Shoot if you dare," and nobody shot. [They will now.]{.class_s2FX} They'll burn the flag with you in it. They'll take over your embassy in Iran (Jimmy Carter), bomb it in Kenya (Clinton), and kill the ambassador in Libya (Obama), and not worry about you doin' nothin' about it because [you won't.]{.class_s2FX} And with your Army, Navy, and Marines full of women and queers under Obama, you ain't gonna make anybody "shake in their boots." Those Moslems will laugh at you, right before they cut your head off or blow you to pieces. Brethren, the Lord's got a controversy with this nation, and He's not going to let it get away with what He wouldn't even let His own chosen people get away with.

12 Else if ye do in any wise go back, and cleave unto the remnant of these nations, even these that remain among you, and shall make marriages with them, and go in unto them, and they to you:

13 Know for a certainty that the LORD your God will no more drive out any of these nations from before you; but they shall be snares and traps unto you, and scourges in your sides, and thorns in your eyes, until ye perish from off this good land which the LORD your God hath given you.

14 And, behold, this day I am going the way of all the earth: and ye know in all your hearts and in all your souls, that not one thing hath failed of all the good things which the LORD your God spake concerning you; all are come to pass unto you, and not one thing hath failed thereof.

15 Therefore it shall come to pass, that as all good things are come upon you, which the LORD your God promised you; so shall the LORD bring upon you all evil things, until he have destroyed you from off this good land which the LORD your God hath given you.

16 When ye have transgressed the covenant of the LORD your God, which he commanded you, and have gone and served other gods, and bowed yourselves to them; then shall the anger of the LORD be kindled against you, and ye shall perish quickly from off the good land which he hath given unto you.

Verse 12 is to be contrasted with verse 8. You will either cleave to the Lord, or you will cleave to the world and your flesh. Jesus said, ["No servant can serve two masters: for either he will hate the one, and love the other; or else he will hold to the one]{.class_s2FW} \[that's cleaving\][, and despise the other. Ye cannot serve God and mammon"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 16:13). You will love and serve one or the other, but not both. If you ["love the world, the love of the Father is not in you"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 2:15).

The warning in verse 12 against marrying the heathen is good New Testament doctrine. The Apostle Paul said, ["Be ye not unequally yoked together with unbelievers: for what fellowship hath righteousness with unrighteousness? and what communion hath light with darkness?"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 6:14). Young lady, don't think you are going to win that fellow to Christ once you marry him; that rarely happens. More likely than not, what you end up with is a hell on earth with that lost spouse fighting every move you try to make toward God. Worse yet, is where the saved party gives up serving God altogether or lives like the unsaved spouse. That's the warning Joshua is giving here.

["They shall be snares and traps unto you, and scourges in your sides, and thorns in your eyes, until ye perish from off this good land which the LORD your God hath given you"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 13 cf. Num. 33:55). That's what happens when a Christian tries to make friends and get along with the Devil and his crowd. The New Testament says that some Christians are trapped and taken captive by the Devil ["at his will"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 3:7; 2 Tim. 2:26). The Bible says, ["In the transgression of an evil man there is a snare"]{.class_s2FW} (Prov. 29:6). So sin is a snare to entrap the Christian for the Devil, and when you let sin slide in your Christian life, you are helping Satan to set the bear trap to catch you.

The ["scourges in your sides"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c28G.xhtml_page_357} is a whip like a cat o' nine tails being used to beat someone, with the straps wrapping around the sides of that person and tearing off the flesh until the ribs and organs are exposed. ["Thorns in your eyes"]{.class_s2FW} is reminiscent of Paul's ["thorn in the flesh"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 12:7). Although the New Testament never states outright what that ["thorn"]{.class_s2FW} is, the implication in Galatians 6:11 is that it is a problem with his eyes.

Now Paul's ["thorn"]{.class_s2FW} wasn't a punishment or a consequence of his sin. Second Corinthians 12:7 says it was ["the message of Satan to buffet me, lest I should be exalted above measure."]{.class_s2FW} Paul had gone up to Heaven and seen all the glory up there that John described in Revelation (2 Cor. 12:1--4). To stop him from being puffed up with pride over being given the privilege of seeing that, the Lord gave the apostle an infirmity to keep him humble (2 Cor. 12:5--7).

That is not the case here in Joshua 23:13. This is looking at something with lust or covetousness until you give the Devil the advantage in your life (2 Cor. 2:11). Jesus said, ["The light of the body is the eye . . . when thine eye is evil, thy body also is full of darkness"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 11:34). When you look at the wrong things, it can lead you into ["the unfruitful works of darkness"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 5:11). We saw that back in chapter 7. Achan ["saw"]{.class_s2FW} the Babylonian garment, the silver, and the gold; and then he ["coveted them, and took them"]{.class_s2FW} (7:21). He looked at what he shouldn't have, and it led him into sin. The same thing happened to David: he ["saw a woman washing herself,"]{.class_s2FW} and that led to adultery (2 Sam. 11:2--4). Eve ["saw that the tree was good for food, and that it was pleasant to the eyes, and a tree to be desired to make one wise"]{.class_s2FW} and then she sinned and ate the forbidden fruit (Gen. 3:6). The ["thorns in your eyes"]{.class_s2FW} here in Joshua 23:13 are the result of ["the lust of the eyes"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 2:16) being catered to in the life of the believer.

["Until ye perish from off this good land which the LORD your God hath given you."]{.class_s2FW} God told those Jews that if they got away from His Law and started worshipping idols and false gods, He would lay their cities waste, make the land a desolation, and scatter the people among the heathen nations (Lev. 26:31--33). He said, ["as []{#c28G.xhtml_page_358}the LORD rejoiced over you to do you good . . . so the LORD will rejoice over you to destroy you"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 28:63). In other words, God would be just as happy at destroying His own chosen people as He was at blessing them and giving them the land.

That's one of the most terrible verses in the Bible, but it goes along with passages like Proverbs 1:26--31; Jeremiah 14:11; Matthew 7:23; and Matthew 25:41. A sinner will either accept God's way of salvation, or he will suffer the wrath of God (John 3:36). And when a sinner exhausts the longsuffering of God, there is no more love or compassion from God to be had. The Lord may not be ["willing that any should perish"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Pet. 3:9), and He may ["have no pleasure in the death of the wicked"]{.class_s2FW} (Ezek. 33:11); but don't think for two seconds that that will stop Him from sending you to Hell for turning down His Son. God is not only ["love"]{.class_s2FW} (1 John 4:8), He's ["A CONSUMING FIRE"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 12:29).

Back to Joshua 23: ["And, behold, this day I am going the way of all the earth"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 14). That's a way of saying he is going to [die.]{.class_s2FX} That's what David said in 1 Kings 2:2. Death is called man's ["long home"]{.class_s2FW} (Eccl. 12:5); it is ["the house appointed for all living"]{.class_s2FW} (Job 30:23). If the Lord tarries, there is one thing for certain: [you are going to be put to bed with a shovel.]{.class_s2FX} The old saying is that there are only two things certain in this life: [death]{.class_s2FX} and taxes. To that, you can add [judgment]{.class_s2FX} (Heb. 9:27). There is only one way of escaping death, and that is by the One who said, ["I am the resurrection, and the life: he that believeth in me, though he were dead, yet shall he live: And whosoever liveth and believeth in me shall never die"]{.class_s2FW} (John 11:25--26).

["Not one thing hath failed of all the good things which the LORD your God spake concerning you; all are come to pass unto you."]{.class_s2FW} Now we have discussed the limitations to this statement under our comments on 21:43--45, which see. The statement is in reference to the promises made in Joshua 1. What follows is the other side of the coin. If God blessed them for following the Law, He will curse them if they break it (vss. 15--16). That was that business of reading the blessings and the cursings on Mt. Ebal and Mt. Gerizim, and you can see our remarks on those things under 8:30--34.
