Those blessings were [conditional:]{.class_s2FX} they were conditioned on Israel []{#c28G.xhtml_page_359}[keeping the Law.]{.class_s2FX}

That is not your case as a Christian. Don't misunderstand me; you will pay for your sins in the flesh. If you sow to the flesh, you will ["reap corruption"]{.class_s2FW} (Gal. 6:8). You can lose rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ for the bad things you did in your body (2 Cor. 5:10). But if you are [in Christ,]{.class_s2FX} you will live to see every good thing God promised you come to pass. Some day, you are going to be up in eternity with your Saviour in the New Jerusalem. There will be no more death, no more disease, no more pain, no more tears. You will be in a glorified body just like your Lord's. You talk about shouting, you will have an old-time Methodist fit.

These modern charismatics don't do any shouting; they just sway, wave their hands, and moan, "Hallelujah, hallelujah, hallelujah; What's it to ya." Those old-time Methodists would jump up in the air, hit the ground, roll around on the floor, and then get up and run around the building. That's how it's going to be with you some day when you finally ["know in all your hearts and in all your souls, that not one thing hath failed of all the good things which the LORD your God spake concerning you."]{.class_s2FW}

[]{#c2AF.xhtml}

# Chapter 24 {.heading_s2B}

24:1 And Joshua gathered all the tribes of Israel to Shechem, and called for the elders of Israel, and for their heads, and for their judges, and for their officers; and they presented themselves before God.

2 And Joshua said unto all the people, Thus saith the LORD God of Israel, Your fathers dwelt on the other side of the flood in old time, even Terah, the father of Abraham, and the father of Nachor: and they served other gods.

3 And I took your father Abraham from the other side of the flood, and led him throughout all the land of Canaan, and multiplied his seed, and gave him Isaac.

4 And I gave unto Isaac Jacob and Esau: and I gave unto Esau mount Seir, to possess it; but Jacob and his children went down into Egypt.

5 I sent Moses also and Aaron, and I plagued Egypt, according to that which I did among them: and afterward I brought you out.

6 And I brought your fathers out of Egypt: and ye came unto the sea; and the Egyptians pursued after your fathers with chariots and horsemen unto the Red sea.

7 And when they cried unto the LORD, he put darkness between you and the Egyptians, and brought the sea upon them, and covered them; and your eyes have seen what I have done in Egypt: and ye dwelt in the wilderness a long season.

8 And I brought you into the land of the Amorites, which dwelt on the other side Jordan; and they fought with you: and I gave them into your hand, that ye might possess their land; and I destroyed them from before you.

9 Then Balak the son of Zippor, king of Moab, arose and warred against Israel, and sent and called Balaam the son of Beor to curse you:

10 But I would not hearken unto Balaam; therefore he blessed you still: so I delivered you out of his hand.

11 And ye went over Jordan, and came unto Jericho: and the men of Jericho fought against you, the Amorites, and the Perizzites, and the Canaanites, and the Hittites, and the Girgashites, the Hivites, and the Jebusites; and I delivered them into your hand.

12 And I sent the hornet before you, which drave them out from before you, even the two kings of the Amorites; but not with thy sword, nor with thy bow.

13 And I have given you a land for which ye did not labour, and cities which ye built not, and ye dwell in them; of the vineyards and oliveyards which ye planted not do ye eat.

The chapter gives the last words of Joshua to Israel, his "swan song." The last words of a man before death tend to be very important. That is the case of Jacob in Genesis 49, Moses in Deuteronomy 32--33, David in 1 Kings 2, Jesus Christ in John 13--17, and Paul in 2 Timothy 4.

["The other side of the flood"]{.class_s2FW} in verse 2 is not a reference to Noah's Flood, for the ["fathers"]{.class_s2FW} that ["dwelt on the other side"]{.class_s2FW} of it included ["Terah, the father of Abraham."]{.class_s2FW} Well, Terah lived after Noah's Flood (Gen. 11:27--28), so ["the flood"]{.class_s2FW} here isn't Noah's Flood.

The Bible has a way of defining its own terms. Look at Psalm 66:6.

["He turned the sea into dry land ]{.class_s2FW}\[the Red Sea---Exod. 14:21--22\][: they went through the flood on foot ]{.class_s2FW}\[the Jordan River---Josh. 3:15--17)[."]{.class_s2FW}

So ["the flood"]{.class_s2FW} here is a reference to a river in flood stage (cf. Psa. 74:15). The river here would be the Euphrates because that's where Abraham and his father lived before God called Abraham out of Ur of the Chaldees (vs. 3; Gen. 15:7 cf. Acts 7:2).

The second way you know ["the flood"]{.class_s2FW} of verse 2 isn't Noah's Flood is because of the multiplicity of ["gods"]{.class_s2FW} in the verse. Before the Flood, you don't read where anyone is a polytheist worshipping many gods; everyone is a monotheist. But in Genesis 6, the ["gods"]{.class_s2FW} show up (see Psa. 82 and our comments on the chapter in that Commentary) and make a name for themselves (Gen. 6:4). It isn't []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_362}until after the Flood that images of the gods show up, and men begin to worship them. The first time the word ["images"]{.class_s2FW} occurs in your Bible in reference to an idol is in Genesis 31:19 where Rachel stole the images that belonged to Laban her father. Laban was from Haran, on the other side of the Euphrates, where Laban's grandfather Terah settled after leaving Ur of the Chaldees with Abraham (Gen. 11:31--32).

An interesting note in regards to the idolatry of Terah is the fact that the main god of Ur of the Chaldees was the [moon god,]{.class_s2FX} called [Sin]{.class_s2FX} by the Sumerians of Mesopotamia (coincidence; of course, of course). It is the god Sin after which the Sinai Peninsula and ["the wilderness of Sin"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 16:1, 17:1; Num. 33:11--12) is named. It is this moon god Sin who was called ["al-ilah"]{.class_s2FX}[ ]{.class_s2G0-0}in ancient Arabia, meaning "the god." That has been shortened in modern Arabic to [Allah.]{.class_s2FX} It was this moon god "Al-ilah" that Mohammed elevated from supreme god to sole god. So "the god" (Allah) of Mohammed (who claimed to be descended from Abraham through Ishmael) is not the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob (Exod. 3:6); he is the god of Terah [before]{.class_s2FX} he left Ur of the Chaldees (vs. 2 cf. Gen. 31:53). (For a full discussion of the archaeological evidence for Allah being a pagan moon god, see Appendix C of [The Islamic Invasion]{.class_s2FX} by Robert Morey, Christian Scholars Press, Las Vegas, NV, 1992.)

Now what Joshua is doing in these first eleven verses is reviewing Israel's history to show them how they got to the point at which they were that day. You see Stephen doing the same thing in Acts 7 and Paul doing the same thing in Acts 13. Nehemiah does it in Nehemiah 9, and David does it several places in the Psalms (e.g., Psa. 78, 105, 106, 136). The purpose of this, as given in Psalm 78:1--8, is three-fold:

1. What you read in Exodus, Numbers, and Joshua is an historical ["parable"]{.class_s2FW} of what will take place in the future at the Second Advent (Psa. 78:2). (The primary interpretation is the [doctrinal]{.class_s2FX} interpretation \[2 Tim. 3:16\], that is oftentimes [prophetic]{.class_s2FX} \[Rev. 19:10\].)

2. Truth should be passed from generation to generation so they will know ["the praises of the LORD, and his strength, and his wonderful works that he hath done"]{.class_s2FW} (Psa. 78:4).

3. And that being reminded of those things, []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_363}["they might set their hope in God"]{.class_s2FW} and not forget those things and become ["a stubborn and rebellious generation"]{.class_s2FW} whose heart is not right with God (Psa. 78:7--8).

Verses 3--4 are a reminder of the identity of the chosen seed. It is [Isaac,]{.class_s2FX} not Ishmael; it is [Jacob,]{.class_s2FX} not Esau. And to that, you can add, it is [Jesus Christ,]{.class_s2FX} not Mohammed. If Mohammed is the seventieth from Ishmael, he is from the [rejected]{.class_s2FX} seed (see Gen. 21:12; Rom. 9:7; Heb. 11:18). Many ethnologists will tell you that Mohammed's Arabians are actually a "hodge-podge" and a "mish-mash" of the [Hamitic]{.class_s2FX} tribes that settled Arabia back in Genesis 10 (from the [cursed]{.class_s2FX} son of Noah---Gen. 9:25) and the [rejected descendants]{.class_s2FX} of Abraham (Gen. 25:1--6; Psa. 83:1--9). Allah's "chosen people" (Dr. Said Al-Buti, [Fiqh Al-Sira,]{.class_s2FX} 7th ed., pg. 50; Dr. Bint Al-Shati, [Daughters of the Prophet,]{.class_s2FX} pg. 14), both physically and spiritually, are [completely rejected]{.class_s2FX} by Jehovah unless they come to Him through His Son (John 14:6).

Now we are not going into all the material covered in the passage. You can read about verses 5--7 in Exodus 5--14. Verses 7--10 are covered in the book of Numbers. We covered Balaam in our remarks under 13:22 here in Joshua, and the conquest of Sihon and Og in chapter 13. We commented on verse 12 under 10:10.

Verse 13: ["And I have given you a land for which ye did not labour, and cities which ye built not, and ye dwell in them; of the vineyards and oliveyards which ye planted not do ye eat."]{.class_s2FW} Now I told you that one of the purposes of this review of Israel's history was so they would hope in the Lord and not forget from where all the blessings came, and so fall into sin. That's why Joshua gives them verse 13. Moses warned them back in Deuteronomy 6 that when they got the cities and got the houses and got the oliveyards and vineyards, ["Then beware lest thou forget the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (Deut. 6:10--12).

That's known in philosophy as [materialism;]{.class_s2FX} it's being preoccupied with the [things]{.class_s2FX} you have and forgetting the One who gave them to you. It's the perfect description of America, and American Christians in the Laodicean church period in particular.

["Because thou sayest, I am rich, and increased with goods, and have need of nothing; and knowest not that []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_364}thou art wretched, and miserable, and poor, and blind, and naked"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 3:17).

Brethren, the measure of a man's, or a ministry's, spirituality is not the Belgian bell tower, the dorms, the multimillion-dollar facilities, the swimming pool, the sports center, the museum filled with Catholic art, the fountains, the immaculately tended grounds, acres of fenced-in prime real estate, \$500 suits, Rolex watches, crystal cathedrals, your own "Christian" theme park, private jets, etc. All that is [junk]{.class_s2FX} that will [burn]{.class_s2FX} (2 Pet. 3:10). Spirituality is measured in how much you believe that Book and how much of that Book you let affect your walk with Christ. Material things have nothing to do with it; they are no evidence at all of "spirituality."

14 Now therefore fear the LORD, and serve him in sincerity and in truth: and put away the gods which your fathers served on the other side of the flood, and in Egypt; and serve ye the LORD.

15 And if it seem evil unto you to serve the LORD, choose you this day whom ye will serve; whether the gods which your fathers served that were on the other side of the flood, or the gods of the Amorites, in whose land ye dwell: but as for me and my house, we will serve the LORD.

["Now therefore fear the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 14). We have discussed the fear of the Lord under our comments on 4:24, which see. Fearing God is good advice for anyone in any age (Eccl. 12:13).

["Serve him in sincerity and in truth."]{.class_s2FW} You are to serve God ["in sincerity"]{.class_s2FW}; i.e., without hypocrisy, without pretense, without deceit. The New Testament equivalent given by Jesus is to worship God ["in spirit and in truth"]{.class_s2FW} (John 4:24).

The Apostle Paul said we are to keep the Lord's Supper ["with the unleavened bread of sincerity and truth"]{.class_s2FW} and not ["with the leaven of malice and wickedness"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 5:8). The believer's ["conversation in the world"]{.class_s2FW} is to be ["in simplicity and godly sincerity, not with fleshly wisdom, but by the grace of God"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 1:12). The Christian is to love his Saviour and the brethren ["in sincerity"]{.class_s2FW} (Eph. 6:24; 2 Cor. 8:8). And he is to []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_365}show his good works in sincerity (Tit. 2:7).

Now if you are going to serve God, you had better do it ["in sincerity."]{.class_s2FW} If your service isn't much or what you wanted it to be, at least let it be sincere. Honest, sincere service for the Lord is better than service that is crooked or twisted, no matter what "results" you get from it. I mean, if you are not spiritual, don't pretend to be spiritual. Serve the Lord with what you've got and pray for the Lord to make you spiritual, but don't pretend to be something you're not.

But notice it is not just serving God ["in sincerity,"]{.class_s2FW} but ["in sincerity AND IN TRUTH."]{.class_s2FW} The late evangelist Paul Levin used to put out a tract that said "you may be [sincerely wrong."]{.class_s2FX} That is, it doesn't matter how sincere you are in your belief, if your faith is based on a [lie,]{.class_s2FX} you will go to Hell just like the worst hypocrite you know. There are many Catholics who are sincere in their worship and sincere in their service. They aren't dishonest like their hierarchy; they just don't know any better. But that sincerity does them no good at all as far as salvation goes because the foundation of their faith is theological thin ice that is cracking and about to give way on them. Your service and worship has to be based on [truth,]{.class_s2FX} and truth is found in the word of God (John 17:17) and not in any "infallible teaching church."

These Bible correctors and the publishers of the modern versions aren't serving God ["in truth."]{.class_s2FW} There may be a few of them ([very few]{.class_s2FX}) who believe they are sincere and have the best of motives for changing your Bible, but when it comes to the [truth,]{.class_s2FX} they are just as rotten as roadkill along the highway after three days. The Apostle Paul said:

["For we are not as many, which corrupt the word of God: but as of sincerity, but as of God, in the sight of God speak we in Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 2:17).

If you change that Book and correct that Book and subtract from that Book, you are not sincere or honest, and you certainly aren't operating by any absolute standard of truth outside of your own (or someone else's) preferences and opinions.

Back to verse 14: ["and put away the gods which your fathers served on the other side of the flood, and in Egypt, and serve ye the LORD."]{.class_s2FW} They couldn't serve the Lord ["in sincerity and in truth"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c2AF.xhtml_page_366} as long as they had idols and false gods among them (see our comments below on vss. 19--20). To serve God properly, they had to get rid of "Allah" (see our remarks above on vs. 2) and Isis, Horus, and Seb (IHS) and the Queen of Heaven, etc.

For the New Testament believer, the application is: ["Casting down imaginations, and every high thing that exalteth itself against the knowledge of God"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 10:5). That means the modern Christian is going to have to put out of his heart and mind the three main gods of America: money, sex, and education. He is going to have to put down the flesh and self. Those things have to be brought ["into captivity . . . to the obedience of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Cor. 10:5), or they will ruin your service to God.

Verse 15:[ "choose you this day whom ye will serve . . . but as for me and my house, we will serve the LORD."]{.class_s2FW} That verse ought to be written above the door or mantelpiece of every Christian home, and it ought to be the [man]{.class_s2FX} of the house who puts it up. (That's "male chauvinism" if you ever saw it.)

Have you ever thought about what "Mrs. Joshua" must have thought about what her husband said? I mean, he didn't ask her or consult her at all. He made up his mind that he was going to serve the Lord, and everyone under his roof was going to follow him in that decision or be "shown the door" (and not let it hit him or her on the "backside" going [out]{.class_s2FX}). Mrs. Joshua had no "say so" in the matter at all except to say, "Yes, dear."

If that had been an American housewife, chances are the response would have been, "Oh yeah? Well, we'll just see about that!" And then she would have made her home a living hell until it got busted up or her husband "knuckled under." Ladies, the man will either rule his home, or he will ruin it. If you have a Christian husband who loves the Lord and tries to serve Him, you had better give him all the support you can, because the "alternative" is [disaster.]{.class_s2FX}

Now those Israelites had to make a choice: ["And if it seem evil unto you to serve the LORD choose you this day whom ye will serve; whether the gods which your fathers served that were on the other side of the flood, or the gods of the Amorites, in whose land ye dwell."]{.class_s2FW} Elijah gave the Jews of his day the same choice: []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_367}["How long halt ye between two opinions? if the LORD be God, follow him: but if Baal, then follow him"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Kings 18:21).

It's black or white, good or evil, God or Satan, Jesus Christ or Mohammed, creation or evolution, the Bible or popular opinion---BUT IT CAN'T BE BOTH. You won't be able to "straddle the fence" or "play both ends against the middle." Jesus said:

["He that is not with me is against me; and he that gathereth not with me scattereth abroad"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 12:30).

There is no middle ground. You are either for God, Jesus Christ, and the Bible; or you are against them. Now choose: which side are you on? Do you accept Jesus Christ or reject Him?

You say, "Well, I don't exactly accept Him, and I don't exactly reject Him." You've just turned Him down like a bedsheet, man. If you don't accept Him, then by default you have rejected Him.

One time, a crowd got to following Jesus. He had fed over 5,000 people, and that bunch followed Him to get a free meal. To "cull the herd," Jesus made some shocking statements about eating His flesh and drinking His blood to offend the thin-skinned sissies among them who weren't interested in the truth. When that crowd went away, Jesus turned to His twelve disciples and asked, ["Will ye also go away?"]{.class_s2FW} (John 6:67). They had to make a choice: leave with the crowd or stick with Jesus. Peter spoke up and made a very astute observation: ["Lord, to whom shall we go? THOU hast the words of eternal life"]{.class_s2FW} (John 6:68).

You can walk away from Jesus Christ if you want, but if you do, you are forsaking the only One Who can save you (Acts 4:12), bring you to God the Father (John 14:6), and give you eternal life (1 John 5:11--13).

16 And the people answered and said, God forbid that we should forsake the LORD, to serve other gods;

17 For the LORD our God, he it is that brought us up and our fathers out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage, and which did those great signs in our sight, and preserved us in all the way wherein we went, and among all the people through whom we passed:

18 And the LORD drave out from before us all the people, even the Amorites which dwelt in the land: therefore will we also serve the LORD; for he is our God.

19 And Joshua said unto the people, Ye cannot serve the LORD: for he is an holy God; he is a jealous God; he will not forgive your transgressions nor your sins.

20 If ye forsake the LORD, and serve strange gods, then he will turn and do you hurt, and consume you, after that he hath done you good.

21 And the people said unto Joshua, Nay; but we will serve the LORD.

22 And Joshua said unto the people, Ye are witnesses against yourselves that ye have chosen you the LORD, to serve him. And they said, We are witnesses.

23 Now therefore put away, said he, the strange gods which are among you, and incline your heart unto the LORD God of Israel.

24 And the people said unto Joshua, The LORD our God will we serve, and his voice will we obey.

["And the people answered and said, God forbid that we should forsake the LORD, to serve other gods ]{.class_s2FW}\
[. . . therefore will we also serve the LORD, for he is our God"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 16, 19). Now doesn't that sound pious? You would almost think they meant business, wouldn't you? But look at Joshua's response to their "rededication for full-time Christian service":

["Ye cannot serve the LORD: for he is an holy God; he is a jealous God; he will not forgive your transgressions nor your sins. If ye forsake the LORD, and serve strange gods, then he will turn and do you hurt, and consume you, after that he hath done you good"]{.class_s2FW} (vss. 19--20).

That just drives this modern "positive-thinking," "possibility-thinking," and "promise-keeping" crowd up the wall. You see, Joshua is not accepting any positive "affirmation" of their faith. What he is looking for is a [negative rejection]{.class_s2FX} of the false gods he knows are among them. [He never gets it.]{.class_s2FX} Look at verse 21.

["And the people said unto Joshua, Nay; but we will serve the LORD."]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c2AF.xhtml_page_369} Nothing about getting rid of their false gods or forsaking their idols. They wanted to be like those Samaritans in 2 Kings 17:41---fearing God while at the same time they served their idols.

The application for the Christian should be obvious. You can't be fully surrendered to Christ while you keep the cigarettes in your pocket, the beer in your refrigerator, the dirty magazines under your mattress, and rock music on your dial or in your player, and hang onto the pride, bitterness, hatred, covetousness, etc. Now giving up those things has nothing to do with your salvation. You are saved by grace through faith in the shed blood of Jesus Christ. But after salvation, you can't serve the Lord properly and carry all that stuff with you.

Now what you read here is Joshua telling the people to serve God and put away their idols (vs. 14). The people say, "OK, we will serve God" (vs. 18). Joshua says, "You can't serve God as long as you have those crucifixes around your neck, those rosary beads on your dresser, those St. Christopher statues on your dashboard, and 'Mary on a half shell' out in your front yard" (vss. 19--20). The people come back again with: "Don't worry, Joshua; we'll serve the Lord" (vs. 21).

Joshua says, "All right, you are ['witnesses against yourselves']{.class_s2FW} that you said you would serve the Lord"; the people say, "That's right; we're witnesses" (vs. 22). Joshua then says, "So bring your dollies down here to the altar and let's have a bonfire" (vs. 23). And the people say, "Listen, we said we would serve the Lord, so get off our backs" (vs. 24).

I know I "ad-libbed" that last bit, but you get the gist of it: [the people never did get rid of their idols.]{.class_s2FX} It was all positive and no negative. They kept the idols and the images and the pictures, and that's what lead to the mess in the book of Judges.

25 So Joshua made a covenant with the people that day, and set them a statute and an ordinance in Shechem.

26 And Joshua wrote these words in the book of the law of God, and took a great stone, and set it up there under an oak, that was by the sanctuary of the LORD.

27 And Joshua said unto all the people, Behold, this []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_370}stone shall be a witness unto us; for it hath heard all the words of the LORD which he spake unto us: it shall be therefore a witness unto you, lest ye deny your God.

28 So Joshua let the people depart, every man unto his inheritance.

Back in verse 1, Joshua had gathered the people to [Shechem]{.class_s2FX}---not Shiloh---to present them before the Lord. If there was any doubt in your mind that the Tabernacle was in Shechem at that time, verses 25--26 settle the matter. ["The sanctuary of the LORD"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 26 cf. Exod. 25:8; Lev. 4:6; Num. 3:31--32) was right there at Shechem.

The [Septuagint,]{.class_s2FX} as found in [Vaticanus]{.class_s2FX} and [Sinaiticus]{.class_s2FX} (!), tries to "help God out" at this point by changing ["Shechem"]{.class_s2FW} to ["Shiloh,"]{.class_s2FX} but it forgot the same construction as verse 1 (["before God"]{.class_s2FW}) turns up in Judges 11:11 (["before the LORD in Mizpeh"]{.class_s2FW}; see also Judg. 20:1). Instead of accusing the text here in Joshua 24 of corruption (Shechem "crept" into the text), why not just believe what it says, as it says it. The Tabernacle was moved from Shiloh to Shechem for the ceremony here in Joshua 24, and in Judges 11 and 20, the Tabernacle was then in Mizpeh.

["So Joshua made a covenant with the people that day, and set them a statute and an ordinance in Shechem"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 25). This is not a new covenant apart from the Abrahamic and Mosaic covenants. This is a covenant of the people which seals their promise to serve the Lord (vss. 18, 21--22, 24). It is like the promise they made back in Exodus 24:3--8 to Moses, and it will be [broken]{.class_s2FX} just like they broke the one in Exodus at the golden calf. The ["statute"]{.class_s2FW} and ["ordinance"]{.class_s2FW} of the verse would be the codification into law of the promise they made.

["And Joshua wrote these words in the book of the law of God"]{.class_s2FW} (vs. 26). As we showed you back in 23:6, this ["book of the law of God"]{.class_s2FW} is ["the book of the law of Moses."]{.class_s2FW} So Joshua is making additions to Genesis, Exodus, Leviticus, Numbers, and Deuteronomy.

Now this is not the "Jehovistic" writer and the "Elohimic" writer and the "Priestly" writer and the "Deuteronomic" writer and the "Redactor" and all the infidelic nonsense put out by the higher []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_371}critics. This is Joshua adding notations to what Moses wrote, but Moses was indeed the author of the first five books of the Bible. Where you read something in the Pentateuch that Moses could not have written, you know that is a place where Joshua inserted something.

Take, for instance, Genesis 14:14---Abraham pursued the armies that took Lot captive ["unto Dan."]{.class_s2FW} Well, there was no ["Dan"]{.class_s2FW} around when Abraham did that. The city of Dan didn't show up until years after Moses died (Josh. 19:47). But Joshua knew where Dan was and put it in there for the readers of his day.

You see it over and over again throughout Genesis--Deuteronomy. The death of Moses and his "eulogy" is recorded in Deuteronomy 34:5--12. Well, Moses was dead; he didn't write that. But that's Joshua tagging that information onto the end of Deuteronomy, see.

Numbers 12:3 says,[ "(Now the man Moses was very meek, above all the men which were upon the face of the earth.)"]{.class_s2FW} Well, if Moses was that humble, why would he be writing about himself like that? He didn't. That's Joshua adding his own "addendum" there because he knew Moses personally and knew what he was like.

Just because the Holy Spirit---the REAL author of the text (2 Pet. 1:21)---moved someone later on to make an addition to the text doesn't mean it wasn't written by the one whom the book says was the author. You are about to read in a few verses about the death of Joshua, and Eleazar who died after him. Well, it could have been Joshua writing prophetically, but that is not how it is presented. In all likelihood, it is the writer of Judges (most likely Samuel) going back and adding the information he recorded in Judges 2:7--9. That doesn't mean Joshua didn't write the rest of the book, for as we saw back in 4:23 and 5:1, it was written by someone right there living through all the events. That was Joshua.

["And took a great stone and set it up there under an oak."]{.class_s2FW} Notice two things in the verse: the ["stone"]{.class_s2FW} and the ["oak."]{.class_s2FW} We'll look first at the oak. The oak tree doesn't have a good connotation in the Bible. The first time it shows up is in Genesis 35:4, where Jacob buries all the idols Rachel had spread among his household (Gen. 31:19 cf. 35:4). They were buried []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_372}["under the oak which was by Shechem"]{.class_s2FW} (Gen. 35:4), which is where Joshua sets up the stone as a witness against the Israelites' idolatry. If we had changed the text to ["Shiloh"]{.class_s2FX} as the [Septuagint]{.class_s2FX} did, we would have lost the cross-reference to Genesis 35:4. Changing the [AV]{.class_s2FX} text always results in lost revelation.

It was ["under an oak"]{.class_s2FW} at Bethel where Rebekah's nurse was buried (Gen. 35:8). Absalom, one of the greatest types of Antichrist in the Bible, got his head caught in an oak, and Joab killed him while he was hanging there (2 Sam. 18:9--14).  Saul, another type of the Antichrist, was buried beneath an oak in Jabesh (1 Chron. 10:12).

It was in oak groves where the Israelites committed their idolatry (Ezek. 6:13), and oak trees were carved into idols (Isa. 44:14--17). When the Antichrist institutes cannibalism as part of the worship service during the Tribulation, a tenth of the Jews ["shall be eaten . . . as an oak"]{.class_s2FW} (Isa. 6:13). Back in the Middle Ages, in the early Thirteenth Century, Europe suffered such severe winters and lightning storms that the crops were destroyed, and the people had to rely on acorns made into bread to survive the famine.

Oaks have quite a history. In Celtic culture, the oak tree represented the male (Baal), and the lime tree represented the female (Ashtoreth). Celtic priests were called "Druids," meaning "oak men." The Celtic word [Drynemetum]{.class_s2FX} means "the sacred oak grove" or "the temple of the oak."

The oldest sanctuaries in Europe were [woods.]{.class_s2FX} In 1840, an Orthodox priest in Livonia, Russia was an eyewitness to a drunken orgy which began with a priest putting incense on a giant oak tree. The people bowed down to it and prayed, "Holy Oak, hallelujah! Pray for us!" In Kildare, Ireland, the Catholics have a church dedicated to St. Bridgett; it is called "the Church of the Oak Tree."

From ancient times, the oak tree has been connected with [thunder and lighting.]{.class_s2FX} The oak is the tree most often struck by lightning. It was believed that lightning was produced in heaven by the gods rubbing two oaken sticks together. Oaks that had been struck by lightning were made into weapons to give those who wielded them the power the gods had bestowed on the tree. Wood from an oak struck by lightning was used to protect a house from []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_373}lightning.

In Norse mythology, the thunder god was Thor, and the oak was sacred to him. In Greek mythology, Zeus controlled lightning; his name in Rome was Jupiter (Acts 14:12--13, 19:35). Zeus and Jupiter are simply the Greek and Roman names for [Baal,]{.class_s2FX} the [storm]{.class_s2FX} god (1 Kings 18). They are all connected with [electromagnetic forces]{.class_s2FX} (Dan. 11:38).

In addition to being the god who controlled thunderstorms, Jupiter was the oak god. All the Greek and Roman Kings wore laurel wreaths made of oak leaves as crowns (1 Cor. 9:25) because all the Greek Kings were called Zeus and all the Roman Emperors demanded worship by impersonating Jupiter. Alexander the Great claimed to be virgin born from Zeus; when he conquered Egypt, he associated Zeus with the chief god of Egypt, Ammon. Ammon was a [goat-headed]{.class_s2FX} god (Dan. 8:5, 8, 21), like Baphomet of Masonry; the Zoroastrians equated him with the [Devil.]{.class_s2FX}

Now with the connection, both in and out of the Bible, of the oak with Satan and idolatry, if I had to make a guess as to what kind of tree on which Christ was crucified, it wouldn't be a dogwood tree. That's a Roman Catholic fable that is just as credible as Veronica's hankey, the holy grail, the Shroud of Turin, and "The Robe." The cross was undoubtedly made from an [oak]{.class_s2FX} tree.

The second thing in verse 26 is the ["great stone"]{.class_s2FW} Joshua set up. Verse 27 says the stone would ["be a witness unto us; for it hath heard all the words of the LORD which he spake unto us: it shall be therefore a witness unto you."]{.class_s2FW} I wouldn't be too quick to dismiss that as an "anthropomorphism" (attributing the attributes of man to non-human things). Throughout the Scriptures, stones are associated with some kind of testimony.

Jacob set up a stone as a pillar to the fact that God had appeared to him at Bethel (Gen. 28:18--22). He set up a stone again at Mizpah on the other side of Jordan as a witness between him and Laban that neither one would pass over it to do the other harm (Gen. 31:45--55). When Jacob got right and returned to Bethel, he set up another stone as a pillar and ["poured a drink offering"]{.class_s2FW} on it (Gen. 35:14--15). Samuel set up a stone as a witness that God had helped Israel when the Philistines attacked (1 Sam. 7:12). And we have already seen how []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_374}Joshua set up twelve stones on the bank of the Jordan and twelve stones in the river's bed as a testimony to God drying up the Jordan for the children of Israel to cross (Josh. 4:3--21).

Now anyone who takes Darwin seriously should love verses 26--27; after all, according to Darwin all organic life came from [inorganic igneous rocks.]{.class_s2FX} That's the evolutionary "fairy tale for grown ups": the earth was slung out of the sun at 6,000 degrees and cooled into rock; water vapor condensed from the cooling rock and developed amino acids that came to life like Frankenstein's monster after being struck by lightning; and after several billions of years (give or take a few billion; science is very exact), here you are.

The Bible had Darwin beat by 3,400 years. Not only could rocks hear, they could [speak.]{.class_s2FX} Jesus said if His disciples didn't praise Him ["the stones would immediately cry out"]{.class_s2FW} (Luke 19:40). John the Baptist said God was ["able of these stones to raise up children unto Abraham"]{.class_s2FW} (see Luke 3:8 and our comments on that verse in that Commentary). Jesus Christ was ["the stone which the builders rejected"]{.class_s2FW} (Mark 12:10) and the ["chief corner stone"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:6). Christians are ["lively stones"]{.class_s2FW} in God's ["spiritual house"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Pet. 2:5).

When it comes to this business of the rocks hearing things and speaking out and testifying to what they heard, when I was a boy, we had crystal radio sets: that was a stone of quartz crystal used to pick up radio waves and turn them into voices and sounds to which you could listen. That crystal radio set was replaced by the transistor radio. Transistors were made from silicon---sand from [stones;]{.class_s2FX} ditto recording tape and computer chips. Stones make it possible to record sound and images and play them back. It has been reported that in 1993, scientists had equipment which they said could pick up sound waves from stone 24 hours after they were recorded. Give them time, and they'll finally [catch up]{.class_s2FX} to Joshua in 1400 B.C.

Now have you ever thought about words and stones? Job cried out one time, ["Oh that my words were now written! oh that they were printed in a book! That they were graven with an iron pen and lead in the rock for ever!"]{.class_s2FW} (Job 19:23--24). They were; that's what you read in the book of Job. When God wrote His words for the first time on this earth, He wrote them on ["tables of []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_375}stone ]{.class_s2FW}\
[. . . with the finger of God"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 31:18). The high priest in the Old Testament had the names of the twelve tribes of Israel graven in two onyx stones that were attached to his garments ["in ouches of gold"]{.class_s2FW} (Exod. 39:6); and on his breastplate were twelve precious stones, each with the name of one of the tribes engraved under it (Exod. 39:10--14). God used those stones to communicate with an inquirer by lighting up those stones like a computer (Exod. 25:7 cf. 1 Sam. 23:9--11, 30:7--8). And Jeremiah wrote, ["The sin of Judah is written with a pen of iron, and with the point of a diamond]{.class_s2FW} \[a precious stone\][: it is graven upon the table of the heart, and upon the horns of your altars"]{.class_s2FW} (Jer. 17:1).

So God's words have been recorded in stone and man's words and sins have been recorded in stone. Think about that for a moment. That Bible says that at the White Throne Judgment, ["the books were opened . . . and the dead were judged out of those things which were written in the books, according to their works"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 20:12). What if those books were [stones]{.class_s2FX} like you read above? All God would have to do is pull up a few of those rocks and play back the relevant information recorded in them about you. After all, people, if man can develop a computer out of [stone]{.class_s2FX} that can record 31,675,383,808 "bytes" of information per square inch, don't you know God has a "computer system" that makes anything Bill Gates or Gerhard Dirks came up with look like a broken abacus. That Bible says:

["Thou hast consulted shame to thy house by cutting off many people, and hast sinned against thy soul. For the stone shall cry out of the wall, and the beam out of the timber shall answer it"]{.class_s2FW} (Hab. 2:10--11).

There's an accounting coming, people; and ["every idle word that men shall speak, they shall give account thereof in the day of judgment"]{.class_s2FW} (Matt. 12:36).

29 And it came to pass after these things, that Joshua the son of Nun, the servant of the LORD, died, being an hundred and ten years old.

30 And they buried him in the border of his inheritance []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_376}in Timnathserah, which is in mount Ephraim, on the north side of the hill of Gaash.

31 And Israel served the LORD all the days of Joshua, and all the days of the elders that overlived Joshua, and which had known all the works of the LORD, that he had done for Israel.

32 And the bones of Joseph, which the children of Israel brought up out of Egypt, buried they in Shechem, in a parcel of ground which Jacob bought of the sons of Hamor the father of Shechem for an hundred pieces of silver: and it became the inheritance of the children of Joseph.

33 And Eleazar the son of Aaron died; and they buried him in a hill that pertained to Phinehas his son, which was given him in mount Ephraim.

Joshua died at 110 years old. He lived to be the same age as Joseph, his forefather (Gen. 50:22, 26), so in verse 32, you have the burial of Joseph. Joshua could say with the Apostle Paul, ["I have fought a good fight, I have finished my course, I have kept the faith"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 4:7).

Verse 31 is key to what follows in the next book, Judges. As long as Joshua lived, and all the elders who had seen what God had done through Joshua, the people stayed right (see Judg. 2:7). As soon as that generation was dead, though, everything went to pieces. You have seen that in the past twenty years here in America: as soon as the generation of preachers who built the great Fundamental works in the 50s, 60s, and 70s passed away in the 80s and 90s, the generation that was in charge from Clinton onward went to pot.

Now Paul said, ["Be ye followers of me, even as I also am of Christ"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Cor. 11:1). My students are always told, "You're following a man; you're following Ruckman." Well, there's nothing wrong with following a man as long as that man is following Christ.

The first few months I was saved, I lived off the spirituality of Hugh Pyle, the man who led me to Christ, and I don't regret it for a minute. I am not ashamed of following any of the men who were an inspiration to me in my Christian life and in the ministry---despite whatever faults they had. I thank God for every one of them.

Bob Jones Sr. was an inspiration to me for the six years I attended Bob Jones University. I know he trusted too much in his faculty and allowed his son to bring in a lot of cultural stuff on which no Christian institution has any business wasting money and time; but the "old man" had a lot of wisdom, and I learned a lot from him personally.

"Old man Bob" is dead now, though. What am I supposed to do, quit? James McGinley was a great inspiration to me in my early Christian life. He died. Should I have quit because he's gone? Glen Schunk was an inspiration to me getting into the ministry. When he died, was I to get out of it? Alex Dunlap was a great inspiration to me; he's dead. Beauchamp Vick was one of the best friends I had in the ministry; he stuck with me through thick and thin. He's dead too. My spiritual father, Hugh Pyle, died a couple of years ago. Do I quit just because they're all gone?

Christian, there's nothing wrong with following a Christian man and his Biblical conduct, but there has to come a time when you grow up enough as a believer to stand on your own two feet. You can no longer live on the faith, Bible knowledge, and spirituality of others; you have to get your own. You are going to have to live on your own Bible study, your own prayer life, your own fellowship with the Lord; not mine or anybody else's. You are going to have to grow up and mature as a believer so that when your "Joshua" dies (whoever that may be for you), you go right on with the Lord.

Amen, amen, amen! I know good preaching when I hear it, and [that's good preaching!]{.class_s2FX}

Verse 32: ["And the bones of Joseph, which the children of Israel brought up out of Egypt, buried they in Shechem, in a parcel of ground which Jacob bought of the sons of Hamor the father of Shechem for an hundred pieces of silver: and it became the inheritance of the children of Joseph."]{.class_s2FW} This is the fulfillment of an oath taken in faith (Gen. 50:25 cf. Heb. 11:22). As he lay dying, Joseph believed God would one day bring the children of Israel out of Egypt and back to the land He promised to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. Historically that took place in Exodus 13:19 and here in verse 32, but prophetically, that is what takes place at the Second Advent.

You see, Joseph is the greatest type of Christ in the Bible (in over 152 particulars---see Arthur W. Pink's work [Gleanings in Genesis]{.class_s2FX}), and Egypt is a type of this world. The bones of Joseph were carried out of Egypt exactly as the bones of Jesus Christ were carried out of this world at His resurrection and ascension (see our comments on Gen. 50:25; Exod. 13:19; Heb. 11:22 in those Commentaries). And when Jesus Christ returns at the Second Advent, His bones end up in the Promised Land, and Israel gets the full inheritance the Lord promised Abraham back in Genesis 15:18.

The next thing to notice from an historical perspective is that coins existed long before the evolutionary archaeologists and historians care to admit. The original "scientific" evidence was that coins were developed by the Romans; then someone got to digging around in some civilization's junk heap over in Turkey and Greece and said, "No, we found coins here from 600 B.C." [Coins were being used as a medium of exchange all the way back in 1900 B.C.]{.class_s2FX} (Gen. 20:16). The "coin" back then was a piece of precious metal (gold, silver, or brass) of a certain weight (Gen. 23:16). According to Edersheim's history (Vol. II, pg. 666), the Romans and Greeks were "Johnny-come-latelys" when it came to inventing "coins."

Now, Jacob buying ["a parcel of ground . . . of the sons of Hamor the father of Shechem"]{.class_s2FW} is a reference to the events of Genesis 33:19--20. Because this plot of land was used to bury Joseph's bones, the cross-reference is run over to Stephen's words in Acts 7:15--16. That last reference is then given as a classic blunder (a "mistake") in the [King James]{.class_s2FX} text, for it is evident that Abraham bought the cave of Macpelah outside of Hebron in southern Judah for a burying place (Gen. 23:19--20)---NOT Shechem in Mt. Ephraim---and [that]{.class_s2FX} is where Jacob was buried (Gen. 50:13)---NOT Shechem in Mt. Ephraim.

We have discussed the solution to this "problem" in our Commentary on Acts (2003, pp. 267--269) and in our work [The "Errors" in the King James Bible]{.class_s2FX} (1999, pp. 32--35), and we refer you to those for the answers. Here we will just point out that any "problem" came from not accepting the [King James]{.class_s2FX} text as it stands. Genesis 33:19 said nothing about Jacob buying any land to bury anybody, and Acts 7:15--16 say nothing about Joseph being buried. []{#c2AF.xhtml_page_379}Joshua 24:32 was read into both passages to create a "problem" for the scholars to "solve" [by correcting your Bible with their own opinions.]{.class_s2FX} Typical apostate "scholarship."

In closing our Commentary on the book of Joshua, notice the burial of three types of Christ in the last five verses: Joshua (vss. 29--30), Joseph (vs. 23), and the [high priest]{.class_s2FX} Eleazar (vs. 33). While all three are indeed types of the Lord Jesus Christ, they are still just [types.]{.class_s2FX} Types are [pictures]{.class_s2FX} of the real thing, but they are [not]{.class_s2FX} the real thing. The real "Joshua" died, was buried, and [rose again.]{.class_s2FX} He is now in Heaven, seated at His Father's right hand, where He exercises an everlasting, unchanging priesthood to intercede on our behalf (Heb. 7:24--25). Unlike Joshua and Joseph, He was (and [is]{.class_s2FX}) [sinless]{.class_s2FX}---["holy, harmless, undefiled, separate from sinners"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 7:26--27).

Joseph could bring [physical, temporary]{.class_s2FX} salvation to his brethren (Gen. 50:20), but Jesus ["became the author of ETERNAL salvation"]{.class_s2FW} (Heb. 5:9). And what Joshua could not do (Heb. 4:8), Jesus Christ will at His Second Coming. When Jesus Christ, the second "Joshua," comes at His Second Advent, He will fight against the heathen nations like He did in the book of Joshua (Zech. 14:3 cf. Josh. 10:14, 42); when He gets through, there won't be any incomplete obedience as you find at the end of Joshua and the beginning of Judges. All the false gods will be put down (Zech. 14:9), and all the "Palestinians" will be kicked out of [His land]{.class_s2FX} (Zech. 14:21). And when He returns, if you belong to Him [now]{.class_s2FX} and serve Him faithfully [now,]{.class_s2FX} He'll reward you with an inheritance in His kingdom (Col. 3:24).

So as we close out this book which devotionally is about the Christian's spiritual warfare and prophetically is about Jesus Christ's Second Advent, here is what you, as a New Testament believer, need to keep in mind. You are to ["Fight the good fight of faith"]{.class_s2FW} to ["lay hold on eternal life"]{.class_s2FW} (1 Tim. 6:12) in the sense of laying up your treasures in Heaven (1 Tim. 6:19 cf. Matt. 6:19--21). Paul calls this pressing ["toward the mark for the prize of the high calling of God in Christ Jesus"]{.class_s2FW} (Phil. 3:14).

As a Christian soldier, you are to ["strive lawfully"]{.class_s2FW} (2 Tim. 2:5); you are to strive with [temperance]{.class_s2FX} and [certainty]{.class_s2FX} (1 Cor. 9:25--26). Why? Because a crown awaits you at the return of your Lord (2 Tim. 4:7--8). You are to ["war a good warfare"]{.class_s2FW}[]{#c2AF.xhtml_page_380} (1 Tim. 1:18) because your Lord is coming back to reward you for victory in the battle.

["He that overcometh shall inherit all things; and I will be his God, and he shall be my son"]{.class_s2FW} (Rev. 21:7). That's not just for the Tribulation saint at the Second Advent; it's for the Christian in this age also (1 John 5:4).
